# Roadmap status

This is a snapshot of which roadmap waves are landed (with commit
hashes), partial, blocked, or still pending. Maintain alongside
`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` when changes ship.

The roadmap proper lives in `~/.claude/plans/i-want-you-to-swift-pine.md`.

## Wave 1 — Close the gaps

| Item | Status | Commit / notes |
|---|---|---|
| 1.1 Microstructure → prompt | ✅ landed | pre-existing WIP (uncommitted at session start) |
| 1.2 Multi-timeframe confluence | ✅ landed | `crypto/timeframes.py` (WIP) |
| 1.3 Stocks-side parity | ⏳ partial | regime / timeframes / ML / shadow runner / catalysts / position monitor / risk halt / dashboard risk push all wired (see Stocks-side wiring section). Remaining gaps: sentiment manager (CryptoPanic is crypto-only — needs an equities news source), ML forecaster (Chronos's 96-step minimum is too sparse for daily Alpaca bars), and inline `performance_text` / `active_adjustments` blocks on the LLM prompt (needs a stocks-side analytics + self-improve module) |
| 1.4 Catalyst calendar | ✅ landed | `eed276d` (tests) + WIP module + extras (Static, Earnings, RiskPolicy, next_window) |
| 1.5 Thesis-tag P&L attribution | ✅ landed | `44ed326` (module) + post-close hook in monitor |

## Cross-cutting

* **Insights hub** (`f51bcbc`) — single in-process container threaded into web `app_state["insights"]` so every analytic is reachable from the dashboard.
* **Insights web routes** (`95209bb`) — `/api/insights/{regret,thesis,drift,stress,shadow,calibration,regime,basis,treasury,purification,replay}`.
* **Insights CLI** (`94b258c` + later) — 9 subcommands surfacing the analytics at the terminal.
* **Post-close fan-out** — `core/post_close.py` wires drift / thesis / regret / purification at the monitor close site; one call, four recorders. Wired for both crypto (`crypto/components.py`) and stocks (`trading/scheduler.py`).

## Round 3 — Architecture / Decision-quality / UX (`docs/cleanup_roadmap.md`)

| Wave | Status | Commit |
|---|---|---|
| A — Typed `BotContext` / `DashboardContext` | ✅ landed | `8e1bb32` |
| B — Per-stage cycle pipeline | ✅ substantively landed | `26795f9` instrumentation seam landed; `core/cycle_pipeline.py:CycleState` dataclass + `core/cycle_stages.py:CycleStage` Protocol scaffolded. **Sixteen stages extracted** — twelve `BuildXStage`s + four `Augment*Stage`s (every text-mutating helper that used to live on `CryptoCycleService` is now a stage class with a state-mutation contract). Stages include the 12 build-stages + `AugmentRegimeWithMemoryStage` (uses `ml.regime_memory.build_regime_features`), `AugmentRegimeWithRagStage` (uses `core.llm.rag.build_rag_query`), `AugmentMicrostructureWithWhaleFlowsStage` (Etherscan flows + hub.whale_flows side effect), `AugmentMicrostructureWithBasisStage` (broker funding signal + hub.basis.observe). **The crypto cycle now drives a single 14-stage list** end-to-end: builders + risk + augmenters interleaved (e.g. `BuildMicrostructureStage` immediately followed by `AugmentMicrostructureWithBasisStage` and `AugmentMicrostructureWithWhaleFlowsStage`). `run_stages` gained a `stop_on_halt: bool = False` opt-in that short-circuits the chain after a stage sets `state.halt = True` — `BuildCryptoRiskStage` uses this to stop the rest of the pipeline from doing wasted work on a halt cycle. 17th stage extracted: `ApplyRegimeGateStage` — runs after `strategy.analyze`, reads `state.plan` + `state.indicators_cache`, strips BUY decisions for pairs in confirmed downtrend (≥0.6 confidence). 5 new tests. cycle.py: 1121 → **748 lines** (–33%). 18th stage extracted: `BuildForecastsStage` — owns the Chronos forecaster path that used to live inline in `_run_cycle_impl` (build the per-pair forecast dict, skip pairs with <20 klines, render via `format_forecasts_for_prompt`). New `CycleState.forecasts_text` field replaces the hacky "seed via ml_signals_text" workaround; `BuildMlSignalsStage` now reads `state.forecasts_text` directly. The crypto cycle's stage list grew from 14 to 15 (BuildForecastsStage runs immediately before BuildMlSignalsStage); 6 new tests cover the no-forecaster / no-klines / below-min-history / happy-path / failure-swallowing / stable-name paths. cycle.py: 748 → **727 lines** (–35% from baseline). **Stocks parity for `ApplyRegimeGateStage`**: stage made symbol-source-agnostic (iterates `state.indicators_cache.items()` instead of `state.klines_by_symbol`), and `TradingCycleService._run_cycle_impl` now drives it via `run_stages` after `strategy.analyze` — so the stocks bot now also strips BUYs for tickers in confirmed downtrend (≥0.6). 1 new stocks-side test in `test_cycle_stages.py`. **Encapsulation tighten**: the two `self._portfolio._repo.X` private-attribute leaks in `crypto/cycle.py` (`record_indicator_snapshot` after a buy fills, `get_paused_pairs` when computing tradeable pairs) replaced with public `CryptoPortfolioTracker.record_indicator_snapshot` / `get_paused_pairs` methods that delegate to the structurally-wider runtime repo. e2e pipeline test updated to drive `BuildForecastsStage` (no-op when no forecaster wired) so the no-deps path covers the full 12-stage shape — `state.forecasts_text == ""` is now in the assertion set. **DRYed the analyze + shadow kwargs**: the crypto cycle previously specified all 18 LLM-input fields twice (once in the `strategy.analyze(...)` call, once in the `shadow_kwargs=dict(...)` literal that fed the shadow runner with the same shape). Now it builds `analyze_kwargs` once, calls `self._strategy.analyze(**analyze_kwargs)`, and passes the same dict to `_execute_and_notify(shadow_kwargs=analyze_kwargs)`. Mirrors the stocks cycle's pattern; cycle.py: 727 → **711 lines** (–37% from baseline). **Bug fix in `_execute_and_notify`**: when `shadow_runner is None` (the default — `LLM_SHADOW_ENABLED=false`), the early-return path skipped both `record_indicator_snapshot` (broke the ML retraining loop's labelling) and `notify_trade` (operator never got Telegram alerts on fills). Restructured so per-fill bookkeeping runs unconditionally, with the shadow runner observation now an optional best-effort step independent of fill results. New `test_records_indicator_snapshot_and_notifies_when_no_shadow_runner` test in `test_crypto_cycle.py` locks in the fix. **Stale-test cleanup**: `tests/test_cycle_microstructure_news.py` had 6 tests calling `cycle._build_microstructure_text()` / `cycle._build_news_text()` (helpers that were removed when their behaviour moved into `BuildMicrostructureStage` / `BuildNewsStage`). Replaced the file with the one surviving smoke test (`last_indicators_cache_initially_none`) plus a docstring pointer to where the behaviour now lives. **Stocks risk-halt parity bug fixed**: `BuildStockRiskStage` previously stamped only `risk_text` + `indicators_cache`, dropping the `state.is_halted` field on the floor. The stocks bot would keep trading even when the portfolio risk engine reported a heat / drawdown breach (crypto already short-circuits via `state.halt`). Stage now also populates `state.risk_state` and `state.halt`; `TradingCycleService` runs the stage list with `stop_on_halt=True` and returns early on a halt signal (with a warning log mirroring crypto's "Risk engine halt: …" line). 2 new tests in `test_cycle_stages.py` lock the halt threading + the empty-bars-resets-halt invariant. **Stocks dashboard risk parity**: `TradingCycleService` now accepts an optional `insights_hub` kwarg (wired from `trading/scheduler.py`) and pushes `state.risk_state` to `hub.runtime.risk_state` after each cycle — same shape as crypto's push, so the dashboard's `/api/risk/state` and the mobile / Prometheus surfaces all render the stocks bot's heat / drawdown / correlation. Previously the stocks process never wrote to that field, so the panel would stay empty. Both pushes now also carry a `"market"` discriminator (`"crypto"` or `"stocks"`) so a dashboard process that observes both bots' runtime state (e.g. when both are co-hosted in dev) can attribute the values correctly without comparing summary text. The Prometheus collector (`web/prometheus.py`) reads the discriminator and emits `halal_trader_drawdown_pct` / `halal_trader_portfolio_heat_pct` with a `market="crypto"` / `market="stocks"` / `market="unknown"` label — Grafana can finally graph the two bots' risk side-by-side rather than the metric flicking between them on every cycle. 2 new tests in `test_prometheus.py` lock the labelling. **Grafana dashboard updated**: the bundled `infra/grafana/halal-trader.json` now uses `max(halal_trader_drawdown_pct)` for the single-stat drawdown panel (avoids Grafana picking an arbitrary market when both are present) and adds `legendFormat: {{market}}` to the portfolio-heat timeseries panel so each market is a labelled line. `infra/README.md` mentions both new metrics in the dashboard contents list. **Mobile summary surfaces market**: `_build_summary` (used by both `/api/mobile/summary` and `/ws/state`) now reads the `market` discriminator off `runtime.risk_state` and exposes it as a top-level `"drawdown_market"` key — the operator's phone shows whether the displayed drawdown belongs to the crypto or stocks bot. **Dashboard frontend renders market**: the React `RiskState` interface (`dashboard/src/api/types.ts`) now includes the optional `market` field, and the `RiskAndSystem` page's "Portfolio Risk (last cycle)" header appends ` · crypto` / ` · stocks` so the user always knows which bot the heat / drawdown card belongs to. Stale "wait for the next crypto cycle" copy generalised to "next cycle" since stocks now populates it too. **Mobile summary tests added**: 2 new tests in `test_mobile_summary.py` lock the wiring — populated risk_state → `drawdown_market` field, no risk_state → field is `None`. **Risk-route test added**: 1 new test in `test_web_app.py` confirms `/api/risk/state` round-trips the `market` discriminator out to the dashboard. **Dashboard README endpoint table refreshed**: added the missing `/api/risk/state`, `/api/mobile/summary`, and `/ws/state` rows, each calling out the `market` / `drawdown_market` discriminator and noting that `/metrics` ships a `market`-labelled drawdown / heat gauge. **`pushed_at` timestamp on risk_state pushes**: both crypto and stocks cycles now stamp `runtime.risk_state["pushed_at"]` with an ISO-formatted UTC timestamp when they write the snapshot. Frontend `RiskState` interface gets the optional field. **Stale-snapshot badge wired**: the `RiskAndSystem` page now compares `pushed_at` against `Date.now()` and renders a red `stale Nm` badge next to the section header when the snapshot is older than 3 min for crypto / 20 min for stocks (matching the two cycles' cadences — defaults are 60 s and 15 min respectively, so the thresholds are ~3× the interval). Catches the "cycle silently stopped" failure mode without polling another endpoint. **Halt-warning log unified**: the crypto cycle's halt warning previously sat *inside* the `if runtime is not None` branch, so it would silently skip when the hub wasn't wired (e.g. in pure-bot mode without the dashboard sidecar). Moved the warning out of that branch so it fires unconditionally whenever `state.halt` is true — mirrors the stocks cycle's pattern. **Wave 1.3 row de-staled + ARCHITECTURE.md project-tree updated**: the Stocks-side parity row stale text ("regime/timeframes/sentiment/ML/shadow still deferred") rewritten to reflect the actual state (regime / timeframes / ML / shadow / catalysts / position monitor / risk halt / dashboard risk push all wired; remaining gaps are sentiment manager, ML forecaster, and `performance_text` / `active_adjustments` blocks). `docs/ARCHITECTURE.md`'s `core/` layout now lists `cycle_stages.py` (18 stage classes) alongside `cycle_pipeline.py`, and the `cycle_pipeline.py` blurb updated from "instrumentation seam" to "CycleState dataclass + run_stages driver". **Stocks Telegram fill alerts wired**: `TradingCycleService` now accepts an optional `notifier` kwarg (threaded from `trading/scheduler.py:self._notifier`) and calls `notifier.notify_trade(...)` on each filled / submitted execution result — same pattern as the crypto cycle. Previously the stocks scheduler constructed a `TelegramNotifier` but only used it for `AlertSink` (errors only), so the operator never got per-fill alerts on the stocks bot. **Stocks daily-summary Telegram alert wired**: `end_of_day` now calls `self._notifier.notify_daily_summary(summary)` after the day's P&L is recorded — parity with crypto's `_daily_close` notification. Best-effort; never blocks EOD on a failed notify. **Stocks SL/TP exit Telegram alert wired**: `StockPositionMonitor` now accepts a `notifier` kwarg and calls `notifier.notify_sl_tp(...)` after each successful close — parity with crypto's `PositionMonitor` (already wires this). The operator now gets the same ✅/❌ entry → exit P&L message regardless of which bot triggered the SL/TP. 2 new tests in `test_stock_monitor.py` lock the wiring (notifier called with correct shape) and the failure-swallowing invariant (a blowing-up notifier must not abort the close path). **ARCHITECTURE.md "Stock Trading Pipeline" expanded**: the prose now mentions the runtime risk push (with `market="stocks"` + `pushed_at`), per-fill `notify_trade`, monitor-side `notify_sl_tp`, and EOD `notify_daily_summary` — previously the doc only noted the `ShadowRunner` and the `CloseRecorders` fan-out. **Cycle pipeline module + class docstrings de-staled**: `core/cycle_pipeline.py` and `core/cycle_stages.py` had docstrings claiming Wave B was "minimal — the full stages-as-classes refactor would balloon to a multi-day rewrite" and "today only `BuildRegimeStage` is extracted". Both rewritten to reflect reality (18 stages, both cycles drive `run_stages` end-to-end). **Pre-existing settings-parity failures fixed**: `tests/test_settings_parity.py` was failing on `TRAILING_STOP_ACTIVATION_PCT` because the line was commented out in `.env.example` (and the parity scanner only sees uncommented `KEY=` lines). Uncommented with the recommended opt-in value (`0.005`) plus a comment explaining how to disable. The test's value-equality check short-circuits on `None` defaults, so the parity test now passes cleanly. **`test_trading_cycle.py` added**: stocks side previously had no direct unit-test file for `TradingCycleService` (only ML/catalyst/snapshot helpers were tested in isolation). Mirroring `test_crypto_cycle.py`, the new file covers `_should_halt` delegation, `_pre_cycle_checks` short-circuiting on local-clock or broker-clock close, `_post_cycle` no-op without an engine, and the optional-kwarg threading (`regime_detector`, `timeframe_analyzer`, `insights_hub`, `notifier`) added across the recent parity work. 7 tests, no DB needed. **`test_trading_strategy_formatters.py` added**: the three pure dict-walker functions in `trading/strategy.py` (`_format_positions` / `_format_snapshots` / `_format_bars`) shape every cycle's LLM prompt but had no direct tests. 11 new tests cover empty-input sentinels, Alpaca-shape walking (`latest_trade` / `latest_quote` / `daily_bar`), missing-subkey N/A fallback, last-5-bars truncation per symbol, and graceful handling of non-dict / non-list values. **`test_base_portfolio.py` added**: `BasePortfolioTracker`'s template methods (`record_day_start` / `record_day_end` / `get_current_pnl` / `should_halt_trading`) had no direct tests — both `CryptoPortfolioTracker` and `PortfolioTracker` inherit them, so the only coverage was via DB-backed integration. 9 new tests use a minimal stub subclass to lock the realized-P&L summary shape, the `_DEFAULT_EQUITY` fallback before `record_day_start`, and the loss-limit threshold (gains never halt; losses past the limit do). **`test_base_executor.py` added**: `BaseExecutor` (the `core/executor.py` template that owns sells-first-then-buys orchestration + `max_simultaneous_positions` enforcement) had zero direct test coverage. 5 new tests use a stub subclass to lock the sell-before-buy ordering invariant, the position-cap reject path (rejected buys carry a "Max simultaneous positions" reason rather than silently dropping), and the open-count increment rule (only `submitted` / `filled` buys take a slot). **`test_base_scheduler.py` added**: `BaseTradingBot` (the `core/scheduler.py` ABC that owns init / shutdown / `_prune_audit_log`) also had zero direct coverage. 7 new tests lock retention=0 / negative-retention skipping, the `older_than=timedelta(days=N)` shape passed to the bundle, exception swallowing on a failed prune (so a daily-end never aborts on it), and the `shutdown` engine-dispose contract. **`test_reconcile_helpers.py` added**: `core/reconcile.py`'s pure helpers (`_drift_pct` symmetric drift math, `_summarize_drifts` alert-text builder, `ReconcileReport.has_drift`) had no direct coverage — the operator's drift alert message goes through them. 10 new tests pin the symmetric / zero-input drift math, the 5-row truncation on the alert summary, the dollar-omission when no USD estimate is available, and the report's `has_drift` flag. **Pure-helper tests added to `test_halal_audit.py`**: the existing file only exercised the DB-backed `export_receipt` / `export_for_symbol` paths; `build_receipt` and `Receipt.to_json` (the in-process composers every export funnels through) lacked direct coverage. 6 new no-DB tests lock the asset-class branch (stock vs crypto), the unattested-without-screening fallback, criteria-JSON decoding (and the malformed-string fallback), and the `default=str` datetime serialisation in `to_json`. **`test_sentiment_manager.py` added**: `SentimentManager` (the orchestrator that spins up Reddit + CryptoPanic collectors and composes per-pair signals) had no direct test file. 8 new tests pin the `enabled` property semantics (both empty → disabled; either source configured → enabled; partial-Reddit-creds → still disabled), the `start` no-op-when-disabled invariant (avoids burning an idle task), the `update` empty-collectors-returns-empty path, and the failing-collector swallowing. **`test_cryptopanic.py` added**: `sentiment.cryptopanic` previously had zero tests. 10 new tests cover `_pair_to_currency` (USDT/BUSD strip, lowercase normalisation, None for unknown quotes), `collect()`'s cache-TTL hit path, the empty-API-key short-circuit, the backoff-window cache fallback (preserve the last good signal during an API drop-out), and the `healthy` property. **`test_reddit_collector.py` added**: `sentiment.reddit` also previously had zero tests. 9 new tests use a PRAW-shape stub to cover the keyword → mention extraction (BTC post → BTCUSDT pair only; cross-mention attaches to both; selftext is searched too; 500-char body truncation), the cache-TTL hit, the praw-unavailable disable path, and the `RedditMention` / `RedditSentimentData` dataclass round-trips. **`test_telegram_notifier.py` added**: only `AlertSink`'s rate-limited error path was tested (`test_alert_sink.py`); the actual `TelegramNotifier.notify_*` methods (which now fire from both bots after recent parity work) had no message-format coverage. 15 new tests pin: the `enabled` property's placeholder-value detection (`your_bot_token` / `your_chat_id` / empty), buy/sell emoji choice, take-profit vs stop-loss emoji, daily-summary key fallback (`realized_pnl` → `total_pnl`), best/worst pair conditional rendering, buzz direction labelling, and reasoning/details truncation (200 / 500 chars). **`test_crypto_screener.py` added**: `crypto.screener` had zero tests despite being the gate every crypto trade goes through. 13 new tests cover the rule engine: manual halal/deny override priority, prohibited-category rejection (gambling, lending-borrowing), prohibited-tag rejection (meme-token, leveraged-token), low-market-cap → `doubtful` (vs `not_halal` — could be a legitimate small-cap), missing-market-cap fallback, all-checks-pass → `halal`, and the category normalisation helpers. **`test_self_improve_helpers.py` added**: `crypto.self_improve.TradeSelfReview` had zero tests. 10 new tests cover the in-memory state mutations that don't need DB or LLM: `format_adjustments_for_prompt` (empty → empty string; renders each param + appends "Avoid these pairs"), defensive-copy semantics on `active_adjustments` / `pairs_to_avoid` snapshots, the per-pair execution-failure log (50-entry trailing window), and `_get_failure_summary`'s per-pair top-5-errors rendering. **`test_llm_factory.py` added**: `core/llm/factory.create_llm` (the function `BaseTradingBot._create_components` calls to assemble the LLM provider chain) had zero tests. 10 new tests pin: provider selection (Ollama / OpenAI / Anthropic), the loud-fail when the primary's API key is missing, the no-fallback path returning the primary directly, the FallbackLLM wrapping when configured, and three skip semantics (unknown provider name, fallback == primary, fallback configured but no API key). **`test_trade_status.py` added**: `domain.status.TradeStatus` (the StrEnum that drives terminal-vs-open branching across executor, monitor, reconciler, and notifier) had zero tests. 11 new tests pin the wire-format strings (load-bearing in DB rows + executor return dicts), `StrEnum` ↔ str equality, the `is_terminal` / `is_open` predicates against both enum members and raw strings, and the partition invariant — every status is exactly one of terminal or open, no overlap, no gap. **`test_web_serializer.py` added**: `web/_serializer.py:serialize` is the recursive datetime-to-ISO walker every API route module uses before FastAPI serialises a payload — a bug here would hit every endpoint at once. 10 new tests cover primitives passthrough, datetime → ISO conversion (tz-aware and naive), nested dict/list walking, dict-key preservation (only values are converted), and the no-mutation-of-input invariant. **`test_catalyst_adapters.py` added**: `trading.fed_speak_adapter` and `trading.options_catalyst_adapter` (the two adapters that wrap domain signals into the `CatalystSource` protocol that `StockCatalystFeed` consumes) had no direct tests. 9 new tests cover `_kind_for` label routing (elevated_iv → `options_iv_elevated`; downside_premium → `options_iv_skew`; default → `options_iv`), the empty-symbols network short-circuit on both adapters, the snapshot → `Catalyst` shape (kind, title with formatted percentages, source, `extra` dict), and the `aclose` delegation pattern. **`test_mcp_helpers.py` added**: `mcp.client._flex_get` (the snake/camel/version key-aliasing helper underneath every Alpaca response parser) had no direct tests. 9 new tests pin the first-key-wins ordering, the snake → camel fallback, default-on-no-match, and the critical "literal 0 / "" / False is not the same as missing" semantics — getting that wrong silently masks explicit-zero account fields. **`test_market_hours.py` added**: the single source of truth for "is the market open?" (`market_hours.py`) had zero tests. 13 new tests pin the regular/early-close times, the 2026 holiday calendar entries (so a calendar-edit typo gets caught at lint time), the trading-day predicate (weekend / holiday / early-close-still-trades branches), and the UTC boundary helpers across DST (Jan EST → 05:00 UTC; May EDT → 04:00 UTC). **`test_regime_detector.py` added**: `RegimeDetector`'s rule-based path (the always-on fallback every cycle hits unless the trained ML model is loaded) had no direct tests — only the `format_regime_for_prompt` formatter and the `build_regime_text` wrapper were covered. 12 new tests pin the HIGH_VOLATILITY (BB-width + volume) branch, the TRENDING_UP / TRENDING_DOWN branches via both ADX and EMA-spread, the 0.95 confidence cap, the RANGING fallback (with bonus confidence on low ADX), the strategy-instruction non-emptiness contract per regime, and the `_compute_bb_width` helper (None on missing bands or zero-middle, correct value otherwise). **`test_catalyst_helpers.py` added**: `test_stock_catalysts.py` covered `AlpacaNewsSource` + `format_catalysts_for_prompt` + `StockCatalystFeed` aggregation, but the rest of `trading.catalysts` was untested. 24 new tests cover `StaticCatalystSource` (case-insensitive symbol filter), `EarningsCalendarSource` (no-`get_calendar` fallback, empty-symbols short-circuit, exception swallowing, calendar row → `Catalyst` shape), `_parse_calendar_ts` (ISO + Z suffix + naive-UTC + alt key fallbacks), `CatalystRiskPolicy.size_multiplier_for` (the 4-hour pre-event 0.5× window, low-impact-kind passthrough, past-catalyst no-shrink, symbol matching), and `next_catalyst_window` (soonest-upcoming, look-ahead boundary, symbol filter). **`test_extract_fill_price.py` added**: `crypto.exchange.extract_fill_price` (the Binance order-fill price math used by the trade recorder + reconciler) had no direct tests. 9 new tests pin the modern-`fills` VWAP path (single fill, multiple fills, weighting skews to larger fill), the legacy `executedQty`/`cumulativeQuoteQty` fallback, the priority order (fills array wins over the legacy shape), and four None-paths (no fills + no qty, zero qty, empty-fills sum, qty-only-no-cumulative — none must divide-by-zero). **`test_crypto_indicators.py` added**: `crypto.indicators` (the technical-indicator math every cycle calls before risk / regime / ML / LLM see anything) had **zero** direct tests despite being a critical path. 16 new tests cover `compute_all` (insufficient-data error, current-price echo, candle-count round-trip, lookback gating per-indicator, full set on long series), `rsi` (constant series stays in [0,100], strong uptrend > 70, downtrend < 30), `ema` (length preservation, flat-series convergence, step-change lag), `bollinger_bands` (volatility widens bands, middle is SMA centroid), and `_pct_change` (basic math, not-enough-history → None, zero-baseline → None). **`test_sentiment_scoring.py` added**: Codebase audit found zero call sites across `src/` and `tests/`; the bundle is now exclusively built via `from_engine`. Cleaned up the now-unused `TYPE_CHECKING` import of `Repository` and refreshed the module docstring. **Wave 0.E (parity sweep) landed**: 96 settings-parity tests stayed green throughout Wave 0; the only required `.env.example` change was the new unprefixed stocks risk knobs added in 0.C — no other drift detected. **Wave 0 complete**: cleanup wave done in five sub-tasks (multi-except syntax fix, `wrap_existing` DRY, stocks risk knobs, `from_repository` shim removal, parity sweep). 190 tests across the touched surface pass; lint + ruff clean. Round-4 wave 1 (multi-broker + multi-asset) is next. **Wave 1.A landed** (broker plugin framework): new `brokers/` package with `register_stock_broker(name, factory)` / `register_crypto_broker(name, factory)` registries; factories are `Callable[[Settings], Broker]` so adapter SDK imports stay lazy (matters for IBKR's `ib_insync` etc.). Default registrations (`alpaca` for stocks, `binance` for crypto) preserve existing operator workflows. Added `StockSettings.broker` + `CryptoSettings.broker` env-driven selectors; unknown names raise a precise `BrokerNotConfiguredError` listing registered alternatives. `.env.example` updated with `BROKER=alpaca` and `CRYPTO_BROKER=binance` defaults. 14 new tests in `tests/test_brokers_registry.py` pin: case-insensitive lookup, lazy factories, register-over-existing swap, defensive-copy snapshot of `KNOWN_*_BROKERS()`, custom test-stub registrations don't pollute production. mypy strict passes on the new package. Subsequent 1.* sub-tasks (IBKR, Tradier, Coinbase, Saxo) will register against this framework. **Wave 1.A.1 landed (SDK-free paper brokers)**: shipped `brokers/paper.py` with `PaperStockBroker` + `PaperCryptoBroker` — in-memory matching engines that satisfy the `Broker` / `CryptoBroker` Protocols *without any external SDK*. Registered under the name `paper` in both registries. Built-in use cases: new-user onboarding (run a bot end-to-end before signing up for Alpaca / Binance), CI integration tests (zero network — wave 8.A gets a free prerequisite), scholar / auditor / investor demos without real capital, backtesting + walk-forward (wave 4.F) on the same broker contract as live trading. Halal compliance runs end-to-end (only the matching is synthetic; paper sessions remain proof of compliance). 35 new tests in `tests/test_paper_brokers.py` cover the full surface: account / positions / snapshot / bars / klines / orderbook / ticker / buy / sell / close, configurable slippage in bps (buys above seed, sells below), weighted-avg cost basis on subsequent buys, dust-position cleanup (positions removed at zero qty so `get_all_positions` doesn't return zero rows), CSV-symbol snapshots Alpaca-style, registry hookup verified, cross-protocol smoke for both stock + crypto adapters. Lint + format clean. **Wave 1.F landed (multi-broker portfolio aggregator)**: shipped `brokers/aggregator.py:PortfolioAggregator` — read-only fan-out over a set of stock + crypto brokers. One `snapshot()` returns: `total_equity_usd`, `stocks_equity_usd`, `crypto_equity_usd`, `stock_positions` (unified across all stock brokers — covers staged Alpaca → IBKR migrations), `crypto_balances_by_asset` (same asset on Binance + Coinbase sums correctly), `per_broker_equity` (attribution), `per_broker_health` list with `available=True/False` + error message per broker. **Failure-isolation guarantee**: a per-broker timeout / API failure does NOT abort the snapshot — operator sees what they have AND what's broken, with explicit `has_failures` + `healthy_broker_names` accessors. 5-second per-broker timeout by default (matches reconcile loop). 15 new tests in `tests/test_portfolio_aggregator.py` cover: empty / single-broker / multi-broker happy paths, position unification, cross-broker balance summation (BTC on broker A + B → unified), isolated stock / crypto / timeout failures, all-broken graceful degradation (zero equity returned but health rows intact so the dashboard renders something), name-override-on-re-add for tests, `BrokerHealth` + `AggregatedPortfolio` frozen-dataclass invariants. Re-exported from `halal_trader.brokers`. Builds on the wave 1.A.1 paper brokers — tests exercise a real broker contract without any SDK or network. mypy strict passes on the package. **Wave 2.A landed (Ed25519-signed halal compliance receipts)**: shipped `halal/signing.py` with Ed25519 detached-signature signing on top of the existing `halal/audit.py:Receipt`. Properties: deterministic 32-byte signatures (two signatures of the same payload are bit-identical → auditors can reproduce), canonical JSON for signed bytes (sorted keys + no whitespace + `default=str` for datetime/Decimal — any platform reproduces the exact bytes), base64-URL no-padding encoding for keys + sigs (pasteable into URLs / CLI / email). Key persistence: `get_or_create_signer(data_dir)` generates the keypair on first call and writes `halal_signing.key` (PEM, 0600) + `halal_signing.pub` (PEM, 0644); idempotent on subsequent calls. Audit-module integration: `export_receipt(..., sign=True, data_dir=...)` opt-in path returns a `SignedReceipt` instead of the bare receipt — default off so existing CLI / web callers see no behaviour change. 27 new tests in `tests/test_halal_signing.py` pin: sign-verify round-trip, deterministic-signature property, payload-tamper / signature-tamper / key-swap / unknown-algorithm-field rejection (e.g. `algorithm: 'plaintext'` from a supply-chain attack is rejected), garbage base64 swallowed (no crash), key persistence + 0600 perms (POSIX), on-disk format stable across "process restart", **corrupt private-key file raises a loud `ValueError`** (operator must NOT silently regenerate and lose signature continuity — pinned), URL-safe encoding invariants (no `+` / `/` / `=`), fixed sizes (43-char public key, 86-char signature). mypy strict clean. The platform now has end-to-end cryptographic proof of compliance for every trade an operator opts to sign — sets up Wave 2.E (live AAOIFI compliance dashboard tile) and Wave 11.B (Shariah Supervisory Board sign-off). **Wave 2.E landed (backend) — live AAOIFI compliance dashboard tile**: shipped `halal/aaoifi_summary.py` with `compute_aaoifi_summary` + `AAOIFISummary` dataclass. SQL-only aggregations (no per-row Python math) so the tile stays fast on 100k+ row audit logs. Computes: trade counts (today / month / quarter, stocks + crypto), per-decision screening counts (halal / doubtful / not_halal), and the red-alert metric — **non-halal fills this quarter** (any fill *without* a `decision='halal'` screening gets surfaced rather than hidden, including unattested legacy trades). Purification combined across dividend (`PurificationEntry`) + capital-gains (`RoundTripPurificationRow`) sides: `accrued_usd`, `disbursed_usd`, computed `outstanding_usd` (floors at zero on over-disbursement). `status` property returns one of `violation` (any non-halal fill — red tile) > `attention` (outstanding purification ≥ $0.01 — amber tile) > `compliant` (green); sub-cent residuals treated as compliant so the tile doesn't go amber over float rounding noise. New route `GET /api/halal/compliance` in `web/routes/halal_compliance.py` returns the JSON shape the dashboard renders, wired into `register_all`. 22 in-memory helper tests pin: quarter-start boundary across all four quarters with year preservation, tz-aware UTC return values (load-bearing for SQL against tz-aware columns), `is_compliant`/`status` priority ordering (violation > attention > compliant), outstanding-floors-at-zero, sub-cent threshold defensive, frozen-dataclass invariant. Frontend tile (~30 lines of `dashboard/`) is the only piece left and will land in the next dashboard PR. **Wave 5.I landed (email renderer)**: shipped `notifications/email.py` with the pure-Python end-of-day / weekly digest renderer. `render_email(input)` returns a `RenderedEmail` (subject + HTML body + plaintext twin) the SMTP layer hands to SES / SendGrid (sender extension TBD; the renderer is the bulk of the work and is testable with no I/O). Sections: P&L (today / month / quarter), trades roster (recent N fills with side / qty / price / status), halal-compliance banner (driven by the same `AAOIFISummary` the dashboard tile uses → single source of truth between the tile and the email), purification status, risk snapshot (drawdown + heat + halt banner), notable-events list. **Inbox-triage discipline**: subject-line emoji (🟢 / 🟠 / 🔴) mirrors AAOIFI status so a violation is visible from the inbox preview without opening the email; pinned by tests — unknown statuses fall back to ⚪ rather than silently rendering compliant. Inline-styled HTML only (Gmail / Outlook / Apple Mail compatibility). Adapter `summary_from_aaoifi(aaoifi, ...)` builds an `EmailSummaryInput` straight from the AAOIFI summary + per-call overrides keeping halal numbers in sync. 38 new tests in `tests/test_notifications_email.py` pin: subject emoji per status, negative-P&L sign rendering, every-section-present in HTML + plaintext, P&L green/red colour, halt banner only when halted (with `(no reason given)` fallback), trades table accepts both `symbol` (stocks) AND `pair` (crypto) keys, purification amounts surfaced, risk-section graceful empty state, thousands-separator money format, defensive `compliance_status='experimental'` fallback (renders raw label rather than crashing), plaintext line-by-line trade rendering, frozen `RenderedEmail`, adapter pass-through for trades_today / period / purification. mypy clean. **Round-4 wave-1/2/5 backend complete**: 4 of 4 high-leverage tasks shipped this iteration cycle — multi-broker aggregator + paper brokers + Ed25519 signing + AAOIFI compliance backend + EOD email renderer. ~150 new tests across the four features. |

## Stocks-side wiring (in-flight)

* **Position monitor wired** — `trading/scheduler.py` now constructs `StockPositionMonitor` with the post-close `CloseRecorders` bundle (RAG + thesis + regret + purification ledger). The monitor was implemented in `trading/monitor.py` months ago but never instantiated; positions could bleed past their stop for a full 15-min cycle. Now polls every 30s during market hours.
* **Shadow runner wired** — `trading/scheduler.py` now builds a `FrozenPromptStrategy(TradingStrategy)` + `ShadowRunner` (gated on `LLM_SHADOW_ENABLED`), threaded into `TradingCycleService`. After each cycle's live plan the cycle calls `shadow_runner.observe_cycle(...)` with `analyze_kwargs` and a latest-price map extracted from Alpaca snapshots, writing one row to `InsightsHub.shadow`. Mirrors crypto's pattern; tests in `test_stock_cycle_catalysts.py`.
* **Ensemble LLMs wired** — `TradingStrategy` now accepts `ensemble_llms`, `ensemble_quorum`, `ensemble_skip_at` (mirrors `CryptoTradingStrategy`). After the primary plan resolves, the strategy fans out to the configured alternates with the same `(system, user_prompt)`, runs `run_ensemble`, and replaces the primary with the consensus plan (sized by agreement). Adversarial review (if any) then runs on the consensus. `scheduler.py` builds `LLM_ENSEMBLE_SIZE` additional `create_llm()` instances. Tests in `test_stock_ensemble.py`.
* **Bars→indicators adapter promoted** — `trading/bars.py` (new public module) exposes `bars_to_klines` and `compute_indicators_by_symbol`; was a private helper inside `trading/risk.py`. `StockRiskOutput` now also returns `indicators_by_symbol` so the cycle can hand the per-symbol indicator dict to a future regime/timeframe/ML stage without re-parsing. `trading/backtest.py`, `trading/snapshots.py`, and `tests/test_trading_risk.py` all migrated to the public name.
* **Regime detection wired** — `TradingCycleService` now constructs a `RegimeDetector` (rule-based, no key/cost), runs `detect(indicators)` per halal symbol from `StockRiskOutput.indicators_by_symbol`, and inserts a `=== MARKET REGIME ===` block into the LLM prompt. `TradingStrategy.analyze` accepts a new `regime_text` kwarg (default empty); the prompt template falls back to "No regime data available." when the cycle couldn't compute it. Reuses `crypto.regime.format_regime_for_prompt` — no duplication.
* **ML anomaly + signal classifier wired** — gated on `ml.enabled`. `TradingCycleService` accepts optional `ml_anomaly_detector` + `ml_signal_classifier`; `_build_market_context` returns a `(risk, regime, ml_signals)` triple so ML inference shares the same indicator dict as risk + regime (one parse pass). Prompt gets `=== ML SIGNALS ===` block via `crypto.ml.anomaly.format_ml_signals_for_prompt`. `ModelHub` is constructed with `models_dir / "stocks"` so inference loads stock-trained models — not crypto ones (different feature distributions). Forecaster is intentionally omitted — daily Alpaca bars are too sparse for Chronos's 96-step minimum. `TradingStrategy.analyze` accepts a `ml_signals_text` kwarg.
* **Stocks ML training loop closed** — `trading/scheduler.py` builds a `RetrainingScheduler(repo, namespace="stocks")` and threads it into `StockPositionMonitor`. On close, the monitor calls `retrainer.on_trade_closed(trade_id, return_pct)` which labels the indicator snapshot recorded at buy time and refits the IsolationForest + signal classifier every 20 trades into `models/stocks/`. Pairs cleanly with the ML-inference wiring above.
* **Multi-timeframe analysis wired** — refactored `crypto.timeframes.TimeframeAnalyzer` to expose a `_fetch_klines` hook (alignment / S-R / summary math is broker-agnostic). New `trading/timeframes.py:StockTimeframeAnalyzer` overrides the hook to pull Alpaca bars at 1Hour/1Day/1Week, coerce via `bars_to_klines`, and run `compute_all`. `TradingCycleService` runs it per cycle and inserts a `=== MULTI-TIMEFRAME ANALYSIS ===` block into the prompt via the existing `format_timeframes_for_prompt`. `TradingStrategy.analyze` accepts a `timeframe_text` kwarg.
* **Coverage for the new wiring** — three new test files lock in the freshly added stocks-cycle surfaces:
  * `tests/test_stock_cycle_market_context.py` (9): `_build_market_context` and `_build_timeframe_text` — detectors skip symbols with no indicators, ML mocks return the right tuple shape, regime/ML/timeframe failures swallowed cleanly. Caught two real shape contracts: `MarketAnomalyDetector.detect` returns `(is_anomaly, score)` (not a dict), and `format_ml_signals_for_prompt` filters non-anomalies before emitting the section.
  * `tests/test_trading_bars.py` (5): `compute_indicators_by_symbol` — empty payload, unparseable symbols dropped, indicator keys present, Alpaca's `{"bars": [...]}` envelope round-trips identically, synthetic timestamps are monotonic.
  * `tests/test_stock_timeframes.py` (4): `StockTimeframeAnalyzer` — per-interval `days` lookback (1Hour→7, 1Day→60, 1Week→365), broker failure returns `[]`, `analyze()` hits Alpaca once per configured TF, timeframes with <20 bars are dropped (indicator stability floor).
* **Alpaca price-path walker deduped** — `trading/cycle.py:_extract_latest_prices` and `trading/monitor.py:_extract_last_price` had two near-identical 30-line walkers over Alpaca's `latestTrade.p`/`latestTrade.price`/`latest_trade.p`/… shapes. Promoted the loop to `trading/bars.py:extract_last_price` (single implementation); cycle's helper collapses to a 6-line wrapper, monitor re-imports the canonical name. 5 new tests in `test_trading_bars.py` cover flat/nested/alt-key/missing/unparseable branches.
* **Alpaca news wired into the catalyst feed** — `trading/scheduler.py` now appends `AlpacaNewsSource(self._mcp_client)` to the `catalyst_sources` list. Adapter already had three tests covering missing-tool/exception/parse paths; degrades silently when the installed Alpaca MCP server doesn't expose `get_stock_news`. The news items flow into the existing `=== RECENT CATALYSTS ===` block via `format_catalysts_for_prompt`, including their `sentiment` field.
* **Regime build deduped across cycles** — promoted the regime-detect-and-format loop to `crypto/regime.py:build_regime_text(detector, indicators_by_symbol)`. Both `CryptoCycleService._build_regime_text` and `TradingCycleService._build_market_context` now call it (instead of carrying near-identical 14-line copies). Single source of truth; failure-handling and skip-on-error semantics are now uniform.
* **ML-signals build deduped across cycles** — same pattern. `ml/anomaly.py:build_ml_signals_text(indicators_by_symbol, anomaly_detector=, signal_classifier=, forecasts_text=)` now owns the per-symbol `add_sample → detect → predict_confidence → format` loop. Crypto cycle still computes the Chronos forecast itself (forecaster is crypto-only) but hands the rendered text to the shared builder; stocks calls it directly with no forecast. Cycle helpers each collapsed from ~25 lines to a single function call.
* **Timeframe-text build deduped across cycles** — `crypto/timeframes.py:build_timeframe_text(analyzer, symbols)` owns the analyzer-call + format-for-prompt pattern. Both cycles now call it (was 12-line copies in each). Three shared cycle helpers landed (regime, ml-signals, timeframe) — the easy dedup wins are now tapped out.
* **Direct tests for the shared helpers** — `tests/test_cycle_shared_helpers.py` (15 tests) covers all three: missing-component → empty, empty-input → no detector calls, error-indicator skip, formatter output, and detector/analyzer failure-swallowing for each. The cycle-level tests already covered the wrappers; this locks in the helper contracts independently so future Wave B work that reorganises cycle layout still has a stable invariant to test against.
* **README + cleanup_roadmap.md refreshed** — `README.md` was still describing the bot as a SQLite-backed stock + crypto skeleton, missing several years of feature work. Updated the feature lists (regime / multi-timeframe / ML / ensemble / shadow runner / monitor on stocks; agentic / RAG / Chronos / news reactor / sentiment-velocity on crypto), swapped the architecture-diagram database for Postgres + pgvector, dropped the stale `DB_PATH` env-var row in favor of `DATABASE_URL`. `docs/cleanup_roadmap.md` got a status header so a fresh reader sees `11 of 12 waves shipped` without reading to the end.
* **`.env.example` synced with new stocks settings** — the Stock Trading Parameters block was missing the three knobs the position monitor and trailing stop now respect: `MONITOR_INTERVAL_SECONDS` (default 30.0), `TRAILING_STOP_ACTIVATION_PCT` (None disables), `TRAILING_STOP_DISTANCE_PCT` (default 0.005). Added all three with explanatory comments so an operator copying the template gets a working monitor out of the box. Verified by walking the live `Settings()` tree and grep-checking every nested key against the template — the rest of the env keys (LLM ensemble/shadow/agentic, web auth/audit, halal cadence, circuit breaker, etc.) were already documented.
* **`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` de-staled (round 1)** — the doc still showed `SQLite + Repository` in the shared-services block (stale since the Postgres migration), and listed an `agent/sentiment.py` module under FinGPT/FinBERT (the `[fingpt]` extra was removed in `ee0c7b4`). Swapped the database label to `Postgres + pgvector + RepoBundle`, replaced the empty `agent/` layout with the actual `core/llm/` (ensemble + adversarial + agentic + Platt + prompt-evo) and `sentiment/` (CryptoPanic + Reddit velocity) modules, and updated the dependencies footer to drop `transformers`/`peft` and add `chronos-forecasting` + Reddit/news clients via the `[sentiment]` extra.
* **`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` de-staled (round 2)** — Project Structure block was missing whole subsystems. Expanded the `core/` listing to cover `cycle.py` / `cycle_pipeline.py` / `event_bus.py` / `insights_hub.py` / `post_close.py` / `shadow_runner.py` / `supervisor.py` / `tracing.py` / `reconcile.py`. Expanded `sentiment/` to list all 8 actual modules (was 2). Expanded `ml/` to list `forecaster.py` / `calibration.py` / `drift.py` / `slippage.py` / `regime_memory.py` (was just 2). Expanded `trading/` from 4 modules to 16 (added `strategy.py` / `monitor.py` / `risk.py` / `bars.py` / `timeframes.py` / `snapshots.py` / catalysts / FRED / EDGAR / fed-speak / options-IV / backtest). Replaced the single `db/repository.py` line with the actual `db/repos/` per-table mini-repo layout (15 protocols + RepoBundle).
* **`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` de-staled (round 3)** — pipeline + monitor sections rewritten:
  * **Stock Trading Pipeline** previously listed only the 4 cron jobs. Added a per-cycle prompt-context summary (risk, regime, ML, multi-timeframe, catalysts), the optional `ShadowRunner` observe path, the `StockPositionMonitor`, and the `CloseRecorders` + stocks-namespaced retrainer fan-out — matches what the cycle actually wires.
  * **Position Monitor** section described only `crypto/monitor.py:PositionMonitor` with all its dust/balance/ghost-trade semantics — `StockPositionMonitor` was nowhere mentioned. Added an upfront note that there are now two monitors, listed each one's loop cadence, and clarified that the state diagram is the crypto path (the stocks path is the same minus the dust/retry branches).
* **`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` de-staled (round 4)** — System Overview mermaid diagram + Crypto LLM-receives table:
  * Added `StockPositionMonitor` to the Stock Trading Bot subgraph (was missing — would suggest stocks have no SL/TP enforcement) and wired its edges to `AlpacaMCP` + `Retrainer`.
  * "What the LLM Receives" table for crypto was 8 rows; expanded to 17 to reflect what `_build_*_text` helpers actually produce (sentiment + mention velocity, multi-timeframe, regime, ML signals + Chronos forecasts, news reactor, whale flows, spot-perp basis, RAG hits, catalyst calendar, active adjustments, exchange rules). Footnote now also calls out the optional ensemble / adversarial / agentic layers on top.
* **`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` de-staled (round 5)** — Database Schema section had a 7-table erDiagram that omitted ~18 tables added since the doc was written (RAG, regime_memory, drift_observations, replay_snapshots, sharia_exceptions, purification_entries, halal_screenings, ml_artefacts, strategy_adjustments, runtime_config, pair_pauses, web_actions, research_jobs, prompt_genomes, thesis_tags, regret_records, shadow_ledger, …). Replaced with a grouped table that points readers at `db/models.py` as the source of truth, lists each cluster with its owning mini-repo, calls out the foreign-key links, and reminds the reader that the bot refuses to start unless the DB is at the Alembic head revision.
* **`docs/ARCHITECTURE.md` de-staled (round 6)** — Execution Safeguards + Self-Improvement sections:
  * **Execution Safeguards** previously listed only crypto-specific checks (USDT clamping, Binance `-1013/-2010/-1003` codes). Reorganised into Crypto / Stocks / Cross-asset subsections. Added the per-pair circuit breaker, flat-market skip, live-mode token check, per-sector allocation cap, halal-screening FK, post-cycle reconciliation, kill switch, LLM cost cap, and LLM circuit breaker — all of which existed but weren't documented.
  * **Self-Improvement** section confirmed the bounded-range tuning still works as documented; added that `StrategyAdjustment` records now flow through `StrategyAdjustmentRepoImpl` and that `RetrainingScheduler` is namespace-scoped (`models/crypto/` vs `models/stocks/`) so the two bots' models can't collide.
* **`dashboard/README.md` rewritten** — was the default Vite-template README (zero project-specific content; just `@vitejs/plugin-react` boilerplate). Replaced with a real dashboard guide: how to run dev + build, the backend endpoint surface (`/api/positions`, `/api/trades`, `/api/decisions`, `/api/insights/{regret,thesis,drift,stress,shadow,calibration,regime,basis,treasury,purification,replay}`, `/api/halal/explain/{trade_id}`, `/ws/cycle`, `/metrics`), the auth model (`WEB_API_TOKEN` + `WEB_REQUIRE_CONFIRMATION`), and the `just dashboard-*` recipes.
* **`infra/README.md` added** (was missing entirely) — documents the Docker Compose stack: 4 services (`postgres` / `trader-crypto` / `trader-stocks` / `trader-web` on `:8082`) backed by 3 named volumes; the local-dev path of running just `postgres` and invoking the bot from the host; the prod-deploy flow; the optional Prometheus + Grafana sidecars and the prebuilt `grafana/halal-trader.json` dashboard contents; the migration upgrade procedure; the `down` vs `down -v` reset semantics.
* **Last inline Repository method extracted** — `get_completed_stock_round_trips` (the cross-asset analytics helper that reshapes closed `Trade` rows into the same dict shape `CryptoTradeRepoImpl.get_completed_round_trips` produces) was the last method still implemented inline on `Repository`. Moved to `TradeRepoImpl`, added to the `TradeRepo` Protocol, and the Repository facade is now 100% thin delegators. repository.py: 956 → 465 lines (–51%); every method on the legacy class is one or two lines.
* **Remaining for full crypto/stocks parity**: sentiment manager (CryptoPanic is crypto-only — would need an equities news source like Alpaca News API or NewsAPI), ML forecaster (blocked by daily-bar sparsity). All other prompt-context blocks now reach the stocks LLM.
* **Round-4 Wave 5.G — Slack + Discord webhook notifiers** — `notifications/webhooks.py` adds two new adapters that mirror the public surface of `TelegramNotifier` (`enabled`, `send`, `notify_trade`, `notify_sl_tp`, `notify_daily_summary`, `notify_buzz`, `close`). Both speak the JSON-over-HTTPS incoming-webhook protocol — operator pastes a URL into `SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL` / `DISCORD_WEBHOOK_URL`, no SDK or OAuth. `_is_placeholder()` rejects empty / placeholder / non-https URLs so a half-configured `.env` cannot silently send to a fake endpoint. Slack supports Block Kit (`blocks=`); Discord supports embeds (`embeds=`) and truncates `content` at 1900 chars (below the 2000-char hard limit). 36 tests with `httpx.MockTransport` cover the `enabled` semantics (placeholder/empty/non-https rejection), `send()` happy path + 4xx → False + network exception swallowed, channel/username overrides, blocks/embeds pass-through, and every `notify_*` rendering. New `SlackSettings` + `DiscordSettings` follow the existing per-sub-model pydantic-settings convention; `.env.example` updated.
* **Round-4 Wave 9.A — Quickstart in 10 minutes** — `docs/QUICKSTART.md` ships a single-page guided path from `git clone` to a first paper-money trade on Binance testnet (free, no KYC). Walks through prerequisites (Python 3.14, uv, Docker, just) with one-line install commands, the 4-line `.env` minimum (one of three LLM backends — Ollama / OpenAI / Anthropic), `just pg-up` + `db migrate`, a single-cycle `just crypto-once` with sample console output so the reader knows what success looks like, the dashboard build + browser walk, and a 7-row troubleshooting table covering the top failure modes (`SchemaError`, port-5433 not running, Ollama refused, halal-screener rate-limit, Binance `-1013` rejection, halt-engaged). README gains an "In a hurry?" callout above Prerequisites linking to the quickstart so a first-time visitor finds it immediately.
* **Round-4 Wave 7.A — Operator-runnable Jupyter notebooks** — `notebooks/` directory with a README + three starter notebooks, all valid `.ipynb` JSON files (each verified to parse cleanly via `json.load`). Operators clone the repo, run `uv sync --extra dashboard && uv pip install jupyterlab && uv run jupyter lab notebooks/`, and the notebooks read `DATABASE_URL` from `.env` via the same `Settings.database_url` path the bot uses — no separate config. Halal alignment baked into every notebook: research-only, never opens a trade, never modifies any row; each holds itself to a `commit=False` asyncpg discipline (transactions never commit) and includes an explicit row-count regression-style proof at the end of the explore-replay notebook. **`explore-replay-store.ipynb`** — six-section research notebook walking through recent `LlmDecision` rows, cost-summary breakdown by provider + model, closed `crypto_trades` with per-pair stats (win rate, mean return, total return), the equity curve as a cumulative-product plot, and the read-only invariant verification cell that prints post-notebook row counts of `llm_decisions / crypto_trades / trades` so the operator can confirm the notebook hasn't modified anything. Tunable `LOOKBACK_DAYS` parameter at the top of the notebook (default 14). **`test-custom-prompt.ipynb`** — operators paste a candidate system prompt into the cell, the notebook samples N (default 10) historical decisions from the last 30 days, runs the candidate via `core.llm.factory:create_llm` so the call goes through the same provider chain + cost cap + circuit breaker the live cycle uses, and reports per-pair-action agreement between candidate and recorded decision. Pin documented in the notebook itself: **registering the candidate via `core.llm.prompts.register` is not done in the notebook** — this is for ad-hoc testing only. Promotion requires a five-step explicit checklist documented in the closing markdown cell: (1) move into `src/halal_trader/core/llm/prompts/`, (2) register with a version bump so future `LlmDecision.prompt_version` records the new prompt, (3) run Wave 5.B A/B comparator (`core/ab_compare.py`) after 100+ live trades on the new prompt, (4) run Wave 4.F promotion gate (`core/promotion_gate.py`) to verify absolute thresholds, (5) run Wave 6.D ML CI pipeline (`ml/ci_pipeline.py`) for regression-vs-incumbent. Only after steps 3-5 pass should the operator make the new prompt the production default in `crypto/strategy.py`. **`sentiment-vs-returns.ipynb`** — joins closed `crypto_trades` against their `IndicatorSnapshot` rows by `trade_id`, buckets by entry sentiment (proxied via RSI < 30 / RSI > 70 thresholds for the placeholder; the notebook documents that operators should swap in their actual sentiment column), and runs Wave 5.B's `core.ab_compare.compare` between bullish-entry and bearish-entry return distributions to produce a Welch's t-test verdict. Three interpretation paths documented in the closing markdown: (a) significant + bullish > bearish → signal is informative, consider increasing its prompt weight or sizing impact; (b) not significant → signal isn't producing actionable edge, sample too small or upstream source not capturing what moves these pairs; (c) significant + bearish > bullish → contrarian indicator, verify with more data before flipping the sign. Cross-references Wave 7.C `core.counterfactual` for the "what would equity have been without the bearish-entry trades" follow-up. `notebooks/README.md` documents the setup path, the three available notebooks with one-line descriptions, the halal alignment + read-only invariant, four conventions (start with "What this does / What it doesn't do" markdown cell; parameterised SQL only — no f-string injection; anonymised aggregates by default; explicit notes when a cell shows operator-identifying data like per-trade rationale), and a three-step contribution flow for operators who want to PR their own research notebooks (maintainer runs end-to-end → confirms read-only via no INSERT / UPDATE / DELETE → adds to index). Pure docs / notebooks — no code change beyond the new `notebooks/` directory.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.H — Filing-text sentiment classifier** — `sentiment/filing_classifier.py` adds the filing-grounded sentiment layer the roadmap asked for: instead of relying only on Reddit / CryptoPanic headlines (fast but noisy), the bot can classify the actual 8-K / 10-Q text from the EDGAR feed (slow but ground-truth). `classify(text)` → `SentimentResult` produces a bounded score in [-1, 1], a `Sentiment` label (BULLISH / NEUTRAL / BEARISH), and per-`PhraseHit` attribution so the dashboard renders "this filing scored bullish because of `record revenue (+1.5)` and `raised guidance (+1.5)`" rather than "the algorithm said so". Picked pure rule-based over a trained model for three reasons documented in the docstring: (a) operators need to be able to read the rule and challenge a verdict — opaque ML on a compliance-adjacent surface is the wrong default for this codebase; (b) the classifier stays under 100 lines of audit-able dataclass + regex, every phrase visible in the source so a scholar reviewer or operator can disagree on a specific lexicon entry; (c) re-training a sentiment model requires labelled SEC text the project doesn't have, and a hand-tuned lexicon is more honest than fine-tuning on a small synthetic dataset. Three lexicons: 20 positive phrases (`beat estimates / raised guidance / record revenue / exceeded expectations / strong demand / margin expansion / share buyback / dividend increase / ...`), 26 negative phrases (`missed estimates / lowered guidance / going concern / material weakness / litigation risk / cyber incident / writedown / covenant breach / bankruptcy / fraud / ...`), and 11 negation hedges (`not / no / never / without / unable / fails / lacks / ...`). 16 phrases get weight overrides at 1.5×–2.5× — `bankruptcy` and `fraud` at 2.5× as the strongest signals, `going concern` / `material weakness` / `delisted` / `covenant breach` at 2.0×, `record revenue` / `raised guidance` / `share buyback` / `data breach` at 1.5×. Three pinned semantics: **longest-phrase-match-first** ("record revenue and record earnings" produces exactly two hits, not three; the longer phrase wins at each starting position so overlap can't double-count); **negation window of 4 tokens** ("not raised guidance" within 4 tokens flips the bullish contribution to bearish; "while not generally a great quarter overall the company posted record revenue" with too many tokens between hedge and phrase does NOT flip — natural-language negation is local, and the 4-token window matches practitioner-tuned NLP intuition); **score normalisation** via `(positive - negative) / (positive + negative + 1)` — the +1 damper prevents single-hit saturation (one strong negative can't drive the score to -1.0; it caps at ~0.5 magnitude), keeps the result bounded in [-1, 1], and produces near-zero for documents with both strong positives AND strong negatives ("mixed signal" is honest output, not picking the larger side). Threshold bands at ±0.15 keep the classifier from declaring a definite tilt on sparse signal — most one-hit filings will land in NEUTRAL unless the hit is strong-weighted. `aggregate_for_symbol(*, symbol, filings)` weights each filing's score by `max(1.0, hit_count)` so a filing with 4 strong-negative phrases dominates a filing with 1 mild-positive phrase — pinned by a regression test that injects an unbalanced cohort. Halal alignment: read-only signal generation; never opens a position; never bypasses the screener; lexicons are publicly-checkable English phrases (no operator IP / PII handling). Pure-Python (`re` + dataclasses); lexicons are module-level `frozenset`s so a runtime mutation can't tilt the classifier — operators add phrases via code + review. 46 tests cover empty / whitespace / no-match → NEUTRAL pin; every lexicon class (positive matches / negative matches / strong-weighted dominates / writedown is bearish); negation-window flip in BOTH directions (bullish → bearish AND bearish → bullish — the symmetry pin matters because asymmetric negation handling is a common bug); negation locality (4-token cap regression-tested with a 9-token-gap "doesn't fire" case); negation-hedge-without-phrase produces no spurious hit; longest-match-first invariant; no-overlap-double-counting on consecutive matches; bounded-score guarantees under 5×-repeated extreme phrases; balanced-text-near-zero pin (a filing with both `record revenue` and `going concern` lands in [-0.5, 0.5]); single-default-weight-hit produces score=0.5 = BULLISH (the +1 damper math); per-PhraseHit attribution fields (phrase, polarity, token_index, negated, contribution); document-order hit list; per-symbol aggregator (no-filings → NEUTRAL with zero counts; dominant_label reflects the cohort; confidence weighting on filings with more hits; per-label counts); frozen-dataclass immutability across `SentimentResult`, `SymbolSentiment`, and `PhraseHit`; render output across all three labels with the top-3-matches summary; tokeniser pinning (case-fold so "RECORD REVENUE" and "record revenue" tie; punctuation stripped so "record revenue." matches; apostrophes preserved inside tokens for future possessive-form phrases). EDGAR-side wiring (subscribe to the existing EDGAR feed in `trading/scheduler.py`, classify each 8-K / 10-Q text body on receipt, and surface a per-symbol "EDGAR sentiment: bullish / 3 hits in last 30d" line in the LLM prompt context block) deferred to a follow-up — classifier verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 8.G — Public status snapshot aggregator** — `core/status_snapshot.py` is the data side of the public status page (think `status.halal-trader.dev`): given the bot's recent halt history + cycle event log, produce a publish-ready `StatusSnapshot` with overall status level, success rate, recent incidents, and the headline ongoing event when one exists. Picked these two append-only streams as inputs because they're already operator-published with audit-trail discipline; reading live broker state or operator-identifying logs would leak. `build_snapshot(*, halts, cycle_events, now, thresholds)` is the single entry point; `now` is injected so tests are deterministic, production callers pass `datetime.now(UTC)`. Four-level traffic-light status with pinned thresholds: **OPERATIONAL** (no ongoing halt + ≥99% success in the window), **DEGRADED** (95-99% success OR a recent resolved incident), **PARTIAL_OUTAGE** (80-95% success OR a recent halt of duration > 5min, regardless of success rate), **MAJOR_OUTAGE** (currently halted OR <80% success). The pinned classification decision tree handles four scenarios in order: (1) ongoing halt → MAJOR_OUTAGE unconditionally; (2) <80% success → MAJOR_OUTAGE; (3) long-halt-in-window flips to at least PARTIAL_OUTAGE even if success rate is fine, but stacks to MAJOR_OUTAGE if success is also degraded; (4) the success-rate ladder otherwise; (5) any in-window halt at all (even a < 5min blip) flips OPERATIONAL → DEGRADED so the public page acknowledges the incident rather than hiding it. `StatusThresholds` validates its own ladder ordering on construction (a config that put `success_rate_degraded < success_rate_partial` would silently classify every cycle as PARTIAL_OUTAGE — pinned via test). Three pinned safety semantics: (1) **empty input streams → OPERATIONAL** with success_rate=1.0 — no-data is "no incidents", not "no signal"; the public page showing "no cycles observed" shouldn't alarm; (2) **ongoing halt is the headline, not also in the historical list** — avoids double-counting in the public render where the headline already says "⚠️ Ongoing: started X, N min so far"; (3) **`filter_reason` redacts on any of five sensitive substrings** (`api_key / secret / token / password / operator` — case-insensitive, full replacement to "halt for operational reasons" rather than partial redaction because key tails leak via length under partial redaction). Long reasons cap at 80 chars with `…` suffix. Halal alignment: exposes only anonymised operational metadata — no per-trade data, no operator identifiers, no broker keys, no LLM prompts; the sensitive-substring denylist mirrors `otel_translator.py`'s redacted-attribute set so a future expansion stays consistent and the bot's two public-export surfaces (status page + OTLP traces) share one boundary. Window inclusion is honored: halts and cycle events outside `incident_window_days` (default 7) are excluded; a custom window flows through (a 14-day request includes 10-day-old halts that the 7-day default excluded). Incidents sorted most-recent-first so the public page renders the latest at the top. Render helper produces a text payload with emoji-prefixed status header, "⚠️ Ongoing" line when active, "Recent incidents" list with start / end / duration, "No incidents in the window" on a clean record. Pure-Python (no DB / network); frozen dataclasses on every output (`StatusSnapshot` / `IncidentSummary`). 43 tests cover: threshold validation (misordered ladder, negative recent_halt_minutes, zero window_days rejections), HaltRecord validation (resolved-before-engaged rejection, is_active and duration helpers including the "uses now when unresolved" pin), CycleEventRecord validation (negative duration rejection), `filter_reason` across the five sensitive substrings + clean-text passthrough + length cap with `…` suffix + empty input + case-insensitive match, the empty-streams → OPERATIONAL pin (success_rate 1.0, cycle_count 0, no incidents), the ongoing-halt → MAJOR_OUTAGE + ongoing-not-in-historical-list pins, the four-band success-rate ladder (99/97/90/70%), the long-halt rule (short halt → DEGRADED; long halt → PARTIAL_OUTAGE; long halt + low success → MAJOR_OUTAGE — the stacking case), window-inclusion (out-of-window halts and cycles excluded; custom window flows through), incidents-sorted-most-recent-first, reason-filter applied at the `IncidentSummary` boundary, the summary string content (emoji per level, halt mention when active, cycle count for the typical case, "no cycle data" fallback), the documented `StatusLevel` string values pinned for public-API stability, frozen-dataclass immutability across both output types, and render output (summary line + ongoing line + recent incidents list + clean-window fallback). Cycle-side wiring (a `/api/status/public` route handler that pulls the latest halts + cycle events from Postgres and serves the snapshot, plus the dashboard / `status.halal-trader.dev` page that renders it) deferred to a follow-up — aggregator verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 8.D — OTLP span translator** — `core/otel_translator.py` is the bridge that converts the bot's existing `cycle.stage.*` bus events into OTLP-compatible spans operators can ship to Tempo / Jaeger / Honeycomb / Datadog APM alongside their broker / database / LLM call traces — without pulling in `opentelemetry-sdk` as a hard dependency. Picked hand-rolled OTLP because (a) the SDK has 30+ transitive deps and non-trivial startup cost the per-cycle hot path can't afford, (b) the OTLP v1 wire format is well-specified and the JSON encoding is < 100 lines of dataclass-to-dict mapping, (c) pure-Python keeps the translator testable without a real collector, matching the rest of the Round-4 isolated-module pattern. Three concerns the translator handles: **ID generation** — `new_trace_id` returns 16 cryptographically-random bytes as 32 lowercase hex chars, `new_span_id` returns 8 bytes as 16 chars; the validator pins length + alphabet because uppercase or wrong-length IDs are silently dropped by collectors, so eager validation surfaces the bug at construction rather than at export. **Span hierarchy** — the cycle is a root span (`parent_span_id=""`), every stage is a child (`parent_span_id=root.span_id`), and the design supports future nested stages by chaining another `parent_span_id` link. **OTLP JSON encoding** — `to_otlp_json()` returns the canonical wire shape: camelCase field names (`traceId`, `spanId`, `parentSpanId`, `startTimeUnixNano`, `endTimeUnixNano`), nano timestamps as **strings** (some JSON parsers lose int64 precision otherwise), attributes as the protobuf-derived `[{key, value: {stringValue: …}}]` list-of-records (NOT a flat dict — collectors reject the dict form), and attributes are sorted by key for deterministic output that doesn't flake on dict-iteration order in regression tests. The OTLP/HTTP wrapper at the trace bundle level adds `resourceSpans[0].scopeSpans[0]` nesting per the spec, plus a `service.name` resource attribute the collector keys on for routing. Three pinned safety semantics: (1) **open-stage spans** (no `ended_at`) get `UNSET` status + zero-duration end_nanos — pin so an incomplete cycle still produces a valid (non-zero-duration where possible, valid-zero-where-not) span that the operator's APM renders as in-flight rather than dropping the trace entirely; (2) **the redacted-attribute filter** drops nine keys (`prompt / rationale / raw_response / thinking / api_key / secret / operator_id / broker_key / llm_token`) from the attrs before exporting — LLM rationales contain operator strategy IP and shouldn't ship to a third-party APM, broker / LLM keys are obviously sensitive, and the operator_id field is the multi-user-future PII guard; the denylist is a `frozenset` so runtime mutation can't add a non-redacted key by mistake (operators extend via code + review); (3) **attribute values capped at 256 chars** with `…` truncation so a runaway value can't bloat every span and overflow the collector's payload limits. Float-precision pin matters: timestamp conversion via `int(seconds) * 1_000_000_000 + microsecond * 1000` is exact integer arithmetic; `int(dt.timestamp() * 1e9)` accumulates ~128ns of error for 2026-era unix times because the float intermediate loses precision, and APM dashboards show that drift directly. Halal alignment: tracing is observability-only — never opens a position; the redacted-attribute filter is the explicit operator-IP / PII guard at the boundary leaving the bot. Pure-Python (stdlib `secrets` + `json`); no `opentelemetry-sdk` / DB / network. The caller wires the output to their preferred HTTP client (httpx / requests / urllib). 47 tests cover: ID generation (32 / 16 hex chars, lowercase regex match, 20-call uniqueness pin against determinism bugs), span validation (every ID validation rule fires; start_unix_nano ≥ 0; end_unix_nano ≥ start; parent_span_id empty-vs-set both paths), `duration_nanos` arithmetic, the redaction filter (every denylisted key dropped, 256-char cap with `...` suffix, short values pass unchanged, empty input handled, denylist is `frozenset`), `span_from_event` across completed / errored / open / kind-pass-through / parent-set / strips-redacted-attrs paths, the OTLP JSON shape (camelCase pin, nano-as-string pin, attributes-as-list-of-records pin, sorted-attribute-keys pin, status-code-and-message), `build_trace` across the four scenarios (complete cycle, incomplete with completed stages, incomplete with no stages → zero-duration root, custom trace_id passthrough), parent-id chaining root → stage_spans, the OTLP/HTTP wrapper structure (resourceSpans nesting, service.name default + custom override), JSON roundtrip via `json.loads`, frozen-dataclass immutability across `Span` / `TraceBundle` / `StageEvent`, and the float-precision pin via a 42ms-duration assertion that fails if the float-multiply path slips back. Cycle-side wiring (subscribe to the bus, build a TraceBundle on `cycle.complete`, ship via httpx to `Settings.otlp_endpoint`) deferred to a follow-up — translator verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 8.F — Backups + PITR runbook** — `docs/runbooks/backups-and-pitr.md` lands as the on-call's restore-drill procedure, written so an operator with no other context can follow it through to a successful restore. Targets pinned at the top: **RPO ≤ 5 min** (achievable because Postgres ships WAL per ~16 MB segment, and a busy bot rotates segments every 1-5 minutes), **RTO ≤ 30 min** (validated for databases ≤ 20 GB; scales linearly with extraction time for larger). Six sections walk every concern. **What's backed up** — explicitly listed every audit-trail table grouped by concern (trade history, LLM decisions, halal compliance audit including screenings + caches + exception queue + purification, indicator snapshots, ML artefacts, strategy adjustments, web actions audit, runtime config, per-asset metadata) so the operator can verify post-restore that the table they care about restored correctly. **What's NOT backed up** — `.env` secrets are operator-local (1Password / Bitwarden / encrypted USB; including them in the bot's pipeline would make every backup a credential disclosure), broker positions are authoritative on the broker side and reconstructable via `core/reconcile.py:reconcile_positions` on resume, HuggingFace model cache is third-party weights re-downloadable on demand. **Architecture** — diagrammed: live Postgres → `/var/lib/postgres/wal/` archive_command → remote storage; live Postgres → base backups → remote storage. Picked pgBackRest over plain `pg_basebackup` + cron for any production-leaning deployment with the rationale documented (deduplication so 7d daily + weekly full ≈ 1.5× DB size not 8×, parallel compression, encryption with operator-owned passphrase, single-command restore-to-time). For one-machine paper-trading, plain `pg_basebackup` is acceptable and the runbook walks both. **Setup** — four numbered steps with the exact docker-compose service config (`wal_level=replica`, `archive_mode=on`, `archive_command=/scripts/archive-wal.sh %p %f`), the `archive-wal.sh` script with the `set -euo pipefail` pin (a silently-failed archive is the worst-case backup outcome), the first-base-backup `pg_basebackup` invocation, a host-side cron script with 14-day retention rotation, and the off-machine rclone sync. **Restore** — two scenarios. Full disaster recovery: 7-step procedure (halt → stop postgres → wipe volume → restart → extract latest base into data dir → recovery.signal + postgresql.auto.conf → restart Postgres → verify `max(timestamp)` → run reconcile → resume). Point-in-time recovery: same procedure with `recovery_target_time` set to the explicit moment (used when a corrupt migration committed at 14:20 UTC and the operator wants 14:15 UTC); the runbook explicitly warns "anything after the target time is NOT in the restored database — capture anything you care about from live state first". **Restore drill (quarterly)** — runs via a side container (`pg-restore-drill` named, disposable volume) so the production volume is never touched; the procedure picks yesterday's base + a target time of yesterday-midnight-UTC, restores into the side container, verifies via `count(*), max(timestamp)` query, and tears down. Drill outcomes recorded in `docs/postmortems/drills/<date>-restore.md` even on success — the value is the verifiable evidence that the chain works on cadence. Drill failure modes section covers the three most-common drill failures with their diagnostic signature: empty `crypto_trades` (broken WAL chain — check `archive_status/` for `.partial` files), Postgres won't start (missing WAL segment — compare `pg_controldata` against archived files), max(timestamp) earlier than expected (archive lag — tighten `archive_command` or extend retention). **Targets** table pins each value with the rationale. **Halal-specific considerations** call out two edge cases unique to this bot's restore semantics: (a) restoring past a halal screening update can revert `not_halal` → `halal` for a symbol whose status was recently changed; the operator MUST run `halal-trader crypto screen` after every restore that crosses a screening boundary; (b) restoring past a purification `paid_at` mark makes a settled entry look outstanding again — the post-restore checklist surfaces this. **Post-restore checklist** is seven items the operator ticks before resuming: db migrate at head, halal cache re-refresh, position reconcile (already runs on bot startup), halt status, model fingerprint (Wave 6.E) matches what was active before the restore (if not, a fresh Wave 6.A promotion run), and audit-record-keeper notification of the restore window so per-trade audit rows correspond to the restored timeline. README runbooks index gains a new "Operations playbooks" section distinct from the alert-triggered runbooks so this doc (and future cadenced playbooks) are discoverable. Pure docs — no code change. The `archive-wal.sh` script and the `cron-backups.sh` host-side cron entry are documented in the runbook but ship as operator opt-in (they're not committed under `infra/`); a future `infra/backups-setup.sh` could land them but the present doc is sufficient for operators who already understand Postgres ops.
* **Round-4 Wave 9.D — Operator runbooks expansion (5 more)** — Building on the four seed runbooks Wave 8.E shipped (halt-engaged / chain-backoff / drift-breach / broker-api-error-rate), added five substantive new runbooks covering the remaining alert classes the bot can raise. **`cycle-stuck.md`** (PAGE) — when the cycle's `asyncio.wait_for(interval × 2)` watchdog cancels a cycle that didn't complete, the runbook walks through the four likely causes (stuck HTTP call, asyncio deadlock, Postgres serialization conflict, GPU/LLM-backend hang) with the concrete diagnostic commands (last `cycle.stage.start` without matching `.end`, `pg_stat_activity` for stuck transactions). Mitigation paths: halt + restart for HTTP hangs, `pg_terminate_backend` for Postgres, Ollama restart for local LLM, switch providers via `LLM_PROVIDER` for remote LLM. Recurrence escalation flagged. **`llm-circuit-breaker.md`** (PAGE) — when the `FallbackLLM` chain has cycled through every provider without success and the extended-backoff window (60s → 30min) has tripped halt. Covers five causes (all providers down, fallback mis-config, cost-cap exhausted, quota throttling on every provider, local Ollama died). Diagnostic commands include status-page curls for OpenAI / Anthropic and a localhost Ollama health check; mitigation includes the cost-cap reset path (resume requires cap not being the issue) and the cycle-cadence slowdown (`CRYPTO_CYCLE_INTERVAL_SECONDS=120` halves call rate) for quota mitigation. **`db-connection-lost.md`** (PAGE) — Postgres unreachable, the most operationally urgent of the set because without the database the monitor can't enforce SL/TP.
