Covers container stopped, network partition, connection-count exhaustion, disk full, auth broken; mitigation includes the `pg_terminate_backend` for idle-stuck connections + the WAL log cleanup for disk-full + the FK reference fix for stale-screening race. **`halal-screener-stale.md`** (WARN) — halal cache age exceeded `HALAL_CACHE_MAX_AGE_HOURS` (default 6h). Pinned the safety invariant explicitly in the runbook: "stale cache is safer than no cache" — STRICT consensus (Wave 2.B) and doubtful-on-unknown defaults already keep the operator safe; staleness affects coverage of the universe (newly-listed tokens won't appear), not correctness on cached symbols. Mitigation paths cover screener-API-down (wait one cycle; halt only on >24h staleness with the API being up), auth rotation, rate-limit upgrade (`COINGECKO_API_KEY` for the higher tier), and refresher-crash recovery. **`snapshot-store-failure.md`** (WARN) — replay snapshot couldn't be persisted (the trade itself executed; what's missing is the audit row). Pinned the audit-trail invariant: "a missing snapshot is a *gap*, not a *corruption* — don't try to backfill from later state, that would corrupt the audit promise". Covers Postgres-write-failure (cross-references `db.connection_lost` runbook), JSON-serialisation errors on new payload fields, schema-drift from migrations adding NOT NULL columns, and FK violations from rolled-back screening transactions. Each runbook follows the five-section template established in the seed set (likely-causes / diagnose / mitigate / escalate / postmortem) with concrete `bash` / `psql` / `curl` commands the on-call can copy-paste — pinned the "operator-readable triage in 10 seconds, mitigate in 5 minutes" target. PAGE-severity runbooks (cycle-stuck, llm-circuit-breaker, db-connection-lost) include the postmortem-filing requirement (file `docs/postmortems/<date>-<alert>.md` within 48h). Each carries an "Acknowledgement window" + "Last reviewed" footer for the quarterly review process documented in the runbooks README. The `runbooks/README.md` index updated to list all nine entries with their severities; the alert router (Wave 8.E) can now route every alert with a real `runbook_url` instead of the placeholder. Pure docs — no code change. The set is substantial enough now that the operator-hardening section in `SECURITY.md` (Wave 8.H) doesn't need to apologise for missing runbooks; the bot has paged-alert coverage for every operationally-critical failure mode the existing alerts can raise.
* **Round-4 Wave 7.D — Research API key registry + token-bucket rate limiter** — `web/research_api_keys.py` is the auth + rate-limit gate that sits in front of the future read-only public research API (anonymised aggregate trade history for academic / external researchers). Read-only by construction; no operator identity / position-level data flows through; the anonymisation happens upstream in the SQL layer. Three composed layers: `ApiKey` registry, token-bucket rate limiter, and permission scopes. The `ApiKey` dataclass holds an opaque `key_id` (the public identifier researchers paste into `X-Api-Key`), a SHA-256 `secret_hash` (the plaintext is shown to the researcher *once* at issuance and never stored or logged), a `frozenset[Scope]` of permissions (immutable so a runtime mutation can't grant access), and a `Tier`. `verify_secret` uses `hmac.compare_digest` for constant-time comparison — pinned against timing-attack secret extraction. The rate limiter is a token-bucket **per-(key_id, endpoint_class)** so a slow query on `trades.list` can't burn the budget for fast queries on `halal.summary`. Three quota tiers hard-coded in source (not `Settings` — a config typo silently 10×-ing a tier is exactly the failure mode this prevents): ANONYMOUS (10/min, burst 20 — for a public "try the API" demo), RESEARCHER (60/min, burst 120 — verified academic), PARTNER (600/min, burst 1200 — institutional). Five `Scope`s: `read:trades`, `read:halal`, `read:regime`, `read:rationale`, `read:aggregate` — pinned additive (no implicit hierarchy; a key without `read:trades` cannot read trades even if it has every other scope). `authenticate(*, key_id, secret, scope, endpoint_class, cost)` returns an `AuthResult` with one of five `AuthOutcome`s: `UNKNOWN_KEY`, `INVALID_SECRET`, `MISSING_SCOPE`, `RATE_LIMITED`, `ALLOWED`. Pinned check order: **auth → scope → rate limit**. The order matters for two security properties regression-tested separately: (a) an attacker spamming a victim's `key_id` with wrong secrets does NOT consume the victim's bucket (the auth check happens first; bad-secret attempts are dropped before the bucket consume), and (b) wrong-scope spam similarly doesn't burn the bucket. Token-bucket math: refill at `tier_limit_per_minute / 60.0` per second; cap at `burst_capacity`; on deny the result includes `retry_after_seconds = deficit / refill_per_second` so the client can wait the right amount. `issue_secret(*, length_bytes=32)` generates a URL-safe ~256-bit secret via `secrets.token_urlsafe` (URL-safe alphabet so researchers can paste it into headers without escaping); a regression test pins 10 calls produce 10 distinct values (guards against a determinism bug silently issuing duplicate secrets). `make_api_key(...)` is the single point of entry that hashes the plaintext via `hash_secret` and builds the frozen `ApiKey` — pin so callers don't accidentally store plaintext in `secret_hash`. `register` rejects duplicate `key_id` (silent overwrites mask key leaks; a future audit reading the registry must see every issued key, not the last one written). `revoke` is idempotent (operators may run revoke twice for safety). `tier_limits(tier)` is the public accessor for the dashboard's quota tile. Why a custom rate limiter rather than `slowapi` or Redis: the research API runs in the same process as the dashboard, pure-Python in-memory keeps the auth path sub-millisecond without an extra Redis trip, and operators can run the bot without Redis (the rest of the codebase stores state in Postgres or in-process — adding Redis as a hard dep just for rate limiting is over-engineered). The token-bucket math is < 100 lines and stays auditable. Halal alignment: the registry never authorises a trade — gates *read* access to anonymised data only. Pure-Python (stdlib `hashlib` + `hmac` + `secrets` + `time`); no DB / network / async; clock injectable via `now_fn` for deterministic tests. 37 tests cover hash determinism + empty-rejection, secret verify on match / mismatch / empty-vs-real, URL-safe alphabet check + 10-call uniqueness pin, low-entropy issuance rejection (< 16 bytes), `make_api_key` validation (empty key_id rejection, plaintext-not-stored invariant via 64-char hex check, scopes are frozenset and reject runtime mutation), `ApiKey` immutability + `has_scope` additivity, every documented tier-limit value (10/20, 60/120, 600/1200) + relative ordering invariant (PARTNER > RESEARCHER > ANONYMOUS for both refill and burst), registry lifecycle (register / revoke / get + duplicate rejection + idempotent revoke + None-on-missing), all five `AuthOutcome`s with the audit-friendly behaviour (registry returns the looked-up key on INVALID_SECRET so audit logs can record "key X tried with bad secret"), the **auth-before-rate-limit-consume security pin** tested twice (100 invalid-secret spam doesn't exhaust the legit user's bucket; 100 missing-scope spam similarly), rate-limit lifecycle (kicks-in-after-burst, refills-after-time-passes, per-endpoint-bucket-isolation, partner-tier-handles-500-burst, retry-after-math = 6.0s for ANONYMOUS at cost=1), revoked-key denial (returns UNKNOWN_KEY post-revoke), and `AuthResult` immutability + string-enum value formats (`"allowed"`, `"read:trades"`, `"researcher"`) so the values JSON-serialise cleanly for the dashboard. FastAPI route adapter (`/api/research/*` with `Depends(authenticate)`), SQL persistence (load `ApiKey` rows from a `research_api_keys` table at startup), and the dashboard's key-management page deferred to follow-ups — gate verified in isolation first so the route layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.E — Order-book microstructure feature extractor** — `ml/microstructure.py` is the feature layer the bot needs ready when L2 tick data lands (Coinbase Advanced Trade adapter or Binance L2 WebSocket). The wave is named after the eventual ML model, but the *feature contract* is what's stable across model iterations — pin the features once here, model layer slots in later. `extract(snapshot, *, levels=10)` produces a `MicrostructureFeatures` block from one `OrderBookSnapshot` carrying five computed features and the consumed metadata (best_bid, best_ask, mid_price, levels_used). The five features: (1) **Imbalance** = `(bid_vol - ask_vol) / (bid_vol + ask_vol)` aggregated over the top-N levels — bounded ∈ [-1, 1] by construction; positive = more buying pressure on the resting book. (2) **Micro-price** = `(best_bid × ask_size + best_ask × bid_size) / (bid_size + ask_size)` — the volume-weighted "true mid" from Cartea / Jaimungal that leads the simple mid by a few seconds; the weighting puts more weight on the side with *less* size (the side about to move *toward*). Surfaced as both an absolute price and a deviation-from-simple-mid in basis points, the latter clamped to ±500bp because anything past that is data corruption. (3) **Spread** in absolute and bp form; bp clamped at 0 lower bound (no upper clamp because wide-spread regimes are real features). (4) **Depth-decay slope** = the slope of `log(volume)` against level index, averaged across both sides via `np.polyfit` — flat book ≈ 0, thinning book negative; clamped to [-5, 5] because past those bounds the slope estimation is unreliable on a thin book. (5) **Top-of-book log-skew** = `log(bid_size / ask_size)` at the touch — positive log-skew = bid side thicker; clamped to [-5, 5]; returns 0 when either size is 0 (log(0) = -inf would corrupt downstream signals). Three input-contract pins: bids must be descending and asks ascending — the extractor doesn't sort (a future adapter that breaks the order surfaces immediately rather than silently mis-computing the spread); zero or negative price rejected at level construction (real data has positive prices, this catches feed glitches); crossed book (best_bid ≥ best_ask) rejected at snapshot construction (corrupted snapshots silently producing a negative spread is exactly the failure mode this catches). Three numerical safety pins: zero-volume on both sides returns 0 imbalance (no information to extract); zero size on one side at the touch returns 0 log-skew rather than -inf; below 3 valid (non-zero-size) levels per side, depth-decay slope is 0 (polyfit on 2 points has no useful information for a stable estimate). Zero-size levels are skipped in the depth-decay regression (log(0) = -inf would corrupt the slope). Picked a feature module rather than wrapping a model directly because the features are stable across model iterations and can also be fed into the LLM prompt as raw values ("bid imbalance: +0.45; micro-price 0.7bp above mid") for explainability without an in-house model — the same module serves both the future tick-data ML layer and the immediate LLM-prompt enrichment path. Halal alignment: read-only signal computation; never opens a position; the L2 snapshot is operator-fetched (the bot already respects exchange terms in `crypto/exchange.py`) and `MicrostructureFeatures` is just numbers. Pure-numpy (uses `np.polyfit` for the slope only — keeps the dependency surface minimal); no scipy / DB / async. Frozen dataclasses on inputs and outputs. 39 tests cover: `OrderBookLevel` validation (positive price required, non-negative size, zero size accepted), `OrderBookSnapshot` validation (rejects empty sides, mis-ordered bids both directions, mis-ordered asks both directions, crossed book), imbalance correctness (zero on balanced, positive on more buying, negative on more selling, [-1, 1] clamp under near-zero ask, zero-on-zero-volume defensive case), micro-price correctness (equals mid on equal sizes, skews toward thinner side, ±500bp clamp under extreme cases), spread arithmetic + non-negativity, depth-decay slope (zero on flat, negative on thinning, zero-when-too-few-valid-levels, zero-size-levels-skipped, ±5 clamp), top-of-book skew correctness + zero-when-one-side-zero + ±5 clamp, the extract entry point's `levels` validation, returned dataclass shape, the `levels_used` record (matches when smaller-than-requested book), the mid_price midpoint formula, the best_bid / best_ask pass-through, frozen-dataclass immutability, and render output (sign on imbalance, "spread" + "bp" in text, micro-price line). Tick-data wiring (Binance L2 WebSocket adapter + per-cycle feature snapshot + integration with the LLM prompt's microstructure block + the eventual model layer) deferred to a follow-up — extractor verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.J — Model voting committee** — `core/committee.py` adds the multi-variant decision aggregator that the existing `core/shadow_runner.py` was always missing: instead of one alternate strategy running in shadow, every cycle gets N variants (GPT-4o + Claude + Llama + RL policy + GA-evolved) running in shadow simultaneously, and a committee vote decides the live trade. The committee is **pure aggregation** — it doesn't run the variants, doesn't call any model, doesn't open positions; it takes a list of per-pair `VariantDecision`s and returns a `CommitteeVerdict` with the aggregated action + per-variant attribution. Three voting policies, all sharing the conservative-tiebreak philosophy used in Wave 2.B halal consensus and Wave 4.F promotion gate: **MAJORITY** (most-common action wins); **WEIGHTED** (per-variant weight sums — typically tied to each variant's rolling Sharpe via the dashboard's accuracy ledger); **UNANIMOUS** (every variant must agree on a non-HOLD action, else HOLD — strictest mode useful when an operator wants only the highest-conviction trades). The conservative-tiebreak ordering is pinned: `HOLD > SELL > BUY`; on a 1-1-1 three-way split the committee says HOLD; on a 2-2 BUY-vs-SELL split SELL wins (more conservative than BUY). The "no opening risk on a split" rule is the operative safety. Two asymmetric aggregations are the centrepiece: **BUY confidence = MIN across agreeing variants** (a 3-of-5 BUY where the lowest agreeing variant says 0.4 should size off 0.4, not 0.9 — opening risk needs the strictest test, not the most-confident outlier extrapolation); **SELL/HOLD confidence = MEAN across agreeing variants** (a closing decision benefits from averaging confidence — the asymmetry is intentional, the docstring + a regression test pin both sides). BUY quantity = **MEDIAN across agreeing variants** (robust to one variant proposing an outsized bet — pinned via a 0.01 / 0.02 / 10.0 input that produces 0.02 not (0.01+0.02+10)/3); SELL/HOLD quantity = 0 (the executor knows the operator's open position and handles the close — committee just authorises). Empty decisions list returns HOLD with zero confidence — a no-variants cycle (every model failed) must not accidentally promote a blank vote into BUY/SELL. WEIGHTED policy semantics: variants without an explicit weight default to 1.0; a negative weight clamps to 0 so a buggy config can't invert a contribution; a zero-total-weight cohort defaults to HOLD ("can't tell" is HOLD, not BUY). UNANIMOUS policy semantics: any single dissenting variant flips the result to HOLD with the dissent split listed in the reason string ("variants split across ['buy', 'sell'] — defaulting to HOLD"); only when every variant agrees on the same non-HOLD action does the committee echo that. Each `VariantAttribution` on the verdict carries the variant's action + confidence + quantity + assigned weight + `agreed_with_committee` boolean so the dashboard renders the audit row directly — operators spot reliably-aligned vs contrarian variants over time and the WEIGHTED weights can be auto-adjusted via the rolling Sharpe ledger without a re-architecture. `render_verdict` produces an emoji-prefixed (🟢 BUY / 🔴 SELL / 🟡 HOLD) text payload visually consistent with the other Round-4 render helpers, with a per-variant attribution table marked `✓` for agreeing and `·` for dissenting. Halal alignment baked in: voting is pure aggregation; never opens a position; the halal screener still gates every candidate before the committee sees it (the committee can't approve a `not_halal` symbol since it's never in the candidate set). Pure-Python (no NumPy / DB / async / LLM); operates on plain dataclasses so the committee tests run without the full strategy stack — fast, deterministic. 33 tests cover input validation (confidence bounds, negative quantity rejection, JSON-string action coercion, unknown-action rejection), the empty-input HOLD safety, all three voting policies (majority pass + tiebreak across both 1-1-1 three-way and 2-2 binary splits + unanimous BUY pass + unanimous mixed-actions HOLD), WEIGHTED policy specifics (uses-weights-not-counts pin, default-1.0, negative-clamp-to-zero, zero-total-defaults-to-HOLD, equal-weights-tiebreak-to-conservative), UNANIMOUS policy specifics (all-agree-buy → buy, any-dissent → HOLD with split reason, all-HOLD → HOLD), the BUY-min-confidence pin via a 5-variant cohort with mixed confidences, the SELL-mean-confidence asymmetry pin, the BUY-median-quantity-robustness pin against an outsized bet, the SELL-quantity=0 pin, attribution per variant + agreement marking + carries-assigned-weight, the `agreement_count` / `total_variants` properties, frozen-dataclass immutability across both `CommitteeVerdict` and `VariantAttribution`, and render output (emoji per action, variant attribution table, agreement markers, BUY confidence + median quantity rendering). Cycle-side wiring (parallel ShadowRunners per variant + per-cycle vote + executor gates on the verdict + per-variant attribution row in the audit trail + dashboard tile rendering the attribution) deferred to a follow-up — committee verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 8.H — SECURITY.md + threat model + disclosure policy** — `SECURITY.md` lands at the repo root as the project's security contract: what the bot defends against, what's explicitly out of scope, and how to disclose responsibly. Picked one comprehensive doc rather than splitting across files because security reviewers (and the eventual external auditor) need a single page that cross-links the threat model with the in-scope-vs-out-of-scope table — splitting would force them to chase references. The threat model section makes the trust boundaries explicit (operator's machine ↔ Postgres ↔ broker / LLM, three external trust boundaries with HTTPS as the only crossing mechanism); enumerates the assets the bot defends (broker keys, LLM tokens, Postgres credentials, halal cache integrity, audit-trail integrity, trading config) with the per-asset defence column; is honest about what's NOT defended (multi-tenant isolation — single-operator by design until Wave 3; cloud side-channel — operators concerned about that should use dedicated hardware; rationale confidentiality — operators encrypt the disk if rationales are sensitive; DoS — circuit breakers exist but aren't anti-DDoS). Secure-defaults table documents the eight pinned defaults that bias toward safety (paper-trade / testnet / empty WEB_API_TOKEN / require-confirmation / 0 LLM spend cap / 50 USD min notional / STRICT halal consensus / kill-switch on first error chain) — every default is the *safer* of any two reasonable choices, and the table makes that explicit so a future operator changing one knows exactly what protection they're trading away. Disclosure section gives the maintainer's contact + a published SLA (72h acknowledge / 7d triage / 30d fix for high-severity / 90d otherwise / status update if longer); credits via SECURITY-HALL-OF-FAME.md rather than paid bounty. In-scope vs out-of-scope is the operator's most-asked question, and the explicit list reduces wasted disclosure work in both directions: in-scope = secret extraction, halal screener bypass, halt-switch bypass, audit-trail tampering, cross-broker secret leakage, paper-to-live escalation, pre-auth code execution on bot-started processes; out-of-scope = brute force of operator-set passwords, social engineering, dependency CVEs < 30d, upstream-service issues, rate-limit shenanigans without data loss, on-host attacks requiring root, cloud side-channel timing. The "security-relevant features by wave" table cross-links the Round-4 modules that *implement* what the policy describes (Wave 2.A signed receipts, Wave 2.B consensus, Wave 2.C profiles, Wave 4.I anomaly, Wave 4.F promotion gate, Wave 8.B chaos, Wave 8.E alert router, Wave 6.E fingerprint, Wave 6.B feature schema, runbooks at 8.E + 9.D) so a reviewer can verify each control has a concrete code citation. Operator-hardening checklist is nine items operators can mechanically tick before deploying beyond a laptop (encrypted disk for `.env`, 0600 perms, Postgres bind, firewall, WEB_API_TOKEN if exposed, LLM cap non-zero, alert routing wired, signing keypair backup, no-shared-VM if cloud). Halal-specific threats section covers three failure modes specific to the screening path: spoofed compliance verdicts (defended via HTTPS-only checks in `_is_placeholder` Wave 5.G + STRICT multi-source consensus Wave 2.B + per-source audit trail), cache poisoning (defended via TTL + per-cycle refresh + original-source preservation in audit), operator override misuse (defended via mandatory exception-queue routing + per-override audit log with operator identifier and reason). The "deprecated / not implemented" section is the honesty test — explicit pointers at the gaps (per-secret encryption at rest, CSRF on mutation endpoints, 2FA on dashboard) all routed to the upcoming Wave 3 multi-user work, so operators can decide on dashboard exposure with full information. README's "In a hurry?" section gains a SECURITY.md pointer so reporters find it immediately. No code change beyond the doc + README link — the existing safeguards already implement what the policy describes; this wave makes the implementation reviewable as a single artefact.
* **Round-4 Wave 6.D — ML CI pipeline orchestrator** — `ml/ci_pipeline.py` is the commit-time gate that runs *before* the human reviewer (and before Wave 4.F's promote-to-live gate runs at deployment). `run_ci(*, candidate_walk_forward, candidate_sharpe, candidate_win_rate, candidate_returns, incumbent_*, ...)` composes four gates into a single `CIPipelineReport(passed, gates, failures, promotion_verdict, summary)`. **Walk-forward gate** delegates to Wave 4.F's `evaluate_promotion` (so the WF acceptance criteria from CI exactly match what the live gate enforces — no drift between commit-time and deploy-time bars). **Sharpe regression gate** enforces `candidate_sharpe / incumbent_sharpe ≥ 0.90` (the roadmap's "block on >10% regression"). **Win-rate regression gate** is symmetric but with a tighter 95% floor — pinned in the docstring with the rationale that win rate is more sensitive to small-sample variability than Sharpe, so the regression check should fire on smaller proportional moves. **Distribution drift gate** computes a KS-style max-absolute-CDF-distance between the candidate's and incumbent's per-trade-return distributions, capped at 0.30; implemented without scipy because the bot's heavy-tailed returns don't fit a parametric distribution well — at each unique observation the helper evaluates both empirical CDFs (right-continuous: count of values ≤ x divided by sample size) and takes the max absolute difference. Picked KS over chi-squared / Anderson-Darling because KS works on raw samples without binning (no operator-tuned bin edges that could hide regressions in the rebalanced bins) and operates in [0, 1] (giving the threshold a clean operator-readable interpretation: "more than 30 percentage points of disagreement at some quantile"). The pivotal pinned semantic across all four gates: **skipped checks count as PASS, never FAIL**. When there's no incumbent (cold start — operator's first model), the regression and drift checks return `passed=True` with a `remediation` string starting with `"skipped: …"`. The `GateOutcome.is_skipped` property is only True when both `passed=True` AND the remediation begins with `skipped` (a separate test pins this — a *failure* with "skipped" elsewhere in the remediation isn't a skip, so the orchestrator never gets fooled into passing a real failure). The renderer displays skipped gates with a `—` marker rather than `✔` so operators can spot at-a-glance which gates ran "for real" vs auto-passed for lack of a baseline. Sample-size-too-small drift (default `min_sample_size=20`) and non-positive incumbent Sharpe (no real baseline to compare against, would divide-by-zero on the ratio) also skip rather than fire. The aggregate `passed` is `True` iff every gate passed (skip counts as pass), the summary mentions skip count on PASS and failure count on FAIL. The Wave 4.F `PromotionVerdict` is exposed on the report for operator drill-in (so a walk-forward failure can be examined without re-running). Picked a separate orchestrator from `promotion_gate.py` because the live-trading gate runs against absolute thresholds (Sharpe ≥ 0.5, drawdown ≤ 20% in the absolute) while CI runs against the *incumbent* (no >10% regression — the absolute number doesn't matter, the comparison does); they share threshold values but compose differently. CI also bundles the regression test that the live gate doesn't run — promotion gate only checks absolute bars + an optional A/B; CI specifically guards against silent regressions when a model commit subtly degrades. Halal alignment: the CI pipeline is metadata only — never opens a position, never bypasses the screener; a failing CI run blocks promotion to live trading but the existing kill-switch + halt mechanism remains the final authority. Pure-Python (no NumPy / scipy / DB / async); operates on already-collected report dataclasses. 35 tests cover: threshold validation (Sharpe ratio in [0, 1], distance in (0, 1], min_sample_size ≥ 1), KS-distance helper edges (zero-on-identical, one-on-disjoint, empty handling, [0, 1] bound across diverse pairs), Sharpe regression (above-threshold pass, below-threshold fail, no-incumbent skip, non-positive-incumbent skip), win-rate regression (above/below threshold, no-incumbent skip), distribution drift (close → pass, disjoint → fail, no-incumbent skip, sample-below-min skip on either side), `run_ci` aggregation (every-gate-passes → PASS, single-fail → FAIL, MC layered through, four-gates count, skip-counts-as-pass), summary content (skip count on PASS, fail count on FAIL), `is_skipped` precedence (passed=False with "skipped" substring is NOT a skip — only the prefix-on-passed=True triggers), promotion-verdict drill-in exposure, output immutability across both `GateOutcome` and `CIPipelineReport`, and render output (overall status, ✘ on failures, `—` for skipped gates distinctly, remediation arrow on failures). CLI command (`halal-trader ml ci run`) and integration with the existing CI workflow files deferred to follow-ups — orchestrator verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 9.C — Halal compliance handbook expansion** — `docs/halal_jurisprudence.md` expanded from 58 → 498 lines into a nine-section handbook that now serves as the single document a future independent scholar reviewer reads to validate the bot's rulings. Picked structuring it as one comprehensive doc rather than splitting across files because operators (and the scholar) need to follow cross-references without juggling tabs — every ruling cites a section number that's already used by `halal/explainer.py` when it explains a trade decision. **Section 1** (foundational prohibitions) covers Riba / Maysir / Gharar / prohibited industries — the hard floors under every methodology that no operator configuration can soften. Each prohibition lists the bot's mechanical implementation: Riba via the AAOIFI 30%-debt cap (Section 2.4) + the crypto rules engine; Maysir via the spot-only / testnet-only broker configuration (the strongest mechanical guarantee — the brokers themselves cannot leverage); Gharar via opaque-redemption-flag in `crypto/screener.py`; prohibited industries via Zoya GICS sectors + crypto category-table rejections. **Section 2** (AAOIFI financial ratios) walks the three default-profile cuts with implementation rationale: backward-looking market-cap average to resist day-of-screening manipulation; 5% non-permissible-income tolerance with the operator-purification trade-off (Section 5) that pays for the tolerance; cash-and-receivables informational by default (real businesses can hold large cash during M&A) but flippable to hard-reject in the DeLorenzo profile. **Section 3** (asset-class rulings) covers equities (AAOIFI sector + ratio); crypto with **Mufti Faraz Adam's 4-pillar framework** explicitly cited as `crypto/screener.py`'s basis (utility / non-interest-bearing / halal-issuer-revenue / material-liquidity); commodities (gold / silver permissible per classical hadith — physical or allocated-custody ETFs only; synthetic / paper rejected); sukuk (permissible by construction since the structure is the ruling); REITs (permissible iff underlying properties + debt structure pass); international equities (framework extends naturally). Each asset class has a forward reference to its Round-4 wave (1.G commodities, 1.H sukuk, 1.I REITs, 1.J international). **Section 4** (decision states) formalises the `halal` / `doubtful` / `not_halal` vocabulary the audit row uses, plus the conservative-wins-on-ties pin from `halal/consensus.py`. **Section 5** (purification) cross-links to Wave 2.D's quarterly disbursement scheduler with the per-trade and per-dividend formulas explicit, the **never-auto-marks-paid** pin (one-way audit-trail commitment), guidance on charity choice, and the dividend / capital-gain split. **Section 6** (scholar profiles) is the new Wave 2.C surface: documents `aaoifi_default` (international standard), `taqi_usmani` (stricter — debt 25% / income 3%, with the rationale that AAOIFI thresholds were a starting concession not a target), `delorenzo_djim` (DJIM-era — debt 33%, MAJORITY consensus); plus the three consensus policies (STRICT default / MAJORITY / WEIGHTED) all sharing the conservative-wins tiebreak; plus the empty-input-defaults-to-doubtful safety pin. **Section 7** (exception queue) documents Approve / Reject / Defer triage with the **approval-doesn't-auto-promote** pin (one cycle's authorisation, not the symbol's ongoing status). **Section 8** (audit trail) lists every field — `halal_screening_id` FK, scholar profile name, consensus policy, criteria JSONB, queue row + override reason — that a future scholar reviewer needs to replay any historical trade without reading code. **Section 9** (limits and disclaimers) makes the handbook honest about what it is: a methodology not a personal fatwa, the kill-switch is risk-control not compliance (so the screener runs *before* the strategy, not after), and paper-only by design with the testnet pins in `.env.example` documented. References section cites AAOIFI Standards 21 + 30, *Introduction to Islamic Finance* by Mufti Taqi Usmani, *Islamic Capital Markets* by Hassan & Mahlknecht, Mufti Faraz Adam's framework, and pointers to Shariah Review Bureau / IFG / Mufti Menk's published frameworks, plus a pointer to `halal.scholar_profiles.register_profile(...)` for operators following a scholarly position not captured by the three built-in profiles. "Last reviewed" footer set with a note pending external scholar sign-off; the handbook sections are written to be ready for review without further engineering work. No code change beyond the doc rewrite — the existing screener, consensus aggregator, scholar profiles, exception queue, and purification scheduler implement what the handbook describes.
* **Round-4 Wave 5.C — Trade rationale full-text search index** — `core/rationale_search.py` builds the search half of the operator's "show me trades that mentioned MACD divergence" or "every losing trade where the LLM cited high vol" research surface. Picked a hand-rolled in-memory TF-IDF over Postgres `tsvector` because (a) the rationale corpus is small enough (≤ 100k decisions over a year) for sub-millisecond in-memory queries that let the dashboard scrub live without a DB round-trip per keystroke; (b) the dashboard's explainability requirement ("why did this rank first?") needs per-token contributions exposed, which is easier when we own the scoring path; (c) pure-Python keeps the index testable without a database, matching the rest of the Round-4 isolated-module pattern. `RationaleIndex.add(doc)` ingests one `RationaleDoc(doc_id, text, metadata)`; `search(query, *, limit, require_all)` returns ranked `SearchHit`s with a per-query-term breakdown. Tokenisation is deliberately conservative: case-fold, word-boundary split via `[A-Za-z][A-Za-z0-9_]*` regex, drop tokens < 2 chars (single-char tokens have IDF approaching zero anyway and add noise), drop a tiny stop-word list (only `a / an / and / as / at / be / by / for / if / in / is / it / of / on / or / the / to / with` — operators search phrases like "the market is overbought" and removing too many stop words kills phrase recall). The scoring math: sub-linear TF dampening `1 + log(tf)` so a 10× repeated term doesn't 10× the score (pinned ratio < 5× via test on a 10-occurrence doc vs 1-occurrence doc); smoothed IDF `log((N+1)/(df+1)) + 1` so a term in every doc still contributes a positive score (zero IDF would make universal terms invisible; the `+1` floor keeps them ranked below rare terms but visible). Each `SearchHit` carries a `terms: list[TermContribution]` with `(term, tf, idf, contribution)` so the dashboard renders the explanation as a stacked bar — operator sees "matched MACD 4× and divergence 1×" rather than "the algorithm said so". Three pinned semantics: (1) query terms are **de-duplicated** before scoring (a typo'd `"MACD MACD"` query is treated as one occurrence — operators occasionally double-type, and the search shouldn't reward it); (2) **stable tie-break** preserves input order on equal scores so older trades surface first when ranks tie; (3) **all-stop-word queries return no hits** rather than every doc at score zero (the empty result is a clearer "I didn't find anything specific" than a noise-ranked list). `require_all=True` flips OR ranking to AND filtering (operator's "must include" search). Snippet builder centres on the first query-term match position (operator's first glance at *why* a result matched should be the matching context, not the document start), truncates at ~200 chars, falls back to a head snippet when the literal substring isn't found in the original text (the tokeniser may have transformed it). The `add` rejects duplicate `doc_id` rather than silently overwriting — pin the append-only audit invariant; operators rebuild via `clear()` if they want to re-index. Halal alignment: pure read-only search over data the cycle already persisted; never opens a position, never bypasses the screener. Pure-Python (no numpy / scipy / DB / async); frozen dataclasses on the inputs / outputs. 39 tests cover tokenisation across case-folding + stop-word drop + length filter + punctuation split + alphanumeric (rsi14 / btc1) preservation + empty-input handling, index lifecycle (add / clear / doc_count / get_doc / duplicate rejection / re-add after clear), basic search (matching doc, no match, empty index, all-stop-word query → empty, zero/negative-limit rejection), ranking invariants (higher TF ranks first; rare-term IDF dominates over common terms; sub-linear TF cap pinned via the < 5× ratio test on tf=10 vs tf=1; per-term contributions list matches actual TFs; query de-duplication produces identical scores for `"MACD"` and `"MACD MACD"`; stable tie-break by input order; limit respected on a 20-doc index), `require_all` filter (filters docs missing any query term; default-False does OR-style ranking), snippet generation across the four cases (centred match, match-at-start, match-at-end, long-text truncation, empty doc), metadata pass-through to results, frozen-dataclass immutability on docs, the render helper output (each hit + score format + match counts arrow + empty-results fallback), and the numerical sanity pins (IDF smoothing keeps universal-term scores positive; TF dampening exactly matches the documented `1 + log(tf)` formula via the exposed contribution field). Dashboard wiring (subscribe to `LlmDecision` rows, build the index on dashboard mount, expose `/api/rationale/search?q=...` endpoint, render highlighted snippets in the search results panel) deferred to a follow-up — index verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 6.H — Active-learning hard-case selector** — `ml/active_learning.py` closes the loop on the "trade post-mortem" data the bot already produces (Wave 5.D lessons-learned cards) by ranking closed trades on labelling-priority so the operator's review time goes to the most informative cases first. `TradeCase(trade_id, pair, predicted_return, actual_return, confidence, age_seconds, indicator_outlier_score, rationale)` is the input shape; `score_case(case, *, weights)` returns a `Priority(case, score, components, reason)` with the per-component breakdown so the dashboard can render the *why* — "this case bubbled up because it was a high-confidence sign disagreement", not "because the algorithm said so". Four weighted scoring components: (1) **confidence × error** — `confidence × |predicted - actual| × 10` capped at 2.0 (a high-confidence prediction that missed by a wide margin is a 2σ teaching moment, but a single 5σ freak event won't dominate the rest of the score); (2) **sign disagreement** — fires only when both predicted and actual are non-zero AND signs differ, scales with `|predicted| + |actual|` × 5 capped at 2.0 (predicted +5%, actual -3% is the canonical "embarrassing confident wrong-direction" — pinned that a "no opinion" zero on either side scores zero, so cases without a real prediction can't masquerade as wrong-direction); (3) **outlier** — passes through the operator-supplied `indicator_outlier_score` clamped to [0, 1] (operators may pass un-normalised z-scores; the clamp prevents a single outlier from dominating); (4) **recency** — exponential decay `exp(-ln2 × age / half_life)` with operator-tunable `recency_half_life_seconds` (default 7 days; an aggressive 1h half-life reduces a 1-day-old case to <0.01 contribution — useful for sweeps after a known regime change). Default weights (0.40 / 0.30 / 0.15 / 0.15) sum to ~1.0 so the raw priority score is roughly comparable across runs; operators tilt toward sign-disagreement on a strategy that's been embarrassed by confident wrong-direction calls, or toward recency during a regime change. `_explain` picks the dominant non-zero component and surfaces a one-line operator-readable reason via a stable lookup table — `confidence_error` → "high-confidence prediction missed by a wide margin", `sign_disagreement` → "predicted direction was wrong", `outlier` → "entry indicators were an outlier", `recency` → "recent trade — informative for the current regime". `select_top_n(cases, *, n, weights)` scores everything and sorts descending; stable Python sort means equal-score cases preserve input order so older trades get reviewed first when scores tie. Pin: the selector **triages**, never auto-labels — operator review is the only authority that produces a label that flows into training; the docstring + the test suite both pin this so a future refactor can't accidentally short-circuit the human into the loop. Halal alignment: the queue is informational; never opens a position; never bypasses the screener. Pure-Python (no numpy / scipy / DB / async); frozen dataclasses safe to cache for the dashboard's "review queue" tile. 34 tests cover `TradeCase` validation (confidence in [0, 1], age ≥ 0, None outlier acceptance), `ScorerWeights` validation (non-negative weights, positive half_life), each component scorer in isolation (confidence × error scaling and zero-on-perfect-prediction and 2.0 cap; sign-disagreement zero-on-match + zero-when-either-zero + magnitude scaling + the canonical predicted-buy-but-lost case; outlier clamping in both directions; recency decay including the t=HL → 0.5× fresh-score numerical pin and the custom-half-life-speeds-decay case), the weighted total summing to the components, the zero-weights-zero-component pin (operators selectively disable contributions), the dominant-component explanation including the all-zero "no notable signal" fallback, `select_top_n` ranking + handles-input-larger-than-n + zero-n rejection + the stable-tie-break invariant + empty-input handling, and the `render_queue` output (each case rendered with score + predicted/actual returns + confidence + the explanation arrow, plus the empty-queue fallback). Dashboard wiring (subscribe to closed-trade events, push the top-N into a review panel, persist operator labels back to the IndicatorSnapshot table for the next retrainer cycle) deferred to a follow-up — selector verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 6.C — Online learner for short-half-life signals** — `ml/online_learner.py` is the streaming counterpart to the batch retrainer, built for signals (orderbook imbalance, spot-perp basis, sentiment-velocity) whose relationship to next-step return shifts on a faster cadence than the daily/weekly retrain. `OnlineLearner` keeps a rolling buffer of the last `window` (default 200) samples and re-fits a closed-form weighted ridge regression on every update — the hot path is O(N × K²) and stays sub-millisecond for K ≤ 20 features, so the implementation stays one-screen-of-numpy auditable. Picked closed-form refit over an online RLS / Kalman-style update because (a) the constant-factor cost is invisible at these window sizes, and (b) auditability matters for a model that gates real-money decisions — operators can read the fit code without recursing through update equations. Two operating modes: **plain ridge** (decay=1.0) and **exponentially-weighted ridge** (decay<1, samples weighted by `decay**(age)` so older observations contribute less). The weighted ridge solves `(XᵀWX + λI)β = XᵀWy` where W is the diagonal age-weight matrix; pin: the intercept is regularised too — a non-zero intercept on noise drifts the prediction; the L2 penalty grounds the model at zero unless the data demands otherwise. Three pinned safeties: (1) **feature_clip + target_clip** bound every input before fitting — a glitched feed sending 1e9 can't dominate the fit; clipping rather than dropping samples keeps the buffer aligned with the time axis (a regression test pins RMSE stays < 1.0 even when an injected target was 1e6); (2) **tanh squash** on `predict` bounds the output to [-1, 1] so a runaway coefficient can't cause a size explosion downstream — even a 100× over-budget input clips through feature_clip + linear + tanh and the output stays bounded; (3) **`min_samples_for_predict` cold-start guard** returns 0.0 below the threshold so strategies treating 0 as "no edge" stay correct on a fresh learner. `update(features, target)` + `predict(features)` + `reset()` (clears buffer and zeros coefs — used on regime-change detection events when the learner should start over rather than slowly forget) + `snapshot()` (exposes coef + intercept + RMSE + sample_count + last_prediction + last_target for the dashboard tile). Validation rejects non-finite features / target (NaN / inf surface immediately rather than producing a garbage fit), wrong feature count (caller mismatch caught at update/predict time), non-positive ridge_lambda (at 0 the closed-form is sensitive to correlated features), zero / out-of-range decay, non-positive clip, zero min_samples_for_predict, and zero n_features. Halal alignment baked in: the learner emits a *signal* (a regression prediction), never opens a position; the downstream consumer (a strategy combining this signal with the LLM's plan) decides whether to act, and the bounded output gives the consumer a hard ceiling on how much the signal can move them. Pure-numpy; no scipy / sklearn / DB / async — single-threaded by contract (the cycle holds the per-pair lock during update + predict). 29 tests cover config validation across every parameter (window / ridge_lambda / decay / clips / min_samples), learner construction (zero-features rejection, fresh state has zero coefs / RMSE / prediction), cold-start zero-prediction guard + above-threshold non-zero output, ridge fit recovering a known linear y=0.05·x1+0.02·x2+noise relationship within bounded error (small targets used so tanh stays near identity), intercept recovery on a constant-target series, rolling-window eviction (10 samples into window=5 keeps last 5), end-to-end regime-flip response (positive slope window flips coefficient to negative when the relationship inverts), exponential-decay speeding up regime response vs plain ridge (decay=0.85 moves further toward the new regime than decay=1.0 over the same number of new samples), the decay=1.0 → plain ridge equivalence pin, feature clipping protecting the fit from outliers, target clipping bounding RMSE under garbage inputs, every input-validation rejection (wrong feature count both directions, NaN / inf in features, NaN target, predict-with-wrong-feature-count), the tanh-bounded output guarantee under runaway coefficients (clipping + tanh keeps the output within [-1, 1] even when input is 100× the clip), the predict([0]) → tanh(intercept) sanity check confirming the intercept is consulted at predict time, reset clearing buffer + coefs and predict-after-reset returning 0, the last_target / last_prediction snapshot tracking, and frozen-dataclass immutability on `LearnerSnapshot`. Cycle-side wiring (instantiate one learner per fast-half-life signal under a per-pair lock, feed orderbook imbalance / basis / sentiment-velocity samples on every kline tick, multiply the LLM plan's confidence by the learner's signal in the executor) deferred to a follow-up — engine verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 8.E — Multi-channel alert router + seed runbooks** — `core/alert_router.py` generalises the existing single-channel `notifications/telegram.py:AlertSink` (rate-limited but Telegram-only) into a multi-channel routing layer. `AlertSpec(type, severity, summary, runbook_url, context)` is the typed payload bot modules raise instead of free-form `notify()`. `Severity` is an IntEnum (INFO=10, WARN=20, PAGE=30) so `severity >= warn` reads naturally in route matching. `Channel` is a Protocol matching the existing Telegram / Slack / Discord notifier shape (async `send → bool` plus `name` and `enabled` properties), so the existing notifiers slot in without changes. `AlertRoute(severity_min, channel)` declares "channel X receives alerts at severity ≥ Y"; `AlertRouter` composes routes and dispatches with three pinned semantics: (1) **per-(type, channel) dedup** — a Slack-suppressed alert can still reach Telegram in the same window, since operators see each alert once *per channel*, not once globally (distinct from the existing `AlertSink` which dedups globally per type); (2) **failure isolation** — a per-channel send failure does NOT abort dispatch to other channels, because the operator wants Telegram delivered even if Slack is down (a regression test pins this with a Slack stub that raises while Telegram succeeds); (3) **send-returning-False is failure not suppression** — and importantly does NOT burn the cooldown, so the next attempt retries rather than being silently suppressed (a separate test pins the no-cooldown-burn invariant). Multiple routes targeting the same channel (e.g. WARN + PAGE both → Slack) de-duplicate to one delivery per alert via name-based set tracking. A channel with `enabled=False` is skipped silently — not counted as suppressed or failed, since the operator deliberately turned it off. `DispatchResult(alert_type, severity, sent, suppressed, failed)` returns the per-outcome channel lists; `reached_any` is the convenience boolean. `render_message` produces an emoji-prefixed (ℹ️ / ⚠️ / 🚨) text payload with the alert type in backticks, severity name, summary, runbook URL (or `(none yet — write one in docs/runbooks/)` when empty so the gap is visible in every alert until a runbook is filed), and sorted context k/v pairs (alphabetical for deterministic rendering). The router's clock is injectable via `now_fn` so dedup tests are fully deterministic — no `time.sleep` in the test suite. Pure-Python; no DB / network; channels are Protocol-typed so the router runs against in-memory stubs.

**Seed runbooks:** `docs/runbooks/` ships a `README.md` index + filename convention (`alert.type` → `alert-type.md`), a `_template.md` with the five-section template (likely-causes / diagnose / mitigate / escalate / postmortem) so future runbooks have a consistent shape, and four production-ready runbooks for the alerts the bot already raises: `halt-engaged.md` (PAGE — kill-switch trip with mitigation paths for operator-engaged / spend-cap / circuit-breaker / drift causes), `chain-backoff.md` (WARN — LLM provider chain in exponential backoff with single-provider / all-throttled / key-rotation cases), `drift-breach.md` (WARN — Wave 4.I detector tripping with regime-change / feature-drift / random-tail diagnoses cross-linked to Wave 6.B feature-schema validation), `broker-api-error-rate.md` (PAGE — broker outage with status-code triage and `curl` reachability check). Each runbook carries an "Acknowledgement window" + "Last reviewed" footer; PAGE runbooks include a postmortem-filing requirement.

28 tests cover severity routing (≥ min, < min skipped, higher reaches lower-min), multi-route same-channel dedup (one delivery per alert even when two routes match), multi-channel distinct dispatch, the cooldown semantics (repeat within window suppressed, repeat after cooldown passes through, per-type isolation across two different alert types, per-channel isolation), failure isolation (one channel raising doesn't block others; send-returning-False classified as failure not suppression; failure does not burn cooldown so the next attempt retries), disabled-channel silent-skip (not failure or suppression), the `reached_any` property aligning with `sent`, `matching_channels` filter + deduplication-by-name, every `render_message` section (emoji per severity, type in backticks, severity name uppercase, runbook URL when present, missing-runbook flag with `docs/runbooks` pointer, sorted context k/v pairs alphabetical, omit context section when empty), and frozen-dataclass immutability on `AlertSpec` + `DispatchResult` (the latter via an async test). Concrete-channel adapters wrapping the existing Telegram / Slack / Discord / email notifiers, plus the cycle-side wiring (replace `AlertSink.notify` callsites in `crypto/cycle.py` / `trading/scheduler.py` / `core/safeguards.py` with `AlertRouter.dispatch(AlertSpec(...))`), deferred to a follow-up — router and runbook scaffolding verified in isolation first so the wiring sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 6.F — Inference latency budget tracker** — `ml/latency_budget.py` is the in-process tracker that gives the cycle a budget verdict *during* execution (so it can gate optional enrichment stages like agentic tools / RAG when the forecaster + anomaly + classifier path has already burned 90% of the budget) without round-tripping through Prometheus. `LatencyBudgetTracker` declares per-stage `StageBudget(name, budget_ms, soft_pct, min_samples)` and maintains a rolling sample window per stage (default 100 — at a 60-second cycle, ≈ 100 minutes of history; tunable for stable long-window regression detection or responsive load-shedding). `record(stage, ms)` is hot-path O(1) (deque append + dirty bit); percentiles are computed lazily on `observe()` read with a cache invalidating on the next record so multiple observers in a single cycle don't pay multiple sort costs. Each observation returns a four-way traffic-light classification: **cold-start** (sample_count < min_samples) checks *only* current vs hard budget so first-sample noise doesn't alarm but a real breach still fires; **steady-state** flips RED if either current OR p95 crosses the hard budget — the "p95 RED even when current is fast" pin matters: a consistently-slow stage where the latest sample happens to be quick must still show RED so the operator's eye lands on the persistent regression, not the lucky tail. AMBER fires when either crosses `soft_pct × budget` (default 80%) so the dashboard has a leading indicator before the hard breach. Picked nearest-rank percentiles over linear interpolation because the dashboard reads "the 95th-worst sample we actually saw" — interpolation would invent data points the system never observed. Three pinned safeties: `record()` for an unknown stage raises with the candidate list (typo'd stage names would otherwise hide samples in a never-checked bucket); negative latency raises (a measurement bug must surface); soft_pct strictly in (0, 1) (at 0 every measurement would AMBER; at 1 nothing would). `aggregate(observations)` sums budgets / current / p95 across stages and takes the worst per-stage status as the overall — pin so a single RED stage flips the whole report regardless of how many GREEN stages surround it. `render_report` emits an emoji-prefixed (🔴 / 🟡 / 🟢) text payload visually consistent with the other Round-4 render helpers. Halal alignment baked in: the tracker is observability + load-shedding only; a RED status causes the cycle to skip optional stages (agentic tools, RAG) and fall back to the canonical signal, **never** to force a trade through. Pure-Python (no NumPy / DB / network); frozen dataclasses on the output + a mutable ring buffer for the sample window. 34 tests cover budget validation (positive budget_ms, soft_pct strictly in (0, 1), min_samples ≥ 1), cold-start three-way (no-samples → GREEN, single 90ms-of-100ms sample → AMBER, single 200ms sample → RED), steady-state classification across all four bucket transitions including the consistently-slow-but-current-fast case (p95 over budget → RED even if current is fine), percentile math invariance on uniform windows + the nearest-rank pin on a known [1..20] sequence (p95 = 19, not interpolated), ring-buffer eviction (10 samples into a window=5 keeps only the last 5), headroom positive when under budget + negative when over, unknown-stage rejection on both record + observe (typo surfaces with the candidate list), tracker-construction validation, the stages property, negative-latency rejection, observe_all parity, aggregate budget/current/p95 summation across stages, the worst-status-wins overall (GREEN+RED → RED, GREEN+AMBER → AMBER), None current_ms handled by aggregate as 0 contribution, empty aggregate returning GREEN with summary noting "no stages declared", render-emoji + stage-lines + empty-fallback + RED-stage-marker output paths, the `is_breaching` convenience property aligning with status, and frozen-dataclass immutability on both StageObservation and BudgetReport. Cycle-side wiring (call `record()` from each ML stage's exit, gate optional enrichment via `aggregate(...).overall_status`) and dashboard tile deferred to a follow-up — tracker verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 6.B — Feature store schema + migration** — `ml/feature_store.py` is the migration layer between feature producers (`crypto/indicators.py`, sentiment, regime) and feature consumers (anomaly detector, signal classifier, RL policy). Today these are coupled — a rename of `rsi_14` to `rsi_period_14` breaks every consumer unless every commit lands together; a dtype shift produces silently-wrong inference. `FeatureSchema(name, version: Semver, features)` declares the contract a model expects, with `version` reusing the Wave 6.A `Semver` so feature schema bumps follow the same major/minor/patch semantics as model versioning (operator only learns one vocabulary). `FeatureSpec(name, dtype, description, producer, required)` declares each feature; `producer` is the operator's free-form label for what computes it (`"crypto.indicators.rsi"`, `"sentiment.cryptopanic"`) so the dashboard's lineage tile can surface per-column provenance. Four declarative migration rules: `Rename(from_name, to_name)` (relabels in flight; rejects no-op `from==to` and collision with existing target); `Drop(name)` (idempotent — no-op if absent so chains compose); `AddDefault(name, default_value)` (never overwrites — operator's intent is "fill in if missing", not "force this"); `Cast(name, target_dtype)` (no-silent-failure: float→int rejects 1.7 lossy round, to-bool rejects ambiguous values, every cast wraps the underlying error). `MigrationPlan(schema_name, from_version, to_version, rules)` composes rules in order — pin the order matters: Drop → Rename can't run as Rename → Drop without changing semantics. `migrate(payload, *, from_schema, to_schema, plans)` finds the matching plan and applies it; rejects schema-name mismatches (cross-schema migration is nonsense), missing plans (no silent inference), and ambiguous plans (two plans for the same versions = config bug). `validate(payload, schema)` returns a `ValidationOutcome(passed, violations, extras)` checking required-feature presence + dtype compatibility; extras (features in payload not in schema) are reported separately so a stale producer surfaces but doesn't fail the validation. Three asymmetric-but-pinned dtype rules: FLOAT accepts int (numpy interop common case where `arr[0]` may return either); INT rejects bool (True passed where INT was expected is almost certainly a bug); BOOL rejects int (5 silently becoming True is a real bug). Picked declarative rules over function-per-migration because migrations stack — a model trained on v1.2.0 served from v1.4.0 needs both v1.2→v1.3 and v1.3→v1.4 plans composed; rule lists compose naturally and the dashboard can render the schema diff by walking the rules without reading function bodies. Pure-Python (no NumPy / DB / network); frozen dataclasses safe to cache. 41 tests cover dtype matching across the bool/int/float asymmetry, schema duplicate-name rejection (corrupt config that lists `rsi_14` twice would silently drop one definition), every migration rule's apply paths (Rename relabels + no-op-on-missing-source + collision-rejection + no-op-rejection + no-mutation; Drop removes + idempotent on absent; AddDefault inserts + never-overwrites; Cast lossy-float-to-int rejection + ambiguous-bool rejection + str catch-all + missing-feature no-op + error wrapping), MigrationPlan rule-ordering pin, the migrate driver across same-version-copy + apply-matching-plan + name-mismatch / missing / ambiguous rejections, validate across required-missing-fail + optional-missing-pass + optional-with-wrong-dtype-fail + extras-listed-not-failing, and render_validation output (PASS / FAIL / violation-count / extras-section). SQL-side persistence (a `feature_schemas` table mirroring `ml_artefacts`) and the cycle-side wiring (validate before inference, migrate on schema drift detected via Wave 6.E fingerprint) deferred to a follow-up — schema layer verified in isolation first so the wiring sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 6.E — Model fingerprinting for deterministic replay** — `ml/fingerprint.py` adds the missing piece for "rerun cycle 12345 against the exact model that produced its decision". The replay snapshot already records cycle inputs (klines / indicators / sentiment); without a stable model identifier, a model file that's changed since (retrained, rebuilt, redeployed) silently produces a *different* answer on replay and the operator can't tell. `fingerprint_bytes(data, *, algorithm)` hashes raw byte streams (pickled sklearn / xgboost / torch state-dicts via `torch.save`); `fingerprint_json(payload, *, algorithm)` canonicalises a JSON-shaped artefact (slippage curve, calibration isotonic, hyperparam blob) before hashing. The canonicalisation pins three properties: `sort_keys=True` (dict insertion order can't shift the hash); `separators=(",", ":")` (no whitespace — a pretty-printer in source can't shift the hash); `ensure_ascii=False` (Unicode roundtrip preserved exactly so a future migration to UTF-8-everywhere doesn't shift hashes). `ModelFingerprint(digest_hex, algorithm, byte_count, captured_at, short_tag)` carries the full lowercase hex + a 12-char short_tag (prefix-aligned with the full hex, so the dashboard correlates against the registry without re-deriving — operator sees "model fingerprint: a3b7c9d1e2f4" in logs). `matches(other)` checks **all three** key fields (digest + algorithm + byte_count) — pin so a freak collision between truncated and full versions of the same file (matching hash on the truncated prefix but mismatched byte count) surfaces as a mismatch. Two algorithms supported: SHA-256 (default — cryptographic standard, no known collision attacks at this cost level) and BLAKE2b-256 (faster on short inputs; useful when the model byte stream is small). Anything else raises rather than silently using a default — a caller passing `"md5"` for compatibility surfaces immediately. `verify(actual, expected)` returns a `VerificationOutcome` with a four-bucket `VerificationStatus` (MATCH / HASH_MISMATCH / ALGORITHM_MISMATCH / BYTE_COUNT_MISMATCH) diagnosed in **precedence order**: algorithm first (two artefacts produced by different hashers can't be compared meaningfully), byte_count next (truncated / oversize cases get a distinct diagnosis), hash last (same size, different bytes = blob change in the middle of the file). The reason string includes both fingerprints' short tags so a Slack alert is self-contained. Halal alignment: fingerprinting is metadata only — never opens a position, never screens an asset. Mismatches during replay surface as warnings, not auto-trades — operator decides whether to halt or continue. Pure-Python (stdlib `hashlib` + `json`); no NumPy / DB / network. The hash digest is computed from the bytes / JSON the caller hands in, so the module never opens a file by itself — every IO surface in the bot is owned by its module; fingerprinting must not introduce a new one. 31 tests cover: byte fingerprint stability (same input → identical output across calls), the SHA-256 known-constant pin for `b"x"` (so a refactor of the hash path can't quietly switch algorithms), BLAKE2b producing different digests, byte_count recording, short_tag length + prefix invariant, bytes-like input acceptance (`bytes` / `bytearray` / `memoryview` all hash to the same digest), non-bytes input rejection, empty-bytes producing the published SHA-256 constant, supplied `captured_at` flowing through, unsupported-algorithm rejection path, canonical_json key-sort + whitespace-strip + Unicode-preserve + nested-structure invariance, fingerprint_json end-to-end dict-order invariance, every VerificationStatus bucket, the precedence-order pin (algorithm > byte_count > hash), the hash-mismatch vs byte-count-mismatch diagnostic separation (same-size-different-bytes is HASH_MISMATCH, not BYTE_COUNT), the freak-collision path (matching hash + algorithm but different byte_count rejected by `matches`), the render helper output (short_tag + algorithm + size + capture timestamp), and frozen-dataclass immutability on both `ModelFingerprint` and `VerificationOutcome`. Cycle-side wiring (record fingerprint in the replay snapshot at decision time; verify on replay against the registry) deferred to a follow-up — engine verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 6.A — Model registry semver + lineage + promotion policy** — `ml/registry.py` adds the policy layer on top of the existing `db/ml_artefacts.py` persistence (which keys models by `(name, version: int)` — useful for "load the latest", less useful for tracing lineage or asking "is v1.2.3 inference-compatible with v1.2.0?"). `Semver(major, minor, patch)` parses from `v1.2.3` or `1.2.3` (whitespace tolerant), totally orders via `dataclass(order=True)` (Python's tuple comparison drives `<` correctly because field order is major / minor / patch), exposes `bump_major / minor / patch` returning new instances (frozen), and `is_compatible_with` returning true iff majors match — pin the meaning: a major mismatch means feature-vector reshape, the only thing that can't be hot-swapped. Pre-release / build metadata (`+sha`, `-rc1`) deliberately omitted; the bot's models don't ship pre-release. Malformed strings raise rather than silently rounding to (0,0,0) — pin so a corrupt registry row surfaces immediately. `ModelLineage` carries parent_version (None for v1.0.0), training_run_id (operator-chosen — commit hash / retrainer timestamp / RL run ID), fitness_score, fitness_metric_name (defaults to `"sharpe"` but the metric name lives on lineage rather than the registry so different model families can use different metrics), and notes. `RegistryRecord` adds payload_kind (`"json"` for slippage / calibration; `"bytes"` for pickled sklearn / xgboost — matches existing `payload_json` vs `payload_bytes` split), size_bytes, and an `is_active` serving-traffic-now flag, with __post_init__ rejecting bad payload_kind and negative sizes. `lineage_chain(records, *, target)` walks parent pointers root → target — pin the ordering so the dashboard renders left-to-right chronologically without re-sorting. Three corrupt-registry rejections pinned in tests: missing parent (referenced but not in records — surfaces immediately rather than silently truncating); cycle (v1 → v2 → v1 — won't loop forever); duplicate versions (race-corrupted writes). `should_promote(*, candidate, incumbent, policy)` composes three checks under a `PromotionPolicy(min_fitness_uplift=0.05, require_compatible_major=True, require_lineage=True)`: (1) compatibility — major-version change blocked unless explicitly opted out (pin: major-bumps need a new dashboard tile + downstream re-test, can't sneak in); (2) lineage continuity — candidate's parent_version must equal incumbent's version (stops a sideloaded fresh-trained model short-circuiting the chain); (3) fitness uplift — candidate must exceed incumbent by ≥ `min_fitness_uplift` (default 0.05 Sharpe — high enough to filter noise on a 100-trade A/B). Cold-start handling pinned: incumbent=None + candidate has a fitness_score → promote (registry can bootstrap); incumbent=None + no fitness → reject (caller must record one); partial-bootstrap (incumbent never recorded fitness) → promote on candidate's score alone with a "incumbent has no fitness_score; promoting on candidate's …" reason line. `render_lineage` produces a CLI-friendly chain summary with ★ marker for the currently-active record, fitness-metric=value display, and "n/a" fallback for missing scores. Picked a separate module from `ml_artefacts.py` because persistence and policy have different lifecycles — a future SQL refactor (e.g. switch to S3 + manifest) doesn't ripple into the policy contract; registry is pure-Python so its tests run without Postgres, matching the rest of the Round-4 isolated-module pattern. 39 tests cover: semver parse (v-prefix optional, whitespace tolerant, malformed → ValueError on five different bad inputs), str↔parse round trip, tuple-ordering comparisons across major / minor / patch axes including the negative case, all three bump methods + frozen-instance preservation, compatibility predicate same-major True / different-major False, RegistryRecord input validation (bad payload_kind, negative size_bytes), lineage_chain across the chronological-ordering pin, root-with-no-parent (length-1 chain), name-filtering across multiple model families, missing-parent rejection, cycle detection, duplicate-version rejection, should_promote across every policy axis (cold-start with/without fitness; major-version blocked by default + relaxable; lineage continuity required by default + relaxable; fitness uplift below threshold / above threshold / negative; partial-bootstrap incumbent-without-fitness; missing candidate fitness), and render_lineage (empty chain, every-record content, ★ active marker, n/a fallback for missing fitness). SQL adapter that maps existing `ml_artefacts` rows → `RegistryRecord`s and the dashboard's lineage panel deferred to follow-ups — policy is verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 8.B — Chaos engineering harness** — `core/chaos.py` is the operational mirror of the existing market-side `crypto/stress.py`: instead of injecting adversarial market scenarios (flash crash, blow-off pump), it injects adversarial *infrastructure* scenarios — broker timeout / 5xx / malformed JSON / rate-limit, WebSocket drop, DB connection drop, LLM timeout / 500. Every fault must result in either successful recovery or a clean halt — never a hang or silent data loss. Three composable layers: (1) **Fault library** — eight `FaultKind`s mapped to sentinel exception classes all descending from a `HarnessError` base, so target callables can catch the base for generic recovery or specific subclasses for fault-specific paths. `BrokerRateLimitError` extends `BrokerHttpError` (status_code=429) so a recovery handler catching the parent automatically handles 429s. (2) **Predicates** — `always()` / `never()` / `on_call_number(n)` (stateful 1-indexed counter) / `for_label(label)` (label-scoped) plus `combine_and()` composition (empty composition falls back to `always()` rather than crashing — pinned). (3) **Evaluator** — `evaluate(scenario, target, *, deadline_seconds, expected_exceptions)` classifies into four buckets: RECOVER (returned normally), CLEAN_HALT (raised an expected exception type), HANG (exceeded deadline), CRASH (raised an unexpected type). Two semantic pins matter: (a) the operator **declares** which exception types are acceptable rather than relying on pytest's blanket "any raise is a fail" — pin so a future refactor that swallows a `MemoryError` or `RecursionError` shows up as a regression rather than masking the failure as a clean halt; (b) the watchdog reclassifies a returned-normally call that exceeded the deadline as HANG so a 10-second hang in a unit test doesn't become a 30-second hang. The default `expected_exceptions=(HarnessError,)` makes every harness fault count as a clean halt by default — operators only need to declare their *application*-side acceptable exceptions (e.g. `core.halt.HaltEngagedError`). `evaluate_all(scenarios, target_factory)` runs every scenario via `target_factory(scenario)` — pinned via test that the factory is invoked once per scenario so state can't leak between iterations. `standard_scenarios()` covers every FaultKind (regression test pinned that the suite covers `set(FaultKind)` exactly so adding a kind without a scenario fails loudly; names are unique; every scenario carries a description). `chaos_call` / `chaos_call_async` wrappers swap the target's call for a fault when the predicate matches; predicates see the label, args, and kwargs so they can switch on call shape. `render_verdicts` produces a CLI / Slack-ready text payload visually consistent with `crypto/stress.render_report` and `core/promotion_gate.render_verdict` so an operator running all three sees a familiar layout (✔ / ✘ markers, scenario name, outcome bucket, elapsed_ms, notes lines, PASS / FAIL footer). Pure-Python; no DB / network / async-loop ownership; the harness never opens a position or screens an asset — pure observability. 34 tests cover every predicate's selection logic (5 predicates including the combine_and empty-composition fallback), the fault library (every FaultKind → matching sentinel; rate-limit is BrokerHttpError subclass with status_code=429; status_code attribute on HTTP error class for switch-on-status recovery; every fault descends from HarnessError so generic catch works), the sync + async `chaos_call` wrappers (passthrough when predicate False, raise when True, predicate sees label/args/kwargs), the evaluator's four-bucket classification including the unexpected-MemoryError-is-CRASH pin, the default `expected_exceptions=(HarnessError,)` pin, the watchdog reclassifying returns-normally-but-slow as HANG, the elapsed_ms recording, `evaluate_all`'s one-target-per-scenario factory pattern + outcome aggregation (half recover, half clean-halt run), `standard_scenarios()` exhaustive coverage of FaultKind + uniqueness + descriptions, the render helper's PASS / FAIL marking + empty-list handling, the verdict's `passed` property matching the four buckets correctly, and frozen-dataclass immutability on the scenario. CLI command (`halal-trader chaos run`) and integration with the cycle's actual broker / DB / LLM call sites deferred to a follow-up — engine is verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.B — Genetic strategy generator** — `ml/strategy_ga.py` extends the existing prompt-evolution GA one level up: instead of evolving the LLM prompt text, it evolves the **strategy itself** as a combination of indicator filters (RSI bands, MACD direction requirement, BB position, volume ratio threshold), an optional regime gate (only trade when the regime label matches), and risk caps (max position pct, max simultaneous positions, min confidence). `evolve(*, fitness_fn, population_size, generations, ...)` returns a `list[GenerationReport]` and is the only operator-facing entry point. Picked a generic in-house GA over scipy / DEAP / pygmo because (a) the genome is small and the population tiny (≤50) — the framework's bookkeeping ends up larger than the algorithm; (b) every operation takes a `random.Random` so the GA is fully reproducible from a seed (frameworks that thread a global RNG break this); (c) genome bounds enforce only-long, no-leverage halal constraints (max_position_pct ≤ 0.30, no negative quantities) — a generic framework's genome wouldn't. Five primitives: `random_genome` (uniform within bounds), `crossover` (uniform two-parent — each gene independently picks parent A or B), `mutate` (per-gene Gaussian nudges + bool flips + regime resamples at the configured `rate`; `sigma` controls step size), `tournament_select` (picked over fitness-proportionate roulette because Sharpe can legitimately go negative and roulette degenerates with negative weights), `elitism` (top-K survival pinned to keep the best-found solution across generations). Three invariants pinned across every operation: (1) bounds-respect — every genome stays inside the search space (100-iteration stress test on full-rate mutation pins this); (2) `rsi_buy_max < rsi_sell_min` band ordering — a genome where buy_max ≥ sell_min would never produce sells, so `_ensure_band` swaps if needed and is invoked from `random_genome`, `crossover`, *and* `mutate`; (3) seed-determinism — same seed + same fitness fn → same final genome (regression test pinned at the engine level). Fitness is fully caller-supplied; the engine is mechanic, not application — doesn't know what BUY looks like, doesn't call brokers, doesn't read backtests. The caller hands over `fitness_fn(StrategyGenome) → float` and the GA selects, crosses over, mutates, iterates. `seed_population` lets operators inject hand-tuned genomes (e.g. the live prompt's current settings) so the GA can build off a known-good start rather than rolling fresh randoms; anything beyond `population_size` is ignored, anything below is padded with random genomes. `GenomeBounds` is operator-tweakable so the GA can be locked to a sub-search — e.g. "only evolve indicator filters, fix regime_gate=uptrend" — by tightening individual range tuples. Halal alignment: bounds default to long-only / no-leverage (max_position_pct in (0, 0.30] by default, max_simultaneous_positions integer in [1, 10]). Pure-Python (no NumPy / SciPy / DB / async); the fitness call is the only blocking point and the caller is responsible for parallel backtests. 27 tests cover bounds-respect on random + mutate, the band-ordering invariant including the cross-violation case (parent A buy_max=29 + parent B sell_min=28 must still produce a child with buy < sell), seed-determinism on every primitive (same seed → same output across `random_genome` / `crossover` / `mutate` / `evolve`), the `mutate(rate=0)` no-op pin, regime-gate lockdown via custom bounds (a `("uptrend",)`-only search must never produce a different gate after 20 mutations), tournament selection logic + population-smaller-than-tournament-size graceful handling + empty-population + zero-size validation, elitism descending order + zero-K, the `evolve` driver's N-generations → N+1-reports off-by-one pin, the monotonic-non-decreasing-best-fitness invariant under elitism, an end-to-end convergence test against a peaked synthetic fitness landscape (final-gen best materially exceeds initial-gen best and lands within 0.5 of the known optimum), seeded-population injection (custom genome appears in generation 0) + padding (one seed gene + 9 random fills the population_size=10), input-validation rejections (non-positive population_size / generations / elite_count > population_size), the `StrategyGenome.to_dict` round-trip across every field, and frozen-dataclass immutability on the genome. Auto-promotion gate (chain the GA's best through `PromotionThresholds` from Wave 4.F after 100+ paper trades cross a Sharpe threshold) and the dashboard's live-evolution view deferred to follow-ups; engine verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.D — Cross-asset macro-regime fusion engine** — `core/cross_asset_signal.py` composes a single macro-regime signal from five reference instruments (VIX / DXY / US 10y + 2y yield + curve / gold / sector breadth) following the textbook practitioner heuristic from Faber's *Tactical Asset Allocation* and Hilpisch's *Quantitative Investing*: risk-off when fear gauges spike + curve inverts + breadth weakens; risk-on when DXY softens + breadth broadens + gold stays calm; everything else = neutral. `fuse(snapshot, *, thresholds)` returns a `MacroRegimeSignal(regime, confidence, risk_bias, reasons, measured_factor_count, summary)`. Each per-factor scorer emits a `MacroSignalReason` with a signed score (positive = risk-off, negative = risk-on) and a one-line detail string the dashboard can display verbatim. Confidence is the **geometric mean** of coverage (fraction of factors measured) and agreement (how unanimous the measured factors are) — pinned so a 2-of-5 partial feed with perfect agreement lands at ~0.45 confidence, suspiciously high for that little data; `risk_bias ∈ [-1, 1]` is scaled by confidence so a thin feed exerts less pull on the strategy. Picked a hand-rolled deterministic rule over an LLM call because the macro signal must be ≤1ms in the cycle hot path *and* operators want regression-tested mappings from known snapshots to known signals; LLM here adds latency, cost, and non-determinism for no edge over published practitioner rules. Cold-start safety: empty snapshot → NEUTRAL with zero confidence and zero risk_bias, so a cold-start cycle (data feeds not yet wired) doesn't tilt the strategy in either direction — strategies that interpret NEUTRAL as "no macro tilt, go on per-pair signal alone" stay correct. Halal alignment baked into the design: the signal can downsize a high-conviction LLM buy into a risk-off regime or raise the entry bar during a neutral-but-weakening period, but it never opens a new position by itself and never shorts — that's the strategy's domain.
