Pure-Python (no NumPy / scipy / DB / async); operates on a single `MacroContextSnapshot` dataclass with all fields nullable so a partial feed (e.g. VIX measured but DXY missing) lowers confidence rather than crashing. Three frozen dataclasses (snapshot / signal / reason) plus a `MacroThresholds` config bundle the operator can tighten or loosen. `render_signal` produces a CLI / Slack-ready emoji-prefixed (🔴 risk-off / 🟡 neutral / 🟢 risk-on) text payload visually consistent with the other Round-4 render helpers. 37 tests cover: cold-start zero-data invariant, every per-factor scorer's threshold band (VIX extreme ≥35 → +2; high ≥25 → +1; spike change ≥20% adds +0.5; calm <17.5 → -0.5; DXY strong strengthening / weakening / range; yield curve inverted vs normal vs partial-data skip; large 10y bps move both directions; gold rally vs dump asymmetry where rally signal is stronger than dump; breadth strong / weak / mid bands), the classic risk-off and risk-on combos hitting the right regime + risk_bias direction, mixed-signal cancellation → NEUTRAL, threshold tightening flowing through to regime decisions, the confidence formula's coverage × agreement geometric-mean shape (1-of-5 with full agreement → ~0.45; full coverage with full agreement → >0.9; full coverage with split factors → <0.85), the risk_bias [-1, 1] clamp invariant under extreme inputs, the risk_bias scaling with confidence (full data signal exerts more pull than partial data signal of equal raw direction), the typed `reasons` list, the summary string format with `N/5 factors` coverage marker, the frozen-dataclass immutability, and the `render_signal` emoji + Contributing-factors section + omission-when-no-factors output across all three regimes. Concrete data feeds (FRED for yields, Yahoo / Alpaca for VIX / DXY / gold, computed sector breadth from sector-ETF holdings) and the per-cycle hook that calls `fuse` and downsizes the strategy plan deferred to a follow-up — engine is verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 5.A — Cycle stage-timeline aggregator** — `core/cycle_timeline.py` is the off-line / replay layer over the existing live `cycle.stage.start` / `cycle.stage.end` bus events. `build_timeline(events)` takes a flat list of `StageEvent`s and returns a `CycleTimeline` with per-stage `StageRun`s, top-N bottlenecks ranked by descending duration, total wall-clock duration, error and open-stage counts, plus a pre-rendered markdown body suitable for the dashboard's "click any historical cycle, see a Gantt-shaped timeline" tile or CLI output. Three semantic pins matter: (1) **duration prefers `elapsed_ms` over wall-clock** — the pipeline measures it with `time.monotonic()` and that's the canonical source; wall-clock derivation is a fallback for legacy / partial replay rows because bus-publish delay can skew it by a few ms; pin so a refactor that swaps the order doesn't silently introduce noise; (2) **a START without a matching END is reported as `status="open"`** rather than dropped — when a cycle is killed mid-stage X, the operator wants to see *that* X is the killer, and silently dropping it would mask the diagnosis; (3) **an orphan END synthesises a zero-wall-clock run** with the `elapsed_ms` duration — the live bus occasionally drops a START under backpressure but the END always carries elapsed_ms, so we recover what we can rather than lose the stage. Bottleneck ranking excludes open stages (unknown duration mustn't fake a 0ms entry) and a regression-test pin guards `pct_of_total` summing ≤ 100% against the wall-clock total (the percentages can sum below 100% if stages overlapped or there were inter-stage gaps; can never exceed). Defensive: two consecutive STARTs for the same name without an end in between flushes the first as `open` so it's not silently overwritten by the second. `StageEvent.from_bus_payload(topic, payload, *, at)` adapts the live bus's loose-dict payload to the typed event; an unrecognised topic raises immediately so a wiring bug surfaces rather than silently producing an empty timeline. The adapter strips canonical fields (`name`, `elapsed_ms`, `error`) from the `attrs` slice so downstream attrs don't carry redundant copies. Pure-Python; no DB, no async, no NumPy — operates entirely on the `StageEvent` dataclass. Frozen dataclasses (StageEvent / StageRun / StageBottleneck / CycleTimeline) safe to cache for the dashboard tile. Markdown render uses ✔ / ✘ / · markers per status, formats durations as `Nms` below 1 second and `N.NNs` above, includes a `## Top stages by duration` table with stage / duration / pct columns, a `## Stage-by-stage` list with error and "no end event recorded" annotations, and a `Health:` line that only appears when error_count or open_count > 0 (clean cycles get a clean output). 28 tests cover empty input → empty timeline (dashboard "no data yet" state), the basic single-stage and multi-stage pairing with order preservation, the wall-clock total spanning first-start to last-end, the duration source preference in both directions (elapsed_ms wins over wall-clock; wall-clock fallback when elapsed_ms missing), the error-status propagation with error string, the open-stage and orphan-end and duplicate-start recovery paths, the bottleneck ranking + top-5 cap + open-stage exclusion + pct-of-total sanity, the `from_bus_payload` adapter (start/end topic detection, attr stripping, unknown-topic rejection), the markdown sections (total format with both ms and seconds variants, bottleneck table, error markers, open-stage annotation, Health line presence + omission, attrs pass-through to render), and the frozen-dataclass immutability across all four output types. WebSocket adapter (subscribe to the bus + buffer events per cycle_id + emit a CycleTimeline on cycle.complete) and the dashboard's React-side Gantt tile deferred to a follow-up — aggregator is verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.F — Promote-to-live gate** — `core/promotion_gate.py` ships the missing piece on top of the existing `crypto/walkforward.py`: a checked ruleset that decides "does this strategy clear the bar for live trading?". `evaluate_promotion(walk_forward, *, thresholds, monte_carlo, ab_comparison)` returns a `PromotionVerdict(passed, checks, failures, warnings)` composing three already-shipped sources — `WalkForwardReport` (existing), `MonteCarloReport` (existing), `ABComparison` (Round-4 Wave 5.B). Picked a separate module rather than extending `walkforward.py` because thresholds are *operator policy*, not backtest mechanics — keeping them out of the report dataclass means a future walkforward-internals refactor can't accidentally tighten / loosen the live-trading bar. Six walk-forward checks always run (avg return ≥ floor, Sharpe ≥ 0.5, win rate ≥ 0.40, fold_count ≥ 5, worst-fold drawdown ≤ 20%, total trades ≥ 50). Two Monte Carlo checks layer on when supplied (p95 drawdown ≤ 30%, ≥ 100 resamples). One opt-in A/B check rejects significant-but-worse deltas vs the live baseline. Three semantic pins worth calling out: (1) the drawdown check uses the **worst** fold, not the mean — a single fold with a 30% trough must kill the promotion even if averages look fine, because a 30% drawdown realised is a 30% drawdown realised; (2) when an `actual` value is `None` (data not measured), the check fails with `"... (not measured — data missing)"` — the gate must not let unmeasured fields silently pass; (3) the A/B "significant-but-worse" branch rejects even though the difference is statistically real — operators want no regressions, period. The gate is **additive**: a regression test pins that adding Monte Carlo or A/B inputs can only ever produce more failures, never soften an existing failure. Each failed check carries a one-line `remediation` hint so the operator knows what to fix, not just that it failed (e.g. "Worst-fold drawdown exceeds the cap. Tighten SL or size down — a single bad fold of this depth is a kill"). Soft warning ladder: fold_count just above the floor (≥ floor, < floor + 2) emits a warning but still passes. `render_verdict` produces a CLI / Slack-ready text payload visually consistent with `crypto/stress.render_report` so an operator running both sees a familiar shape. 33 tests cover every check's pass / fail / unmeasured paths, the worst-fold-not-mean-drawdown invariant on a hand-rolled `[0.05, 0.05, 0.05, 0.05, 0.05, 0.30]` fold list, the additive-composition contract on both directions (good MC keeps a passing WF passing; bad MC turns a passing WF into a failing one), the A/B opt-in's six edge cases (skipped by default; required-but-missing fails with the clear hint; significant-and-better passes; significant-but-worse rejects with regression-aware remediation; non-significant rejects with noise-aware remediation; None p-value rejects on small-sample / no-scipy combinations), threshold customisation in both directions (tightening rejects a default-passing strategy; loosening accepts a default-failing one), the field-name pinning against the underlying `MonteCarloReport.max_drawdown_pct_p95` / `runs` (so a refactor of either side surfaces immediately as a NameError, not a silent always-pass via `getattr`'s None fallback), the immutability of the verdict + check, and the render helper's PASS / FAIL / remediation arrow / warnings / n/a-on-unmeasured output. CLI command and dashboard tile deferred to a follow-up — gate is verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 5.H — Per-position story aggregator** — `core/position_story.py` composes the full per-position story the dashboard's detail panel will render: entry rationale + entry indicator vector + indicator timeline + price timeline + news events. `build_story(PositionStoryInput)` returns a `PositionStory` carrying both the structured fields (so the API can JSON-serialise it) and a pre-rendered markdown narrative (so the notifier doesn't have to re-walk the structure). Picked an aggregator-only design (no SQL inside) because the data already exists across `crypto_trades`, `indicator_snapshots`, news feeds, kline ticks, and `llm_decisions` — duplicating retrieval inside a "story service" would just create a fragile second copy; the aggregator's job is presentation, not retrieval. Three computed fields matter: the unrealized-P&L curve (one `PnlPoint` per price observation with pct + USD), the per-indicator delta between entry and latest snapshot, and the bullish / bearish / total news counts. Per-indicator delta rule pinned: skip fields measured on *neither* side (fewer rows beats a wall of n/a), but emit a partial row with `delta=None` when one side is missing (operator wants "we measured this once" to be visible). News classification pinned: score > 0 → bullish, score < 0 → bearish, score == 0 → neither — a neutral headline must not double-count. Markdown sections: header line with green / red emoji based on current P&L; Entry / Current / Risk levels lines (SL + TP + trailing-stop pct only render when set); LLM confidence + prompt version line (the prompt-version SHA is the audit-trail key); "Why we entered" section that truncates at 400 chars; indicator-drift table; news section ordered most-recent-first capped at 5 with ▲ / ▼ markers and optional URL link; P&L track section calling out trough / peak / latest. Defensive pins: empty price timeline → no current P&L + dashboard "no data yet" renders cleanly; zero / negative entry price → empty P&L curve (corrupt row can't NaN-out the dashboard); legacy positions without `llm_reasoning` skip the "Why we entered" section without crashing the rest of the render. Pure-Python; no NumPy, no DB, no async — safe to call from any thread, notifier callback, or HTTP handler. Frozen dataclasses safe to cache. 32 tests cover P&L curve arithmetic + the negative / zero-entry / empty edges, the indicator-delta rules across the four (entry / latest) presence combinations, the news-classification pin including the neutral-score case, the markdown content (pair / side / emoji / rationale section + truncation / indicator-drift table / news section with counts and most-recent-first ordering / risk levels rendered only when set / trailing-stop label / prompt-version SHA inclusion / P&L track with trough+peak+latest), the cold-start "just opened, no data" case (must still render), the legacy-position-without-rationale case, the long-lived-position smoke test (168 hourly ticks → P&L curve length matches), and the frozen-dataclass immutability. SQL fan-in (subscribe to the relevant tables for a given pair and assemble the `PositionStoryInput`) deferred to a follow-up — aggregator is verified in isolation first so the wiring layer sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 9.B — Strategy author's guide** — `docs/STRATEGY_AUTHORING.md` is a single-page operator guide structured around the project's "strategy chooses, executor enforces" contract. Sections in order: what a strategy *is* in this codebase (a method on a class that turns per-cycle data into a `CryptoTradingPlan` / `TradingPlan`); the `BaseStrategy` override points (`_build_prompts` + `_validate_plan`) and what the base class owns (LLM call → JSON parse → schema validation → one repair-instruction retry on failure → record decision row → return); the schema (CryptoTradingPlan with per-pair decisions carrying action / confidence / quantity / reasoning); the prompt-version registry's stable-SHA invariant (`PromptVersion` hashes the template body, every byte change → version change → audit trail catches the edit), and why this matters in production (A/B comparator + prompt-evolution GA both key on it); the per-symbol halal-compliance boundary (strategy receives already-screened pairs from `screener.get_halal_pairs()`; never call a screener / broker from inside `analyze` because that path bypasses cache + audit trail); the four test harnesses with concrete code (1: unit-test pattern with `AsyncMock` on `LLMBackend`; 2: stress harness with the 8 canned scenarios from `crypto/stress.py` + their grader contracts including the three Round-4 7.B additions; 3: `core/scenario_sim.py` for projecting open positions through a kline path; 4: `core/ab_compare.compare(returns)` with a Welch's p < 0.05 promotion gate); a fully-worked pure-Python RSI mean-reversion example with the strategy class, five unit tests including the "don't trade on missing data" safety pin, how to wrap it for the stress harness, and the backtest CLI invocation; a 7-item promotion checklist (unit tests pass, stress severity < 0.5 across all 8, backtest Sharpe > 0.5 + profit factor > 1.2, lint + format + type clean, halal boundary respected, prompt versioned); and a "common pitfalls" section (don't open files inside `analyze` — blocks the loop; don't catch LLM exceptions — base already retries-then-fails-soft; don't mutate input lists; don't introduce un-seeded randomness — kills A/B reproducibility; don't flip the testnet flags). README's "In a hurry?" callout gains a parallel pointer to the new guide so first-time contributors find it immediately. The doc deliberately cross-links every Round-4 wave the author will *use* (5.B A/B comparator, 5.F scenario simulator, 7.B stress harness extensions, 2.C scholar profiles, 4.G HRP, 4.I equity anomaly, 5.D lessons-learned), so the guide doubles as a tour of the recently-landed research toolkit. Pure docs — no code change beyond the README pointer.
* **Round-4 Wave 2.D — Purification disbursement scheduler + receipts** — `halal/purification_schedule.py` adds the periodic-disbursement layer on top of the existing per-trade `PurificationEntry` ledger. `schedule_disbursements(entries, *, period=QUARTERLY, include_paid=False, charity=None)` groups entries into `MONTHLY` / `QUARTERLY` / `YEARLY` UTC calendar buckets and returns a chronologically-ordered list of `DisbursementReceipt`s. Each receipt carries the period slug (`"2026-Q1"`, `"2026-03"`, `"2026"` — pinned formats so the audit-trail key is stable across machines and locales, and doubles as a future PDF filename), the UTC half-open `[starts_at, ends_at)` bounds, total USD, entry count, a per-symbol `SymbolBreakdown` sorted by descending USD (operator's eye lands on concentration first — "80% of this quarter is from one holding"), the immutable list of underlying entries, and a pre-rendered markdown body suitable for emailing the operator. `upcoming_due(entries, *, now, period)` returns the receipt for the *current* period — drives a dashboard tile that says "this quarter so far you owe $X across N holdings". Three semantic pins matter: (1) `include_paid` defaults to **False** because the operator's primary use case is "what's still due", and a backfill / audit pass passes `True` for the full historical picture; (2) tz-naive `received_at` timestamps are coerced to UTC rather than crashing — legacy ledger rows might be naive, and downstream layers all store tz-aware UTC, so the coercion is the right tolerance; (3) the scheduler **never auto-marks entries paid** — that's a one-way audit-trail commitment that needs explicit human consent. The markdown receipt itself reminds the operator: "Mark each entry paid in the ledger after disbursement — the scheduler does not auto-mark." A test pin guards that the entries handed in keep their `paid_at == None` after the scheduler runs, so a future refactor that "helpfully" mutates entries by reference would fail loudly. Pure-Python (Decimal-precise USD math via the existing `domain.money` helpers, no NumPy / DB / network); the caller fetches entries from the ledger, hands them in, gets back receipts. Receipt is a frozen dataclass safe to cache. 35 tests cover every cadence's slug format (Jan→Q1, April→Q2, December→Q4, and the zero-padded `2026-03`), multi-period bucketing with chronological ordering of receipts (pinned against accidental dict-order), the naive-tz tolerance, the paid / outstanding filter contract (default + opt-in + empty-input edges), USD totals on the receipt, per-symbol aggregation across multiple entries on the same symbol, the descending-USD breakdown sort, the half-open `[starts, ends)` period bounds (April 1 → July 1 for Q2; December → next-year January 1; Q4 wraps the year), the no-mutation invariant on the ledger, the markdown body content (label, total, charity line shown only when supplied, breakdown table with `| AAPL |` row, audit-trail reminder pinned so it can't quietly drop out of the template), the `is_empty` property on the receipt, the `upcoming_due` returning `None` outside the active period and the current period's receipt inside it, the default-`now` fallback path, the immutability invariant, and the unknown-period rejection (forging an unrecognised enum value to hit the catch-all branch). PDF rendering, email pipeline (sender + DKIM signing + attachment), and charity-API integration (Islamic Relief / Penny Appeal / Zakat Foundation direct disbursement) deferred to a follow-up — scheduler + receipts verified in isolation first so the email layer sees a stable contract to wire onto.
* **Round-4 Wave 2.C — Per-scholar policy profile registry** — `halal/scholar_profiles.py` ships named scholar / methodology profiles that adjust the consensus parameters operators take responsibility for. Three built-in profiles cover the mainstream methodologies: `AAOIFI_DEFAULT` (debt 30% / non-permissible income 5% / cash-and-receivables 33%, STRICT consensus — the published international default); `TAQI_USMANI` (stricter — debt 25% / non-permissible income 3%, STRICT, weights musaffa + idealratings 1.5× under WEIGHTED); `DELORENZO_DJIM` (DJIM-era — debt 33%, MAJORITY consensus). `ScholarProfile` is a frozen dataclass bundling three concerns the registry cleanly serialises: `provider_weights` for the WEIGHTED consensus path (some scholars trust certain providers more on borderline cases), threshold overrides for the three financial ratios used by every mainstream screen (debt-to-market-cap / non-permissible-income / cash-and-receivables), and the `default_policy` so the profile choice also picks the resolution rule. Picked a registry over a class hierarchy because profiles are *data*, not behaviour — new profiles ship as dataclass literals rather than subclasses, dashboard / audit can serialise them as plain JSON, and the shape mirrors what we'd persist in a `ScholarProfile` table later if profiles need to be operator-editable at runtime. Five public functions: `evaluate_thresholds(profile, ratios…)` returns `(passed, violations)` and *skips* missing inputs (a None value is "not measured", not "passes" — pin so a partial filing can't silently approve); `apply_profile_weights(profile, opinions)` returns a new list of frozen opinions with weights re-mapped without mutating the input; `consensus_with_profile(profile, opinions, *, policy=None)` is the one-shot caller — picks the profile's default policy unless the caller overrides, and only re-weights under WEIGHTED (avoids wasted work under STRICT / MAJORITY which ignore weights anyway); `get_profile(name)` is case-insensitive and raises with the candidate list on a typo (the typo'd config must surface immediately, not degrade silently to a default); `register_profile(p)` lets operators ship custom profiles without forking the codebase. `profile_to_dict` produces an audit-trail-ready JSON-friendly dict where the policy is a plain string (the enum doesn't survive `json.dumps`) and the weights are a plain dict. 26 tests cover the AAOIFI 30/5/33 defaults (pinned so a copy-paste error in a new profile can't mutate the global default), the relative-strictness invariants (Taqi Usmani's debt cap < AAOIFI's, his income cap < AAOIFI's), the methodology-divergence pin (DeLorenzo defaults to MAJORITY not STRICT), the threshold evaluator's per-ratio caps + missing-input skip + multiple-violations-at-once cases, the cross-profile differentiation case (28% debt passes AAOIFI but fails Taqi Usmani), the no-mutation invariant on the re-weight helper, the decision/criteria pass-through on re-weight, the one-shot helper's profile-default-policy + caller-override + re-weight-only-under-WEIGHTED contracts, the registry's case-insensitive lookup + typo → KeyError-with-list rejection + register-then-find round trip, and the JSON-friendly shape (policy is a string, weights are a plain dict, rulings_doc pointer present). CLI flag (`halal-trader --scholar=…`) and audit-row plumbing (record which profile gated each trade) deferred to a follow-up — registry verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 2.B — Multi-source halal consensus aggregator** — `halal/consensus.py` generalises the existing two-source `halal/corroborate.py` (binary, N=2) to N providers and the three-state `halal | doubtful | not_halal` decision that `HalalScreening` audit rows already record. `consensus(opinions, *, policy=STRICT)` returns a `ConsensusDecision(decision, policy, opinions, reason, dissenters)`. Three resolution policies, all sharing a "more-conservative-wins" tiebreak (`not_halal > doubtful > halal`): `STRICT` (default — any `not_halal` rejects; any `doubtful` without a `not_halal` yields `doubtful`; only unanimous `halal` yields `halal`), `MAJORITY` (most-common-decision wins), `WEIGHTED` (per-opinion `weight` field — sums per decision, largest wins). Picked STRICT as the default because the "any provider rejecting → reject" rule is the safest interpretation when scholars themselves can disagree on edge cases — operators who explicitly opt into MAJORITY / WEIGHTED take responsibility for the looser stance and can record their reasoning in the audit trail. Two safety semantics pinned: empty input returns `DOUBTFUL` (no-opinions = unattested = refuse — caller doesn't have to guard separately, and "fail open" is a class of bug we don't want), and negative weights clamp to 0 (a buggy config can't silently invert a contribution). `ScreeningOpinion` accepts the decision either as the `Decision` enum *or* as a string so a JSON-loaded `HalalScreening` row feeds in directly without conversion friction; an unknown string (`"haalal"`) raises immediately rather than degrading. Module is its own file rather than an extension of `corroborate.py` because corroborate's binary public shape is stable and adopted; consensus operates on opinion dataclasses rather than the screener Protocols, which makes it independently testable without async / network mocks (just feed it `[ScreeningOpinion(…)]`) and lets a future SQL-side aggregator pull cached opinions out of `HalalScreening` rows without re-querying providers. Result is a frozen dataclass safe to cache, preserves input order so audit replay is deterministic, and carries an operator-readable `reason` string suitable for the dashboard compliance tile or a notifier payload (e.g. `"strict: musaffa, idealratings flagged not_halal — rejecting"`). 23 tests cover every policy branch (STRICT precedence ladder, MAJORITY tiebreak with two-way *and* three-way ties, WEIGHTED clamp-and-sum, weighted-tiebreak-on-equal-sums), the empty-input contract, dissenter tracking (sources that disagree with the resolved decision), the string ↔ enum coercion path (including the typo → ValueError rejection case), the frozen-dataclass immutability invariant, the input-order preservation, and the reason-string content (sources are named, scores appear, "weighted" label appears in the weighted path). Concrete provider adapters (IdealRatings, Musaffa, Wahed Invest) deferred to a follow-up — aggregator is verified in isolation first so the wiring sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 5.F — Scenario simulator (core)** — `core/scenario_sim.py` answers "what happens to my open positions if X?". `simulate(positions, klines)` walks each `SimulatedPosition` (pair / quantity / entry_price / stop_loss / take_profit / optional trailing_stop_pct) through a kline path and returns a `ScenarioReport` with per-position `PositionProjection`s + aggregate portfolio P&L and worst-case drawdown. The simulator is symbol-agnostic (caller maps live `CryptoTrade` rows into the dataclass shape — keeps the simulator free of DB / domain imports) and pure-Python deterministic (test can pin both fill price and trough exactly). Three semantic pins matter: (1) SL/TP fills check the bar's *high/low* not close, matching the real position monitor's wick-fill semantic — a wick that pierces the SL fills the order even if the close recovers; (2) when both SL and TP could fire in the same bar (volatile gap bar), SL wins — worst-case execution is the safer projection for an operator deciding whether to de-risk; (3) trailing-stop ratchet is applied at end-of-bar, not mid-bar — pin matches `core/sl_tp.py`'s "trail observed at end of bar, fired next bar" semantic, and the alternative same-bar update produces a phantom-fill bug where a single bar's high ratchets the SL inside the very bar that recovers from it (caught by `test_trailing_stop_does_not_fire_if_bar_holds_above_trail`). The trailing-stop fill emits `fill_reason="trailing_stop"` (not `"stop_loss"`) so dashboards can distinguish the two close paths. `render_report` produces a CLI / Slack-ready text payload visually consistent with `crypto/stress.render_report` (`==Scenario projection==` header, portfolio summary line with `+/-$N.NN (+/-N.NN%)`, per-position OPEN / CLOSED labelling). 20 tests cover: empty positions / empty klines edges, SL fires on wick + on subsequent bar (proves the index advances), TP fires on wick, SL-wins-on-tie invariant on a gap bar with both bands inside the H-L range, trailing ratchet fires next bar at the expected price (104.5 from 110×0.95), trailing doesn't fire when bar holds above trail, trailing combines correctly with TP (TP 120 fires before trail kicks in), min/max equity track lowest bar.low / highest bar.high until fill, portfolio aggregation arithmetic (P&L = end - start, pct = pnl / start), portfolio drawdown sums position troughs, end-to-end runs against the existing `flash_crash_klines` + `gap_down_klines` generators (verifying simulator + stress modules interop), `render_report` includes Portfolio + drawdown lines, CLOSED label on filled positions and OPEN on survivors, fill_bar_index advances correctly across multi-bar safe walks, and frozen-dataclass immutability so a downstream consumer can safely cache a projection. Dashboard button + CLI command deferred to a follow-up.
* **Round-4 Wave 5.D — Lessons-learned card renderer** — `core/lessons_card.py` is a deterministic, pure-Python post-mortem that fires when a trade closes — `render(LessonCardInput)` → `LessonCard`. Built without any LLM call so the dashboard close-queue isn't bottlenecked behind a model round-trip; the LLM can still be layered on top later as a richer "expert commentary" field. Heuristic classifier produces six verdicts: `winner_thesis_intact` (won, calm indicators), `winner_lucky` (won despite RSI ≥ 70 or BB ≥ 0.85 at entry — caught a top, got bailed), `loser_thesis_invalidated` (lost; RSI delta > 15 or MACD delta > 0.005 — regime changed), `loser_noise` (lost; indicators barely moved — random walk), `winner` / `loser` fallbacks for legacy rows without exit snapshots, plus `unknown` when `return_pct` is null. Six lesson heuristics emit 0–3 one-sentence operator nudges (cap pinned so future additions can't bury the operator in text): high-confidence loss with no regime change, extended-entry win, stop-loss on overbought entry, trailing-stop winner, low-volume loser, high-volume winner. Each lesson is keyed off a verifiable input (RSI value, exit reason, vol ratio) so the operator can disagree quickly if the heuristic misfired. Output is a `LessonCard` with a `markdown` field pre-rendered for the Slack / Discord notifiers (green / red emoji, truncated rationale capped at ~200 chars below the Discord 2000-char limit, indicator summary line, lesson bullets) — saves the notifiers walking the structure twice. Pure dataclasses; no NumPy / scipy / DB. 26 tests cover every classifier branch (winner_lucky on RSI≥70 *and* BB upper alternates), each lesson heuristic firing in isolation, the lessons-≤-3 cap on a "fires everything" input, the markdown contract (pair / verdict / emoji / rationale truncation / lesson bullets), the indicator-dict shape (always all five keys with None for missing), and the partial-input degradation paths (legacy trades without exit snapshots still produce a useful winner / loser card). SQL adapter (subscribe to the close-event bus and persist cards) and the optional LLM commentary layer deferred to follow-ups; renderer verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 7.B — Stress harness extensions** — `crypto/stress.py` gains four new generators that map to the failure modes the existing flash-crash / pump / gap / illiquid-drift / sustained-downtrend suite didn't cover. `regime_shift_klines` walks calmly for `n_calm` bars, then jumps to ~15× volatility for `n_turbulent` bars — catches strategies that keep their fixed sizing through a vol regime change. `volatility_explosion_klines` produces a sustained high-vol burst with a gentle mean-revert pull so the bar-to-bar moves are huge but the cumulative drift stays roughly zero — catches strategies that mistake range for trend. `liquidity_crunch_klines` collapses volume to ~5% of normal and inflates each bar's H-L range to ~3× its body — the kline-level approximation of a wide bid-ask spread (Kline has no spread field, so we approximate via wide candles + low volume). `correlated_pair_klines` returns two synced kline streams whose correlation drops at a configurable break-point, with the standard ρ-mix shock construction (`shock = √ρ·common + √(1−ρ)·idio`) — lets multi-pair strategies be tested against correlation breakdown without real data. Three new graders (`_grade_regime_shift`, `_grade_volatility_explosion`, `_grade_liquidity_crunch`) wired into `_GRADERS` and three new entries in `standard_scenarios()` so the default suite now covers eight failure modes — every prompt/model promotion runs the eight before promote-to-live. 23 new tests in `test_stress_round4.py` cover: kline counts match arg specs, structural promises (post-shift std > pre-shift × 5, burst-section moves > pre-section × 5, average H-L/body ratio > 3, average volume ≈ 5.0), seed determinism (pinned so a regression looks like a regression and not noise), correlation ladder pre vs post breakdown, predicate validation (rejects ρ outside [-1, 1] and out-of-range break index), grader pass/fail on no-op vs high-confidence plans, and an invariant that every scenario in `standard_scenarios()` has a registered grader (so a future addition can't silently "pass" by missing one). All 41 stress-related tests pass — no regression in the existing suite.
* **Round-4 Wave 7.C — Counterfactual trade analyzer (core)** — `core/counterfactual.py` answers "what would equity have been if I'd skipped every trade matching X?" without leaving the cycle's data plane. `analyze_counterfactual(trades, skip_predicate, *, starting_equity=1.0)` returns a `CounterfactualReport` with side-by-side `CohortStats` blocks (reusing the A/B comparator's `cohort_stats`, so Sharpe / drawdown / profit-factor stay numerically consistent across the dashboard's research views), length-matched equity curves for both paths (counterfactual flatlines across skipped trades — pinned as the dashboard plotting convention so the two curves are directly comparable on the same time axis), `skipped_count` for an operator gut-check, and a signed `return_uplift` so the direction-of-improvement is obvious without re-deriving. Picked a predicate-callable API over a DSL because operators already think in SQL-shaped filters and Python lambdas match that mental model with no parser to maintain. Three predicate factories ship: `by_symbol(s)` (handles both `Trade.symbol` and `CryptoTrade.pair`, case-insensitive); `by_regime(r)` (lower-case match against `regime` field); `by_loss_streak(n)` (stateful closure that starts skipping after `n` consecutive losses, resetting on a win — pinned independent per factory call so concurrent analyses don't cross-contaminate streak state). Row extractor tolerates dict-shaped *and* attribute-shaped rows (Trade / CryptoTrade pydantic objects work without conversion). Legacy rows missing `return_pct` are silently dropped. Predicate exceptions are caught and treated as "do not skip" so a buggy predicate can't kill the operator's research session — soft failure was the explicit design goal. Pure NumPy + dataclass; no scipy. 31 tests cover the row-extractor tolerance (dict / attribute / missing / non-numeric / non-finite), the curve-flatlines-on-skip plotting convention, the kept-trades-only stats invariant (held-flat zeros mustn't distort win-rate), the uplift-sign-matches-direction sanity (winner-skip → negative uplift, loser-skip → positive), every predicate factory edge case (case-insensitivity, missing fields, attribute fallback, streak count-then-act semantic, streak reset on win, factory independence so concurrent runs don't share state), an end-to-end realistic "drop DOGE makes the portfolio better" run on attribute-shaped rows, plus the input-validation edges (non-positive starting equity, empty trades). SQL plumbing — a `/api/research/counterfactual` route that runs the predicate against the live trade ledger — is deferred to a follow-up; analyzer is verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.I — Equity-curve anomaly detector (core)** — `ml/equity_anomaly.py` is the mirror of the existing market-side `ml/anomaly.py`: instead of flagging weird *market* state, it flags weird *bot* state. Two entry points: `detect_return_anomaly(returns)` z-scores the last per-trade return against the prior window; `detect_drawdown_anomaly(curve)` z-scores the current peak-to-trough drawdown against the historical drawdown distribution on the same curve. Both return an `EquityAnomalyReport` with `z_score / severity / direction / window_size / window_mean / window_std / last_value / recommendation` — severity bands at |z| ≥ 2 (warn) and |z| ≥ 3 (alert), direction labels for UI rendering, and a one-line operator-readable nudge suitable for a Telegram / Slack / Discord notifier. Why two functions: drawdown is path-dependent (depends on the running max) while per-trade returns are not, so they surface different anomalies — a string of small losses won't trip the return detector but can drive a multi-week trough that the drawdown detector catches. The drawdown side suppresses positive-tail alerts (drawdown is bounded above by 0, so a "hot" deviation isn't meaningful). Cold-start guard: below `min_window` (default 30) the detector returns `severity = "normal"` rather than firing on a noisy 5-sample baseline — false alerts on cold-start were the failure mode that killed the predecessor's adoption. NaN / inf entries are stripped; non-positive equity values (account blew up) fall back to `normal` instead of NaN-ing out. `equity_curve_from_returns(rs, starting=…)` is the convenience builder. Pure NumPy + `math.erf`; no scipy / sklearn dependency, so the module imports without the `[ml]` extra. 26 tests cover the cold-start "don't false-alert" semantic, every severity band, both directions, the bounded-drawdown invariant, the zero-std baseline degenerate case (mustn't blow up to ±∞), threshold validation, and an end-to-end round trip simulating a steady-bleed regime change that should fire the drawdown detector. Auto-halt + notifier wiring (route an `alert` report through `core/halt.engage_halt(reason=…)` plus `AlertSink.notify`) is deferred to a follow-up — the detector is verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 5.B — Strategy A/B comparator (backend math)** — `core/ab_compare.py` ships the math half of the dashboard's "compare two strategies side by side" feature. `cohort_stats(returns)` produces `n_trades / win_rate / mean / median / std / Sharpe / max_drawdown / total_compound_return / profit_factor` for one cohort; `compare(a, b)` runs both cohorts plus Welch's unequal-variance t-test (Welch–Satterthwaite df) and a two-tailed p-value. Picked Welch over Student because trade-return distributions across two strategies are virtually never homoscedastic. P-value is precise when scipy is available, falls back to the standard-normal SF for df ≥ 30 without scipy, and returns `None` for the small-df + no-scipy combination so the dashboard never lies with a wrong answer. NaN / inf return entries are dropped silently — closed-trade rows occasionally have a missing `return_pct` and one bad row mustn't poison the stat. Pure NumPy + math.erf; no `[ml]` extra needed. 30 tests cover every helper (`_safe_array` / `_max_drawdown` / `_profit_factor` / `_welch_t` / `_two_tailed_p` / `_normal_cdf`), the cohort-block formulas (Sharpe = mean/std, total return = compound, win-rate counts strict positives, all-loss cohort doesn't divide by zero), the t-test direction sanity (positive when A > B), and the integration paths — including a deterministic seeded "doesn't false-flag iid samples" run and a clean detect-significance run on clearly-separated distributions. The scipy-missing branch is exercised by monkey-patching `__import__` so the test gives both code paths real coverage. SQL plumbing (a `/api/strategies/compare?a=…&b=…` route pulling returns from `LLMDecision.prompt_version` cohorts) is deferred to a follow-up — the math is verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.G — Hierarchical Risk Parity allocator (core)** — `ml/hrp.py` is a pure-NumPy implementation of López de Prado's HRP (JoPM 2016): correlation matrix → distance metric `√(½(1−ρ))` → single-linkage hierarchical clustering → quasi-diagonalisation → recursive bisection with inverse-variance allocation factor. Picked HRP over mean-variance / Black-Litterman because (a) it needs only covariance (the bot already has a separate per-pair conviction signal in `core/sizing.py`); (b) it never inverts the cov matrix, so it stays numerically stable when assets are highly correlated (BTC + ETH + alts hugging them); (c) the cluster tree is operator-interpretable. Halal constraints are first-class: weights are always non-negative (no shorts) and sum to ≤ 1.0 (no leverage); zero-variance assets are silently dropped so universe churn cycle-to-cycle doesn't crash the allocator. `HRPAllocation` exposes both the weight dict and the `cluster_order` leaf traversal (useful for dashboard tile rendering). Pure NumPy, no SciPy / sklearn, so the module imports cleanly without the `[ml]` extra. 26 tests cover the algorithmic invariants (non-negativity, sum-to-budget, lower-vol → higher-weight, equal-vol → equal-weights, highly-correlated cluster gets a diversification penalty), the input-validation edges (1D returns, mismatched symbol count, history < min, invalid `cash_buffer_pct`, empty universe, single asset, all-zero variance), and direct helper-level tests for `_correlation_to_distance` / `_single_linkage_order` / `_inverse_variance_weights` / `_cluster_variance` / `_recursive_bisection`. Wiring into the cycle (replacing the flat `max_position_pct` cap) is deferred to a follow-up so the algorithm can be verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 3.A — User accounts + auth (primitives core)** — `web/auth.py` is the pure-Python authentication primitives core that the FastAPI route layer + OAuth callback handlers compose with. The roadmap pins Wave 3.A as the multi-user enabler: "Add a `User` table, OAuth2 sign-in (Google + Apple), JWT bearer auth on the FastAPI app. Each user has isolated bots / portfolios / purification ledgers. Existing operator-mode keeps working when no auth is configured." This module ships the deterministic primitives the OAuth integrations compose with: password hashing, constant-time verification, session lifecycle, and login-rate-limit policy. Picked stdlib `hashlib.scrypt` over bcrypt / argon2 because (a) scrypt is in the standard library — no extra dependency for what's a load-bearing security boundary, (b) RFC 7914 scrypt with `n=16384, r=8, p=1` is documented as sufficient for password hashing per modern NIST guidance, (c) operators can tune the cost parameters via `PasswordPolicy` if hardware advances. Five `AuthOutcome` values pinned for JSON / DB stability (SUCCESS / INVALID_CREDENTIALS / RATE_LIMITED / SESSION_EXPIRED / SESSION_NOT_FOUND). `PasswordPolicy` defaults to ≥12 chars + digit + symbol with NIST SP 800-63B 8-char floor enforced at construction (operator can't accidentally set min_length=6). `PasswordHash` frozen dataclass carries algorithm + scrypt params (n/r/p) + salt_b64 + hash_b64 ready for persistence on the users row. `hash_password(plaintext, *, policy)` validates the policy at hash time then produces a fresh-salt scrypt hash. `verify_password(plaintext, hashed)` returns False on any error path (unknown algorithm, malformed base64 salt, mismatched password) — never raises into the auth path because raising-from-verification would leak timing information about the failure mode. `Session` frozen dataclass carries session_id (32-byte URL-safe base64 token, ≥16 chars enforced via construction) + user_id + issued_at + expires_at (timezone-aware required). `issue_session(*, user_id, now, ttl_minutes=60)` rejects out-of-bounds TTL [5min, 24h]. `is_session_valid(session, *, now)` returns boolean — boundary inclusive at issued_at, exclusive at expires_at (the `<` comparison matters because at the exact expiry moment the session must already be invalid). `LoginAttempt` records per-attempt for rate-limit bookkeeping; persistence layer appends one per attempt. `RateLimitPolicy` defaults max_failures=5, window_minutes=15. `evaluate_rate_limit(*, user_id, history, now, policy)` walks recent attempts newest-first and returns False when N consecutive failures hit the threshold; a successful login within the window resets the counter — the success-resets-counter semantic is the load-bearing pin because brute-force resilience requires distinguishing "user locked out" from "user just had one bad keystroke". `authenticate(*, user_id, plaintext_password, stored_hash, history, now, ...)` composes the full pipeline: rate-limit gate → password verify → session issue. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **password ≥12 chars + digit + symbol** — minimum-length and character-class requirements catch trivially-weak passwords; enforced at `hash_password` not at user-input time so the policy is module-level not UI-level (a UI-level check is bypassable via direct API call); (2) **constant-time verify via `hmac.compare_digest`** — prevents timing-attack password extraction; pinned by the structural choice of `compare_digest` over Python's `==` operator; (3) **session TTL bounded [5min, 24h]** — operators can tune within the window; below 5min is operationally awful (forces re-auth during normal flows); above 24h is security-debt territory (use refresh tokens for longer-lived auth); (4) **failed-attempt rate limiter with success-resets-counter** — N failures in window → block; default 5 failures in 15min; the success-resets pin distinguishes "user locked out" from "user mistyped once and then logged in"; (5) **render output never includes password hash bytes / salt / session_id** — mirrors no-secret patterns of Wave 3.B vault + Wave 8.D OTLP + Wave 12.G co-pilot — the bot's six secret-leakage boundaries share one structural denylist surface. `verify_password` returns False on every error (unknown algorithm, malformed base64) rather than raising — important for the auth flow because raising-into-the-error-path would leak which kind of failure occurred (helping attackers narrow the attack). Halal alignment: auth primitives are read-only with respect to operator portfolio — never opens a position; the structural choice of stdlib + standard cryptographic primitives means no external dependency for the core security boundary; pure-Python (stdlib `hashlib` + `hmac` + `secrets` + `base64` + `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`PasswordPolicy` / `PasswordHash` / `Session` / `LoginAttempt` / `RateLimitPolicy` / `AuthResult`). 74 tests cover: PasswordPolicy validation (8-char NIST floor; strict 20-char operator-tunable); password hashing (returns scrypt hash; **unique-salt-per-call regression-pin** — 2 hashes of identical password differ in both salt + hash; rejects short / no-digit / no-symbol / non-string; custom strict policy enforced; relaxed policy operator-override); password verification (correct → True; wrong → False; empty → False; non-string → False; **unknown algorithm → False not raises**; **malformed base64 → False not raises** — the never-raise-into-auth pin); PasswordHash field validation (empty algorithm / zero scrypt params / empty salt all rejected); **session lifecycle in 11 flavours** (default 60min TTL; custom TTL; high-entropy session_id; unique IDs across calls — Python's `secrets.token_urlsafe(32)` is collision-resistant for any plausible session population; rejects empty user_id / naive now; boundary-inclusive 5min minimum + 24h maximum + below-5min + above-24h rejected; Session field validation including 16-char-minimum session_id pin); is_session_valid (within window True; after expiry False; **boundary-inclusive at issued_at**; **boundary-exclusive at expires_at** — the asymmetric pin matters because at the exact expiry moment the session must already be invalid); RateLimitPolicy + LoginAttempt validation; **rate-limit pins in seven flavours** (no-history allowed; under-threshold allowed; **at-threshold blocked**; **success-resets-counter** — the load-bearing brute-force-resilience pin; old-failures-outside-window don't count; other-users' attempts don't count — the per-user-isolation pin; custom 3-failures-per-5min strict policy enforced); authenticate composition (success → SESSION carrying user_id + issued_at + expires_at; invalid creds → INVALID_CREDENTIALS with no session; **rate-limited blocks even with correct password** — the most-insidious-bypass pin guards against the "operator types correct password while still locked out" race condition); frozen-dataclass immutability across all six output types; AuthOutcome string values pinned for JSON / DB stability; render output across SUCCESS / INVALID_CREDENTIALS / RATE_LIMITED with emoji per outcome (✅ / 🔑 / 🚫 / ⏰ / ❓); **render-no-secret pins in three flavours** (session_id never in render; plaintext password never; password hash bytes + salt never — the structural regression check across all secret types); session expiry rendered as non-secret (it's just a timestamp); cryptographic-determinism pins (two hashes of same password differ — defends against rainbow-table attacks; round-trip hash → verify works); **end-to-end realistic flows in three flavours** — full login lifecycle (operator hashes password, persists, later authenticates 2h later → SUCCESS; session valid at 30min; expired at 61min); **brute-force attack blocked** — 5 wrong guesses lock out the 6th attempt even with the correct password (the realistic attack-defence regression pin); **per-user isolation pin** — attacker hammering user-a's login doesn't lock out user-b (the isolation pin matters because shared-rate-limit would let an attacker DOS legitimate users by guessing their password). OAuth provider integration (Google + Apple authorisation servers via httpx + pyjwt; Apple's JWT-signed-with-ES256 form requires the apple-jwt-helper library), Postgres `users` + `sessions` + `login_attempts` tables wired to `db/repository.py` with the user_id columns participating in Wave 3.D tenant-isolation guards, the FastAPI middleware that extracts the session token from the `Authorization: Bearer ...` header + opens a `tenant_isolation.enter_user_scope(user_id)` for the request handler, the dashboard's auth-event audit log showing recent successful + failed login attempts per user, the email-verification flow that emits a sign-up confirmation token, the password-reset flow with the token TTL set to 30 minutes, the refresh-token flow for sessions extending beyond the 24h ceiling, and the multi-factor authentication adapter (TOTP via stdlib + WebAuthn via the `pywebauthn` library) deferred to follow-ups — primitives core verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 auxiliary — Halal compliance attestation generator** — `halal/compliance_attestation.py` is the pure-Python annual compliance-attestation document generator that consolidates all the landed Round-4 evidence into one auditor-citable artefact. Operators preparing for an AAOIFI certification audit (Wave 11.F), a SOC 2 audit's halal-side cross-references (Wave 11.E), or the SSB's own quarterly review (Wave 11.B) need a deterministic, operator-readable attestation document — this module is the engine that produces it. Cross-cuts every halal-side wave: consumes signed-receipts count from Wave 2.A, purification ledger totals from Wave 2.D, SSB ruling list from Wave 11.B, screener-decisions aggregate from Wave 1.G commodities + Wave 1.H sukuk + Wave 1.I REIT + Wave 2.G regulator-index, exception-queue resolutions from Wave 2.F, halt-event count from the kill-switch infrastructure. Picked an attestation generator over an "auto-render to PDF" flow because (a) the auditor wants the deterministic narrative + the evidence-pointer block, not a glossy PDF; (b) the regression-pinned attestation properties (no user-level data leaks; SSB ruling list required; period bounds enforced) are testable in a way an ad-hoc generation script isn't; (c) the rendered output is plain-text suitable for any downstream renderer (markdown, PDF via Pandoc, ReST via Sphinx, JSON for the dashboard tile). Three composed primitives. (1) `AttestationPeriod` carries timezone-aware start_at + end_at; period length validated in [30, 366] days at construction — below 30 is quarterly-review territory (use Wave 11.B `needs_quarterly_review` instead); above 366 isn't annual any more (operator splits into multiple periods). Boundary-inclusive at exactly 30 and 366 days (pinned both directions). (2) `DeploymentEvidence` aggregates the seven evidence fields the persistence layer queries from existing Round-4 audit-trail tables: `signed_receipts_count` (Wave 2.A); `purification_disbursements_usd` + `purification_outstanding_usd` (Wave 2.D — disbursed and unpaid); `ssb_ruling_ids` tuple (Wave 11.B period-filtered); `screener_decisions_count` (sum across the screener set); `exception_queue_resolutions` (Wave 2.F resolved count); `halt_events_count`. Every numeric field validated non-negative. The engine doesn't query — it consumes the aggregate the persistence layer hands it. (3) `AttestationStatement` carries `section` + `text`; sections include `screening` / `audit_trail` / `purification` / `ssb` / `exception_queue` / `halt_events`. `ComplianceAttestation` is the top-level document with firm_name + period + evidence + outcome + statements + warnings + failures. `generate_attestation(*, firm_name, period, evidence)` is the entry point — produces the deterministic narrative + classifies the outcome. Three `AttestationOutcome` levels: SUFFICIENT (ready to submit), INSUFFICIENT (gaps prevent submission), PROVISIONAL (attestable but flagged warnings). **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **attestation period 30-366 days** — bounded at construction; (2) **requires ≥1 SSB ruling in period** — a platform without any SSB activity in the attestation period can't credibly attest to shariah governance; the engine surfaces INSUFFICIENT with the explicit failure reason rather than producing a misleading attestation; (3) **statements deterministic from evidence** — given the same inputs, the engine produces byte-identical attestation text (regression-pinned via the "two attestations with same inputs render to same string" test); operators can diff two attestations to prove what changed across periods; (4) **firm name preserved, user-level data redacted** — the attestation is for the operator's auditor and the firm name appears on the document (the auditor needs to know which firm is attesting); other operator-identifying fields (user IDs, account numbers, individual customer data) never appear; mirrors no-PII patterns of Wave 11.D + 11.C + 3.B; (5) **non-zero evidence requirement** — zero signed receipts → INSUFFICIENT (the platform isn't operating, can't attest); the structural friction prevents misleading "we attest to nothing" submissions. The narrative builders for each section format USD amounts via `_format_usd` ($X.XX for < $1k, $X.XXk for $1k-1M, $X.XXM for ≥ $1M); SSB statement renders 1 vs >1 ruling in grammatically correct form; halt-events statement explicitly mentions "no halt events occurred" when zero (the auditor wants to see this affirmatively, not infer from absence); exception-queue warning fires when active screening (count > 0) but zero resolutions (suggests accumulated unresolved items). Halal alignment: the attestation generator is the cross-cut that makes Round-4's evidence auditable — every halal-side wave (1.G / 1.H / 1.I / 2.A / 2.D / 2.F / 2.G / 11.B / 11.F) feeds into it; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 53 tests cover: AttestationPeriod validation (naive datetime rejected; end-before-start rejected; <30d rejected; >366d rejected; exactly 30d accepted; exactly 366d accepted; length_days property); DeploymentEvidence validation (every numeric field non-negative; zero-outstanding accepted as the clean case); AttestationStatement field validation; ComplianceAttestation field validation (empty firm_name rejected); **outcome-classification pins** (clean evidence → SUFFICIENT; no SSB rulings → INSUFFICIENT with specific failure message; zero signed receipts → INSUFFICIENT; outstanding purification → PROVISIONAL with disbursement warning; active screening + zero resolutions → PROVISIONAL with queue warning; **no-screening + zero-resolutions doesn't false-positive** the queue warning); halt-events statement (recorded in narrative when present; explicit "no platform-halt events" when zero); generate rejects empty firm_name; **statement coverage pin** asserts every attestation has the standard six sections (screening / audit_trail / purification / ssb / exception_queue / halt_events); per-section content pins (screening includes count; audit_trail includes signed_receipts; purification includes disbursed amount + USD formatting at three magnitudes — < $1k, $1k-1M, ≥ $1M; SSB lists single vs multiple rulings with correct grammar; exception_queue includes resolution count); **determinism pin** (same inputs → byte-identical render); frozen-dataclass immutability; AttestationOutcome string values pinned for JSON / DB stability; render output (firm_name preserved; period dates ISO-formatted; outcome shown; emoji per outcome ✅/⚠️/❌; **no-user-PII render pin** asserts user_id and email-shaped strings never in render); render shows all six statements + warnings + failures sections; **end-to-end realistic flows** in three flavours (full-year clean attestation with 5847 receipts + $18.7k purification + 4 SSB rulings + 42100 screener decisions + 78 exception resolutions + 2 halt events → SUFFICIENT with full 365d period; failed attestation operator forgot SSB → INSUFFICIENT with explicit "SSB" failure message; provisional attestation with $5k outstanding purification → PROVISIONAL with disbursement warning suggesting next-period resolution). Postgres `compliance_attestations` table that persists each generated attestation for the audit trail, the FastAPI route adapter (`/api/compliance/attestation` returning the rendered text + JSON), the Pandoc-driven PDF rendering pipeline that operators submit to AAOIFI / SOC 2 auditors, and the `just compliance-attestation --year=2026` CLI recipe that wraps the full pipeline + posts the result to the operator's compliance dashboard tile deferred to follow-ups — engine verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 10.A — Public strategy gallery curation engine** — `web/strategy_gallery.py` is the pure-Python publication-curation engine for the voluntary public strategy gallery. The roadmap pins Wave 10.A: "Operators voluntarily publish their strategies + performance. Sortable by Sharpe, by halal-compliance strictness, by simplicity. Forkable into the operator's own account." This module is the engine that takes an operator's strategy artefact + performance metrics + publication intent and produces a gallery-ready `StrategyEntry` with anonymised author identity, halal-strictness rating, simplicity score, and pre-publication safety gates. Picked a focused publication-curation engine over an "auto-publish" flow because (a) the gallery's value depends on quality + safety — operators expect their strategies to remain private by default, and the engine refuses to publish anything without an explicit opt-in flag, (b) the regression-pinned anonymisation properties (no PII regex matches survive; salt is required; visibility default is PRIVATE) are testable in a way an ad-hoc publish script isn't, (c) the gallery becomes the public face of the project — the engine encodes the operator's quality bar so submissions are uniformly comparable. Three-tier `StrategyVisibility` enum (PRIVATE default — operator-internal, never appears in gallery; PUBLIC_UNLISTED — direct-URL share but doesn't appear in listings; PUBLIC_LISTED — appears in gallery search). Four-tier `HalalStrictnessLevel` enum (BASIC follows AAOIFI Standard 21 baseline; MODERATE adds default Wave 1.G/1.H/1.I screeners; STRICT layers all three; MAX_STRICT requires the full Wave 11.B SSB-board ruling chain) — closed enum the gallery sorts on. `PublicMetrics` carries Sharpe ratio + win rate % + max drawdown % + total trades + time period days; every field validated (win/drawdown 0-100; non-negative trades; positive period). `StrategyEntry` carries strategy_id + anonymous_author + name + version + summary + halal_strictness + simplicity_score + visibility (default PRIVATE) + optional metrics + optional parent_fork_id + opt_in_publication boolean (default False). `validate_for_publication(entry)` is the publication gate; `GalleryViolationError` raised on unsafe entries. `compute_simplicity_score(*, lines_of_code, symbol_list_size, reasoning_depth)` produces a 0-100 score using a heuristic that penalises LOC linearly past 50, symbol count sub-linearly past 5, and reasoning depth linearly past 1; clamped at [0, 100]. `assemble_lineage(entries, *, target_id)` walks the fork chain back to its root with cycle detection. `hash_author(user_id, *, salt)` produces deterministic salt-hashed author tokens (`anon-{16hex}`) — sharing the HMAC-SHA256 construction with Wave 10.B open-dataset anonymisation, so an operator's anonymous identity is consistent across the gallery and the open dataset under the same salt. **Six pinned safety semantics**: (1) **PRIVATE default visibility** — `StrategyEntry.__init__` defaults visibility to PRIVATE; the publication gate refuses non-PRIVATE entries without `opt_in_publication=True`. The pin matters because the most-insidious failure mode would be an operator updating their strategy and accidentally publishing private logic — the structural friction of two flags (visibility + opt_in_publication) ensures publication requires conscious operator intent; (2) **anonymous author token** — operator's user_id is replaced by a deterministic salt-hashed `anon-…` token. The same salt produces the same token (deterministic within an export so researchers can correlate same-author strategies); different salts produce different tokens (re-publication under fresh salt produces fresh anonymous identity — anti-linking across exports). 16-byte salt minimum required at construction; (3) **PII denylist on summary + name** — same five regex patterns as Wave 10.B (email / SSN / IP / phone / ETH-address); summary or name containing any pattern is REJECTED at validation rather than auto-redacted. The reject-not-redact pin matters because operators need to *notice* the leak and rewrite — auto-redaction would silently mangle their strategy description without the operator realising they had PII in there to begin with; (4) **halal-strictness closed enum** — operator declares the strategy's strictness level; the gallery sorts on it; the closed-enum-with-stable-string-values pattern lets the dashboard render filter dropdowns from the type system; (5) **simplicity score** — heuristic-based 0-100 score where simpler strategies sort to the top. The load-bearing pin matters operationally because new operators browsing the gallery should see approachable examples first; the heuristic penalises LOC + symbol-count + reasoning-depth, all proxies for cognitive load. Boundary cases pinned: 50 LOC + 5 symbols + depth 1 → 100; 100 LOC + 5 + 2 → ~92; 500 LOC + 50 + 5 → ~32; 1000+ + 100+ + 10+ → 0; clamping enforced; (6) **render output never includes operator's raw user_id / portfolio / wallet addresses** — only the anonymous_author token + name + metrics + halal-strictness + simplicity. Mirrors the no-PII patterns of Wave 11.D + 11.C + 3.B + 10.B + every other Round-4 wave's defensive surface. The regression-pinned tests assert "user_id" and "@" never appear in the rendered output. **Fork lineage** preserved: every fork carries `parent_fork_id` pointing to the strategy it was forked from; `assemble_lineage` walks the chain back to root in chronological order. **Cycle detection** raises `GalleryViolationError` if the operator somehow constructs a cycle (DB-import bug, hand-edited rows) rather than infinite-looping — the structural defence against pathological lineages. **Detached parent** (orphaned fork whose parent_fork_id isn't in the entries set) stops the walk at the orphan rather than raising, so partial imports of fork chains don't crash the lineage display. Halal alignment: read-only curation; never opens a position; pure-Python (stdlib `hmac` + `hashlib` + `re` + `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`PublicMetrics` / `StrategyEntry`). 65 tests cover: PublicMetrics field validation (win_rate above 100; negative drawdown; negative trades; zero period); StrategyEntry field validation (empty strategy_id / author / name; zero version; simplicity above/below bounds; empty parent_fork_id when set; None parent_fork_id accepted); **default visibility = PRIVATE pin**; **default opt_in_publication = False pin**; hash_author semantics (token starts with `anon-`; contains no original ID; deterministic within salt; different users → different tokens; **different salts → different tokens** — the anti-linking pin); short-salt rejection; empty-user-id rejection; simplicity-score scoring boundary cases (50 LOC + 5 + 1 → 100; 100 LOC + 5 + 2 → 85-95; 500 + 50 + 5 → 25-40; 2000+200+20 → 0); clamping at 0 and 100 in both directions; input validation for negative LOC / symbols / depth; **publication gate semantics** in eight flavours (PRIVATE passes silently — operator-internal; PUBLIC_LISTED without opt-in raises; PUBLIC_UNLISTED without opt-in raises; PUBLIC with opt-in passes when clean; PII email in summary rejected; PII SSN in summary rejected; PII ETH-address in summary rejected; PII in name rejected; clean summary passes; PUBLIC_LISTED without metrics raises; PUBLIC_UNLISTED without metrics passes — the asymmetry pin matters because UNLISTED is direct-URL share where metrics aren't required); fork lineage walking in five flavours (root only; 2-level; multi-level chain; target-not-found raises KeyError; **detached parent stops walk** — partial-import resilience; **cycle raises GalleryViolationError** — the infinite-loop defence pin); frozen-dataclass immutability across PublicMetrics + StrategyEntry; all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability across StrategyVisibility + HalalStrictnessLevel; render output (anonymous_author shown; visibility emoji per kind 🔒/🔗/🌍; strictness emoji per level 🟢/🟡/🟠/🔴; metrics shown when present formatted with Sharpe + win % + DD % + trades + period; metrics omitted when None; parent_fork_id shown when set; parent_fork_id omitted when None; **render-no-PII pin** asserts `user_id` and `@` never in render output — the structural regression check); simplicity score formatted to 1 decimal place; end-to-end realistic flows (typical publication lifecycle: hash author + compute score + construct entry + validate → no exception; full 3-deep fork lineage walk regression-tested; **publication blocked for PII in summary realistic flow** — operator accidentally includes their email and the engine raises GalleryViolationError demanding a rewrite; simplicity ordering pin — simpler scores higher than medium higher than complex). Postgres `gallery_strategies` + `gallery_audit_log` + `gallery_fork_relationships` tables wired to `db/repository.py`, the FastAPI route adapters (`/api/gallery` listing public-listed strategies with sort by Sharpe / strictness / simplicity + filter by halal-strictness; `/api/gallery/{strategy_id}` returning the entry + assembled lineage; `/api/gallery/publish` for the operator's opt-in flow with `validate_for_publication` invoked before persist; `/api/gallery/fork/{strategy_id}` for the fork-into-account flow), the dashboard gallery tile rendering top-N strategies by selected sort with the visibility + strictness emoji prominent, the fork-flow that copies a published strategy into the operator's account preserving the lineage chain, the per-strategy discussion threads + star count + fork count features (the social / community layer the gallery becomes once Wave 10.C Discord / Slack community lands), and the periodic featured-strategy curation flow that highlights operator-submitted strategies passing a manual quality bar deferred to follow-ups — engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 11.A — Investment-advisor registration readiness aggregator** — `web/advisor_registration_readiness.py` is the pure-Python deployment-readiness aggregator for investment-advisor registration across major regulators. The roadmap pins the requirement: "Once we serve real-money users, we're an investment advisor. File the relevant registrations. ~6 months lead time." This module is the operator-side readiness check that runs BEFORE the application paperwork is filed, scoring the deployment against each regulator's requirement set. Mirrors the design of Wave 11.E (SOC 2 readiness) and Wave 11.F (halal certification readiness) — same closed-set-enum + module-level-frozen-requirement-sets + render-no-PII pattern — applied to investment-advisor registration. Six `RegulatorAuthority` values: SEC_RIA (US Investment Advisers Act of 1940 — registered investment adviser), FCA_UK (UK Financial Conduct Authority), SAUDI_CMA (Saudi Capital Market Authority), UAE_VARA (UAE Virtual Assets Regulatory Authority), SINGAPORE_MAS (MAS Capital Markets Services licence), AUSTRALIA_ASIC (ASIC AFSL). Picked a focused readiness aggregator over an "auto-file" flow because (a) registration paperwork requires human signatures + a notarised Form ADV / FCA SUP submission (the engine doesn't sign attestations), (b) the audit-trail evidence is the operator's existing artifacts (firm registration documents + executive backgrounds + compliance program + recordkeeping policies + AML program), and (c) the readiness report's actionable output — "you have 8 of 10 SEC RIA requirements met, the 2 gaps are SURETY_BOND and ANNUAL_FORM_ADV_AMENDMENT" — lets the operator focus pre-filing work on the actual gaps rather than generic "be more compliant" advice. Nine `RegistrationCategory` labels (FORM_FILING / BACKGROUND_CHECKS / EXAMS_LICENSURE / SURETY_BOND / AML / COMPLIANCE_PROGRAM / RECORDKEEPING / CLIENT_MONEY / DISPUTE_RESOLUTION). Two `RequirementSeverity` levels (BLOCKING — filing can't proceed; WARNING — flagged but proceeds). 22 `EvidenceKind` artifact labels covering the full registration audit trail across four functional groups: form filings (FORM_ADV_PART_1A / 2A / 2B; ANNUAL_FORM_ADV_AMENDMENT; FCA_SUP_FORM; FCA_GABRIEL_RETURN); identifiers / registration numbers (CRD_NUMBER; IARD_REGISTRATION; FCA_FIRM_REFERENCE_NUMBER; SAUDI_CMA_LICENCE; SINGAPORE_CMS_LICENCE; AUSTRALIA_AFSL); personal qualifications (SERIES_65_PASSED — Uniform Investment Adviser Law Exam; SERIES_66_PASSED — Uniform Combined State Law Exam; SMCR_CERTIFIED_PERSONS — UK Senior Managers and Certification Regime; EXEC_BACKGROUND_CHECK — FINRA U4 form); compliance program (SURETY_BOND; AML_PROGRAM; COMPLIANCE_MANUAL — Rule 206(4)-7; RECORDKEEPING_PROCEDURES — Rule 204-2); UK / Singapore-specific (CLIENT_MONEY_RULES_DOCUMENTED — CASS 7; FOS_MEMBERSHIP — Financial Ombudsman Service; DISPUTE_RESOLUTION_PROCEDURES — DISP). Four-level `ReadinessLevel` ladder (READY / NEARLY_READY / GAPS / NOT_READY) shared with Wave 11.E + 11.F. Module-level frozen requirement catalogue: 10 SEC RIA controls covering Form ADV Parts 1A + 2A + 2B; Series 65; exec background check (FINRA U4); surety bond (state-specific minimum); AML program with designated AML compliance officer; Rule 206(4)-7 written compliance manual; Rule 204-2 recordkeeping procedures; warning-severity annual Form ADV amendment; 6 FCA controls covering SUP authorisation form; SMCR-certified senior managers + DBS check; CASS 7 client money rules documented; FOS Financial Ombudsman Service membership; SYSC 6.3 MLR-2017 AML program with nominated MLRO; warning-severity annual Gabriel / RegData return. Saudi CMA + UAE VARA + Singapore MAS + Australia ASIC ship empty for operator-side extension (operators in those jurisdictions extend the requirement tuples per their specific regulator's published spec). `RegistrationPolicy` defaults `staleness_horizon_days=365` (the standard annual filing cadence for SEC RIAs + FCA firms; Type II SOC-aligned). `evaluate_registration_readiness(*, authority, evidence, now, policy)` returns a `RegistrationReadinessReport` with overall_level + per-requirement assessments + counts. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **closed regulator-authority set** — operators add a new authority via code review with bundled requirement set + regression-test coverage; (2) **per-authority requirements module-level frozen** — runtime config drift can't silently weaken the floor before an application deadline; (3) **critical-requirement gap → BLOCKING** — missing Form ADV Part 1A is BLOCKING (filing can't proceed); missing annual amendment is WARNING (auditor will note but doesn't block initial filing); (4) **12-month staleness horizon (default 365d)** — SEC RIAs file annual Form ADV amendments; FCA firms file annual Gabriel / RegData returns. Past 12 months → stale; the boundary at exactly 365d is stale (pinned via test); evidence with `last_updated=None` (no timestamp recorded) also stale; custom 180d strict policy catches 300d artifacts; (5) **render output never includes operator-identifying detail** — references abstract evidence-kind labels (e.g., "form_adv_part_1a: present, refreshed 30d ago") never raw firm name / CRD number / executive PII / IARD codes. Mirrors no-PII patterns of Wave 11.D + 11.C + 3.B + 11.E + 11.F — every public-facing render in this codebase shares one defensive surface. The same readiness ladder as 11.E + 11.F: 0 blocking + 0 warning + 0 stale → READY; 0 blocking + (warnings or stale) → NEARLY_READY; 1-2 blocking → GAPS; ≥3 blocking → NOT_READY. Halal alignment: registration readiness is operational compliance; never opens a position; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 45 tests cover: policy validation (zero / negative horizon rejected); per-authority requirement-set queries (SEC RIA 10 controls including Series 65 + surety bond + AML; FCA 6 controls including SMCR + CASS-7 + FOS; Saudi CMA / UAE VARA / Singapore MAS / Australia ASIC empty by design); RegistrationRequirement + EvidenceArtifact field validation; **READY happy paths in two flavours** (SEC RIA full evidence; FCA full evidence); **NOT_READY pins** (no evidence; ≥3 blocking gaps); GAPS (1 blocking gap drop SURETY_BOND); **NEARLY_READY** (only warning unmet — drop ANNUAL_FORM_ADV_AMENDMENT); **stale-evidence pins in four flavours** (>365d → stale + nearly_ready; exactly-365d boundary inclusive; no last_updated → stale; strict 180d policy catches 300d artifact); empty-authority → NOT_READY with "requirement set is empty" note (the operator-extension sentinel for unsupported regulators); input validation (naive now rejected); per-requirement assessment count matches requirements; **unmet assessment carries note** ("missing evidence (BLOCKING)" with severity surfaced); stale assessment carries note with day count; frozen-dataclass immutability; all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability across authority + category + severity + evidence_kind + level; render output across all four levels with emoji; per-requirement breakdown shows requirement_id + category + severity; **render-no-operator-PII pin** (asserts firm_name not in render; raw CRD number values like 12345 not in render — only the artifact-kind label CRD_NUMBER is allowed); end-to-end realistic scenarios — typical pre-filing SEC RIA with annual amendment gap → NEARLY_READY (the realistic "first-time RIA filing" case); UK FCA filing missing SMCR-certified persons → GAPS (the realistic "we have most things but the senior-manager attestation is delayed" case); assessment-count regression; met_pct aggregates to 100% on full evidence. Postgres `registration_evidence` + `registration_audit_log` + `registration_remediation_tasks` tables wired to `db/repository.py`, the FastAPI route adapters (`/api/registration/{authority}/readiness` per-authority drill-down; `/api/registration/gaps` returning the actionable remediation list across all authorities the operator targets), the dashboard's registration tile rendering per-authority progress with the actionable-gaps list + readiness arrow, the per-day CI step that emits a readiness warning when any required evidence's `last_updated` falls past horizon (catches stale evidence before the annual filing deadline), the operator-extension flow for adding Saudi CMA + UAE VARA + Singapore MAS + Australia ASIC requirement sets bundled per their specific regulator's published spec, and an audit-evidence-export utility that bundles all the artifacts + their hashes into a single ZIP for submission to the regulator deferred to follow-ups — aggregator verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 10.B — Open dataset anonymisation engine** — `web/dataset_anonymisation.py` is the pure-Python anonymisation engine for the public halal-trading research dataset. The roadmap pins Wave 10.B as the academic-cite-able dataset that draws halal-finance researchers to the platform: "The aggregated, anonymised LLM decision history becomes a public dataset. Academic research community downloads it, cites the platform. Halal-finance researchers get a goldmine of empirical data." This module is the engine that takes the operator's raw `LlmDecision` rows and produces a public-research-safe dataset with (a) per-user identifiers stripped to deterministic salt-hashed tokens, (b) free-form rationale text scrubbed of PII via a denylist, (c) USD amounts bucketed into coarse tiers, (d) timestamps rounded to the hour, (e) k-anonymity enforced via QID-tuple grouping. Picked a focused anonymisation engine over an "export everything the operator has" flow because (a) academic users want a clean, de-identified, cite-able dataset — they don't need raw operator data, (b) the regression-pinned anonymisation properties (no PII regex matches survive; salt is required; k-anonymity floor) are testable in a way an ad-hoc export script isn't, (c) the explicit `AnonymisationPolicy` lets operators tune the aggressiveness per their compliance posture (some operators may want stricter k=10 for higher-risk publication, or k=1 for non-public internal exports). `RawDecision` frozen dataclass carries the nine fields from the operator's database (decision_id + user_id + timestamp + symbol + sector + regime + action + notional_usd + rationale); validates non-empty IDs / symbol + timezone-aware timestamp + non-negative notional. `AnonymisedDecision` is the public-dataset row carrying anonymous_user (the salt-hashed token) + timestamp_hour + symbol + sector + regime + action + usd_bucket + rationale_redacted. `USDBucket` enum has five tiers (MICRO < $100; SMALL $100-1k; MEDIUM $1k-10k; LARGE $10k-100k; WHALE > $100k) coarse enough to prevent re-identification via amount fingerprints. `AnonymisationPolicy` carries `k_anonymity_floor` (default 5), `enable_pii_redaction` (default True), `bucket_usd_amounts` (default True). `anonymise_decision(raw, *, salt, policy)` is the per-row transform; `anonymise_dataset(decisions, *, salt, policy)` runs the full pipeline including the k-anonymity filter. **Six pinned safety semantics**: (1) **salt required (≥16 bytes)** — anonymisation refuses short / empty salt input at construction; without it, the user_id hash is reversible by anyone with a list of plausible user_ids (HMAC-SHA256 with empty key is just SHA256 which any attacker can replay).
