The 16-byte minimum is the standard cryptographic-salt floor; (2) **deterministic hash within a single salt** — same user_id maps to same anonymised token within one run, so researchers can correlate the same anonymised user's decisions across the dataset; across runs with different salts the mapping changes — so re-exports can't be cross-referenced, the anti-linking pin that prevents cross-export deanonymisation attacks; (3) **PII denylist on free-form text** — five regex patterns (email-shaped via `[\w.+-]+@[\w-]+\.[\w.-]+`; SSN-shaped via `\d{3}-\d{2}-\d{4}`; IP-shaped via `(?:\d{1,3}\.){3}\d{1,3}`; phone-shaped via `\+?\d[\d\s().-]{8,}\d`; ETH-address-shaped via `0x[0-9a-fA-F]{40}`) matched and replaced with `<redacted-{kind}>` placeholders. The patterns intentionally err on the side of false positives — better to redact a non-PII string than leak a real email. The pin is regression-tested for each pattern individually + the clean-rationale-unchanged invariant + the multi-PII pipeline test that scrubs email + IP + SSN + ETH-address simultaneously. Operators can disable redaction via `enable_pii_redaction=False` for already-clean data — but the default-on-by-default protects against operator-rationale containing accidental PII; (4) **k-anonymity floor (default k=5)** — a row whose quasi-identifier tuple `(anonymous_user, sector, regime)` doesn't appear in ≥k other rows is dropped. The QID grouping is the load-bearing pin: same user across different sectors forms different QID groups, so a user with 5 crypto trades + 1 tech trade has the tech-row dropped (only 1 row in that QID group) while the crypto rows survive. Operators tune k upward for stricter publications (k=10 strict pin tested); k=1 disables the check entirely (operator opt-out for non-public internal exports — the regression-pinned escape hatch); (5) **timestamp rounded to hour** — `dt.replace(minute=0, second=0, microsecond=0)` reduces timing-correlation attack surface (researchers see the hour-of-day pattern but not minute-precision identifiers); pinned via test that 14:35:12 → 14:00:00 and top-of-hour unchanged; (6) **USD bucketed into coarse tiers** with boundary-inclusive transitions (exactly $100 → SMALL not MICRO; $99.99 → MICRO; pinned in both directions). Each tier covers a 10× range so researchers see the magnitude pattern without a re-identification fingerprint. Halal alignment: read-only export pipeline; never opens a position; the engine doesn't write back to operator tables (the persistence layer reads raw rows, the engine transforms in-memory, the export script writes the anonymised result to a separate research-dataset table or CSV); pure-Python (stdlib `hmac` + `hashlib` + `re` + `collections.Counter`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output. The HMAC-SHA256 hash truncated to first 16 hex chars (64 bits of entropy) is collision-resistant within any plausible export size — much smaller than birthday-collision probability for a few million rows. `render_summary(result)` produces an operator-facing summary showing count + dropped + bucket distribution; pinned no-raw-data contract — the summary never includes raw user_ids / rationale text / notional amounts (only counts), regression-tested by injecting `alice-secret-id` and `SECRET-OPERATOR-TEXT-XYZ` into raw decisions and asserting they don't appear in the rendered text. 53 tests cover: policy validation (zero k_anonymity_floor rejected; k=1 accepted as opt-out); RawDecision field validation (every field invariant fires); salt-requirement pin (short rejected on both `anonymise_decision` and `anonymise_dataset`; 16-byte minimum accepted); **user-id hash semantics in four pins** (token starts with `anon-`; contains no original ID; deterministic within salt; different users → different tokens; **different salts → different tokens** — the cross-export-anti-linking pin); timestamp rounding (14:35:12 → 14:00:00; top-of-hour unchanged); **USD bucketing across all five tiers** with boundary inclusivity pinned in both directions ($100 → SMALL; $99.99 → MICRO); **PII redaction in five flavours** (email; SSN; IP; ETH-address; clean-rationale-unchanged invariant — the no-spurious-redaction pin); PII redaction disable-via-policy flow; symbol + sector + regime + action preserved (the academic-value-preservation pin); **k-anonymity filter in five flavours** (5 same-QID rows kept under k=5; 4 dropped under k=5; k=1 keeps all single-row groups; **QID grouping by (anon-user, sector, regime)** — same user different sector forms different QID; strict k=10 flips); empty-dataset returns empty result; frozen-dataclass immutability across RawDecision + AnonymisedDecision + AnonymisationPolicy + AnonymisationResult; USDBucket string values pinned for JSON / DB stability; **render-summary no-raw-data pins** in three flavours (omits user_ids; omits raw rationale; shows bucket distribution + drop count); end-to-end realistic flows — full-dataset 100-decision flow (3 users × 10 crypto-risk-on decisions = 30 same-QID rows survive k=5); **realistic-PII-scrubbing pipeline** (a single rationale containing email + IP + SSN + ETH-address simultaneously → all four PII vectors redacted with their respective placeholders; the multi-vector regression-pin that catches the most-realistic operator-leak failure mode where a debug-rationale string contains multiple identifiers). Postgres `research_dataset_exports` audit table tracking each export's salt-hash + k-floor + row count for the cite-able-DOI provenance, the FastAPI route adapter (`/api/research/dataset/{export_id}.csv` returning the anonymised CSV with the salt + k-floor + timestamp metadata in HTTP headers), the operator console for triggering exports with the policy parameters + auditor-friendly export-history viewer, the public-dataset cite-able DOI registration flow (Zenodo / DataCite integration), and the `just research-export` recipe that wraps the full pipeline deferred to follow-ups — engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 3.D — Multi-tenant database isolation guards** — `db/tenant_isolation.py` is the pure-Python tenant-scope guard layer that enforces row-level user_id checks *before* the SQL query runs, so a forgotten WHERE clause in a repository method can't silently leak one tenant's data to another. The roadmap pinned the choice between row-level user_id + Postgres RLS vs per-user schemas: "Pick (a) for simplicity. Update every repo to filter by user_id from the request context." This module is the application-layer guard that catches the "developer forgot to pass user_id" failure mode early with a descriptive `TenantViolationError`. Picked an explicit `TenantContext` + `TenantViolationError` over a Postgres-only RLS approach because (a) the bot's tests run against the same SQLAlchemy + asyncpg layer the production deploys to, and a Python-side guard is testable without spinning up Postgres in unit tests, (b) RLS policies are still recommended at the DB layer as defence-in-depth — this module is the operator's first defensive boundary, not the only one, (c) the failure mode this guards against is a developer forgetting to pass user_id into a query, which a database policy catches but with a less-descriptive error than "TenantViolationError: query targeted user 'A' but active scope is user 'B'". ContextVar-based active scope with two-mode `ScopeKind` (USER for normal user-bound operations / ADMIN for explicit cross-tenant compliance / debug operations). `TenantContext` frozen dataclass carries user_id + scope; rejects empty/whitespace user_id at construction (mirrors Wave 11.C KYC + Wave 11.D privacy validation patterns). `enter_user_scope(user_id)` and `enter_admin_scope(admin_user_id)` are the explicit context managers — admin scope is opt-in only, never implicit; the explicit entry makes admin-side queries traceable in audit logs. The `require_tenant()` helper raises `TenantViolationError` when called without an active scope (the explicit raise prevents silent fallthrough when a developer forgets to enter a scope). `assert_row_scope(*, row_user_id, operation)` is the read-side guard repositories call after fetching a row to verify the SQL WHERE clause was correctly applied. `assert_payload_scope(*, payload_user_id, operation)` is the write-side guard repositories call at the entry of every write method to catch the "developer passes user_id from request body without validating it matches the auth context" failure mode. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **TenantContext required for every scoped operation** — `current_tenant()` returns None when no scope is active; `require_tenant()` raises explicitly rather than silently allowing fallthrough. The pin matters because the most-insidious bug would be a repository method that silently runs a no-WHERE-clause query when the user-context isn't set (returning all users' data); (2) **ADMIN scope opt-in only** — admin scope can't be entered implicitly via config or environment variable; the operator's admin console explicitly calls `enter_admin_scope(admin_user_id)` with the operator's own user_id (so the audit trail attributes the cross-tenant query to the specific admin); admin scope bypasses the row-level user_id check but every repository method that detects admin scope should emit an audit-log entry (the engine doesn't enforce this — it's the repository's responsibility, but the structural friction of explicit entry makes it discoverable); the regression-pinned test asserts admin scope rejects empty admin_user_id, so even with an opt-in path the audit attribution can't be empty; (3) **empty user_id rejected** at TenantContext construction (both regular `__post_init__` for direct construction and via the `enter_user_scope` / `enter_admin_scope` paths) — silent acceptance of an empty string would create a "ghost tenant" that could match any row's empty-string user_id (which is a common DB-default in poorly-migrated tables); (4) **row-validation helper raises on cross-tenant** — when a fetched row's user_id doesn't match the active scope, `TenantViolationError` is raised; SQL bugs (missing JOIN, wrong WHERE clause, parameter-binding mismatch) are caught at the application layer rather than silently rendering another tenant's data to the user. Admin scope bypasses the check but the call is still expected (the operator's audit-log capture is what makes admin queries traceable); (5) **render output redacts other tenants' user_ids** — `TenantViolationError.message` (what `str(error)` returns) references the active scope's user_id but the would-be-leaked `target_user_id` is rendered as `<other-tenant>` so error logs / Slack alerts / Sentry exception captures can be safely shipped to ops channels without leaking cross-tenant identifiers. The actual `target_user_id` stays accessible on the exception object's `target_user_id` attribute for debugging in dev environments — operators in dev can introspect programmatically while production logs stay safe. Mirrors the no-PII patterns of Wave 11.D privacy + Wave 11.C KYC + Wave 3.B vault — the bot's defensive surfaces share one redaction discipline. The error also carries `active_user_id` + `operation` for the audit-trail context. Halal alignment: isolation guard is operator-side privacy / multi-tenancy; never opens a position; pure-Python (stdlib `contextvars` + `contextlib` + `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. The ContextVar-based scope is async-safe — different async tasks see their own scopes if they use the standard contextvars propagation. Frozen dataclass on TenantContext. 44 tests cover: TenantContext validation (empty + whitespace user_id rejected; default scope is USER; admin scope accepted); default-no-scope state (current_tenant is None; require_tenant raises TenantViolationError; is_admin_scope is False); enter_user_scope lifecycle (sets current_tenant; restores previous scope on exit — the regression pin for nested scope correctness; rejects empty user_id; is_admin_scope still False under user scope); **enter_admin_scope explicit-opt-in pin** (sets ADMIN kind; is_admin_scope True; restores previous scope on exit; rejects empty admin_user_id — the structural friction that prevents empty-attribution admin queries); assert_row_scope semantics (passes for matching row; raises with active + target user_ids carried in exception attributes for mismatch; admin bypasses the check; raises without scope — the no-implicit-fallthrough pin; rejects empty row_user_id; operation label flows through to the violation error); assert_payload_scope semantics (matching user_id passes; mismatch raises with operation in error; admin bypasses; raises without scope; rejects empty payload_user_id); **TenantViolationError no-PII pin** (str() shows `<other-tenant>` placeholder not the actual target_user_id — the structural redaction for safe error-log shipping; target_user_id stays on exception object for debug; default operation is "query"); frozen-dataclass immutability on TenantContext; ScopeKind string values pinned for JSON / DB stability; render output across no-scope (🔓 emoji + "no tenant scope" message) / user-scope (👤 emoji + user_id) / admin-scope (🛡️ emoji + ADMIN label + operator user_id); render shows active user_id only — never any other tenant's identifier (the engine doesn't even have access to other tenants in this state, but the test pin verifies the active user_id literal appears); end-to-end realistic flows in five flavours — simulated repository.get_trade with SQL bug returning wrong-tenant row → blocked by assert_row_scope (the regression-pin for the most-common multi-tenancy failure mode); correct row passes the check; admin compliance-ops review across tenants permitted by admin scope; write with payload-user-id mismatch (malicious request body trying to insert under another user's ID) blocked by assert_payload_scope; nested admin-into-user-scope correctly restores admin context on exit (the layered-scope pin for admin-impersonating-user debug flows); ContextVar-isolation regression (scope doesn't leak after exit; multiple sequential scopes work correctly without contamination); operation label flows through to the violation error in both row + payload paths (the audit-log usability pin). Postgres RLS policies (the defence-in-depth layer at the DB — the operator's deployment script creates `CREATE POLICY ... USING (user_id = current_setting('app.current_user_id'))` per tenant-scoped table), Wave 3.A user-auth integration (FastAPI middleware extracts user_id from JWT bearer token, enters user_scope for the duration of the request handler), the operator admin console that enters admin_scope explicitly with audit-log capture (`POST /api/admin/impersonate/{user_id}` route opens an admin-scoped session with the requesting admin operator's identifier), per-repo updates to call `assert_row_scope` / `assert_payload_scope` at every read / write entry, and the SQLAlchemy event listener that automatically appends `WHERE user_id = :current_user_id` to scoped queries (to make the user_id filter declarative not imperative — operators register tables under tenant-scope and the listener handles the filter) deferred to follow-ups — guards verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 9.F — API reference auto-generator (introspection core)** — `core/api_reference.py` is the pure-Python module-introspection-based API reference generator. The roadmap pins the API reference as one of the documentation deliverables ("Sphinx + autoapi over `domain/`, `core/`, every public module. Versioned with the codebase.") This module is the **pure-Python introspection core** — given a Python module object, extract the public symbols (classes / functions / dataclasses / enums / constants), their docstrings, and their signatures into a structured `ApiReference` dataclass that the operator's docs build (Sphinx, MkDocs, plain markdown) consumes. Picked module-introspection over Sphinx-autoapi for the core because (a) the operator's docs build pipeline can plug in any renderer (markdown, ReST, JSON, OpenAPI), (b) the introspection result is testable + regression-pinnable in a way that Sphinx output isn't (operators can write tests asserting that specific symbols appear in the reference), (c) the existing wave-pattern is "ship the data structure, defer the rendering" — Sphinx integration is an operator-side build script not a Round-4 module. `SymbolKind` enum has five values pinned for JSON / markdown rendering stability (CLASS / DATACLASS / FUNCTION / ENUM / CONSTANT). `ApiSymbol` frozen dataclass carries qualified_name (the dotted import path like `halal_trader.web.kyc.KYCLevel`) + short_name + kind + summary (first line of docstring) + description (full docstring) + signature (kind-specific human-readable form). `ApiModule` aggregates per-module symbols + module-level summary + description. `ApiReference` is the top-level package surface across multiple modules. `extract_module_reference(module, *, include_private=False)` walks a module via `inspect.cleandoc` for docstrings, `inspect.signature` for function signatures, `dataclasses.fields` for dataclass field lists, and `__members__` for enum members. `extract_api_reference(*, package_name, modules)` covers multiple modules with deterministic alphabetical sorting by qualified_name. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **public-by-default** — symbols whose names start with `_` are skipped unless `include_private=True`; the rule applies to top-level module attributes (the introspector doesn't recurse into class methods, deferring that to the renderer if needed); (2) **deterministic ordering** — symbols sorted alphabetically within a module via `sorted(dir(module))`, modules sorted by qualified_name. The pin matters because operators diffing two reference outputs to track API changes need to see real changes, not iteration-order noise (Python dict iteration is insertion-order which is unstable across module reloads); (3) **`__all__` honoured when present** — a module declaring `__all__` exports only the listed symbols; the introspector filters by `__all__` after the public-by-default check, so the explicit list overrides the underscore-prefix heuristic. The pin matters because `__all__` is the explicit Python API contract — respecting it lets operators control the docs surface precisely; (4) **imported symbols not re-documented** — `_is_module_local` checks the value's `__module__` attribute and filters out symbols defined elsewhere (e.g., `dataclass` imported from `dataclasses` should not appear in `web/kyc`'s reference). The pin is regression-tested with the real `kyc.py` module verifying `KYCLevel` appears (defined locally) but `dataclass` doesn't (imported); a sloppy implementation that documented every importable name in the module's namespace would silently triple-count common imports; (5) **render output never includes operator secret values** — `_SECRET_NAME_FRAGMENTS` frozenset names six denylist fragments (password / secret / api_key / token / private_key / session_id); `_is_secret_name(name)` does a case-insensitive substring check; `render_markdown` outputs `<redacted>` for constants whose name matches the denylist. Mirrors the no-secret-leak patterns of Wave 8.D OTLP translator + Wave 3.B vault + Wave 12.G co-pilot — the bot's six secret-leakage boundaries share one structural denylist surface. The regression test creates a synthetic module with `API_KEY = "sk-secret-leaked"` and asserts the rendered markdown contains the constant name `API_KEY` plus `<redacted>` but never the underlying string `sk-secret-leaked` value. Signature extraction per kind: function → `func_name(params)` via `inspect.signature` (handles parameter types + defaults); dataclass → `Name(field: type, ...)` via `dataclasses.fields` (the type may be a string annotation in `from __future__ import annotations` modules — handled via `f.type.__name__` if available else `str(f.type)`); enum → `Name(MEMBER_A, MEMBER_B)` via `__members__` keys sorted; class → empty (intentional simplicity — non-dataclass non-enum classes have varied surface area; the renderer can introspect further if needed); constant → empty (the value renders separately, redacted via the secret-name denylist if applicable). Halal alignment: read-only introspection; never opens a position; the secret-name denylist is the explicit operator-IP / secret-leakage guard at the boundary leaving the bot; pure-Python (stdlib `inspect` + `dataclasses` + `enum` + `types`); no DB / network / async / HTTP; the inspection runs in-process so a malicious module can't escape into the docs surface (operators choose which modules to introspect; the engine doesn't auto-walk filesystems). Frozen dataclasses on every output (`SymbolKind` / `ApiSymbol` / `ApiModule` / `ApiReference`). 41 tests cover: **symbol classification** in five flavours (public function; public class; public dataclass; public enum; public constant — every kind correctly identified); **public-by-default pin** in two flavours (private function excluded; private constant excluded; include_private=True flag includes both); **imported-symbol filtering pin** via the real `web/kyc` module verifying KYCLevel appears (defined locally) but `dataclass` (imported from `dataclasses`) does not — the regression test that catches the most-common over-documenting bug; **`__all__`-honoured pin** via synthetic module with `__all__ = ["fn_a"]` verifying `fn_a` appears but `fn_b` doesn't; **docstring extraction** (module summary first line; function summary first line; description includes longer text; no-docstring returns empty without crashing); **signature extraction** per kind (function signature includes parameter list; dataclass signature includes fields; enum signature includes members; class signature empty for non-dataclass non-enum); **deterministic ordering pins in two flavours** (symbols sorted alphabetically within a module; modules sorted by qualified_name); ApiReference + ApiModule + ApiSymbol field validation (empty package_name / qualified_name / short_name rejected); frozen-dataclass immutability; SymbolKind string values pinned for JSON / DB stability; render output (module header includes package + module name; kind groups present "Classes" / "Dataclasses" / "Functions" / "Enums" / "Constants"; **secret-constant redacted pin** — synthetic API_KEY constant renders with `<redacted>` placeholder and the underlying value never appears in the rendered text — the structural regression check that protects against future template changes that might leak secret values into the docs surface; empty reference handled; module-with-no-symbols handled; function signature renders in code block; summary appears under header); end-to-end extraction of real modules (extract `web/kyc` and verify KYCLevel + KYCStatus + permits all in `__all__` and present in the reference; multi-module extraction across kyc + privacy with deterministic ordering preserved; real-module summary extracted; real-module symbols have summaries from their docstrings). Sphinx / MkDocs build script that consumes `extract_api_reference` and writes the rendered output to `docs/api/` (operators run `just docs-build`), the CI step that emits a warning when a public symbol gains or loses a docstring (regression-pinning docstring coverage so future contributors can't silently delete a docstring), and the `just docs-serve` recipe that regenerates the full API reference + serves locally for preview deferred to follow-ups — introspection core verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 11.E — SOC 2 readiness aggregator** — `web/soc2_readiness.py` is the pure-Python deployment-readiness aggregator for SOC 2 Type II audits — the institutional badge that hedge funds and family-office customers ask for once the bot grows past the operator-laptop deployment. SOC 2 audits are 12-month evidence-collection exercises followed by a 3-6 month auditor review; this module scores the operator's current state against the five Trust Services Categories (TSC) BEFORE the audit window opens. Mirrors the design of Wave 11.F (halal certification readiness) — same closed-set-enum + module-level-frozen-control-sets + render-no-PII pattern — applied to the SOC 2 control framework. Picked a focused readiness aggregator over an "auto-attest" flow because (a) SOC 2 audits require human auditor sign-off (the engine doesn't issue attestations; AICPA SSAE 18 requires CPA-firm review), (b) the audit-trail evidence is the operator's existing artifacts (access logs / MFA records / PR review logs / incident reports / backup runbooks / DR drill reports / vendor SOC 2 reports etc.), (c) the readiness report's actionable output — "you have 22 of 35 Security controls met, gaps are in CHANGE_MANAGEMENT and INCIDENT_RESPONSE" — lets the operator focus pre-audit work on actual gaps rather than generic "be more secure" advice. Five `TrustServiceCategory` values per AICPA TSP 100-2017 (SECURITY mandatory for every SOC 2 audit; AVAILABILITY / PROCESSING_INTEGRITY / CONFIDENTIALITY / PRIVACY optional but most institutional customers expect Security + Availability + Confidentiality at minimum — pinned with stable string values for DB / JSON migration safety). Ten `ControlCategory` labels mapping to AICPA Common Criteria families (ACCESS_CONTROL → CC6; CHANGE_MANAGEMENT → CC8; SYSTEM_OPERATIONS → CC7; RISK_ASSESSMENT → CC3; INCIDENT_RESPONSE → CC7.4; LOGICAL_SECURITY → CC6.1; MONITORING → CC4; BUSINESS_CONTINUITY → A1.2; VENDOR_MANAGEMENT → CC9; DATA_CLASSIFICATION → C1.1). Two `ControlSeverity` levels (BLOCKING — gap blocks the audit; WARNING — auditor will note but doesn't block). Nineteen `EvidenceKind` artifact labels covering the full operator-side audit trail (ACCESS_LOGS / MFA_ENABLED / PR_REVIEW_LOGS / DEPLOYMENT_LOGS / BACKUP_RECORDS / INCIDENT_REPORTS / DR_DRILL_REPORTS / VULNERABILITY_SCANS / PEN_TEST_REPORTS / EMPLOYEE_ONBOARDING / EMPLOYEE_OFFBOARDING / SECURITY_TRAINING / VENDOR_SOC2_REPORTS / RISK_REGISTER / DATA_CLASSIFICATION_POLICY / ENCRYPTION_AT_REST / ENCRYPTION_IN_TRANSIT / UPTIME_MONITORING / STATUS_PAGE) — pinned values let operators populate the evidence catalogue deterministically without free-form artifact names that could silently mismatch a control. Two `AuditType` values (TYPE_I point-in-time attestation with 30-day default horizon; TYPE_II 12-month observation window where the auditor verifies controls are operating effectively over time). Four-level `ReadinessLevel` ladder (READY / NEARLY_READY / GAPS / NOT_READY). Module-level frozen control catalogue: 10 Security controls (CC6.1 logical access controls + ACCESS_LOGS evidence; CC6.2 MFA on admin and user access + MFA_ENABLED — the load-bearing security pin; CC6.3 onboarding/offboarding documented; CC7.1 vulnerability scans with remediation tracking; CC7.4 incident-response procedures with documented incidents; CC8.1 code changes through PR review with documented approvals — the change-management pin; CC9.1 vendor SOC 2 reports collected — warning severity; CC3.2 annual risk assessment with documented register; CC2.3 annual security training — warning; CC6.7 annual penetration testing — warning); 4 Availability controls (A1.1 uptime monitoring with documented SLA targets; A1.2 backup procedures with point-in-time recovery — composes with Wave 8.F backups runbook; A1.3 disaster recovery drills documented — composes with Wave 8.C drill runbook; A1.4 public status page for service disruptions — warning, composes with Wave 8.G status snapshot); 3 Confidentiality controls (C1.1 data classification policy; C1.2 encryption at rest — the load-bearing data-protection pin, composes with Wave 3.B vault; C1.3 encryption in transit). Processing Integrity + Privacy ship empty for operator-side extension (Privacy partly covered by Wave 11.D GDPR/CCPA engine; the remaining SOC 2 PI / PR controls are operator-bundled per their specific deployment). `SOC2ReadinessPolicy` defaults: `audit_type=TYPE_II` (the institutional standard), `evidence_horizon_days=365` (Type II requires 12-month observation; Type I uses 30-day default). `evaluate_soc2_readiness(*, trust_services, evidence, now, policy)` returns a `SOC2ReadinessReport` with per-trust-service breakdown plus the overall verdict computed as the strictest of the per-service levels. The per-service evaluator uses the same readiness ladder as Wave 11.F (0 blocking + 0 warning + 0 stale → READY; blocking met, warnings/stale present → NEARLY_READY; 1-2 blocking gaps → GAPS; ≥3 blocking → NOT_READY). **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **closed Trust Services Category set** per AICPA TSP 100-2017 — operators add controls within a category via code review; runtime config drift can't introduce a non-AICPA category; (2) **control catalogue module-level frozen** — `_SECURITY_CONTROLS` + `_AVAILABILITY_CONTROLS` + `_CONFIDENTIALITY_CONTROLS` are top-level constants; runtime mutation can't weaken the required-evidence floor before an audit window opens (the most-insidious failure mode would be a deployment that lowers control requirements in production-config just before the audit submission — the structural friction prevents it); (3) **critical-control gap → BLOCKING** — missing MFA on admin access is BLOCKING (operator can't pass the audit); missing customer-facing status page is WARNING (auditor will note but doesn't block). The severity differentiation matters because conflating hard requirements with nice-to-haves would either over- or under-report readiness; (4) **Type II default 12-month evidence horizon** with operator-tunable `evidence_horizon_days`; the Type I 30-day default catches recent operational changes that haven't yet been observed for the 12-month window. Boundary at exactly horizon-day is stale (pinned via test); evidence with `last_updated=None` (no timestamp) also stale; (5) **render output never includes operator-identifying detail** — the report references abstract evidence-kind labels (e.g., "access_logs: present, refreshed 30d ago") never raw user IDs / IP addresses / audit-trail contents (the regression test asserts neither "user_id" nor "ip_address" nor `10.0.0` nor `192.168` IP-shaped strings appear in the rendered output). Mirrors no-PII patterns of Wave 11.D privacy + Wave 11.C KYC + Wave 3.B vault + Wave 11.F halal certification — every public-facing render in this codebase shares one defensive surface. **Multi-service overall verdict = strictest per-service level** — operator picks their target service set (typical institutional combination: SECURITY + AVAILABILITY + CONFIDENTIALITY); the report flags the weakest service. The strictest-wins pin matters because the auditor doesn't pass the operator on three services and fail one — the audit succeeds or fails as a unit. Halal alignment: SOC 2 readiness is operational compliance not shariah compliance, but the no-PII render contract carries the same defensive boundary; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`SOC2Control` / `EvidenceArtifact` / `SOC2ReadinessPolicy` / `ControlAssessment` / `TrustServiceReport` / `SOC2ReadinessReport`). 47 tests cover: policy validation (zero / negative horizon rejected; Type I + 30-day horizon accepted); per-trust-service control-set queries (Security CC6.1 + CC6.2 + CC8.1 present; Availability A1.1 + A1.2; Confidentiality C1.2 + C1.3 encryption — the pin matters because encryption is the load-bearing data-protection control; Processing Integrity + Privacy empty by design); control + artifact field validation; **READY happy paths in three flavours** (Security only; Security+Availability; three-service combo); **NOT_READY pins** (no evidence; ≥3 blocking gaps); GAPS (1 blocking gap); NEARLY_READY (only warnings unmet — drop pen-test + security-training + vendor-soc2 which are warning-severity); **stale-evidence pins in four flavours** (>365d Type II → stale + nearly_ready; Type I 30-day catches 60-day artifact; no last_updated → stale; exactly-365d boundary inclusive); empty-PROCESSING_INTEGRITY → NOT_READY with note (the operator-extension sentinel); **multi-service overall verdict pin** (one ready + one not-ready → overall not_ready; one ready + one gaps → overall gaps — the strictest-wins pin); overall_met_pct aggregates correctly across services; input validation (naive now rejected; empty trust_services rejected); frozen-dataclass immutability across all six output types; all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability across TrustServiceCategory + AuditType + ControlSeverity + EvidenceKind + ReadinessLevel; render output across all four levels with emoji (✅ READY / 🟢 NEARLY_READY / ⚠️ GAPS / ❌ NOT_READY) + audit_type label + per-service breakdown showing met/total counts + percentage + per-service level + blocking-gap counts when > 0 + warning counts + stale counts; **the no-user-PII pin** asserts user_id / ip_address / 10.0.0 / 192.168 IP-shaped strings never in render output; and four end-to-end realistic scenarios (typical pre-audit Security-only with all blocking met but warnings unmet → NEARLY_READY; full three-service institutional set with complete evidence → READY; partial-evidence flow with Availability gap dropping overall to GAPS — the realistic mid-pre-audit case; assessment-count-matches-controls regression). Postgres `soc2_evidence` + `soc2_audit_log` + `soc2_remediation_tasks` tables wired to `db/repository.py`, the FastAPI route adapters (`/api/soc2/readiness` for the multi-service overview; `/api/soc2/{trust_service}/readiness` for per-service drill-down; `/api/soc2/gaps` for the actionable remediation list), the dashboard's SOC 2 tile rendering per-service progress with the actionable-gaps list + readiness arrow, the per-day CI step that emits a readiness warning when any required evidence's `last_updated` falls past the operator's horizon (catches stale evidence before audit time), the operator-extension flow for adding Processing Integrity + Privacy controls bundled per their specific deployment, and an audit-evidence-export utility that bundles all the artifacts + their hashes into a single ZIP for submission to the SOC 2 auditor deferred to follow-ups — aggregator verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 4.C — Causal regime detection** — `ml/causal_regime.py` is the pure-Python discrete Bayesian network for macro→regime inference with do-calculus intervention support. The roadmap calls for replacing the rule-based regime detector (`crypto/regime.py`) with a causal model that takes current macro state (rates, VIX, dollar index, sector breadth) and outputs a probability distribution over regimes gating strategy selection. Wave 4.D landed the correlation-based fusion engine (`core/cross_asset_signal.py`); this wave ships the **causal** counterpart — a discrete Bayesian network supporting **do-calculus interventions** ("what if I intervened to set VIX=40?") distinct from observations ("VIX is currently 40"). The distinction matters operationally: observation `vix=CRISIS` propagates through the graph via Bayes' rule (and updates upstream beliefs about rates_change because rates_change → vix); intervention `do(vix=CRISIS)` does NOT update upstream beliefs because we *forced* vix to that state regardless of its parents. Intervention is the right primitive for "stress test" / "what-if" scenarios; observation is the right primitive for inference from real-time data. **Picked discrete Bayesian network with brute-force enumeration** over sample-based methods because (a) the graph has 5 variables with 3 states each (3^5 = 243 cells) so brute force is fast and exact, (b) operators can read the CPTs and debug a misfire at the source rather than re-tuning an opaque sampler, (c) sample-based methods (Gibbs, importance) require burn-in and convergence checks operationally tedious for a per-cycle hot path. The full pgmpy-style symbolic engine would be over-kill; we ship the small focused engine the bot actually needs. Six discrete state enums: `RatesLevel` (LOW < 2% / NORMAL 2-5% / HIGH > 5%); `RatesChange` (EASING / HOLDING / TIGHTENING with the 6-month-lookback semantic); `VIXState` (CALM < 15 / ELEVATED 15-25 / CRISIS > 25); `DXYState` (WEAK / NORMAL / STRONG); `BreadthState` (NEGATIVE < 30% / MIXED 30-70% / POSITIVE > 70% sectors above 50-day MA); `Regime` target (RISK_ON / NEUTRAL / RISK_OFF / CRISIS). The graph structure: rates_change → vix; rates_level → dxy; vix → breadth; (vix, dxy, breadth) → regime. Module-level frozen CPTs with documented hand-tuned values reflecting operator's macro mental model: priors P(rates_level), P(rates_change); P(vix | rates_change) — tightening cycles → more crisis risk; P(dxy | rates_level) — higher rates → stronger dollar; P(breadth | vix) — high VIX → negative breadth; P(regime | vix, dxy, breadth) — 27 cells covering every (vix, dxy, breadth) combination. `MacroEvidence` and `MacroIntervention` are frozen dataclasses with optional fields for each variable; `infer_regime(*, evidence, intervention)` returns a `RegimeInferenceResult` with the full distribution + most_likely + confidence + warnings. The inference algorithm enumerates all 3^5 = 243 joint assignments × 4 regimes = 972 cell evaluations; each evaluation computes the joint probability with the intervention's delta-function for forced variables (skipping their CPT contribution and zeroing out non-matching assignments); evidence-matched assignments are summed into the regime marginal; the result is renormalised to handle float drift. **Six pinned safety semantics**: (1) **closed variable + state set** — `MacroVariable` lists the five inputs + the regime output; each has a closed `*State` enum. Adding a variable or state is a code-review change with regression-tested CPT updates; (2) **CPTs module-level frozen** — runtime config drift can't change the conditional probabilities; operators tune via code review with regression-tested before/after distributions; (3) **intervention overrides observation** — when both are provided for the same variable, intervention wins and a warning is emitted. The pin matters because the most-insidious bug would be silently treating the observation as the truth when the operator explicitly intended to stress-test; (4) **partial evidence supported** — operator can supply observations for any subset of variables; the engine marginalises out the rest. Empty evidence returns the prior P(regime) — pinned via test; (5) **probability distributions sum to 1.0 within tolerance** — inference outputs are renormalised at the end so float drift doesn't accumulate. Pinned via the every-call distribution-sum invariant; (6) **render output shows regime marginal as percentages** plus most-likely + confidence + bar chart visualisation; doesn't dump raw CPT cells (operators audit the source if they want raw numbers). Halal alignment: read-only inference; never opens a position; the regime distribution gates strategy selection upstream of the executor; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum`); no NumPy / scipy / DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`MacroEvidence` / `MacroIntervention` / `RegimeInferenceResult`). The brute-force enumeration is < 1ms in the per-cycle hot path; deterministic for a given input. 43 tests cover empty-evidence-returns-prior; **distribution-sums-to-1 invariant pin**; every regime has a probability; **single-variable observation pins** (CALM VIX skews RISK_ON; CRISIS VIX skews CRISIS+RISK_OFF; negative/positive breadth correctly skews); full-evidence scenarios (full RISK_ON config → RISK_ON; full CRISIS config → CRISIS or RISK_OFF; NEUTRAL middle config → NEUTRAL); confidence properties (equals most-likely probability — the load-bearing definitional pin; in [0, 1]; full evidence locks to the specific CPT cell — the regression test directly imports the CPT and verifies the distribution matches); **do-calculus intervention pins** in six flavours (single-variable intervention forces state regardless of upstream evidence; intervention does not propagate upstream — verified by comparing observation vs intervention behaviour; multi-variable simultaneous intervention; **intervention-overrides-evidence-with-warning** for same-field collision — the load-bearing pin emits the explicit "intervention wins" warning); no-intervention-no-warnings pin; result fields preserved through to the audit (evidence_used + intervention_used both reflected); frozen-dataclass immutability across MacroEvidence + MacroIntervention + RegimeInferenceResult; all six enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability (15 individual value pins across the six enums); render output (most-likely with regime emoji 🟢⚪🟠🔴; distribution bar chart with per-regime percentage; do(...) clause when intervention set; warnings shown when collision detected); end-to-end realistic scenarios — **2008 GFC macro state** (HIGH rates + EASING + CRISIS VIX + STRONG DXY flight-to-dollar + NEGATIVE breadth → RISK_OFF + CRISIS combined > 70%); **late-2020 recovery** (LOW rates + EASING + CALM VIX + WEAK DXY + POSITIVE breadth → RISK_ON > 70% confidence); **what-if-VIX-doubles intervention** (today is calm but stress-test the regime under a forced CRISIS-VIX scenario without changing other observations — demonstrates the intervention's distinct semantics from observation); partial-evidence-marginalises-over-unknowns; CPT structural validation (every cell of P(regime | vix, dxy, breadth) sums to 1.0 — the math-correctness pin; complete coverage of all 27 (vix, dxy, breadth) combinations — the comprehensiveness pin guards against missing entries that would silently zero out a region of the joint). Live macro-data ingest (FRED API for rates; Yahoo / CBOE for VIX; ICE for DXY; sector-breadth computed from constituent ETF closes vs 50-day MA), Postgres `macro_observations` + `regime_inferences` tables wired to `db/repository.py`, the per-cycle hook that infers the regime + feeds it into `crypto/strategy.py` for regime-gated entries (composes with the existing rule-based regime detector during a transition period — both signals shown side-by-side for operator validation before flipping the gate), the dashboard's regime tile rendering the full distribution as a stacked bar with the most-likely arrow + intervention-mode toggle for stress-testing, and an automated weekly back-test that compares the causal-regime classifier's predictions against rule-based for the same week's data deferred to follow-ups — engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 11.F — Certification readiness aggregator** — `halal/certification_readiness.py` is the pure-Python deployment-readiness aggregator that scores the operator's current state against each halal-certification body's requirement set BEFORE the application is submitted. The roadmap pins halal certification from a recognised authority (AAOIFI / Saudi Tadawul / Malaysian SAC / Bahrain CBB / Indonesia DSN-MUI) as the badge that unlocks institutional adoption in Muslim-majority markets — the actual application + audit + on-site review takes 3-12 months end-to-end, but the deployment-readiness check is operator-driven pre-application work the bot can automate. Picked a focused readiness aggregator over an "auto-certify" flow because (a) certification bodies require human auditor sign-off (the engine doesn't issue certificates), (b) the audit-trail evidence is the operator's *existing* artifacts produced by previously-landed waves (Wave 2.A signed receipts; Wave 2.D purification ledger; Wave 11.B SSB rulings + quarterly reviews; Wave 11.C KYC verified users + AML sanctions screening; Wave 11.D privacy policy), and (c) the readiness report's actionable output — "you have 8 of 12 AAOIFI requirements met, the 4 gaps are in PURIFICATION_LEDGER and SSB_GOVERNANCE" — lets the operator focus pre-application work on the actual gaps rather than generic "be more shariah-compliant" advice. Five `CertificationBody` values with pinned BCP-style string values (AAOIFI / SAUDI_TADAWUL / MALAYSIAN_SAC / BAHRAIN_CBB / INDONESIA_DSN_MUI) — closed enum, operators add via code review. Six `RequirementCategory` labels (SCREENING / AUDIT / PURIFICATION / SSB_GOVERNANCE / KYC_AML / DOCUMENTATION) — operators routing to per-category dashboards key on these. Two `RequirementSeverity` levels (BLOCKING — gap prevents certification; WARNING — flagged but doesn't block). Ten `EvidenceArtifactKind` labels precisely matching the existing Round-4 artifacts so the operator's persistence layer maps deterministically (HALAL_SCREENER_DECISIONS for Wave 1.I + 2.B + 2.G; SIGNED_TRADE_RECEIPTS for Wave 2.A; PURIFICATION_LEDGER for Wave 2.D; SSB_RULINGS + SSB_QUARTERLY_REVIEWS for Wave 11.B; KYC_VERIFIED_USERS + AML_SANCTIONS_SCREENING for Wave 11.C; ANNUAL_AUDIT_REPORT; PUBLIC_PRIVACY_POLICY for Wave 11.D; SHARIAH_AUDIT_REPORT). Four `ReadinessLevel`s (READY / NEARLY_READY / GAPS / NOT_READY). Per-body requirement sets pinned via module-level frozen tuples: AAOIFI has 7 requirements across S21 (Standard 21 — Financial Paper, Shares and Bonds), GS (Governance Standards), and S17 (Standard 17 — Investment Sukuk); Tadawul has 4 (Halal Stock Index methodology + Saudi-jurisdiction KYC + OFAC/UN/Saudi sanctions screening + SOCPA-licensed annual audit); Malaysian SAC has 3 (SC Malaysia Shariah list + SAC-recognised advisor panel + annual purification disclosure); Bahrain CBB + Indonesia DSN-MUI start empty for operator-side extension. `CertificationRequirement` carries body + spec_id (the body's own reference like "AAOIFI-S21-2.3" — operators cite this in application paperwork) + category + severity + description + expected_artifact. `EvidenceArtifact` is the operator's evidence: kind + present (boolean) + last_updated (timezone-aware required when set; None accepted for "no timestamp recorded" → treated as stale). `ReadinessPolicy` defaults to `staleness_horizon_days=180` (six months — typical certification-body re-attestation cadence); operators in stricter jurisdictions drop to 90 days. `evaluate_readiness(*, body, evidence, now, policy)` returns a `ReadinessReport` with overall_level + per-requirement assessments + counts + per-category breakdown. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **closed body set** — operators add a new body via code review with bundled requirement set + regression test that exercises the spec_ids; runtime config drift can't introduce an unsupported body; (2) **per-body requirements module-level frozen** — the requirement-tuple is a top-level constant; runtime mutation can't silently weaken the floor (the most-insidious failure mode would be a deployment that lowers AAOIFI requirements just before submitting an application — the structural friction prevents this); (3) **critical-requirement gap → BLOCKING** — missing SSB ruling for AAOIFI is BLOCKING (operator can't even apply); missing privacy policy is WARNING (apply but flagged for the auditor's follow-up question). The severity differentiation matters because certification bodies care about hard requirements vs nice-to-haves and conflating them would either over- or under-report readiness; (4) **stale evidence (> 180d default) → WARNING** — the operator's certified evidence is presumed valid for six months; past that the artifact needs refresh because (a) certification bodies request re-attestation on a six-month cadence, and (b) data older than that may not reflect the current operational reality. Boundary at exactly 180d is stale (pinned both directions); evidence with `last_updated=None` (no timestamp recorded) also stale because we can't verify recency; custom 90d strict policy catches 100d-old artifacts (the customisation-flow regression-pin); (5) **render output never includes operator-identifying detail** — the readiness report references abstract artifact-kind labels (e.g., "ssb-ruling: present, refreshed 30d ago") never raw rule_id contents, member names, KYC secrets, or any per-user data. Mirrors the no-PII patterns of Wave 11.D privacy + Wave 11.C KYC + Wave 3.B vault + the no-PII regression-pin patterns of every other Round-4 wave — every public-facing render in this codebase shares one defensive surface. The **ReadinessLevel ladder decision tree**: 0 blocking unmet + 0 warning unmet + 0 stale → READY; 0 blocking unmet + (any warning or stale) → NEARLY_READY (the operator can apply but the auditor will ask follow-up questions); 1-2 blocking unmet → GAPS (the operator must close these before applying); ≥3 blocking unmet → NOT_READY (multiple structural gaps; pre-application work is substantial). Halal alignment: read-only aggregation; never opens a position; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`CertificationRequirement` / `EvidenceArtifact` / `ReadinessPolicy` / `RequirementAssessment` / `ReadinessReport`). 47 tests cover: policy validation (zero / negative staleness rejected); per-body requirement-set queries (AAOIFI populated with 7 reqs including S21-2.1 + GS-1.1; Tadawul with KYC-2.1 + AML-2.2; SAC with RES-1; Bahrain + Indonesia empty by design — pin matters because the empty-body case is the operator-extends-via-code-review default and confusing it for a "spec missing in this build" failure would mis-route the application); requirement validation (empty spec_id + empty description rejected); artifact validation (naive datetime rejected; None accepted); **READY** happy path (all AAOIFI artifacts present + recent → READY with 100% met_pct + zero blocking + zero warning + zero stale); **NOT_READY in two flavours** (no evidence at all → NOT_READY; ≥3 blocking gaps → NOT_READY); **GAPS in two flavours** (1 blocking gap; 2 blocking gaps — the boundary pin matters because GAPS upper threshold is 2; 3+ becomes NOT_READY); **NEARLY_READY** (drop PUBLIC_PRIVACY_POLICY which is warning-severity → blocking met, warning unmet → NEARLY_READY); **stale-artifact pins in five flavours** (200d-old artifact → stale + nearly_ready; **exactly-180d boundary inclusive** is stale; 179d fresh — the asymmetry pin; **None last_updated → stale** with "no timestamp" note; **strict 90d policy catches 100d artifact** — the customisation flow); **empty-body pin** (Bahrain CBB → NOT_READY with "requirement set for bahrain_cbb is empty — operator must load the spec" note; the structural sentinel that prevents an operator from accidentally evaluating an unloaded body); evaluate input validation (naive now rejected); per-requirement assessment count matches requirements; **unmet assessment carries note** ("missing artifact (BLOCKING)" with severity surfaced); **stale assessment carries note** with day count; frozen-dataclass immutability across CertificationRequirement + EvidenceArtifact + ReadinessReport + ReadinessPolicy; all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability across body / category / severity / artifact_kind / level (15 enum value pins total — every value tested against its expected string for migration safety); render output across all four levels with emoji (✅ READY / 🟢 NEARLY_READY / ⚠️ GAPS / ❌ NOT_READY) + body name + met_pct + blocking-gap count when > 0 + warning count + stale count + per-requirement breakdown showing spec_id + category + severity for each assessment; **the no-operator-PII pin** asserts "user_id" / "ssn" / "passport" never appear in the rendered output — guards against future template changes that might inject operator-identifying detail; and three end-to-end realistic flows — typical pre-AAOIFI-application readiness flow (operator has screening + signing + purification + SSB rulings + privacy policy but missing SSB_QUARTERLY_REVIEWS + SHARIAH_AUDIT_REPORT → 2 blocking unmet → GAPS, the realistic "we have most things but two big audit-side gaps" case); Tadawul-readiness flow (the four Tadawul requirements all met → READY, demonstrating cross-body applicability); Malaysian SAC readiness with warning-severity purification gap only (blocking met, only warning unmet → NEARLY_READY — the typical "ready to apply but auditor will note one item" case). Postgres `certification_evidence` + `readiness_history` tables wired to `db/repository.py`, the FastAPI route adapters (`/api/certification/bodies` listing supported bodies + their spec; `/api/certification/{body}/readiness` returning the current assessment; `/api/certification/{body}/gaps` returning just the blocking gaps), the dashboard's certification-readiness tile rendering per-body progress with the actionable-gaps list, a per-day CI step that emits a readiness warning when any required artifact's `last_updated` falls past the operator's staleness horizon (catches stale evidence before audit time), the operator-extension flow for adding Bahrain CBB + Indonesia DSN-MUI requirement sets (since they ship empty for operator review), and an audit-evidence-export utility that bundles all the artifacts + their hashes into a single ZIP for submission to the certification body deferred to follow-ups — aggregator verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 12.B — Halal options-strategy screener** — `web/halal_options.py` is the pure-Python halal screener for option strategies that composes with the Wave 11.B SSB governance engine. The roadmap pins options as scholar-debated: classical fiqh treats most options trading as gharar (excessive uncertainty) because the option contract pays for a *right* not an asset, and the seller commits to deliver something they may not own. Modern AAOIFI guidance and a growing minority of scholars carve out a narrow permissible set — covered calls (writer owns the underlying so selling the right to deliver isn't gharar; classical *urbun* analogy), cash-secured puts (writer can deliver cash to buy shares; murabaha-pre-commitment analogy), protective puts (buying insurance — defined premium for defined coverage, classical sale of *amanah*), with naked calls/puts and multi-leg spreads with embedded short legs categorically rejected. Full integration deferred (the bot doesn't trade options today and won't until the SSB issues a clear ruling) but the screener ships **the rule** so when SSB approves a specific strategy, the dashboard routes through the gate first. Thirteen `OptionStrategy` values across four classes plus an OTHER catchall: single-leg longs (LONG_CALL / LONG_PUT — debated by classical fiqh because the buyer is paying premium for uncertainty); naked shorts (NAKED_CALL / NAKED_PUT — unconditional gharar; classical + modern consensus); covered structures (COVERED_CALL — writer owns underlying; CASH_SECURED_PUT — writer holds cash equal to strike × 100; PROTECTIVE_PUT — buyer holds underlying and buys put as insurance); multi-leg spreads (BULL_CALL_SPREAD + BEAR_PUT_SPREAD + IRON_CONDOR + BUTTERFLY + STRADDLE + STRANGLE — every one embeds at least one short leg without underlying or cash backing). Five `OptionsScreenVerdict` values: HALAL (PROTECTIVE_PUT default + SSB-permitted with no other concern); NOT_HALAL (naked / spreads / non-halal underlying); DOUBTFUL (debated strategies pending SSB); HALAL_WITH_CONDITIONS (debated strategy with operator's SSB ruling cited); UNKNOWN (OTHER catchall). `OptionsScreenPolicy` carries the operator's `ssb_ruling_id` (the Wave 11.B ruling that approves the debated strategies) and `permitted_with_ssb_ruling` (the explicit allow-list of debated strategies the operator's SSB has approved). The policy's `__post_init__` enforces two construction-time guards: (a) **`permitted_with_ssb_ruling` non-empty requires `ssb_ruling_id`** — no auditable conditional approval without a citable ruling; the audit trail must point to the specific SSB document that justified the verdict escalation; (b) **operator can only opt-in to debated strategies, not gharar strategies** — the policy refuses to accept `NAKED_CALL` or `IRON_CONDOR` in `permitted_with_ssb_ruling` even if a creative operator tries to bypass via config. The construction-time refusal is the load-bearing structural pin: even an operator with the most flexible scholar profile cannot accidentally (or intentionally) opt-in to the categorically-forbidden strategies, because the engine raises before the policy is even constructed. Three module-level frozen sets organise the strategies: `_GHARAR_NAKED_STRATEGIES` (NAKED_CALL + NAKED_PUT); `_GHARAR_SPREAD_STRATEGIES` (every spread + straddle + strangle); `_DEBATED_STRATEGIES` (COVERED_CALL + CASH_SECURED_PUT + LONG_CALL + LONG_PUT); `_PERMITTED_STRATEGIES` (PROTECTIVE_PUT only). `OptionsScreenRequest` carries the strategy + underlying_symbol + `underlying_is_halal_screened` boolean — the underlying-screened gate is the first check, before strategy classification, because even a HALAL strategy on a non-halal-screened underlying inherits the underlying's haram status. `screen_options_strategy(request, *, policy)` is the entry point. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **closed strategy enum** — the OTHER catchall surfaces unrecognised combinations as UNKNOWN with a "classify before allocating" warning; the safe-block default protects against exotic combinations (calendar spreads, ratio spreads, jade lizards, even more obscure stuff) the engine doesn't recognise; the operator must classify them via Wave 2.F scholar review queue first; (2) **NAKED_CALL / NAKED_PUT unconditionally NOT_HALAL** — no scholar ruling reverses these per classical and modern consensus; the policy construction guard refuses to accept them in any allow-list (regression-pinned with the explicit "operator tries to add NAKED_CALL → ValueError" test); (3) **multi-leg spreads with any short leg unconditionally NOT_HALAL** — a bull-call spread embeds a naked-call short leg; iron condor / butterfly / straddle / strangle all the same; the spread's long leg does NOT redeem the short leg's gharar (the operational + theological point: hedging gharar with another contract doesn't dissolve it). Construction guard same as for naked legs; (4) **COVERED_CALL / CASH_SECURED_PUT / LONG_CALL / LONG_PUT DOUBTFUL by default** with SSB-citable escalation — operator's Wave 11.B SSB issues a ruling (typically PERMISSIBLE_WITH_CONDITIONS); operator cites the ruling_id in the policy's `ssb_ruling_id` field and adds the strategy to `permitted_with_ssb_ruling`; the screener returns HALAL_WITH_CONDITIONS instead of DOUBTFUL with the ruling_id surfaced in the audit trail. Selective approval pin: an operator approving COVERED_CALL but not CASH_SECURED_PUT keeps the latter at DOUBTFUL; (5) **PROTECTIVE_PUT HALAL by default** — the cleanest case (insurance: defined premium for defined coverage, no gharar); doesn't need SSB approval. The **underlying-halal-screened gate** runs first: even PROTECTIVE_PUT on a non-halal-screened underlying blocks NOT_HALAL because the strategy inherits the underlying's status. Render output never includes contract symbols (full OPRA-style), strike prices, or expiration dates — mirrors no-PII / no-financial-detail patterns of Wave 11.D + 11.C + 3.B + 12.E + 12.G + 12.C — every public-facing render in this codebase shares one defensive surface; the engine's data shape doesn't even hold strike / expiry fields, so the no-leak pin is structural. Halal alignment: read-only screening; never opens a position; the construction-time guard against approving categorical gharar is the structural guarantee that no operator misconfiguration can authorise haram trading; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`OptionsScreenPolicy` / `OptionsScreenRequest` / `OptionsScreenResult`). 51 tests cover: policy validation (default no SSB approval; ssb_ruling_id required when permitting; **NAKED_CALL / NAKED_PUT / IRON_CONDOR / BUTTERFLY explicitly rejected from permitted set** at construction — the construction-guard pin in four flavours; COVERED_CALL + CASH_SECURED_PUT + multi-strategy combinations accepted with ruling_id); request validation (empty / whitespace underlying); the **underlying-halal-screened gate pin** in three flavours (PROTECTIVE_PUT blocked when underlying not screened; COVERED_CALL blocked; LONG_CALL blocked — the inheritance pin); **naked-strategy pins** in three flavours (NAKED_CALL → NOT_HALAL with gharar message; NAKED_PUT same; even with halal underlying + SSB approval of debated, naked still NOT_HALAL — the override-everything pin); **spread-strategy pins** in six flavours (BULL_CALL_SPREAD with "short leg" message; BEAR_PUT_SPREAD; IRON_CONDOR; BUTTERFLY; STRADDLE; STRANGLE — every multi-leg structure categorically blocked; the comprehensive coverage pin); PROTECTIVE_PUT happy path (HALAL with no failures or warnings; works without any SSB ruling — the cleanest case pin); **debated-strategy default-DOUBTFUL pins** in four flavours (COVERED_CALL with scholar-debated message; CASH_SECURED_PUT; LONG_CALL — paying premium for uncertainty; LONG_PUT); **SSB-approval escalation pins** in three flavours (COVERED_CALL with SSB-2026-Q1-001 → HALAL_WITH_CONDITIONS with cited ruling_id surfaced; CASH_SECURED_PUT with different ruling_id; **selective approval** — operator approves COVERED_CALL but not CASH_SECURED_PUT, the latter remains DOUBTFUL — the asymmetry pin matters because per-strategy granularity is the operator's expected configuration model); OTHER → UNKNOWN with classify-first warning; frozen-dataclass immutability across OptionsScreenRequest + OptionsScreenResult + OptionsScreenPolicy; all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability across all 13 strategies + 5 verdicts; render output across all five verdicts with emoji per verdict (✅ HALAL / ❌ NOT_HALAL / ⚠️ DOUBTFUL / 📋 HALAL_WITH_CONDITIONS / ❓ UNKNOWN — distinct emojis matter because the dashboard renders different actions per verdict); HALAL_WITH_CONDITIONS render includes the ssb_ruling_cited field; **the no-strike-or-expiry pin** asserts neither "strike" nor "expiry" nor "expires" appears in the rendered output — guards against future template changes injecting financial details that operators audit on the broker side; **closed-set guarantees** for naked / spread / debated sets via category-coverage tests (every member of each set behaves correctly — the comprehensive coverage pin protects against future additions to the enum without test coverage); and four end-to-end realistic flows — typical PROTECTIVE_PUT journey for downside hedge against owned AAPL → HALAL; covered-call-with-SSB-ruling journey (operator owns AAPL + SSB-2026-Q1-001 permits COVERED_CALL + CASH_SECURED_PUT with conditions; operator writes covered call → HALAL_WITH_CONDITIONS with the ruling cited prominently); attempted-iron-condor-blocked-via-policy-construction (even an operator with an SSB ruling can't add IRON_CONDOR to `permitted_with_ssb_ruling` — the policy construction itself raises ValueError; the most-creative-jailbreak-blocked pin); result-shape sanity (preserves strategy + underlying through to the audit trail). Live options-chain ingest (Tradier / IBKR options API adapter behind an `OptionsChainProvider` Protocol), strategy-construction layer (compose multi-leg orders from individual legs at the route layer; the screener doesn't construct, it only classifies), exit management (profit-target / stop-loss + delta-hedging routines for the live-trading side), Postgres `options_strategies` + `options_audit_log` tables wired to `db/repository.py`, the FastAPI route adapters (`/api/options/screen` for ad-hoc screening; `/api/options/strategies` listing screened proposals; `/api/options/positions` for open-position tracking), and the dashboard's options tile rendering historical strategy proposals with their verdicts deferred to follow-ups — screener verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 12.C — On-chain settlement route screener** — `web/settlement_route.py` is the pure-Python halal screener for proposed DEX swap routes. The roadmap pins on-chain settlement as the long-term escape from centralised-exchange counterparty risk: instead of trusting Binance to honour fills, the bot routes a halal-token swap through a DEX on Ethereum / Solana / a Layer 2. Full integration is deferred (a live router needs both the swap-construction side AND the per-cycle gas/MEV strategy), but the **route-screen logic** is operator-supplied / CSV-fed pure-Python, exactly the isolated-module pattern of every Round-4 wave. DEX settlement raises concerns the centralised-exchange path doesn't: liquidity model (constant-product + concentrated-LP HALAL because the swap is a price-discovered exchange of two permissible tokens at a deterministic price; off-chain order books raise gharar because the matched price isn't fixed at submission and the relayer's shariah status is unclear); MEV exposure (a swap submitted to public mempool without protection can be sandwich-attacked — operationally inferior even if not haram per se); slippage tolerance (5% widely accepted; > 10% raises gharar concerns about price-move-on-fill consent); smart contract audit (an unaudited router is a custody-mechanism gharar concern); cross-chain bridge use (bridges add custody + liveness assumption); routing token (a swap through a non-halal intermediate inherits its concerns). Six `SettlementChain` values (ETHEREUM_MAINNET / OPTIMISM / ARBITRUM / BASE / POLYGON / SOLANA_MAINNET) — closed enum, operators add new chains via code review. Nine `DEXProtocol` values (UNISWAP_V3 / V4 / SUSHISWAP / CURVE / BALANCER / AGGREGATOR_1INCH / JUPITER / RAYDIUM / OTHER). Six `LiquidityModel` values with `_HALAL_LIQUIDITY_MODELS` frozenset (CONSTANT_PRODUCT + CONCENTRATED_LP + STABLE_CURVE + ORDER_BOOK_ON_CHAIN pass — the on-chain orderbook pin matters because dYdX V4 + Hyperliquid use this model; ORDER_BOOK_OFF_CHAIN drives DOUBTFUL with gharar warning; UNKNOWN → INSUFFICIENT_DATA). Four `MEVProtection` values (NATIVE_PROTECTION CowSwap-style / FLASHBOTS private mempool / MEV_BLOCKER private RPC pass; NONE → DOUBTFUL). Five `IntermediateTokenStatus` values with `_FORBIDDEN_INTERMEDIATES` closed frozenset (FORBIDDEN → NOT_HALAL; DEBATED_STABLECOIN USDT-shaped → DOUBTFUL; HALAL_STABLECOIN USDC + HALAL_NATIVE ETH/SOL + NONE direct-swap pass). Reuses Wave 12.E's `SmartContractAudit` four-tier ladder — a router contract audited by Trail of Bits + Quantstamp passes the same standard as a tokenised-RE custody contract. `SettlementRoutePolicy` defaults: `max_acceptable_slippage_pct=5.0` with `> 10` rejected at construction (gharar threshold); `soft_slippage_warning_pct=2.0` (drives DOUBTFUL warning between 2% and max); `flag_off_chain_orderbook=True`; `require_mev_protection=False` (DOUBTFUL warning, not blocking). The policy validates `soft_slippage_warning_pct` cannot exceed `max_acceptable_slippage_pct` — a misconfigured policy that accidentally swapped the two values would silently surface false-positive warnings. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **slippage > max threshold is NOT_HALAL** — gharar on price uncertainty; the user consenting to a 7% price-move-on-fill is consenting to a highly uncertain outcome, and AAOIFI explicitly addresses gharar in price-discovery contexts. The policy hard ceiling at 10% protects against operator misconfiguration that would otherwise silently approve haram-level slippage; (2) **FORBIDDEN intermediate token is unconditionally NOT_HALAL** — routing through interest-bearing wrapper (aTokens, cTokens, etc.) or synthetic-asset inherits the riba even if the swap endpoints are halal. The override-everything pin matters because the most insidious bug would be a "halal AAVE→USDC swap" that silently passes — the engine refuses; (3) **DOUBTFUL** for ORDER_BOOK_OFF_CHAIN (the matched-price-not-fixed-at-submission gharar; off-chain relayer's shariah status unclear — operator can override via `flag_off_chain_orderbook=False` if their scholar profile permits 0x-style RFQ matching, but the default is to flag), UNAUDITED + SELF_AUDITED contracts, MEV_PROTECTION=NONE (sandwich-attack exposure surfaces a warning so operator understands trade-off), DEBATED stablecoin intermediate (USDT's commercial-paper backing needs scholar review), cross-chain bridge use (the additional custody + validator-honesty assumption is real even when the destination is HALAL), > 3 hops (compounding gharar + slippage), slippage above soft threshold but below max; (4) **INSUFFICIENT_DATA** when liquidity_model UNKNOWN — never silent HALAL on undisclosed routing logic; (5) **render output never includes wallet addresses, contract addresses, or transaction hashes** — wallet addresses are PII (Wave 11.D); contract addresses are operationally sensitive (phishing-link risk per the Wave 12.E precedent — a malicious renderer could inject 0xLOOKALIKE phishing addresses); transaction hashes are user-correlatable. Render shows protocol + chain + verdict + per-flag warnings; operators audit on-chain side via blockchain explorer separately. Mirrors the no-PII / no-address / no-message-echo patterns of Wave 11.D + 11.C + 3.B + 12.E + 12.G — every public-facing render shares one defensive surface. Halal alignment: read-only screening; never opens a position or executes a swap; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`SettlementRoutePolicy` / `SettlementRoute` / `SettlementScreenResult`). 58 tests cover: policy validation (zero / negative / above-10 max slippage rejected; soft-warning-cannot-exceed-max guard); route validation (negative slippage; zero hops rejected; zero slippage accepted as rare-but-valid stable-stable); the **slippage hard-rejection pin in three flavours** (6% above 5% default → NOT_HALAL with specific message; exactly 5% boundary inclusive falls to DOUBTFUL via soft-threshold-warning; strict 1%/0.5% policy flips a 2% verdict NOT_HALAL — the customisation-flow regression-pin); the **FORBIDDEN-intermediate pin** in two flavours (alone with riba message; even with all-other-clean still NOT_HALAL — the override-everything pin); INSUFFICIENT_DATA for UNKNOWN liquidity in two flavours (alone; with all other clean); HALAL happy paths in five variants (Uniswap V3 + Big Four + Flashbots + 0.5% + direct → HALAL; Curve stablecoin pool; Jupiter Solana; **dYdX V4 ORDER_BOOK_ON_CHAIN HALAL pin** — the on-chain orderbook structural difference from off-chain matters; HALAL_STABLECOIN intermediate with 2 hops); **DOUBTFUL pins** in eight categories (off-chain orderbook with operator-override-disable; UNAUDITED + SELF_AUDITED + AUDITED_INDIE-passes asymmetry pin; MEV NONE with native / Flashbots / MEV_BLOCKER all passing; DEBATED stablecoin; bridge use; > 3 hops with exactly-3 boundary inclusive HALAL; slippage above soft threshold; slippage at exactly 2% soft threshold does NOT trigger — boundary asymmetry pin); **multiple-warnings aggregation** (UNAUDITED + NONE-MEV + 4% slippage + DEBATED stablecoin + bridge → ≥5 distinct flags); frozen-dataclass immutability across all three output types; all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability across chain / protocol / liquidity / MEV / intermediate / verdict; render output across all four verdicts with emoji + chain + protocol + slippage %; the **render-no-address-or-tx-hash pin** asserts neither `0x` nor `tx hash` appears in the rendered output — guards against future template changes injecting on-chain identifiers that could become phishing vectors; result-shape sanity carrying chain + protocol metadata through for the audit trail; and five end-to-end realistic flows — Uniswap V4 on Optimism with Flashbots + 0.5% slippage → HALAL (the best-case ETH-side path); Jupiter aggregator on Solana routing through USDC with native MEV protection → HALAL (the typical SOL-side path); cross-chain ETH→Polygon bridge → DOUBTFUL with the bridge warning surfaced; **worst-case multi-flag aggregate** (UNAUDITED + NONE MEV + 4.5% slippage + DEBATED stablecoin + bridge + 4 hops → ≥6 distinct warnings, the realistic "complicated, send to scholar review" case); **excessive-slippage-blocks-everything pin** (7% slippage on an otherwise pristine Uniswap V3 + Big Four + Flashbots route → still NOT_HALAL, the "even one hard-fail rule wins" guarantee). Live router integration (httpx client to 1inch / 0x / Jupiter quote APIs that returns the route's structural metadata for screening; per-cycle gas-strategy estimator that adjusts slippage tolerance based on volatility; the cycle-side hook that wraps every executor swap with the gate before submitting on-chain — composes with the existing crypto/exchange.py executor's circuit-breaker layer), Postgres `settlement_routes` + `settlement_audit_log` tables wired to `db/repository.py`, the FastAPI route adapter (`/api/settlement/screen` for ad-hoc screening; `/api/settlement/routes` listing historical swaps with their verdicts), and the dashboard's settlement-route tile rendering historical swaps + per-DEX verdict aggregation deferred to follow-ups — screener verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 12.E — Tokenised REIT screener** — `web/tokenised_reit.py` is the pure-Python halal screener for tokenised real-estate platforms (RealT, Lofty, Propy fractional, etc.). Tokenised real-estate platforms sell on-chain tokens that represent fractional ownership of specific physical properties — the roadmap notes the long-term diversification value beyond public markets, but defers full integration because none of these platforms hold AAOIFI certification yet. The screening *logic* is operator-supplied / CSV-fed pure-Python, exactly the isolated-module pattern of Wave 1.G commodities + 1.H sukuk + 1.I REIT + 12.A robo-advisor + 12.D halal-VC. Tokenised REITs raise concerns the traditional REIT screen (Wave 1.I) doesn't catch: **custody model** (the token might represent direct fractional ownership of the deed — RealT-style SPV per property — or a derivative right that tracks the property's price without legal ownership; derivative-rights tokens fail Shariah on gharar because the holder doesn't actually own anything physical); **settlement certainty** (most US states still don't recognise NFT-based property records as legal title; the on-chain transfer is only as binding as the off-chain SPV resolution); **regulator backing** (unregistered tokenised offerings carry both legal risk AND a stronger gharar argument because the off-chain enforceability is unclear); **smart contract audit** (an unaudited contract is a malware vector — even if the underlying property is halal, the custody mechanism failing is a form of gharar); **yield denomination** (many tokenised RE platforms pay rental yield in stablecoins — the stablecoin's own halal status matters: USDC is fully cash-backed and generally accepted; USDT's commercial-paper backing is debated; PYUSD / RLUSD vary); **DeFi integration** — the classic riba-via-back-door pattern for tokenised RE: the platform allows holders to lend out their tokens as collateral for interest-bearing loans, or borrow against them, both making the holder a participant in riba even if the underlying property is halal. The module re-uses Wave 1.I's `REITPropertyType` enum for the underlying physical asset (the tokenisation wrapper doesn't change whether warehouses or hotels are inherently halal property types) and layers on six tokenisation-specific enums. `TokenStandard` (ERC20 / ERC721 / ERC1155 / SPL_FUNGIBLE / NATIVE_OTHER / UNKNOWN). `RegulatorRegistration` (SEC_REG_A_PLUS / SEC_REG_D / MICA_ARTICLE_16 / OTHER / NONE). `CustodyModel` with three values where DIRECT_OWNERSHIP is rare (only a few US states recognise NFT deeds), SPV_OWNERSHIP is the typical RealT model (token = unit in an SPV LLC owning the property), DERIVATIVE_RIGHTS is the categorical-block (price tracker without legal ownership). `SmartContractAudit` four-tier ladder (AUDITED_BIG_FOUR / AUDITED_INDIE / SELF_AUDITED / UNAUDITED). `YieldDenomination` six values plus the `_HALAL_YIELD_DENOMINATIONS` closed frozenset (RENT_DIRECT_FIAT / USDC_STABLECOIN / NONE accepted; USDT_STABLECOIN / OTHER_STABLECOIN / NATIVE_CRYPTO drive DOUBTFUL). `DeFiIntegration` four values with the `_RIBA_DEFI_INTEGRATIONS` closed frozenset (LENDING_ENABLED / BORROWING_ENABLED / BOTH_ENABLED categorical NOT_HALAL). `TokenisedREITDeal` carries the ten inputs the screener needs. `screen_tokenised_reit(deal)` returns a `TokenisedREITScreenResult` with verdict + per-rule failure / warning lists for the audit trail. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **DERIVATIVE_RIGHTS custody is unconditionally NOT_HALAL** — the holder owns no physical asset; classical Shariah requires actual ownership of a tangible asset for the trade to be valid (gharar — excessive uncertainty in the underlying); pinned via the "even with everything else clean — direct USDC yield, Big Four audit, Reg A+ regulator, residential property — derivative-rights still NOT_HALAL" regression case; (2) **LENDING_ENABLED / BORROWING_ENABLED / BOTH_ENABLED is unconditionally NOT_HALAL** — even if the underlying property is a halal industrial warehouse, the protocol enabling lending or borrowing makes the holder a participant in riba. The **asymmetric pin** matters operationally: a halal warehouse REIT that the operator can't borrow against (STANDALONE) is HALAL; the same REIT with on-chain borrowing enabled is NOT_HALAL because the *protocol* enables riba even if the operator doesn't personally borrow — the financial-rule difference between "I'm choosing not to borrow" and "this product cannot offer borrowing" is load-bearing under classical fiqh; (3) **DOUBTFUL** for the operator-decides cases: SPV_OWNERSHIP (legal-title transferability depends on jurisdiction; the SPV's resolution must be respected by the relevant courts), unregistered offerings (operator must verify off-chain enforceability), UNAUDITED + SELF_AUDITED contracts, USDT / OTHER / NATIVE_CRYPTO yield denominations, hotel / specialty property types (the Wave 1.I property-level DOUBTFUL flag carries through unchanged); (4) **INSUFFICIENT_DATA when token_standard is UNKNOWN** — never silent HALAL; operator must verify before allocating, mirrors the conservative-default pattern across every other halal-side wave; (5) **render output never includes wallet addresses or token contract IDs** — wallet addresses are PII (Wave 11.D) and token contract addresses are also operationally sensitive (a malicious renderer could inject phishing links via address-formatted strings). Mirrors the no-PII pattern of Wave 11.D + 11.C + 3.B and the no-message-echo pattern of Wave 12.G — every public-facing render in this codebase shares one defensive surface. Halal alignment: read-only screening; never opens a position; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`TokenisedREITDeal` / `TokenisedREITScreenResult`). 44 tests cover: deal validation (empty symbol / platform; negative lockup_days; zero-lockup accepted as rare-but-valid liquid offering); the **DERIVATIVE_RIGHTS pin** in two flavours (alone with gharar message; even with all-other-clean still NOT_HALAL — the override-everything pin); the **DeFi-riba pins** in four flavours (LENDING_ENABLED → riba message; BORROWING_ENABLED; BOTH_ENABLED; LENDING_ENABLED overrides clean flags — the asymmetric pin that catches the most-insidious "halal property + halal custody + RIBA-ENABLED protocol" failure mode); multiple-failure aggregation (DERIVATIVE_RIGHTS + LENDING_ENABLED → exactly 2 failures listed);
