**FIXED_PROFIT_RATE is HALAL by default** — AAOIFI permits a contractually-fixed ijarah rental that *uses* a benchmark like LIBOR for transparency without making the rental itself an interest payment, so the screener's pin is "FIXED_PROFIT_RATE coupon → HALAL" (a sloppy implementation that conflated "uses LIBOR" with "is interest" would reject every modern sukuk; the regression-pin guards against that); INTEREST is the riba red line and categorically NOT_HALAL. `SukukIssue` carries the ten inputs the screener needs (isin / issuer_name / issuer_type / structure / asset_class / coupon_type / is_aaoifi_certified / is_asset_backed / maturity_days / expected_yield_pct); validates non-empty isin + issuer_name + non-negative maturity + non-negative yield at construction. `screen_sukuk(issue, *, thresholds)` returns a `SukukScreenResult` carrying the verdict (HALAL / NOT_HALAL / DOUBTFUL / INSUFFICIENT_DATA), the contributing flags surfaced for the audit trail (structure / asset_class / coupon_type / aaoifi-certified / asset-backed / maturity_days), and per-rule failure + warning lists. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) HALAL requires every check pass — AAOIFI-approved structure + AAOIFI-certified issuance + halal asset class + non-interest coupon + permissible issuer + asset-backed (preferred); any single failure flips verdict, never silent HALAL; (2) **NOT_HALAL is unconditional** for INTEREST coupon (the riba red line), PROHIBITED_OPERATIONS asset class, and FINANCIAL_RECEIVABLES asset class — even if everything else is clean, these three failures override every other flag (the regression pin tests "INTEREST coupon overrides every other clean flag" specifically because the most insidious bug is a pretty issue from a sovereign issuer with allocated assets but interest coupon — the "wrong reason but right structure" trap that would silently approve ribawi exposure); (3) **DOUBTFUL** covers the operator-decides cases — not-AAOIFI-certified (lacks third-party scholar attestation), MURABAHA under strict mode (some scholars dispute tradability), CONVENTIONAL_BANK issuer (the most contested case — the sukuk itself can be structured halal but the issuer's other operations disqualify it for stricter operators), CORPORATE_MIXED issuer, asset-based (vs asset-backed) under strict mode, very short tenor (money-market-shaped); (4) **INSUFFICIENT_DATA** when asset_class is UNKNOWN — prospectus didn't disclose the underlying assets clearly; never silent HALAL just because nothing rejected (mirrors the conservative-default pattern across every other halal-side module); (5) **FIXED_PROFIT_RATE coupon is HALAL by default** — AAOIFI is explicit that a contractually-fixed rental which uses a benchmark for transparency is not interest; the pin guards against the most common "every modern sukuk gets rejected" bug. Threshold customisation: `require_aaoifi_certified` defaults True (operators trusting sovereign issues can relax to False); `accept_murabaha` defaults True (AAOIFI-permitted; strict-Hanafi operators set False); `accept_asset_based` defaults True (most modern GCC sukuk are asset-based; strict operators set False to require true-sale); `min_maturity_days` defaults to 1d (filters out money-market-instrument-shaped issues that need different treatment). Halal alignment: read-only screening; never opens a position; the screener's verdict feeds the existing screening cache, not the executor; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async; frozen dataclasses on every output (`SukukThresholds` / `SukukIssue` / `SukukScreenResult`). Render helper produces emoji-prefixed (✅/❌/⚠️/❓) ops display with structure / asset_class / coupon / maturity / aaoifi-certified / asset-backed sections — visually consistent with the other halal-side renderers (Wave 1.G commodities, 1.I REIT, 2.F scholar review, 2.G regulator index). 50 tests cover: threshold validation (negative min_maturity rejected; zero accepted as "include any tenor"), SukukIssue field validation (empty isin / issuer_name; negative maturity / yield), every hard-rejection path with the specific failure message (INTEREST → "interest" / "riba"; PROHIBITED_OPERATIONS → "prohibited"; FINANCIAL_RECEIVABLES → "conventional debt"), the override-everything-else-clean pin (sovereign + ijarah + real-estate + AAOIFI + asset-backed but INTEREST coupon → NOT_HALAL), the INSUFFICIENT_DATA-on-UNKNOWN pin in two flavours, HALAL happy paths across seven structures × multiple asset classes (clean ijarah-sovereign-real-estate-rental; musharaka-supranational-infrastructure-profit-share; wakala-corporate-halal; istisna-aircraft; salam-utilities; hybrid; the every-halal-asset-class-passes loop), the **FIXED_PROFIT_RATE → HALAL pin** (the LIBOR-isn't-interest regression pin), DOUBTFUL paths (not-AAOIFI-certified; conventional-bank-issuer; corporate-mixed-issuer; zero-maturity money-market; murabaha-strict-mode; asset-based-strict-mode), the **murabaha-default-mode-passes pin** (under AAOIFI defaults, MURABAHA → HALAL; only `accept_murabaha=False` flips it), the **asset-based-default-mode-passes pin** (under defaults asset-based → HALAL), AAOIFI-uncertified-with-override flow (operator's relaxed thresholds → HALAL), multiple-warning aggregation (a CONVENTIONAL_BANK + uncertified + asset-based + zero-maturity case under strict mode lists ≥4 distinct warnings), multiple-failure aggregation on hard rejections (PROHIBITED_OPERATIONS + INTEREST → ≥2 failures), threshold customisation flow (strict thresholds flip marginal verdicts in both directions), frozen-dataclass immutability across all three output types, all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability (`ijarah` / `musharaka` / `mudaraba` / `wakala` / `murabaha` / `salam` / `istisna` / `hybrid` for structure; `real_estate` / `infrastructure` / etc. for asset_class; `sovereign` / `supranational` / `corporate_halal` / `corporate_mixed` / `conventional_bank` for issuer; `profit_share` / `rental_income` / `fixed_profit_rate` / `interest` for coupon; `halal` / `not_halal` / `doubtful` / `insufficient_data` for verdict), render output across all four verdicts with the right emoji + section headers + maturity formatting, result-shape sanity, and three real-world end-to-end cases (Saudi sovereign 5y ijarah → HALAL; Dubai-Islamic-Bank-shaped wakala-infrastructure → DOUBTFUL because of CONVENTIONAL_BANK issuer registration; synthetic credit-linked note over conventional-loan-pool → NOT_HALAL because of financial-receivables underlying). Live ingest (Bloomberg / Refinitiv vendor feed adapter behind the existing screener interface; or a CSV-import path for operators with their own data sources), the cycle-side wiring (delegate from `halal/screener.py` for sukuk-classified ISINs, surface the verdict in the dashboard's halal-status tile, route DOUBTFUL into the scholar-review queue from Wave 2.F) deferred to follow-ups — screener verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 1.G — Halal commodities ETF screener** — `halal/commodities_screener.py` is the pure-Python ETF-specific Shariah screen for commodity vehicles (gold-backed PHYS, silver PSLV, platinum PPLT, copper CPER, oil USO/UCO, etc.). The roadmap's interim path for crypto-bot operators who want commodity exposure: gold / silver-backed ETFs (the strict path of physical-spot possession is operationally complex). Picked a focused module over wedging the rules into the general stock screener (Zoya / Wahed) because the failure modes are commodity-specific — the question isn't "does this ETF's company have ≤33% debt", it's "is the underlying gold actually allocated bullion in the unitholder's name or a synthetic swap pretending to be gold". Eight `CommodityType`s split into three classes pinned in module-level frozensets: **ribawi** (gold + silver — AAOIFI Standard 57 + classical fiqh treatment require the strongest backing); **debated** (oil + natural_gas + agricultural — sector-scholar disagreement, DOUBTFUL even with clean backing per Hanafi readings on energy / agricultural futures); **industrial non-ribawi** (platinum + palladium + copper — clean backing → HALAL). `BackingMode` enum names the five financing structures: `ALLOCATED_PHYSICAL` (strongest — unitholder claim on specific bars / barrels in named account or by serial number in segregated storage), `UNALLOCATED_PHYSICAL` (pooled vault, commingled across unitholders), `FUTURES_BACKED` (rolled futures contracts, raises gharar / roll-yield questions), `SWAP_BACKED` (derivative-only synthetic that doesn't hold the commodity at all — categorical NOT_HALAL), `UNKNOWN` (filings didn't disclose, INSUFFICIENT_DATA). `StorageLocation` enum (SEGREGATED / COMMINGLED / PAPER) layers on top — PAPER means no physical bars exist, only ledger entries, unconditional NOT_HALAL. `CommodityETFFinancials` carries the seven inputs the screener needs (symbol / name / commodity / backing_mode / storage_location / leverage_factor / physical_holdings_pct / has_audited_holdings); validates symbol + name non-empty + physical_holdings_pct in [0, 100] at construction. `screen_commodity_etf(financials, *, thresholds)` returns a `CommodityScreenResult` carrying the verdict (HALAL / NOT_HALAL / DOUBTFUL / INSUFFICIENT_DATA), the contributing numbers (physical %, leverage, backing mode, storage), and per-rule failure + warning lists for the audit trail. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **HALAL requires every check pass** — allocated-physical + segregated + ≥95% physical (default threshold) + leverage = 1.0 + audited holdings; any single failure flips to NOT_HALAL or DOUBTFUL, never silent HALAL — the regression surface a future contributor would have to overcome to silently approve a non-compliant ETF is structural, not just code review; (2) **NOT_HALAL is unconditional** for SWAP_BACKED (synthetic exposure is gharar), PAPER storage (no physical commodity), leverage > max threshold (categorically NOT_HALAL because leveraged products require derivatives + interest-bearing financing), inverse / short ETFs (negative leverage factor — same financing requirement), and physical holdings below threshold; (3) **DOUBTFUL is the operator-decides bucket** for unallocated-but-physical (commingled or pooled — operator should choose allocated for ribawi commodities), debated commodity types, commingled storage, missing audit attestation; (4) **INSUFFICIENT_DATA when backing UNKNOWN** — filings undisclosed, mirrors the conservative-default pattern of Wave 1.I REIT screen + Wave 2.G regulator index (DOUBTFUL / INSUFFICIENT_DATA on missing data, never silent HALAL); (5) **float boundaries inclusive** at the threshold — 95% physical → HALAL, 94.99% → NOT_HALAL; 1.0× leverage → HALAL, 1.01× → NOT_HALAL — pinned in BOTH directions because asymmetric boundary handling is a common bug, and a single one-direction test would let a future refactor silently shift the boundary the other way. **Ribawi commodities take additional rules** beyond the base screen: gold / silver with unallocated backing trip a ribawi-specific warning even when audited / segregated / 99% physical (gold ETF using GLD-style commingled vault → DOUBTFUL not HALAL); gold / silver with commingled storage trip a ribawi-storage warning even with allocated backing (silver ETF in pooled vault → DOUBTFUL). Non-ribawi copper with the same commingled flag triggers a generic commingled warning but no ribawi-specific one — pinned via differential test that the ribawi-only warning fires only for gold / silver. Debated commodities (oil / gas / agricultural) trigger the scholar-disagreement warning regardless of backing — even an oil ETF with allocated physical barrels in segregated storage lands DOUBTFUL because oil itself has scholar disagreement on permissibility for ETF-form trading. Threshold customisation flows through: a stricter operator bumping `min_physical_holdings_pct` to 98% flips a 96%-physical ETF from HALAL to NOT_HALAL — pinned. Halal alignment: read-only screening; never opens a position; the screener's verdict feeds into the existing screening cache, not the executor; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async; frozen dataclasses on every output (`CommodityThresholds` / `CommodityETFFinancials` / `CommodityScreenResult`). Render helper produces emoji-prefixed (✅/❌/⚠️/❓) ops display visually consistent with the rest of the halal-side renderers (Wave 1.I REIT, Wave 2.F scholar review, Wave 2.G regulator index). 53 tests cover: threshold validation (min_physical_holdings_pct rejects zero / negative / above-100; max_leverage_factor rejects zero / negative), CommodityETFFinancials field validation (empty symbol / name rejected; physical_holdings_pct out of [0, 100] rejected), every hard-rejection path with the specific failure message (SWAP_BACKED → "swap-backed" message; PAPER → "paper" message; leverage > 1.0 → "leverage" message; inverse leverage → "inverse" or "short" message; physical < threshold → "physical holdings" message), threshold inclusivity in BOTH directions (95% physical inclusive → HALAL, 94.99% fails; 1.0× leverage inclusive → HALAL, 1.01× fails — the symmetry pin matters), the INSUFFICIENT_DATA-on-UNKNOWN-backing pin in two flavours (alone, and even when all other flags are clean), HALAL happy paths across three real-world-shaped ETFs (PHYS-shaped allocated-segregated-99%-1×-audited gold; PSLV silver; PPLT platinum), DOUBTFUL paths (unallocated gold → ribawi-allocated warning; unallocated copper → commingled warning but no ribawi warning; futures-backed gold with segregated storage → futures-backed warning; commingled storage on gold → ribawi-segregated + commingled warnings; no audited holdings → audit warning), the ribawi-stricter-rules differential pin (gold + unallocated + segregated → DOUBTFUL with ribawi-allocated warning; silver + allocated + commingled → DOUBTFUL with ribawi-segregated warning; non-ribawi copper + allocated + commingled → DOUBTFUL with no ribawi-specific warning — the asymmetry is the load-bearing pin), the debated-commodities pin (oil / gas / agricultural with clean allocated-segregated still land DOUBTFUL with the scholar-disagreement warning; platinum / palladium with the same backing land HALAL — they're not in the debated set), multiple-failure aggregation (a SWAP + PAPER + 2× + 0% physical case lists ≥ 3 distinct failures all surfaced), threshold customisation flips marginal verdicts (a 96% physical ETF passes with the default 95% threshold, fails with the stricter 98% — the customisation flow regression-pinned), frozen-dataclass immutability across CommodityThresholds + CommodityETFFinancials + CommodityScreenResult, all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability (`gold` / `silver` / etc. for type; `allocated_physical` / `unallocated_physical` / `futures_backed` / `swap_backed` / `unknown` for backing; `segregated` / `commingled` / `paper` for storage; `halal` / `not_halal` / `doubtful` / `insufficient_data` for verdict), render output across all four verdicts with the right emoji + section headers + physical % formatted to 2 decimals + leverage with `x` suffix, result-shape sanity (every field carried through), and two real-world end-to-end cases (GLD-shaped unallocated-commingled-99.5%-audited-1× gold trust → DOUBTFUL because of ribawi-strictness; UCO-shaped 2× swap-financed crude oil ETF → NOT_HALAL with at least three distinct failures across swap + paper + leverage). Cycle-side wiring (delegate from `halal/screener.py` for symbols classified as commodity ETFs via SIC code lookup, surface verdict in dashboard's halal-status tile, route DOUBTFUL into the scholar-review queue from Wave 2.F, plumb a CSV / Yahoo-Finance / SEC EDGAR fundamentals fetcher for the backing_mode / storage_location / leverage_factor / physical_holdings_pct inputs) deferred to follow-ups — screener verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 3.C — Per-user resource quotas (engine)** — `web/quotas.py` is the per-user resource-quota accounting layer Round-4 needs once the bot grows past single-operator-laptop mode. Today the bot has one global LLM cost cap (`LLM_DAILY_USD_CAP`) and a single Binance / CoinGecko / Zoya rate limit shared across the whole instance — the moment the bot has more than one user, that breaks because one user's runaway prompt loop or screener storm could exhaust the whole instance's daily budget before any other user gets a turn. This module is the stateless engine: tier-based daily limits, rolling 24-hour windows that auto-reset, and a clean `QuotaExceededError` so the LLM router / screener / broker / cycle scheduler all gate-keep their own spend without each re-deriving the budget math. **Picked rolling 24-hour windows over calendar days** because users sit across time zones — a calendar-day window resets at the operator's UTC midnight which is mid-afternoon for a US-East user and could wipe out their morning's cumulative usage in a way that feels random; a rolling 24-hour window means each user's budget refreshes 24 hours after they started spending regardless of clock time, fairer for distributed usage. Three composed primitives. (1) `Tier` enum (FREE / PRO / ENTERPRISE) with stable string values pinned for DB / JSON migration safety; tiers add via code + review (rather than DB insert) so a tier drift can't silently change limit math. (2) `ResourceKind` enum names five resource categories the engine tracks (LLM_USD / LLM_TOKENS / BROKER_API_CALLS / SCREENER_API_CALLS / CYCLE_RUNS) with stable string values; the set is deliberately small because every new resource adds a column to the `ResourceUsage` row + a field to `TierLimits`, so adding one is a code-review change not a runtime config knob — guards against a future contributor adding a "tracked" resource without thinking through the persistence side. (3) `TierLimits` carries per-resource daily caps with positive-or-zero invariants on every field — zero is valid (FREE tier disables broker_api_calls because free-tier users only get paper trading via a shared simulator); the `for_resource(kind)` selector returns the right limit so callers don't have to re-write the kind→field mapping at every call site. `DEFAULT_TIER_LIMITS` ships documented best-guesses for a multi-user paper-trading deployment: FREE=$0.50 LLM/200k tokens/0 broker/200 screener/24 cycles per day; PRO=$10/2M tokens/10k broker/2k screener/288 cycles (one every 5 minutes); ENTERPRISE=$100/20M tokens/100k broker/20k screener/1440 cycles (one per minute). Production deployments tune them to actual cost recovery via the `limits_by_tier` constructor arg. `ResourceUsage` is the per-user rolling-window accounting row carrying `user_id` / `tier` / `window_started_at` / per-resource counters; every counter validates non-negative at construction (a row with negative usage is by definition corrupt — surfacing the bug at construction beats silent budget recovery). `QuotaTracker` is the stateless engine: `check(usage, *, resource, requested=0)` returns a read-only `QuotaCheckResult` snapshot carrying used / limit / remaining / pct_used / state / window_started_at / warnings; `consume(usage, *, resource, amount)` returns a new usage row with the amount added (or raises `QuotaExceededError` carrying the full user_id / resource / tier / used / limit context for the operator's exception handler to render an actionable message); `remaining(usage, *, resource)` is the convenience accessor. The tracker is stateless — usage rows flow through (caller persists; tracker computes); a future Postgres adapter would simply pass `ResourceUsage` rows through the same surface, keeping the budget math independent of the persistence layer. **Five pinned safety semantics**: (1) **rolling 24-hour windows** — `consume()` past the 24h boundary auto-resets the window with the consumed amount as the new starting usage; pinned via three tests (25h elapsed → reset, 23h59m → no reset, exactly 24h boundary inclusive — the symmetry pin matters because asymmetric boundary handling is a common bug); (2) **WARNING band starts at 80%, EXCEEDED at 100%** — both thresholds inclusive (8.0 of 10.0 → WARNING; exactly 10.0 → EXCEEDED); zero-limit resource (FREE tier broker_api_calls) with zero use lands OK, zero-limit with any use lands EXCEEDED rather than divide-by-zero; the zero-limit case is regression-pinned because it's exactly the kind of edge a future refactor would silently break; (3) **negative consumption rejected** — refunds aren't a quota concern (the caller persists corrected usage rows directly and operators audit the refund event separately); the guard prevents an integer-overflow / accidental-credit class of bug where a buggy LLM-cost-recompute could silently grant a user free budget; (4) **consuming up to but not past the limit succeeds** — operator-friendly: lets a user spend their last cent rather than rejecting the call that brings them to exactly the cap; the next consume of any positive amount fails (regression-pinned); (5) **fractional token consumption rounds down** via `int()` — half a token consumes zero tokens (user gets benefit-of-the-doubt for partial counts; alternative — round up — would silently over-bill on every fractional call). `check()` does not mutate the input usage row even when it auto-rolls the window in the returned snapshot — pinned via the explicit "input row stays at 9.5 USD even after check rolls the snapshot's window forward" test (a sloppy implementation that mutates would silently corrupt every persisted row when the dashboard does a read-only quota check). `remaining()` clamps at zero when over (no negative remaining — the operator dashboard wants "0 remaining" not "−5 remaining" which would render confusingly). Render helper produces emoji-prefixed (✅/⚠️/🚫) one-user lines visually consistent with the rest of the ops-display surfaces (Wave 1.I REIT screen, Wave 2.F scholar review, Wave 2.G regulator index, Wave 3.B vault); USD renders with `$` prefix and 2/4 decimal precision, token counts render as plain integers (no dollar formatting). Halal alignment: quota engine is purely operational — never opens a position; the budget gate sits in front of LLM / screener / broker calls so a runaway user can't burn the whole instance's spend, mirroring the conservative-default cost-control pattern of the existing single-user `LLM_DAILY_USD_CAP`. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output (`TierLimits` / `ResourceUsage` / `QuotaCheckResult`). Not in scope (load-bearing distinction): the Wave 7.D research-API token-bucket limiter handles **external** per-key rate limits at the public research API boundary; this module handles **internal** per-user quotas (the budget gate the LLM / screener / broker call sites consult before spending). They share no state and have different semantics (token bucket vs rolling-window accounting). 60 tests cover: default-tier-limits sanity (every tier present in DEFAULT_TIER_LIMITS; FREE disables broker_api_calls; PRO > FREE on every dimension; ENTERPRISE > PRO; the relative-ordering invariant pinned because a future config drift could silently invert a tier ladder), TierLimits + ResourceUsage field validation (negative-rejection on every USD / token / call counter; zero accepted as the disable case), `for_resource` + `used_for` selectors return the right field for every resource (the kind→field mapping pinned via test so a future field rename surfaces immediately), QuotaTracker construction (default limits used when None passed; partial limits map rejected with "missing tier"; custom limits flow through), the three-band classification ladder pinned at the boundary in BOTH directions (below 80% → OK; exactly 80% → WARNING; 95% → WARNING; exactly 100% → EXCEEDED; 150% → EXCEEDED), the zero-limit edge cases (zero limit + zero use → OK with pct_used=0; zero limit + any use → EXCEEDED at 100% pct without divide-by-zero), `check()` with `requested>0` simulates consume without mutating input (the read-only-snapshot pin), negative-requested rejected, `remaining` clamps at zero when over, consume lifecycle (adds to existing; returns new frozen row not the input; raises QuotaExceededError on overage with full context; at-exact-limit succeeds with the next-call-fails followup; rejects negative amount; zero-amount is no-op; fractional token count floors via int), the rolling 24h window pin (25h elapsed → reset with the consumed amount as the new starting usage; 23h59m → no reset preserves accumulating usage; exactly 24h inclusive), check() also rolls the window in returned snapshot without mutating input row (the dashboard-read-only pin), QuotaCheckResult shape carries every field with warnings populated on WARNING/EXCEEDED and empty on OK, render output across every state with emoji per state name (USD format with `$` prefix vs integer format pin for token counts), window-start in render output, frozen-dataclass immutability across TierLimits / ResourceUsage / QuotaCheckResult, all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB stability (`free` / `pro` / `enterprise` for tier; `llm_usd` / `llm_tokens` / `broker_api_calls` / `screener_api_calls` / `cycle_runs` for resource; `ok` / `warning` / `exceeded` for state), cross-tier scenarios (FREE user blocked immediately on broker_api_calls because limit is 0; ENTERPRISE has 200× the LLM headroom of FREE — the relative-tiers pin), an end-to-end realistic PRO-user flow (across-the-day spending: $1 → OK; $5 cumulative → OK; $7 cumulative → OK; $9 cumulative → WARNING at 90%; rejects $2.01 over the cap with QuotaExceededError; next-day window reset starts fresh), and the QuotaExceededError context regression (carries user_id / resource / tier / used / limit; str(exc) mentions all four for the operator's log line to be parseable). Postgres persistence (a `resource_usage` table + repository wired to `db/repository.py`), the LLM-router gate (every `core/llm/factory.py` call site checks quota before the LLM call, charging the user's tier on the cost-recovery side), the broker-side gate (every `crypto/exchange.py` request consumes a broker_api_call from the user's quota), the screener-side gate (every Zoya / CoinGecko refresh consumes a screener_api_call), and the dashboard quota tile rendering per-user state with current pct + trend deferred to follow-ups — engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 3.B — Per-user encrypted secrets vault (crypto core)** — `web/secrets_vault.py` is the cryptographic core of the multi-user secrets vault that Round-4 needs once the bot grows past single-operator-laptop mode. Today every broker / LLM / screener key sits in the operator's `.env`; the moment the bot has more than one user, that breaks because every user's broker API keys can't share the same env file. The vault is a pure-Python module sitting on top of `cryptography.fernet` + HKDF-SHA256: a server-side master KEK (≥ 32 bytes; the `SECRET_KEY` env var) derives a per-user Fernet DEK via HKDF (salt=owner_id, info=`halal-trader-vault-v{version}`); secrets ship encrypted at rest as `EncryptedSecret` frozen-dataclass rows; decryption requires presenting the right `owner_id` so a leaked ciphertext alone is insufficient to recover plaintext (different owner_id → different derived DEK → Fernet `InvalidToken`). Picked Fernet on top of HKDF rather than AES-GCM directly because (a) Fernet handles the auth-tag + IV bookkeeping correctly out of the box and (b) the surface error `InvalidToken` collapses both "wrong key" and "tampered ciphertext" into one well-defined exception so the vault doesn't leak which one happened — important for not giving an attacker oracle access to differentiate "I have the right key but tampered ciphertext" from "I have the wrong key but valid ciphertext". HKDF is the documented best-practice for deriving per-user keys from a single high-entropy master KEK; the alternative (per-user random DEK stored under the KEK as an envelope) trades a single derived key per user for a two-step decrypt path with the same security properties — picked HKDF for the simpler audit trail. Three composed primitives: `SecretKind` enum names seven storage categories (broker_api_key / broker_api_secret / llm_api_key / news_api_key / cryptopanic_key / reddit_client_secret / screener_api_key) with stable string values pinned for DB / JSON migration safety; `EncryptedSecret` is the frozen audit row carrying owner_id / kind / label / ciphertext / created_at / last_rotated_at / last_accessed_at / key_version, every datetime validated timezone-aware (load-bearing for staleness arithmetic); `SecretVault` is the stateless cryptographic engine — `store(...)` encrypts and returns the row, `reveal(secret, *, owner_id)` decrypts and returns the plaintext bytes plus an access-time-updated row the caller persists, `rotate(...)` re-encrypts under a new master KEK + version, `needs_rotation(secret)` flags rows past the cadence. The vault has no internal storage state — `EncryptedSecret` rows are returned to the caller for persistence (Postgres / sqlite / file / in-memory dict), keeping the cryptographic core independent of the persistence layer so a future migration from sqlite to Postgres doesn't risk re-implementing the crypto incorrectly. **Five pinned safety semantics** are the load-bearing surface: (1) **plaintext is never stored** — the vault holds EncryptedSecret rows only, `reveal()` returns plaintext bytes that the caller must scrub from memory after use, the frozen-dataclass shape means a future field addition can't accidentally include plaintext alongside the ciphertext (the regression surface a future contributor would have to overcome to leak plaintext is structural, not just a code-review concern); (2) **wrong owner_id → InvalidToken** — decryption derives the DEK from `(master_kek, owner_id, key_version)`, presenting a different owner_id at reveal time produces a different DEK, Fernet rejects the ciphertext, and the operator gets a clean cryptographic boundary rather than a "permission denied" check the application layer could accidentally bypass — pinned via the explicit "secret stored under user-A, reveal attempt by user-B → SecretIntegrityError" test; (3) **tampered ciphertext → InvalidToken** — Fernet's auth-tag catches any single-byte mutation, vault re-raises as `SecretIntegrityError` so the operator's exception handler doesn't depend on `cryptography` package internals — pinned via single-bit-flip + truncation tests; (4) **master KEK ≥ 32 bytes** — HKDF input minimum, shorter keys rejected at construction so a misconfigured `SECRET_KEY` env var fails fast rather than silently weakening every derived DEK with low-entropy input — `SECRET_KEY=changeme` would silently work without this guard; (5) **render output never contains plaintext / ciphertext / any derived key** — `render_secret_metadata()` shows owner / kind / label / created_at / last_rotated_at / last_accessed_at / key_version only, audit display can't accidentally leak the secret it's auditing — the regression test asserts neither the plaintext nor the ciphertext bytes (in raw or hex form) appear in the rendered output, so a future render template change that adds a "ciphertext: ..." line for "debugging" fails CI rather than shipping silently. Rotation flagging is age-based on `last_rotated_at` (not `last_accessed_at`) — operators rotate on cadence regardless of usage; pinned via test that frequently-accessed-but-never-rotated secrets still trip `needs_rotation` (a sloppy implementation that "this is being used so it must be fine" would mask exactly the lost-key scenario rotation is meant to address). KEK rotation flow: decrypt under current KEK → re-encrypt under new KEK + new version → return new row; if current-KEK decrypt fails (operator already lost the current KEK), `rotate()` surfaces `SecretIntegrityError` rather than silently re-encrypting garbage — the failure mode where a partial-rotation script silently corrupts every secret is the worst case this guard prevents. Halal alignment: secret-vault security is a privacy-of-operator concern; the bot doesn't trade based on the vault, but a leaked broker key would let someone trade on the operator's behalf — the conservative-default cryptographic boundary mirrors the Wave 8.D OTLP-translator and Wave 7.D research-API-keys denylist patterns (operator-IP / PII / secrets are the boundary the bot actively guards). Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `base64`; `cryptography` already a transitive dep at v46+); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output. Both encryption-deterministic property pins regression-tested: (a) Fernet uses a random IV per encrypt so two encrypts of identical plaintext produce different ciphertexts (a vault that produced the same ciphertext twice would let an attacker confirm "this user re-uses this secret across services" via comparison); (b) round-trip preserves Unicode plaintext via UTF-8 encoding (a passphrase containing emoji or non-Latin characters survives store→reveal). 52 tests cover: KEK length validation (short rejected at construction, 32-byte accepted, 64-byte os.urandom accepted), `VaultPolicy` field validation (rotation_days / max_label_length / min_plaintext_bytes all reject zero or negative), happy path round-trip (str plaintext, bytes plaintext), the `last_accessed_at` update flow (reveal returns a new row with updated access time; the input row stays frozen — the immutability invariant is structurally enforced and tested), cross-user isolation pins in three flavours (wrong owner_id → SecretIntegrityError; same plaintext under different owner_ids → different ciphertext; forged secret claiming user-A's ownership of user-B's ciphertext → InvalidToken at the cryptographic boundary, NOT at the application-layer owner_id-string-equality guard), tamper detection (single-bit-flip in the middle of the ciphertext rejected; truncation rejected), cross-KEK isolation (old-KEK ciphertext attempted-decrypt under new-KEK vault → SecretIntegrityError), storage-time validation (empty owner / empty label / too-short plaintext below the 8-byte default / too-long label above the 64-char default / custom min_plaintext_bytes from a stricter policy flows through), EncryptedSecret field validation (every non-empty / non-naive-datetime / positive-key-version invariant fires; last_accessed_at=None accepted; last_accessed_at=naive rejected when set), KEK rotation lifecycle (re-encrypts under new KEK + version; preserves owner / kind / label / created_at across rotation; rejects short new KEK; rejects zero new version; fails cleanly when current KEK already changed — the worst-case scenario regression-pinned), `needs_rotation` semantics (fresh→False, 120-day-old→True, threshold inclusive at exactly 90d, uses last_rotated_at NOT last_accessed_at — pinned by storing 120 days ago + accessing yesterday + asserting needs_rotation still fires, custom rotation_days from a stricter policy flows through), render output's no-secret-leak contract (plaintext absent; ciphertext bytes absent in raw + hex form; owner / kind / label / dates / key_version present; "accessed: never" for unaccessed; formatted ISO timestamp when accessed), frozen-dataclass immutability across `EncryptedSecret` and `VaultPolicy`, all `SecretKind` string values pinned for DB stability (`broker_api_key` / `broker_api_secret` / `llm_api_key` / `news_api_key` / `cryptopanic_key` / `reddit_client_secret` / `screener_api_key`), and two cryptographic-property pins (Fernet random IV → two encrypts of identical plaintext produce different ciphertexts; round-trip preserves Unicode plaintext including emoji + üñîcödé characters). Postgres persistence (an `encrypted_secrets` table + repository wired to `db/repository.py`), the FastAPI route adapter (`/api/users/{user_id}/secrets` with `Depends(authenticate)` from Wave 7.D), the operator settings UI for per-user key entry, and the cycle-side hook (every broker / LLM client construction at startup looks up the user's keys via the vault, replacing the `.env` reads in `core/llm/factory.py` and `crypto/exchange.py`) deferred to follow-ups — vault verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 2.G — Pakistani SECP / Saudi CMA filings ingest (matcher)** — `halal/regulator_index.py` is the pure-Python ingestion + matching layer for regional regulator halal indices. Saudi (Tadawul Halal Index, CMA broader screening) and Pakistan (KSE-Meezan Index 30, SECP broader screening) regulators publish authoritative halal-compliance lists for their listed equities — these outrank a third-party screener (Zoya / Wahed) for home-market listings because the regulator has access to the issuer's full filings and the verdict is the legally-recognised shariah classification in-country. Operators trading Saudi or Pakistani equities should fold the regional verdict into the consensus screener as a high-priority source. Three composed primitives: (1) `RegulatorSource` enum names the four indices the bot can ingest (TADAWUL / CMA_HALAL / KMI30 / SECP_HALAL); (2) `Market` enum (SAUDI / PAKISTAN / OTHER) gates which regulators apply to which symbols — `_AUTHORITY` maps every regulator to exactly one market and the screener silently skips cross-market rows; (3) `IndexListing` is the per-symbol row carrying symbol / verdict / listed_at / optional notes, validated to require timezone-aware datetimes (load-bearing for staleness arithmetic — a naive datetime would silently mis-compute the age delta). `RegulatorIndex` aggregates the source, a fetch timestamp, and the listings tuple; rejects duplicate symbols at construction with case-insensitive whitespace-stripped normalisation so a fetcher that double-ingests a row surfaces the bug at construction. `lookup` matches case-insensitively after whitespace-stripping so Saudi 4-digit numerics (`1010` Riyad Bank) and Pakistani alphanumerics (`HBL` Habib Bank) coexist without market-specific parsing. The screener entry-point `screen_with_regulator(*, symbol, market, indices, now, thresholds)` returns a `RegulatorScreenResult` carrying the combined verdict, the contributing-source list, the oldest listing age in days, stale + expired booleans, the per-warning audit list, and the matched listings for the audit trail. **Three pinned semantics** are the load-bearing safety surface. (1) **Authority is per-market** — querying TADAWUL with `market=Market.OTHER` returns UNKNOWN with no source, *not* a silent NOT_HALAL — cross-market authority is a category error, not a failed screen, so the bot doesn't silently disqualify Apple just because it's not in the Tadawul index. The pin is tested in both directions (US symbol with TADAWUL index → UNKNOWN; Pakistani symbol with only Saudi indices → UNKNOWN); the symmetry pin matters because asymmetric authority handling is a common bug. (2) **Absence ≠ NOT_HALAL** — a symbol not present in any covering regulator's index returns UNKNOWN, not NOT_HALAL — the index is a positive list (these are halal), not a negative list (these are forbidden). Mistaking absence for forbidden would silently disqualify every newly-listed Saudi equity between quarterly index updates; the pin protects the bot from this failure mode and surfaces an explicit "not present in any covering index for X" warning so the operator sees the gap. (3) **Staleness ladder**: listings within `stale_days` (default 90) are fresh; between `stale_days` and `expired_days` (default 365) carry a stale warning but the verdict still applies; older than `expired_days` are demoted to UNKNOWN with the staleness in warnings — past a year the underlying corporate facts may have shifted enough that the index hasn't re-confirmed, so blindly trusting a 14-month-old HALAL would risk trading a symbol whose financial structure changed. Both threshold boundaries are inclusive (90d → stale; 365d → expired) — pinned via tests against silent boundary drift. Multiple covering indices combine via conservative-tiebreak: NOT_HALAL > UNKNOWN > HALAL is the override order, so any single regulator saying NOT_HALAL is enough to disqualify (mirrors Wave 2.B halal consensus + Wave 4.J committee voting). The mixed-staleness pin: a "one fresh + one expired listing" cohort uses the fresh verdict — the expired source contributes UNKNOWN; the fresh source HALAL; combined → HALAL. The screener exposes `oldest_listing_age_days` reflecting the *worst* case so the operator audit trail captures the underlying staleness even when a fresh source carries the verdict. Render helper produces emoji-prefixed (✅/❌/❓) ops display with `(stale)` / `(expired)` markers visually consistent with the rest of the halal-side renderers (Wave 2.F scholar-review, Wave 1.I REIT screen, Wave 8.G public status). Halal alignment: ingestion is read-only; never opens a position; the matcher never silently downgrades a verdict; pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async — the live fetcher (httpx Tadawul + KMI-30 + SECP + CMA clients with quarterly cron + CSV-fallback for offline operators) is a deferred follow-up, the matcher verified in isolation first so the fetcher sees a stable contract. 58 tests cover the authority registry (every regulator → its market mapping pinned), IndexListing + RegulatorIndex + RegulatorThresholds field validation (timezone-aware datetimes required with naive rejected; duplicate-symbol rejection at construction with case-insensitive whitespace-stripped normalisation; threshold-ladder ordering — misordered ladder rejected, equal ladder accepted for operators who want zero warning band), case-insensitive + whitespace-stripped lookup (HBL / Hbl / hbl / "  hbl  " all match a single registered listing; whitespace-only and empty strings return None), basic outcomes (Saudi listing in TADAWUL → HALAL; Pakistani listing in KMI30 → HALAL; NOT_HALAL flows through with the right verdict), the cross-market authority guard pinned in BOTH directions (US symbol with TADAWUL index → UNKNOWN with empty sources; Pakistani symbol with only Saudi indices → UNKNOWN), the absence ≠ NOT_HALAL pin (symbol missing from a covering index → UNKNOWN with the "not present in any covering regulator index for SAUDI" warning; empty indices flow to UNKNOWN), Market.OTHER → UNKNOWN with the "no regional regulator covers Market.OTHER" warning, multiple-index combination (two HALAL → HALAL with both sources in `result.sources`; one HALAL + one NOT_HALAL → NOT_HALAL conservative tiebreak with both matched_listings recorded for audit; one HALAL + one UNKNOWN → HALAL because UNKNOWN doesn't override), the staleness ladder (fresh listing / stale listing / expired listing with both 90d and 365d boundaries inclusive — both directions tested), the mixed-staleness-across-sources pin (one fresh + one expired → fresh source's verdict wins, oldest_age reflects expired source so the audit trail captures the underlying staleness), custom thresholds flowing through (200d listing + strict 30/180 thresholds → expired), screener input validation (naive `now` rejected, empty symbol rejected at the screener boundary), convenience helpers (`listing_age_days` rejects naive datetime; `newest_index` returns the most-recently-fetched / None on empty), frozen-dataclass immutability across all four output dataclasses (IndexListing / RegulatorIndex / RegulatorThresholds / RegulatorScreenResult), all enum string values pinned for JSON / DB serialisation stability (`tadawul` / `cma_halal` / `kmi_30` / `secp_halal` for sources; `saudi` / `pakistan` / `other` for markets; `halal` / `not_halal` / `unknown` for verdicts), and render output across HALAL / NOT_HALAL / UNKNOWN with stale + expired markers and source list. Live fetcher (httpx clients per regulator with quarterly cron) and Wave 2.B consensus integration (fold the regional verdict in as a `RegulatorIndex` source with elevated weight on home-market symbols) deferred to follow-ups — matcher verified in isolation first.
* **Round-4 Wave 1.I — Halal REIT screening (screener core)** — `halal/reit_screener.py` is the REIT-specific shariah screen the general-purpose Zoya / sector-limit pipeline delegates to when the candidate is a real-estate trust. The general screener catches the broad-strokes failures (alcohol / gambling / pork / conventional banking) but slips on REITs whose own SIC code is "real estate" while the mall-anchor tenant is a conventional bank or wine retailer — the non-permissible exposure lives in the *tenants*, not the REIT itself. This layer applies the AAOIFI Standard 21 + Mufti Faraz Adam REIT framework: debt-to-marketcap ≤ 33%, NPI from forbidden-tenant rents ≤ 5%, property type cannot be inherently non-permissible. `screen_reit(financials, *, thresholds)` returns a `REITScreenResult` carrying status (HALAL / NOT_HALAL / DOUBTFUL / INSUFFICIENT_DATA), debt %, NPI %, liquid-assets %, purification % (equals NPI % when HALAL with marginal NPI — the operator's actionable "fraction of dividend to purify"), and per-rule failure / warning lists for the audit trail. **Three property-type classes are pinned**: (1) **inherently halal** (RESIDENTIAL / OFFICE / INDUSTRIAL / HEALTHCARE / DATA_CENTER / SELF_STORAGE) — pass without tenant detail because the tenant base is many small lessees with no systemic non-permissible exposure; (2) **tenant-dependent** (RETAIL_MALL / DIVERSIFIED) — need the tenant breakdown to clear; absent breakdown → DOUBTFUL not silent HALAL (this is the conservative-default pin: missing data is operator-decides, never assumed clean); (3) **inherently doubtful** (HOTEL / SPECIALTY) — even with clean tenant data they need scholar review for the underlying hospitality / specialty activities that the tenant list doesn't capture (room service, conference operations, amenity dining are all hotel-internal not tenant-side). Pinned semantics: HALAL requires both checks pass *and* the data present (missing tenant on retail mall → DOUBTFUL); zero market cap → INSUFFICIENT_DATA (can't compute ratios safely; alternative would be silent NOT_HALAL which is wrong because the data is *missing*, not failing); float-comparison boundaries inclusive (33.0% debt is HALAL; 33.0001% is NOT_HALAL — both directions pinned via tests against silent boundary drift); tenant-pct sum above 100% rejected at construction as data-entry error; below-100% sum accepted because the documented case is "operator labels the suspicious tenants, halal others implicit" (the rule is about *forbidden* income, not exhaustive coverage); purification % equals NPI % when HALAL with marginal NPI (operator gets the actionable dividend-purification fraction directly without re-deriving). The 70% liquid-assets check fires as a mis-classification guard (a financial-services-shell-pretending-to-be-a-REIT will breach this even if everything else passes — pinned via test). Thresholds configurable via `REITThresholds` for stricter operator profiles (the 30% / 3% profile flips marginal verdicts the other way — both flips pinned in tests). Halal alignment: the screener mirrors the conservative-tiebreak philosophy of Wave 2.B halal consensus and Wave 4.J committee voting (DOUBTFUL on missing data, never silent HALAL); no DB / network / async; frozen dataclasses on every output (REITFinancials / TenantContribution / REITThresholds / REITScreenResult); render helper produces emoji-prefixed (✅/❌/⚠️/❓) ops display visually consistent with the rest of the halal-side renderers (`scholar_review.render_recorded_verdict`, `aaoifi_summary`). 56 tests cover threshold validation (zero / negative / >100 rejections), TenantContribution + REITFinancials field validation (every non-negative invariant fires; whitespace-only tenant name rejected; tenant-pct sum > 100% rejected at construction), every property-type class outcome (each of the six inherently-halal types passes without tenant data; both tenant-dependent types without breakdown → DOUBTFUL with a "tenant breakdown missing" warning; both inherently-doubtful types → DOUBTFUL with a property-specific warning), the debt threshold's inclusive boundary tested in BOTH directions (33.0% passes, 33.0001% fails — the symmetry pin matters because asymmetric boundary handling is a common bug), liquid-assets > 70% mis-classification rejection, NPI boundary inclusive (5% pass with 5% purification, 8% fail with the right failure message), the marginal-NPI-HALAL-with-purification path (2.5% NPI on an office REIT lands HALAL with purification_pct=2.5), multiple-failure aggregation (a 50% debt + 80% liquid + 20% casino-tenant cohort surfaces 3 distinct rule failures all listed in `failures`), threshold customisation in both directions (a 30% strict profile flips a 32% debt verdict NOT_HALAL; a 3% strict NPI profile flips a 4% verdict NOT_HALAL — both pin the customisation flow end-to-end), frozen-dataclass immutability across all four output dataclasses, status string-value pins (`halal` / `not_halal` / `doubtful` / `insufficient_data`) for JSON serialisation stability with the dashboard / exception-queue UI, property-type string-value pins for the same reason, render output across all four statuses with the right emoji + section headers, render-omits-purification-when-zero pin (a clean residential REIT's render shouldn't have a purification line), and an end-to-end real-world Simon-property-trust-shaped retail mall with mixed tenants (60% halal anchor + 4% conventional bank + 4% cinema + 20% halal restaurants → 8% NPI total → NOT_HALAL with the right failure message). Wiring into the existing screener (delegate from `halal/screener.py` when the candidate symbol's SIC code or property classification flags a REIT, surface the result through the dashboard's halal-status tile, route DOUBTFUL verdicts into the scholar-review queue from Wave 2.F) deferred to a follow-up — the screener verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.
* **Round-4 Wave 2.F — Scholar review workflow** — `halal/scholar_review.py` is the pure-Python brief-and-verdict layer that sits on top of the existing `halal/exception_queue`: when the bot encounters a symbol with insufficient screening data (an IPO Zoya hasn't classified yet, a token whose CoinGecko description is borderline) it queues a `pending` exception entry; this module renders the operator-or-scholar-facing markdown brief and validates the recorded verdict before it flips the queue entry's status. Six surfaces compose the workflow. (1) `VerdictKind` enum with four values aligned to `ExceptionStatus` literal — `APPROVED` / `REJECTED` / `DEFERRED` / `WITHDRAWN` — the literal alignment is pinned so `apply_verdict` can write the queue entry's status field directly without a translation step that could silently drift. (2) `ReviewContext` frozen dataclass carries the shariah-relevant facts a scholar needs to issue an opinion: `sector`, `market_cap_usd`, `recent_revenue_breakdown` (per-segment dict), `debt_to_marketcap_pct`, `non_permissible_income_pct`, plus `notes` and `references` lists for citations. **Pinned no-PII contract**: `ReviewContext` has no operator-identifying fields by design — no account ID, no balance, no operator notes from the queue, no per-trade history. The regression test (`test_packet_does_not_leak_operator_pii`) asserts the rendered markdown never contains `account` / `balance` / `operator id` / `holdings` substrings, so a future field addition that leaks PII fails CI rather than shipping silently. The pin matters because review packets travel over email or chat to a third-party scholar — the contract is "shariah-relevant facts only, not operator identity". (3) `render_review_packet(*, entry_id, instrument, kind, reasoning, context, profile_name="aaoifi_default")` produces a markdown brief with seven sections: header (instrument + kind), Why this review (the queue entry's `reasoning`), Symbol context (sector / market cap / per-segment revenue), Financial screen inputs (debt-to-marketcap%, non-permissible-income% — the AAOIFI 33% / 5% thresholds the scholar checks against), Notes (free-form context), References (citation list — Mufti Faraz Adam crypto framework links, AAOIFI Standard 21 references, etc.), and How to respond (instructions for the scholar to reply with VERDICT + RATIONALE). The `profile_name` defaults to `aaoifi_default` and is rendered in the brief so the scholar knows which standard the bot is asking against — a future Hanafi or Maliki profile would change the thresholds. (4) `ScholarVerdict` frozen dataclass with strict `__post_init__` validation: `entry_id` non-empty, `decided_by` non-empty (audit-trail attribution — every verdict must be attributable to a specific reviewer), and **rationale required for APPROVED/REJECTED**, while DEFERRED and WITHDRAWN allow empty rationale. The asymmetry is intentional: APPROVED and REJECTED are decisions that affect future trades, so the rationale becomes part of the audit-trail justification; DEFERRED is "I want more info" and WITHDRAWN is "the operator no longer needs this reviewed", neither of which mints a screening decision. The validation rejects whitespace-only rationale (`"   "`) on APPROVED/REJECTED — pinned so a scholar can't slip a no-content verdict past audit by typing spaces. (5) `RecordedVerdict` audit row: `entry_id`, `instrument`, `kind`, `decided_by`, `rationale`, `decided_at`, `previous_status` — captures the queue state before the verdict mutated it so the audit trail can replay "this verdict took the entry from `pending` to `approved` at `2026-04-30 13:14 UTC`, decided by `scholar@example.org`, rationale `…`". (6) `apply_verdict(verdict, *, pending_entry_status, pending_entry_instrument, now)` enforces a status guard: raises `AlreadyDecidedError` if `pending_entry_status != "pending"` — pinned so one scholar's late-arriving verdict can't override another scholar's already-recorded decision. The `pending_entry_instrument` argument lets the caller assert the verdict matches the queue row (a verdict on `BTC:halal_review` arriving for an entry tagged `ETH:halal_review` is an integrity violation). `render_recorded_verdict(...)` formats the audit row for ops + Telegram with kind-specific emoji (✅ approve, ❌ reject, ⏳ defer, ↩️ withdraw) so the operator's notification channel renders the result distinctly. Halal alignment: review workflow is **read-and-decide**, never opens a trade — the verdict feeds the screening cache, not the executor; rationale text becomes part of the audit ledger; the no-PII contract is the explicit operator-privacy guard at the boundary leaving the bot. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async; the queue + cache wiring (FastAPI route at `/halal/review/<entry_id>` that renders the packet, accepts the verdict via signed-token from a configured scholar email list, and writes the verdict back into `halal/exception_queue`) is deferred to a follow-up — the workflow is verified in isolation first so the route layer sees a stable contract. 34 tests cover packet rendering (header / section presence / sector + market cap rendering / per-segment revenue iteration / threshold values appear / notes + references rendering / no-PII regression pin); `ScholarVerdict` validation (entry_id non-empty, decided_by non-empty, rationale required for APPROVED, rationale required for REJECTED, whitespace-only rationale rejected, DEFERRED accepts empty rationale, WITHDRAWN accepts empty rationale, frozen-dataclass immutability); `apply_verdict` status guard (rejects already-decided entries — both `approved` and `rejected` and `deferred` past states all raise, instrument mismatch raises, valid pending → APPROVED writes RecordedVerdict with previous_status="pending", valid pending → REJECTED similarly); render output (emoji per kind, decided_by visible, rationale visible, decided_at formatted).

* **Round-4 Wave 3.F — Stripe billing + tier upgrades (state engine)** — `web/billing_state.py` is the pure-Python billing state machine the Stripe webhook handler composes with. The roadmap calls for "Pro tier $19/mo, real-money trading + larger universe; Enterprise custom; Stripe webhooks update user tier" — the SDK integration (webhook receiver for `invoice.paid` / `invoice.payment_failed` / `subscription.created/updated/deleted`) is operator-side; this module ships the deterministic state-transition primitives the handler composes with. Picked a focused state machine over a "hand-roll subscription logic per route" approach because (a) the state transitions need to be deterministic + regression-pinnable (the same event applied to the same state always produces the same next state, so operators can replay event history to audit historical tier-at-moment for any past timestamp — a billing dispute "what was their tier on 2026-03-15 at 14:22 UTC" answer comes from re-feeding events into the engine, not from peering at log scraps), (b) the Wave 3.C quota system (LLM budget gate) keys on the *effective* tier — which isn't the same as the Stripe-stated tier when the user is in a grace period or cancellation, so the engine computes the effective tier deterministically and the quota gate trusts the result. Tier is re-used from Wave 3.C `web/quotas.py` so billing + quota engine speak the same vocabulary — adding a new tier means one Enum entry in one file, not two. Six-state lifecycle with pinned string values (TRIALING / ACTIVE / PAST_DUE / GRACE_PERIOD / CANCELLED / EXPIRED) — string values pinned for JSON / DB stability so the dashboard's billing-event audit log keys on stable literals; seven event kinds (SUBSCRIPTION_CREATED / INVOICE_PAID / INVOICE_PAYMENT_FAILED / TIER_UPGRADED / TIER_DOWNGRADED / SUBSCRIPTION_CANCELLED / TRIAL_ENDED) — the Stripe webhook handler maps Stripe event types to these literals before calling `apply_event`. `BillingPolicy` validates `default_trial_days` in `[7, 30]` (default 14): below 7d is operationally awful (user doesn't have time to evaluate); above 30d is revenue leakage (tier should convert by then) — both boundaries inclusive, both directions tested. `grace_period_days` validated positive (default 7d — Stripe's default grace period). `Subscription` enforces `current_period_start` / `current_period_end` / optional `trial_end_at` / optional `grace_period_end_at` are all timezone-aware (load-bearing for staleness arithmetic) plus `current_period_end > current_period_start` invariant (a misconfigured webhook payload that produces zero-length or backwards period is rejected at construction rather than silently weakening every effective-tier comparison downstream). `BillingEvent` requires `target_tier` for `TIER_UPGRADED` and `TIER_DOWNGRADED` (an upgrade-without-target-tier event is meaningless data) but NOT for the other five kinds; the asymmetry is intentional and pinned in tests. `create_trial(*, user_id, tier, now, policy)` rejects `Tier.FREE` — FREE doesn't trial; the bot's "free tier user" is a separate `create_active_free` flow, not a 14-day countdown to the same FREE state. `apply_event` is deterministic + idempotent on `SUBSCRIPTION_CREATED` (Stripe might re-deliver after a network hiccup; engine just returns the subscription as-is), and dispatches to one of `_apply_invoice_paid` (extends period by the previous period length, restores ACTIVE, clears trial + grace timestamps), `_apply_invoice_failed` (enters GRACE_PERIOD with grace-end at `now + grace_period_days`), `_apply_trial_ended` (sets EXPIRED + clears trial timestamp), or the inline TIER_UPGRADED / TIER_DOWNGRADED / SUBSCRIPTION_CANCELLED branches. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface: (1) **Trial period 7-30 days** — both inclusive boundaries pinned both directions; (2) **Grace period 7d default** before downgrade to FREE — Stripe's default; gives users time to update payment methods; after 7d effective tier drops to FREE; the operator's manual reactivation flow can restore by injecting an INVOICE_PAID event; (3) **Cancellation downgrades at period end, not immediately** — the user paid for the period; they keep PRO/ENTERPRISE features until the period naturally ends. SUBSCRIPTION_CANCELLED sets `cancel_at_period_end=True` while keeping tier + status; `compute_effective_tier` checks `cancel_at_period_end and now >= current_period_end` to drop to FREE. (4) **Upgrades take effect immediately** — a user upgrading from PRO to ENTERPRISE gets ENTERPRISE features in the same request; pro-rated billing is the Stripe SDK's concern. (5) **Render output never includes invoice amounts / Stripe customer IDs / dollar signs** — `render_subscription` shows status emoji (🆓 TRIALING, ✅ ACTIVE, ⏰ PAST_DUE, ⚠️ GRACE_PERIOD, 🛑 CANCELLED, ❌ EXPIRED) + user_id + tier + effective tier (when different) + period dates + trial/grace/cancel markers; the no-secret-leak regression asserts no `$` and no `USD` substrings appear in rendered output, mirroring no-secret patterns of Wave 3.B vault + Wave 8.D OTLP + Wave 12.G co-pilot. The load-bearing `compute_effective_tier(subscription, *, now)` covers every status × `cancel_at_period_end` × time combination: EXPIRED → FREE; CANCELLED before period end → tier; CANCELLED at-or-after period end → FREE (boundary inclusive); GRACE_PERIOD before grace end → tier; GRACE_PERIOD at-or-after grace end → FREE (boundary inclusive); TRIALING before trial end → tier; TRIALING at-or-after trial end → FREE (boundary inclusive); PAST_DUE → tier (transient bookkeeping status before webhook progresses to GRACE_PERIOD); ACTIVE-without-cancel → tier; ACTIVE-with-`cancel_at_period_end` before period end → tier; ACTIVE-with-`cancel_at_period_end` at-or-after period end → FREE. The boundary-inclusive comparisons are pinned both directions per status to guard against silent boundary drift (the `>= ` vs `> ` distinction matters: at 7d 0s after grace start, the 7d grace has *expired*, not *almost expired*). 76 tests cover: BillingPolicy validation (boundaries 7/30 accepted; 6 / 31 rejected; 0 / -1 grace rejected; immutability); Subscription validation (timezone-aware required for every datetime field with naive rejected; period-end-equal-to-start rejected; period-end-before-start rejected; whitespace user_id rejected; immutability); BillingEvent validation (empty event_id rejected; naive timestamp rejected; TIER_UPGRADED + TIER_DOWNGRADED require target_tier; INVOICE_PAID + others don't; immutability); SubscriptionStatus + BillingEventKind enum string-value pins for JSON / DB stability; `create_trial` happy paths (default 14d; custom 21d via policy) + FREE rejection + naive-now rejection + empty user_id rejection + PRO/ENTERPRISE both supported; every event-kind transition (SUBSCRIPTION_CREATED idempotent; INVOICE_PAID extends period + restores ACTIVE + clears trial/grace; INVOICE_PAID with custom grace policy; INVOICE_PAYMENT_FAILED enters GRACE_PERIOD with default 7d + custom 14d; TIER_UPGRADED takes effect immediately + restores ACTIVE from GRACE_PERIOD; TIER_DOWNGRADED stages cancel_at_period_end + sets new tier on the subscription with the period-end gate handled by compute_effective_tier; SUBSCRIPTION_CANCELLED stages cancel_at_period_end keeping tier + status; TRIAL_ENDED → EXPIRED + clears trial); `apply_event` naive-now rejection; `compute_effective_tier` across every status × time combination including boundary-inclusive grace expiry + trial expiry + period-end cancellation pins both directions; render output (user_id + status + tier + period present; status emoji per status; effective-tier shown when different from subscription tier; trial-end / grace-end / cancel-scheduled markers conditional; no-`$` and no-`USD` no-secret-leak regression pins); end-to-end realistic flows (trial → conversion via INVOICE_PAID; invoice failure → grace → recovery via second INVOICE_PAID; invoice failure → grace expires past 7d → FREE; cancellation lifecycle — keeps PRO until period end, drops to FREE at boundary; immediate upgrade — effective tier ENTERPRISE the same request; trial expires without conversion → EXPIRED → FREE; downgrade-takes-effect-at-period-end — tier ENTERPRISE → PRO with cancel_at_period_end staged, FREE at the period-end boundary); determinism regression pins on both `apply_event` and `compute_effective_tier` (same inputs always produce same outputs, so operator audit replay is reliable). The Stripe webhook receiver (FastAPI route at `/api/billing/webhook` validating Stripe signature + mapping Stripe event types to BillingEventKind literals + calling `apply_event` + persisting Subscription rows), the per-tier knob wiring into `core/llm/budget.py` (the Wave 3.C quota gate already keys on `Tier`; the integration is calling `compute_effective_tier(user_subscription, now=datetime.now(UTC))` at the budget-check boundary), the Postgres `subscriptions` + `billing_events` tables + repository, and the operator settings UI for tier upgrades all deferred to follow-ups — the state engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 3.G — Admin console view-model engine** — `web/admin_console.py` is the pure-Python admin aggregator that composes the multi-tenant primitives landed in earlier waves (3.A user auth, 3.C resource quotas, 3.F billing-tier-state) into a single view-model the admin route consumes. The roadmap calls for "hosted-tenant admin: see all users, their LLM spend, their portfolio P&L, halt-switch any user's bot, billing override; restricted to configured admin emails" — this module ships the deterministic aggregation + admin-action audit primitives the route layer composes with. Picked a focused view-model over a "hand-roll admin route logic" approach because (a) the admin-email gate is a single load-bearing authorization check that should not be re-derived at every route — if the admin list logic drifts between routes, an admin de-listed in one place but still trusted in another is an audit-failure class, (b) every admin action against a tenant's bot must be attributed + reasoned + timestamped — the audit row needs to survive a future "why did the bot halt at 14:22?" question against a stable schema, and (c) the aggregation totals (active users, total LLM spend, halt count) are read-only summaries that the admin console renders the same way the operator email summary renders its end-of-day report — pure functions of the input snapshot. Six composed surfaces. (1) `AdminEmailList` frozen dataclass — operators populate from env / config at boot; emails are normalised to lowercase + whitespace-strip at construction (so `Admin@Foo.com` / `  bob@bar.com  ` / `ADMIN@FOO.COM` all match a single registered entry); the list is immutable after construction so a runtime mutation can't silently elevate a user; rejects empty list / empty / whitespace-only / `@`-less emails. (2) `AdminAuthorizationError` exception carries the offending email so the operator's exception handler can render an actionable message (rate-limit logging, audit-pin notification). (3) `AdminAction` enum with six values pinned for JSON / DB stability (HALT_USER / RESUME_USER / OVERRIDE_TIER / REVOKE_SESSION / SUSPEND_USER / INSPECT_USER) — operators add new actions via code review (rather than DB insert) so action drift can't silently change the destructive-action set. (4) `UserSummary` frozen dataclass carries the cross-cutting triage facts the admin needs to act: user_id / email / effective_tier (the Wave 3.F `compute_effective_tier` output, not the Stripe-stated tier) / subscription_status / llm_usd_used_today / llm_usd_limit_today / halt_active / last_active_at / joined_at. The dataclass *deliberately* does NOT carry: password hash, scrypt salt, session tokens, broker API keys, Stripe customer ID, invoice amounts — the no-secret-leak contract is structural (a future field addition that surfaced any of these would be a deliberate code-review change, not a slip-through), pinned via render regression tests asserting `cus_` / `sub_` / `password` / `hash` / `salt` / `session_` / `bearer` substrings never appear in rendered output. The `llm_usage_fraction` property guards divide-by-zero (zero-limit returns 0.0 rather than raising) — important because the FREE tier has zero `broker_api_calls` and a future tier could have zero `llm_usd_daily`, and a render that crashed on the FREE row would take the whole admin view down. (5) `AdminActionRequest` + `audit_admin_action` is the authorization boundary: every admin action passes through `audit_admin_action` which checks the admin list before producing the audit row; a non-admin caller never gets to the action's side-effect logic. The validation is asymmetric by design: HALT_USER / OVERRIDE_TIER / SUSPEND_USER / REVOKE_SESSION (the four destructive actions) require non-empty rationale; RESUME_USER + INSPECT_USER do not. The asymmetry matters because "halted" with no reason is a mystery to the next on-call (the audit row must be self-explanatory at 3am), but a resume action is naturally a follow-up to a previously-recorded halt and doesn't add new audit information. Whitespace-only reason on a destructive action is also rejected — pinned so an admin can't slip a no-content destructive action past audit by typing spaces. `target_tier` required for OVERRIDE_TIER (an upgrade-without-target-tier is meaningless data). The audit record's `performed_by` is the *normalised* admin email, not the input email — a future log analysis querying "all actions by admin@foo.com" returns hits regardless of whether the admin signed in with mixed case. (6) `build_admin_view(users, *, now, active_window=24h)` aggregates a user iterable into `AdminView` with: `total_users`, `active_users_24h` with the boundary explicitly inclusive (a user active *exactly* 24h ago is still active — pinned via test against silent boundary drift), `halt_active_count`, `total_llm_usd_today`, `tier_breakdown` (a tuple of `(Tier, count)` pairs in fixed Tier-enum order; every Tier appears even with zero users so the dashboard's tier-pie-chart can iterate without missing-tier branches), `users` sorted by `joined_at` ascending (deterministic ordering across renders — the admin viewing the page twice gets the same row order both times). The custom `active_window` argument lets the same engine produce a 7-day-active aggregate by passing `timedelta(days=7)`, so the same module powers both the daily-active dashboard and a weekly retention view; both `<= 0` and zero windows rejected. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Admin email match is case-insensitive after whitespace strip** — operators add admin emails through env config; mixed-case + extra spaces are normal data-entry slop; rejecting `Admin@Foo.com` while accepting `admin@foo.com` would be an opaque misconfiguration. The pin is tested in both directions (`Admin@Foo.com` registered → `admin@foo.com` matches; `admin@foo.com` registered → `ADMIN@FOO.COM` matches; whitespace stripped). (2) **Non-admin email → AdminAuthorizationError at the audit boundary, not at a downstream route** — the authorization is a single load-bearing check inside `audit_admin_action` so every admin route that wants to act on a user goes through the same gate. The pin is tested with an explicit "attacker email submitting a HALT request → AdminAuthorizationError, no audit record produced". (3) **Reason required for destructive actions, optional for read-only / recovery actions** — both directions tested per action kind; whitespace-only reason on destructive action rejected. (4) **Render output never includes session tokens / Stripe customer IDs / API keys / password hashes / scrypt salts** — three render functions (`render_user_summary` / `render_admin_view` / `render_action_record`) all carry the no-secret-leak regression assertion. The contract mirrors no-secret patterns of Wave 3.B vault + Wave 8.D OTLP + Wave 12.G co-pilot + Wave 3.F billing — the operator's rendered admin view goes into incident-response Slack threads + on-call email summaries, so the no-secret guarantee is the boundary leaving the bot. (5) **Aggregation is deterministic** — same input list + same `now` + same `active_window` → same `AdminView`. The admin route can render the same view twice and not get inconsistent counts; pinned via test. Halal alignment: admin-console actions are **operator-tooling**, never open a trade — the halt action defers to the existing kill-switch `core/halt.is_halted(engine)` (Wave referenced in CLAUDE.md), which gates the cycle's run path. The audit trail is the same audit-trail philosophy as Wave 2.F scholar-review (every verdict attributable + reasoned + timestamped) and Wave 11.B SSB governance (every meeting + vote + minute attributable). Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async / HTTP. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 76 tests cover: AdminEmailList normalisation (case-insensitive + whitespace-strip in both directions; rejects empty list / empty / whitespace-only / `@`-less emails; immutability), UserSummary validation (empty user_id / empty email / `@`-less email / negative LLM-used / negative LLM-limit / naive joined_at / naive last_active_at all rejected; None last_active_at accepted; immutability), llm_usage_fraction edge cases (basic 0.25 / zero-limit returns 0.0 / at-limit returns 1.0), AdminActionRequest validation (empty action_id / empty target_user_id / empty performed_by / `@`-less performed_by / naive performed_at all rejected), the asymmetric reason-requirement pin (HALT_USER / OVERRIDE_TIER / SUSPEND_USER / REVOKE_SESSION reject empty + whitespace-only reason; RESUME_USER + INSPECT_USER accept empty reason), OVERRIDE_TIER target_tier requirement, audit_admin_action authorization gate (non-admin → AdminAuthorizationError carrying the offending email; admin → record with normalised performed_by; deterministic), build_admin_view aggregation (empty input; correct user-count + active-count with 24h boundary inclusive; halt-count; total-spend; tier-breakdown with zero-count tiers present; users sorted by joined_at; rejects naive `now` and zero / negative active_window; custom 7-day window flows through; deterministic), AdminAction string-value pins for JSON / DB stability, render no-secret-leak regression across user / view / record (no `cus_` / `sub_` Stripe IDs; no `password` / `hash` / `salt`; no `session_` / `bearer` tokens), and end-to-end flows (admin halts then resumes; non-admin attempt blocked at boundary; full multi-user view-render with 3 users across all tiers showing correct totals + tier breakdown + per-user rows). The FastAPI route layer (`/api/admin/users` + `/api/admin/users/{id}/halt` + `/api/admin/users/{id}/override-tier` with `Depends(authenticate)` from Wave 3.A returning the request user's email + the AdminEmailList loaded from `Settings`), the Postgres `admin_actions` audit table + repository, and the dashboard admin pages all deferred to follow-ups — view-model verified in isolation first so the route layer sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 3.H — Strategy leaderboard with opt-in privacy** — `web/leaderboard.py` is the pure-Python ranking + anonymisation engine that the public leaderboard route consumes. The roadmap calls for "aggregated (anonymised) leaderboard: top 10 strategies by Sharpe this quarter, by win rate this month; lets users discover what's working and clone a public strategy template; privacy: opt-in only" — this module ships the deterministic pipeline that turns a heterogeneous list of per-user strategy entries into a privacy-respecting public leaderboard. Picked a focused engine over a "hand-roll a SQL query per route" approach because (a) the privacy contract is the load-bearing surface — opt-in is a per-strategy switch, *not* a per-user-account switch; an account that opted out at signup but later opts in for a single strategy must surface only that strategy and nothing else; a single chokepoint that filters opt-in at the boundary is far safer than 8 different routes that each have to remember to filter, (b) the ranking metrics need consistent boundary semantics across windows — pure functions of (entries, window, metric) regression-pin those boundaries, and (c) anonymisation needs a minimum sample threshold (k-anonymity-like) — a leaderboard with one entry isn't a leaderboard, it's a personal page. Three composed enums + four dataclasses. `LeaderboardMetric` (SHARPE / WIN_RATE / TOTAL_RETURN_PCT) + `LeaderboardWindow` (MONTHLY=30d / QUARTERLY=90d / YEARLY=365d / ALL_TIME=no-bound) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. `LeaderboardPolicy` (default `min_entries_to_publish=5`, `top_n=10`, `min_sample_size=10`) is the operator-tunable knob — the 5-entry k-anonymity floor is the privacy guard (below 5, individual entries become re-identifiable by elimination, especially when paired with the strategy_kind hint), `top_n` is the rendered cohort size, `min_sample_size` is the per-entry trade count threshold below which an entry is excluded (a strategy with 3 trades has too-noisy a Sharpe to rank). Validation rejects `min_entries < 2` (a 1-entry leaderboard is meaningless), zero / negative `top_n`, negative `min_sample_size`. `StrategyEntry` is the input row — carries user_id (recorded for opt-in lookup + audit but NEVER surfaced) + strategy_id + display_handle (chosen by the user, what surfaces in render output) + strategy_kind + opt_in flag + created_at + last_traded_at + sharpe + win_rate + total_return_pct + sample_size. Validation rejects empty user_id / strategy_id / display_handle / strategy_kind, naive datetimes (timezone-aware required for window-arithmetic correctness), win_rate outside [0,1] (both boundaries inclusive — pinned in both directions), negative sample_size. `LeaderboardRow` (the rendered output) intentionally has NO user_id field — anonymisation is *structural*, not just a render-time filter; a future field addition that surfaced user_id would have to overcome the dataclass shape, not just the render formatter. The dataclass-introspection regression test (`test_leaderboard_row_is_anonymous`) asserts via `__dataclass_fields__` that `user_id` and `email` keys never appear on the row. `Leaderboard` is the full view-model carrying metric + window + generated_at + rows tuple + `eligible_count` (after opt-in + window + sample-size filtering) + `excluded_below_min_sample` (audit count for "how many low-sample-size entries were dropped") + `suppressed_below_k_anonymity` (boolean signalling "we have N < min_entries opted-in qualifiers, so we're returning empty rows"). The `build_leaderboard(entries, *, metric, window, now, policy)` pipeline is the load-bearing function. Step 1: filter to `opt_in=True`. Step 2: filter to entries within the window (`last_traded_at >= now - window_duration`; ALL_TIME bypasses); the boundary is inclusive (a trade exactly 30 days ago is still in the monthly window — pinned to guard against silent drift). Step 3: filter to `sample_size >= policy.min_sample_size`; the count of dropped entries is recorded on the result for audit. Step 4: if remaining count < `policy.min_entries_to_publish`, return an empty `Leaderboard` with `suppressed_below_k_anonymity=True` (the route layer renders a "not enough data yet" message rather than the empty cohort). Step 5: sort by metric descending; tie-break by older `created_at` first (more battle-tested strategies rank above brand-new copycats with the same Sharpe — operators expect deterministic ordering across renders), then by `strategy_id` for full lexicographic determinism. Step 6: take top `policy.top_n`.
