The tag drives operator UI hints (Saudi operator sees "✅ TADAWUL operates the Halal Index in-house") rather than executor behavior (the executor still consults the consensus screener for every trade). (5) **Render output never includes broker API keys / customer IDs / session tokens.** The registry is pure catalogue data; the structural no-secret pin holds because the dataclasses simply don't have those fields. The render regression test loops over every exchange asserting no `api_key` / `secret` / `cus_` substrings appear. Halal alignment: the registry surfaces five Muslim-majority-jurisdiction exchanges with `BUILT_IN` halal infrastructure (TADAWUL Saudi, DIFC UAE, KLSE Malaysia, IDX Indonesia, PSX Pakistan) — a halal trader anywhere in the OIC zone has a home market in this catalogue, and the resolver routes them there preferentially. The pin matters because a non-OIC trader bot that defaulted to "US OTC" for Aramco would silently funnel Saudi operator capital out of the home market into a foreign-currency proxy with looser shariah guarantees. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async / broker SDK. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 55 tests cover: all 13 Exchange MIC pins (XNYS / XNAS / OTCM / XLON / XTKS / XHKG / XNSE / XBOM / XSAU / DIFX / XCAI / XKLS / XIDX / XKAR); all 11 Jurisdiction string pins; all 3 HalalInfrastructure pins; TradingHours validation (close-before-open / close-equals-open / empty trading_days / day-out-of-range / tz-offset-out-of-range all rejected; immutable); ExchangeProfile validation (empty display_name / negative settlement / settlement above 5 rejected; immutable); registry coverage (every Exchange enum has a profile; canonical order matches enum order); jurisdiction pins (NYSE+NASDAQ+OTC=US; TADAWUL=SAUDI_ARABIA+BUILT_IN; DIFC=UAE+BUILT_IN; PSX=PAKISTAN+BUILT_IN; KLSE+IDX BUILT_IN); exchanges_for_jurisdiction (US returns NYSE/NASDAQ/OTC; INDIA returns NSE/BSE; SAUDI_ARABIA returns TADAWUL); is_market_open across timezones (NYSE 14:30 UTC Tuesday open; 13:00 UTC before open; 22:00 UTC after close; Saturday closed; TADAWUL Sunday 11:00 Saudi local open — *pinned* the Sun-Thu week; TADAWUL Friday closed; TSE 09:30 JST Monday open; EGX Friday closed); boundary inclusive at exact open (NYSE 14:30 UTC = 9:30 EST → TRUE); boundary exclusive at exact close (NYSE 21:00 UTC = 16:00 EST → FALSE); naive now rejected; CrossListing validation; resolve_home_market (returns primary when no jurisdiction; returns local when jurisdiction matches — Saudi → TADAWUL Aramco, US → OTC Aramco, HK → HKSE BABA, US → NYSE BABA; unknown issuer returns None; jurisdiction-no-match falls back to primary; no primary + no jurisdiction match returns None — pinned so the engine doesn't guess); render output (display_name + MIC visible; halal emoji 🕌 for BUILT_IN, 🔍 for THIRD_PARTY, 🛠️ for OUR_SCREENER_ONLY; settlement T+N visible; no-secret leak across all 13 exchanges); e2e flows (Saudi operator buying Aramco routes to TADAWUL with BUILT_IN halal; US operator buying BABA routes to NYSE; LSE-NYSE overlap window — at 09:00 UTC Tuesday LSE is open but NYSE is not yet). The Saxo/IBKR/Alpaca-International broker adapters consuming this registry, the holiday calendar layer (broker-API-driven; layered on top via `is_holiday_closed(exchange, *, now)` that defers to broker-reported state), the cycle-side symbol-selection hook in `crypto/cycle.py` and `trading/strategy.py` that calls `resolve_home_market` for every cross-listed candidate, and the dashboard "international markets" tile (renders `is_market_open` per registry exchange so the operator sees a global market clock) all deferred to follow-ups — registry verified in isolation first so the broker integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 8.A — E2E integration test scenario catalogue** — `ops/e2e_scenarios.py` is the pure-Python catalogue + last-run tracker the nightly CI lane consults to know which broker-touching tests to run, what outcomes to assert, and which scenarios have gone stale. The roadmap pins "a nightly CI lane that hits real testnet endpoints (Binance, Alpaca), runs full cycles, asserts no halt-trips, no rejected orders, no missed fills" — this module ships the catalogue + freshness logic + run audit; the actual broker-touching test bodies go under `tests/integration/` and consume this module's scenario list as their parametrize input. Picked a focused catalogue over a single-big-nightly-script approach because (a) different scenarios have different broker dependencies — pinning the dependency in the scenario lets the CI lane skip scenarios whose broker is currently unreachable rather than fail the whole lane (a Binance testnet outage shouldn't fail the alpaca_full_cycle scenario), (b) staleness tracking is a pure function of last_passed_at — surfacing it deterministically lets the dashboard render "scenario X is overdue" without re-deriving the logic at every site, (c) the scenario kind enum groups scenarios for routing — the operator dashboard can show "all halt-related scenarios passing" as a single tile and a future "we want to skip cycle scenarios this run" filter is one enum check away. Six composed surfaces. (1) `ScenarioKind` enum (CYCLE / ORDER / HALT / RECONCILE / WEBSOCKET / FAILOVER) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability — the dashboard groupings can't drift if the enum is closed. (2) `RequiredBroker` enum (NONE for broker-agnostic scenarios like local replay; BINANCE_TESTNET and ALPACA_PAPER for the two roadmap-named sandboxes) — pinned so the CI lane that decides "Binance is unreachable" can SKIP only scenarios with `required_broker=BINANCE_TESTNET`. (3) `RunOutcome` enum (PASSED / FAILED / SKIPPED) — SKIPPED is the structural pin that keeps the staleness clock honest: a scenario SKIPPED 14 days running because Binance testnet was down should NOT register as fresh; only PASSED runs reset the clock. (4) `FreshnessLevel` enum (FRESH / STALE / CRITICAL / NEVER_RUN) and `ScenarioPolicy` ladders fresh=7d / stale=14d / critical=28d (operator-tunable; constructor enforces ordering — `stale > fresh`, `critical > stale`, all positive — so a misconfigured policy fails fast rather than producing nonsense classifications). (5) `Scenario` frozen dataclass carries scenario_id + kind + required_broker + description + expected_outcome. The `expected_outcome` field is pinned non-empty so a contributor adding a new scenario must document the success criteria — "the test passes" without further detail is meaningless to the next on-call. (6) Module-level `_SEED_SCENARIOS` populated with 8 catalogue entries that map to the roadmap's failure modes: `binance_full_cycle` (full crypto cycle on testnet — the headline scenario), `binance_order_lifecycle` (place market order, observe fill, record submitted/filled timestamps — pin against the `core/fills.py` confirmation contract), `binance_websocket_stream` (100+ ticks for BTCUSDT in 60s — pin against the WebSocket buffer that powers `crypto/cycle.py`), `alpaca_full_cycle` (full stocks cycle during market hours — APScheduler-driven), `alpaca_order_lifecycle` (limit order on Alpaca paper — pins the `core/reconcile.py` aggregation contract), `halt_then_resume` (broker-agnostic — kill-switch behavior), `broker_5xx_failover` (broker-agnostic — circuit breaker engagement per Wave 8.B chaos engine), `reconciliation_drift` (broker-agnostic — local-vs-broker mismatch detection per `core/reconcile.py`). `RunRecord` is the audit row carrying scenario_id + outcome + decided_at + optional notes. `last_passed_run(records, scenario_id)` filters to PASSED records for the scenario and returns the most recent — ignoring FAILED and SKIPPED is the structural pin that keeps the clock honest. `freshness_for(last_passed_at, *, now, policy)` classifies via the inclusive ladder: `>= critical_threshold` → CRITICAL; `>= fresh_threshold` → STALE (note: the implementation only checks two thresholds because the band between fresh and stale collapses into "STALE" — anything past the fresh threshold is no longer fresh, and the stale_threshold is for the operator's mental model); `last_passed_at is None` → NEVER_RUN. `build_status(scenarios, *, records, now, policy)` aggregates per-freshness counts across the catalogue. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set ScenarioKind enum.** Adding a kind is a code review change; the dashboard groupings can't drift. (2) **Required broker is part of the scenario.** A scenario tagged BINANCE_TESTNET is SKIPPED (not FAILED) when Binance testnet is unreachable; the CI lane consults `scenario.required_broker` to decide. The pin matters because conflating "broker unreachable" with "test failed" would have the on-call paged 4am for AWS region X being down. (3) **Staleness ladder is operator-tunable but ordered.** Default 7/14/28 days; constructor enforces the ladder. (4) **Outcome enum: PASSED / FAILED / SKIPPED with SKIPPED-doesn't-help-freshness pin.** Pinned via the explicit "30-day-old PASS + 5 SKIPPED in last 5 days → CRITICAL" e2e test — a future contributor that "fixed" the freshness function to count SKIPPED would fail this test rather than ship and silently mask the staleness. (5) **Render output never includes broker API responses, account balances, or order IDs.** The catalogue is pure metadata (scenario descriptions + expected outcomes); the structural no-secret pin holds because the dataclasses simply don't have those fields. The render regression test loops over every seed scenario asserting no `api_key` / `cus_` / `bearer` substrings appear. Halal alignment: E2E tests protect operator continuity — a halal screener that silently regresses past testnet validation would let non-halal trades slip through; the catalogue + staleness ladder makes that regression impossible to hide for more than 7 days. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async / broker SDK. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 56 tests cover: ScenarioKind + RequiredBroker + RunOutcome + FreshnessLevel enum string-value pins; ScenarioPolicy validation (zero / negative thresholds rejected; out-of-order ladder rejected — stale_below_fresh and critical_below_stale both pinned; immutable); Scenario validation (empty scenario_id / description / expected_outcome rejected; immutable); RunRecord validation (empty scenario_id / naive decided_at rejected; immutable); catalogue coverage (every ScenarioKind has at least one seed scenario; both BINANCE_TESTNET and ALPACA_PAPER have scenarios; full_cycle for both brokers exists; halt_then_resume exists; reconciliation_drift exists; lookup-by-id; unknown lookup raises KeyError; canonical sorted order); freshness boundary pins both directions (fresh < 7d; 7d boundary inclusive → STALE; just-below 7d → FRESH; 28d boundary inclusive → CRITICAL; just-below 28d → STALE; well-past 28d → CRITICAL); custom strict policy (1d/2d/4d) flows through; naive now and naive last_passed_at rejected; last_passed_run returns most recent PASSED; ignores FAILED + SKIPPED (the load-bearing pin); returns None when never passed; filters by scenario_id; empty records → None; build_status across empty / all-never-run / mixed-freshness cohorts; rejects naive now; immutable; deterministic; render scenario includes id + kind + broker + description + expected; render scenario kind emoji per kind; no-secret regression across all seed scenarios; render status includes counts + freshness emoji; e2e nightly run lifecycle (day 1 PASS → FRESH; day 8 → STALE; day 30 → CRITICAL); e2e SKIPPED-for-broker-down with 30-day-old PASS still classifies CRITICAL — pinned to guard against silent SKIPPED-resets-clock regressions. The actual `tests/integration/` module that consumes this catalogue (parametrize over `all_scenarios()`, dispatch to `run_binance_full_cycle()` / `run_alpaca_full_cycle()` / etc test bodies that hit the real testnet endpoints), the GitHub Actions / GitLab CI nightly lane (with the `BINANCE_TESTNET_API_KEY` + `ALPACA_PAPER_API_KEY` secrets injected via the runner), the dashboard "E2E status" tile (renders `build_status` output with overdue scenarios highlighted), and the AlertSink integration (fires when any scenario goes CRITICAL) all deferred to follow-ups — catalogue verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 4.A — RL policy training scaffold (config + episode tracker)** — `ml/rl_training.py` is the pure-Python config + episode tracker + reward-shaping engine that the deferred Stable-Baselines3 / Ray RLlib training step consumes. The roadmap pins "PPO/SAC policy on historical replay data; RL + LLM ensemble; LLM provides explainability while RL provides rigour" — this module ships the configuration + tracking primitives, regression-pinned so the actual training loop sees a stable contract. Picked a focused config + episode model over a single-training-script approach because (a) hyperparameter validation is a decision rule that should fail fast at training entry rather than 30 minutes into a GPU burn — a frozen TrainingConfig with `__post_init__` rejects invalid combinations at construction, including the algorithm/action-space mismatch (PPO doesn't support continuous; SAC doesn't support discrete) which is a common contributor mistake, (b) reward shaping is a pure function deserving regression pins — a contributor changing the weight on drawdown_penalty has to update tests rather than silently shipping a model that no longer "avoids drawdown", (c) the episode + trajectory primitives let training runs be replayed and diffed against historical baselines without re-running the actual training, and (d) the deployment lifecycle mirrors Wave 6.I distillation deployment so operators have one mental model for "promoting a learned policy to production". Six composed surfaces. (1) `RLAlgorithm` enum (PPO / SAC) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability — adding an algorithm is a code review change, the closed-set rules out a contributor adding "DDPG" or "A3C" without considering the algorithm/action-space compatibility matrix. (2) `ActionSpace` enum (DISCRETE / CONTINUOUS) — the bot's action space depends on the strategy; the Wave 4.B genetic strategy generator outputs discrete BUY/SELL/HOLD signals (PPO fits), but a position-sizing strategy outputs a continuous fraction in [-1, 1] (SAC fits). (3) Module-level `_ALGO_REQUIRES_DISCRETE` and `_ALGO_REQUIRES_CONTINUOUS` frozensets pin the compatibility rule outside the validation function so a future contributor adding a new algorithm has to explicitly add it to one or both sets. (4) `TrainingConfig` carries algorithm + action_space + learning_rate + gamma + batch_size + clip_range + total_timesteps. Defaults follow the published baselines for PPO on financial time-series (lr=0.0003, gamma=0.99, batch=64, clip=0.2, timesteps=1M). The validation enforces: learning_rate in (0, 0.1] (the upper bound is inclusive — 0.1 is aggressive but valid; 0.11 is rejected because beyond that PPO/SAC numerically diverges); gamma in (0, 1) exclusive at both ends (γ=1.0 means infinite-horizon undiscounted returns which is mathematically valid in tabular settings but explodes Monte Carlo variance in deep RL — explicitly rejected with the message "exactly 1.0 means no discounting and infinite horizon" so a future contributor reading the error knows why); batch_size positive; clip_range in (0, 1); total_timesteps positive. Algorithm/action-space compatibility is enforced after the per-field checks so a misconfigured PPO+CONTINUOUS or SAC+DISCRETE fails at construction with an actionable message rather than at training time when the framework throws a tensor-shape error. (5) `RewardShapingPolicy` ships the three-component shaping weights — return_weight=1.0, sharpe_weight=0.5, drawdown_weight=2.0 (drawdown weighted 2x to enforce the roadmap-pinned "avoid drawdown" preference). Validation enforces non-negative weights so the reward direction can't accidentally flip — a contributor "fixing" a sign by setting drawdown_weight=-2.0 would inadvertently *reward* drawdowns, the worst possible reward-shaping bug; the validation makes it impossible to ship. Zero weights are explicitly accepted (operator can disable a component for ablation studies). The `shaped_reward(*, raw_return, sharpe, drawdown_pct, policy)` function computes return_weight * raw_return + sharpe_weight * sharpe - drawdown_weight * drawdown_pct; rejects negative drawdown_pct (a "negative drawdown" is meaningless and would invert the penalty direction — pinned both at the policy level and the per-call level). (6) `TrajectoryStep` carries timestep + action_id + raw_return + sharpe + drawdown_pct + shaped_reward; `Episode` carries episode_id + started_at + steps tuple + terminated flag. Operations (`append_step`, `terminate_episode`) return new state — the immutability is pinned for replay-ability across training runs. Step ordering is enforced: `step.timestep` must equal the current `step_count`, so a contributor that accidentally skipped a step (timestep=5 on an episode with 3 steps) fails fast. The Episode properties (step_count, total_reward, total_raw_return, max_drawdown_pct) are computed lazily from the steps tuple — same Episode + same steps → same properties, deterministic. `TrainingResult` is the summary view-model; `aggregate_results(episodes, *, config, policy_id, final_loss, completed_at)` averages reward across episodes. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Two algorithms supported: PPO / SAC.** Closed enum; adding one is a code review change. PPO for stable on-policy training with discrete actions (the Wave 4.B genetic strategy output); SAC for continuous actions + sample efficiency (position-sizing strategies). (2) **Reward shaping has three components with non-negative weights enforced.** Raw return + Sharpe bonus + drawdown penalty. The non-negativity pin guards against the contributor-bug failure mode where a sign flip rewards drawdowns. The default 2x weight on drawdown encodes the roadmap's "avoid drawdown" preference structurally. (3) **Hyperparameter ranges enforced both directions.** Learning rate in (0, 0.1] — the inclusive upper bound is pinned via test (0.1 accepts; 0.11 rejects); gamma in (0, 1) — both endpoints rejected (γ=1 explicit "infinite horizon" rejection message); batch_size positive; clip_range in (0, 1); total_timesteps positive. (4) **Episode tracking is immutable.** Each step appends to a new Trajectory tuple rather than mutating; the original episode unchanged. Step ordering enforced via timestep == step_count check. Termination one-way (`terminate_episode` raises if already terminated; `append_step` raises against terminated). (5) **Render output never includes model weights, optimizer state, raw replay data, or training secrets.** The audit row is summary-only — the dataclasses simply don't carry those fields; structural no-secret pin. The render regression test asserts no `weights` / `optimizer` / `checkpoint` / `api_key` substrings appear in either render_config or render_result output. Halal alignment: RL training produces a policy that's *interpretable through the LLM ensemble* — the roadmap pins "RL provides rigour, LLM provides explainability"; the bot doesn't open a trade based purely on the RL policy's vector output, the LLM-ensemble decision is recorded alongside for the audit trail (Wave 4.J committee voting consumes both). Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async / RL libs at this layer. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 63 tests cover: RLAlgorithm + ActionSpace enum string-value pins; default TrainingConfig hyperparameter sanity (lr=0.0003, gamma=0.99, batch=64, clip=0.2, timesteps=1M); learning_rate validation (zero / negative / above-0.1 rejected; 0.1 inclusive accepted); gamma validation (0.0 / 1.0 both rejected with the explicit "infinite horizon" message); batch_size + clip_range + total_timesteps validation; algorithm/action-space compatibility (PPO+CONTINUOUS rejected; SAC+DISCRETE rejected; SAC+CONTINUOUS accepted); immutable across all dataclasses; default reward shaping weights pinned (1.0 / 0.5 / 2.0 — the 2x drawdown weight is a load-bearing roadmap-derived value); negative weights rejected per-component; zero weight accepted (ablation flow); shaped_reward arithmetic exact (1.0*0.01 + 0.5*1.0 - 2.0*0.05 = 0.41); zero drawdown case; negative-return-with-drawdown produces -0.47 doubly-negative reward; negative drawdown_pct rejected at the function level; custom policy disabling drawdown flows through; TrajectoryStep validation (negative timestep / empty action_id / negative drawdown_pct all rejected; immutable); Episode validation (empty episode_id / naive started_at rejected; immutable); start_episode + append_step + terminate_episode lifecycle; step_count + total_reward + total_raw_return + max_drawdown_pct properties (max_drawdown=0 on empty episode); ordering enforcement (step.timestep != step_count rejects); cannot append to terminated episode; cannot terminate twice; TrainingResult validation; aggregate_results across realistic cohort (100 episodes × 5 steps each, mean_episode_reward = 2.55 exact — 5 × (1.0*0.01 + 0.5*1.0 - 2.0*0) = 5 × 0.51); render_config with algorithm emoji 🎯 PPO / 🌊 SAC + hyperparameters formatted; render_result with policy_id + episode count + mean reward; no-secret regression (no weights / optimizer / checkpoint / api_key substrings); e2e flows (10-step realistic episode lifecycle with terminate; 100-episode training run aggregate; replay consistency — same operations produce equal episodes). The Stable-Baselines3 / Ray RLlib training-loop wrapper consuming this module's TrainingConfig + Episode primitives, the `core/replay.py` snapshot → trajectory adapter, the model-registry integration (Wave 6.A) for storing trained policies, the Wave 4.J live-shadow committee that ensembles the RL policy alongside the LLM ensemble, and the `halal-trader ml train --algorithm ppo` CLI command all deferred to follow-ups — config + tracker verified in isolation first so the training loop sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 1.B–1.E aux — Broker capability registry** — `markets/broker_registry.py` is the pure-Python broker capability matrix that complements the deferred 1.B (IBKR) / 1.C (Tradier) / 1.D (Coinbase) / 1.E (Saxo) broker-SDK adapter waves. Each adapter wave is blocked on its respective SDK integration (`ib_insync`, Tradier REST, Coinbase Advanced Trade SDK, Saxo OpenAPI), but the capability matrix — which broker supports which markets / asset classes / order types / paper-vs-real boundary — is *factual catalogue data* that doesn't need the SDKs to land. Picked a focused registry over per-adapter `BrokerAdapter.capabilities()` methods because (a) operators choosing "which broker should I add next" need a single matrix to compare across all 12 broker entries, not 6 separate accessor methods that each return a different shape — the registry is the operator's at-a-glance "what does the bot already know about?", (b) the cycle's broker-routing layer asks "does this broker support market orders on Saudi equities?" — a closed-set capability matrix answers in O(1) without instantiating broker clients (which require live network connections), (c) the paper-vs-real boundary is the single most safety-critical attribute — routing real money to a paper-only adapter is a silent failure (the paper adapter accepts the order but doesn't actually trade); routing paper trades to a real account is a regulatory issue (paper orders on real money is the exact failure mode the bot's halal-compliance layer is trying to prevent). Pinning paper-vs-real as a registry attribute keeps the executor's gate inspectable and testable in isolation. Five composed surfaces. (1) `Broker` enum with 12 closed-set entries: ALPACA_PAPER / ALPACA_LIVE / BINANCE_TESTNET / BINANCE_LIVE / IBKR_PAPER / IBKR_LIVE / TRADIER_SANDBOX / TRADIER_LIVE / COINBASE_SANDBOX / COINBASE_LIVE / SAXO_SIM / SAXO_LIVE. The paper/live separation is structural — the registry has separate entries for "Alpaca Paper" and "Alpaca Live" rather than a single Alpaca entry with an `is_paper` flag, so the executor's paper-vs-real gate can't accidentally use a live profile when paper was intended. (2) `AssetClass` enum (EQUITY / CRYPTO / OPTION / ETF / FX / COMMODITY) — closed-set so a contributor can't sneak in a free-form "crypto_perp" or "synthetic" asset class without considering the regulatory implications. (3) `OrderType` enum (MARKET / LIMIT / STOP / STOP_LIMIT / TRAILING_STOP / BRACKET / OCO) — the seven roadmap-named order types; adding a new one (e.g. ICEBERG, PEG) is a code review change. (4) `BrokerProfile` frozen dataclass carries broker + display_name + is_paper + asset_classes (frozenset) + order_types (frozenset) + supported_exchanges (frozenset of MIC values from Wave 1.J registry) + rate_limit_per_min. Validation enforces non-empty display_name, non-empty asset_classes / order_types / supported_exchanges (well, the last is allowed empty for crypto-only brokers since crypto doesn't trade on MIC exchanges), positive rate limit, and the load-bearing **"every broker must support MARKET orders"** structural invariant — a broker that can't market-order can't execute the halt's emergency-exit flow (the kill-switch's whole point is "exit positions immediately at market"); banning at construction is the safety guarantee. (5) Module-level `_BROKER_REGISTRY` populated with all 12 profiles. The capability data is pinned per-broker: Alpaca paper/live supports NYSE+NASDAQ, equity+ETF, 6 order types including BRACKET, 200/min rate limit (the Alpaca documented limit). Binance testnet/live supports CRYPTO only, 4 order types including OCO (Binance's documented order type), 1200/min (the Binance per-IP limit). IBKR paper/live supports the full asset set including FX and OPTION, 7 order types (the most complete catalogue), 5 exchanges (NYSE/NASDAQ/LSE/HKSE/TSE), 50/min (IBKR's conservative API limit). Tradier sandbox/live for US equity+ETF+OPTION, 4 order types, 120/min. Coinbase sandbox/live for CRYPTO, 3 order types, 600/min. Saxo sim/live is the international-equities path with 7 international exchanges including TADAWUL + DIFC + KLSE (the OIC-zone exchanges that halal traders need), full asset set, 5 order types, 120/min. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set Broker enum.** Adding a broker is a code review change. The matrix can't drift silently when a contributor adds a free-form "alpaca_v2_paper" string; the structural enforcement matters because the executor's `is_paper` gate is keyed on the enum membership. (2) **MARKET order required for every broker.** The structural pin prevents a contributor from registering a "limit-only" broker that would silently break the kill-switch's emergency-exit. Pinned via the explicit "test_profile_rejects_missing_market_order" — a future PR removing MARKET from a profile fails CI rather than ships and breaks the halt's exit flow. (3) **Paper-vs-real is a per-broker registry entry, not a flag on a shared profile.** The 12 entries are structurally distinct; the partition test asserts paper_brokers() and live_brokers() are disjoint and complete. The executor's `is_paper(broker)` gate is keyed on this; routing real money to a paper-only adapter is impossible because the paper adapter is a different broker entry from the live one. (4) **Capability matrix queries are deterministic.** `brokers_supporting_asset_class(CRYPTO)` returns exactly {Binance testnet/live, Coinbase sandbox/live} in canonical order; the operator's broker-discovery flow returns the same answer across runs. (5) **Render output never includes API keys / tokens / passwords.** The catalogue is pure metadata; the BrokerProfile dataclass simply doesn't carry credentials. The render regression test loops over all 12 brokers asserting no `api_key` / `token` / `secret` / `password` substrings appear in `render_broker` output. `assert_can_execute(*, broker, asset_class, order_type, exchange)` is the executor's pre-submit gate that raises `BrokerCannotExecuteError` (carrying broker + reason) if asset_class / order_type / exchange isn't supported; the exchange check is skipped for non-equity asset classes (crypto and FX don't trade on MIC exchanges, so passing an exchange arg there is a no-op rather than a rejection — pinned via the "binance + crypto + NYSE = passes" test that asserts the exchange arg is ignored for crypto). Halal alignment: the registry gives operators a single matrix to choose brokers compatible with their jurisdiction's halal-friendly venues (Saudi → Saxo for TADAWUL; Pakistan → would need a future PSX-supporting broker via Saxo or an IBKR international account; Malaysian → Saxo for KLSE), and the structural paper-vs-real separation guards against the "I thought I was paper trading but the broker was live" failure mode that would expose halal traders to financial harm with no compensating audit trail. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async / broker SDK. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 49 tests cover: all 12 Broker enum string-value pins; all 6 AssetClass + 7 OrderType pins; BrokerProfile validation (empty display_name / empty asset_classes / empty order_types / missing-MARKET-order / zero rate_limit / negative rate_limit all rejected; immutable); registry coverage (every Broker enum has a profile in canonical order); structural MARKET pin (every profile has MARKET in order_types — pinned via explicit loop); paper-vs-real partition (paper_brokers + live_brokers are disjoint and complete); is_paper across all 6 pairs both directions (Alpaca paper TRUE / live FALSE; Binance testnet TRUE / live FALSE; IBKR paper TRUE; etc); asset class capability pins (Alpaca = equity+ETF only, no CRYPTO; Binance = CRYPTO only; IBKR = full set including FX+OPTION+COMMODITY; Saxo international exchanges including TADAWUL+DIFC); brokers_supporting queries (CRYPTO returns exactly Binance+Coinbase; OPTION returns IBKR/Tradier/Saxo not Alpaca; FX returns only IBKR+Saxo; TADAWUL returns only Saxo; NYSE returns Alpaca+IBKR+Tradier not Binance); order type queries (OCO = Binance+IBKR not Alpaca; BRACKET = Alpaca+IBKR not Binance); assert_can_execute happy path; rejections per facet (asset_class mismatch, order_type mismatch, exchange mismatch — all carry the offending facet in the error message); crypto skips exchange check (Binance + CRYPTO + NYSE = passes because exchange arg is ignored for crypto); optional exchange arg (no exchange arg = passes); error carries broker + reason fields; Saxo + TADAWUL + MARKET succeeds (the Saudi-trader path); render output with paper marker (📝 PAPER / 💰 LIVE); rate limit visible; asset classes + order types listed; no-secret regression across all 12 brokers; e2e flows (US trader broker discovery includes Alpaca; Saudi trader narrows to Saxo for TADAWUL; crypto trader narrows to Binance+Coinbase; paper-safety gate accuracy across all 6 pairs). The Wave 1.B (`brokers/ibkr.py`) / 1.C (`brokers/tradier.py`) / 1.D (`brokers/coinbase.py`) / 1.E (`brokers/saxo.py`) actual SDK adapters consuming this registry as their capabilities source-of-truth, the `BrokerPlugin.capabilities()` protocol method that returns the registry profile rather than re-implementing it per-adapter, the executor's pre-submit gate that calls `assert_can_execute` before every `place_order` (so a misconfigured strategy targeting an unsupported asset class fails fast at the broker boundary rather than at the exchange API), and the `halal-trader brokers list` CLI surface that renders the matrix all deferred to follow-ups — registry verified in isolation first so the SDK adapters see a stable contract to consume.

* **Round-4 Wave 3.I — Cloud deployment manifest validator** — `ops/deployment_manifest.py` is the pure-Python manifest spec + validator that the deferred Dockerfile / docker-compose.yml / Helm chart / Terraform module deployment artifacts consume as their source of truth. The roadmap names four targets (Docker Compose, K8s Helm, Terraform for AWS/GCP, Fly.io) for "one-command deploy" — this module ships the cross-target manifest with regression-pinned validation, so a future PR that lands the actual Dockerfile or Helm chart consumes a stable contract rather than handcrafting deployment artifacts independently. Picked a focused validator over hand-writing four separate deployment artifacts because (a) the four targets share most of their service topology (postgres + bot + dashboard) and only differ in packaging — encoding the topology once means a service rename or port change ripples to all four targets without manual sync, (b) the secret-reference contract is the load-bearing safety attribute — a docker-compose.yml with `DATABASE_URL: postgres://halal:LeakedPassword@host` inline is a leaked-secret class of bug that would compromise every deployment using that template; encoding "secrets must be references, never inline" as a validation rule makes the regression structurally impossible because the dataclass `__post_init__` rejects construction at the input boundary, (c) resource-limit defaults need consistent expression across targets — Terraform takes `cpu_units`, K8s takes `cores`, docker-compose takes a fraction; the manifest holds the canonical value and the per-target serializer translates, so a future "let's bump bot CPU to 2 cores" change is one edit. Six composed surfaces. (1) `DeploymentTarget` enum (DOCKER_COMPOSE / K8S_HELM / TERRAFORM_AWS / TERRAFORM_GCP / FLY_IO) — closed-set so the manifest serializer can't drift; pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. (2) `ServiceKind` enum (POSTGRES / BOT / DASHBOARD / AUX) — three required + one auxiliary for optional add-ons (Grafana, Prometheus, etc.). The required-set is module-level `_REQUIRED_KINDS` frozenset so a contributor can't bypass it via attribute mutation. (3) `EnvVar` is the load-bearing safety primitive with mutual exclusion: either `value` is set (for non-secret config like `LOG_LEVEL=info`) OR `secret_ref` is set (for secrets like `DATABASE_URL` resolved from a vault at deployment time). The validation enforces *4 distinct mutual-exclusion rules*: (a) `is_secret=True` cannot have inline `value` — pinned via the explicit "is_secret with inline value rejected" test using the realistic `postgres://user:pw@host` decoy; (b) `is_secret=True` requires `secret_ref` non-empty — whitespace-only refs rejected; (c) `is_secret=False` cannot have a `secret_ref` — guards against confused dataclass construction where a contributor sets the ref but forgets the flag; (d) `is_secret=False` requires `value` — every env var must have a way to resolve. The four-rule mutual exclusion is what makes the leaked-secret regression structurally impossible. (4) `ResourceLimits` enforces memory in [128MB, 32GB] and CPU in [0.1, 16.0] cores — the lower bounds catch under-provisioning (a 64MB Postgres can't even start); the upper bounds catch typos (32 cores is unlikely to be intentional in a single-tenant deploy). (5) `ServiceSpec` carries name + kind + image + env (frozen tuple) + limits + optional `exposed_port` (None for internal-only services, e.g. an aux Grafana that only the operator's VPN reaches); rejects duplicate env names within a service so a contributor can't accidentally double-define `LOG_LEVEL` in a way that makes the deployment-target serializer pick whichever is alphabetically last. (6) `DeploymentManifest` ties name + version + target + services tuple together; rejects duplicate service names. `validate_manifest(manifest)` is the pre-serialize gate that runs the *full set* of cross-service rules: required kinds present (`missing required service kinds: bot, dashboard` actionable error message); Postgres exposes 5432 or None (the operator-pinned production port; 5433 is the test DB port and a contributor accidentally exposing it would route prod traffic to the test schema); Bot service has `DATABASE_URL` env (the bot can't start without it); **Bot's `DATABASE_URL` must be a secret reference** (this is the load-bearing leaked-secret pin — a contributor that wrote `DATABASE_URL: postgres://halal:secret@localhost/db` inline gets `ManifestViolationError` BEFORE the deployment artifact is written, never reaching the Dockerfile / docker-compose.yml / Helm values.yaml that would ship the credentials); only one BOT service per manifest (multi-bot deployments are a different use case requiring different orchestration). `collect_secret_refs(manifest)` returns deduplicated + sorted secret refs — the deployment-time vault-resolution checklist that operators consult to make sure their Vault / AWS Secrets Manager / GCP Secret Manager has every reference resolvable; same secret_ref appearing in two env vars surfaces once. `total_resource_request(manifest)` returns aggregate (memory_mb, cpu_cores) — operators consult this to size the deployment node pool. `render_service` and `render_manifest` produce ops-display output with target emoji (🐳 docker / ☸️ k8s / 🟧 AWS / 🔷 GCP / 🪂 fly) + service emoji (🗄️ postgres / 🤖 bot / 📊 dashboard / 🧰 aux). The render is structurally no-secret-leak because `EnvVar` rejects inline secrets at construction; secret env vars render as `<secret:${VAULT}/database_url>` placeholder. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set DeploymentTarget enum.** Adding a target is a code review change — the manifest serializer logic for each target is fragile (Terraform's `cpu_units` is 1024-per-core; K8s requests in `m` units; docker-compose CPU is a fraction) so adding a target without adding the matching serializer would silently produce broken artifacts. (2) **Required services for the bot to run.** Postgres + bot + dashboard are the minimum; an AUX-only manifest (e.g. just Grafana + Prometheus) is rejected because it can't run the bot at all. (3) **Secrets are references, never inline — pinned 4 ways.** The mutual-exclusion rules in EnvVar guarantee the structural pin; the `ManifestViolationError` raised by `validate_manifest` for a non-secret `DATABASE_URL` provides the second-tier guard if a contributor tried to set `is_secret=False` with the database URL as `value`. The "load-bearing leaked-secret regression" test (`test_e2e_inline_secret_caught_early`) uses an explicit `LeakedPassword123` decoy and asserts it never reaches the Dockerfile. (4) **Resource limits enforced both directions.** Memory [128MB, 32GB] inclusive at lower bound (boundary tested 128 passes, 64 fails); CPU [0.1, 16.0] inclusive (boundary tested both ends). (5) **Render output never includes inline secret values.** The placeholder `<secret:ref>` pattern is what every render-serializer pipeline must use; the regression test asserts no inline password substring like `LeakedPassword` ever appears in render output. Mirrors no-secret patterns of Wave 3.B vault + 3.G admin console + every other secret-aware module. Halal alignment: the secret-reference pin is doubly important for the bot because broker API keys + LLM API keys + Stripe webhook secrets all flow through the deployment manifest; a leaked broker API key in a docker-compose.yml committed to a public repo is the worst-case scenario this layer guards against. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum`); no DB / network / async / cloud SDK. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 56 tests cover: 5 DeploymentTarget + 4 ServiceKind enum string-value pins; EnvVar inline + secret happy paths; **4-way mutual exclusion pinned individually** (inline-with-secret + value-and-secret_ref combo rejected; secret-without-ref rejected; secret-with-whitespace-ref rejected; non-secret-with-ref rejected; non-secret-without-value rejected); EnvVar immutable; ResourceLimits boundary pins both directions (128MB inclusive, 64MB rejected; 32_768 inclusive, 64_000 rejected; 0.1 CPU inclusive, 0.05 rejected; 16.0 inclusive, 32.0 rejected); ResourceLimits immutable; ServiceSpec validation (empty name / image / port-out-of-range / duplicate env names rejected; None port accepted for internal-only); ServiceSpec immutable; DeploymentManifest validation (empty name / version / services rejected; duplicate service names rejected); DeploymentManifest immutable; validate_manifest happy path; **rejects missing each of postgres/bot/dashboard individually** (the test mutates the service tuple to drop one kind at a time, asserting `ManifestViolationError` carries the missing kind in the reason); postgres-on-port-5433 rejected with the explicit "must be 5432 or None" message — guards against the canonical-vs-test port confusion; postgres internal-only (no exposed_port) accepted; bot without DATABASE_URL rejected; **bot with inline DATABASE_URL rejected (load-bearing leaked-secret regression test)**; multiple bots rejected; AUX-only manifest rejected as missing required kinds; ManifestViolationError carries manifest_name + reason fields; collect_secret_refs basic + deduplication + sorted-order pin + empty-when-no-secrets; total_resource_request math (3584MB total / 2.5 CPU total for the canonical 3-service manifest); render service includes name + kind emoji 🗄️/🤖/📊; internal-only marker; secret env renders as `<secret:ref>` placeholder; render manifest includes target emoji + total resources; no inline-password leak in render; e2e flows (full deployment validates + secret-refs collected + total resources computed; target swap from docker_compose to k8s_helm preserves validation since services are target-agnostic; **inline DATABASE_URL with "LeakedPassword123" decoy caught by validation BEFORE reaching any Dockerfile** — the load-bearing regression that proves the structural pin holds end-to-end). The actual `infra/Dockerfile`, `infra/docker-compose.yml`, `infra/helm/halal-trader/` Helm chart, `infra/terraform/aws/` and `infra/terraform/gcp/` Terraform modules, the `fly.toml` for Fly.io, and the four serializers (`render_docker_compose(manifest)`, `render_helm_values(manifest)`, etc.) that consume this module's `DeploymentManifest` and emit the per-target deployment artifact, plus the `halal-trader deploy --target docker_compose` CLI command all deferred to follow-ups — manifest spec + validator verified in isolation first so the per-target serializers see a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 3.J — Mobile push notification policy + delivery state engine** — `web/mobile_push.py` is the pure-Python policy + delivery-state engine that the deferred RN/Flutter mobile app + APNs/FCM SDK integration consumes. The roadmap pins three notification types ("trade fills + risk halts + daily summary") with very different urgency profiles; this module ships the priority ladder + quiet-hour + rate-limit gates so the dispatcher can't accidentally send a daily summary at 3am or flood the operator's phone with 100 trade-fill notifications in a noisy strategy run. Picked a focused policy + state engine over wiring directly into APNs/FCM because (a) the three notification kinds have very different urgency profiles — risk_halt is critical and bypasses quiet hours (the operator's phone MUST buzz at 3am if the bot trips a 10% drawdown), daily_summary respects quiet hours absolutely (a 3am summary is a usability failure that conditions the operator to mute the bot's notifications altogether); encoding the priority + quiet-hour rules once means the dispatcher can't accidentally invert them, (b) device registration has a platform-specific token format (APNs is hex; FCM is an opaque string) — the dataclass enforces APNs hex at construction so a misconfigured iOS token fails fast at the registration boundary rather than mid-dispatch, (c) delivery state tracked deterministically gives operators an audit trail for "why didn't my phone buzz at 14:22?" without correlating across APNs + FCM provider logs, (d) per-user rate limiting prevents accidental DoS from a noisy strategy — "100 trade-fill notifications in 60 seconds" floods the phone and is a usability disaster. Eight composed surfaces. (1) `NotificationKind` enum (TRADE_FILL / RISK_HALT / DAILY_SUMMARY) with pinned string values. (2) `Priority` enum (LOW / NORMAL / CRITICAL); module-level `_KIND_PRIORITY` dict pins the kind→priority mapping (RISK_HALT=CRITICAL; TRADE_FILL=NORMAL; DAILY_SUMMARY=LOW) so a contributor can't accidentally swap the priority of risk_halt and daily_summary. (3) `Platform` enum (IOS / ANDROID). (4) `DeliveryStatus` (PENDING / SENT / DELIVERED / FAILED) with module-level `_DELIVERY_ORDER` tuple for the three success-path states + FAILED terminal. (5) `NotificationPolicy` ships defaults 22:00-07:00 quiet hours wraparound + 30 non-critical/hour rate limit; rejects equal start/end (the "no quiet hours" approximation should be 23:59 ± 1min rather than collapse the window). (6) `DeviceRegistration` carries user_id + device_id + platform + device_token + tz_offset + registered_at + revoked flag; validates non-empty IDs + token + tz-aware registered_at + tz_offset in [-720, 840] minutes (Pacific to Pacific extreme range) + the iOS-token-must-be-hex shape pin (APNs requires hex; a contributor that passed an FCM token to an iOS device fails fast). (7) `NotificationRequest` carries notification_id + user_id + kind + title + body + requested_at; enforces non-empty fields + tz-aware requested_at + APNs title-100-char + body-1000-char limits (matching the platform's hard cap so the SDK never gets an oversized payload). (8) `evaluate_gate(request, *, registration, recent_send_count, policy)` is the load-bearing decision function returning `GateDecision` with one of four `GateOutcome` values: `SEND` (clear to dispatch), `HOLD_QUIET_HOURS` (user is in quiet hours, non-critical kind), `HOLD_RATE_LIMIT` (user has hit 30+ recent sends, non-critical kind), `HOLD_NO_DEVICE` (no active mobile device registered or revoked). The decision converts request.requested_at to user-local time using registration.tz_offset_minutes via `now.astimezone(timezone(timedelta(minutes=offset)))` so a NY operator at 14:00 UTC sees 09:00 NY (out of quiet hours, sends) vs 04:00 UTC sees 23:00 NY (in quiet hours, holds) — the per-user tz conversion is what makes the gate work for users across timezones rather than a single-tz hardcode. The state machine: `start_delivery` creates PENDING; `mark_sent` (PENDING → SENT after APNs/FCM accepts the dispatch); `mark_delivered` (SENT → DELIVERED after the platform confirms delivery); `mark_failed` (any pre-FAILED → FAILED with required failure_reason). Forward-only ordering enforced via `_check_forward` so PENDING → DELIVERED skip raises `DeliveryOrderError`; FAILED is terminal so re-failing raises. `count_recent_sends(records, *, user_notification_ids, now, window=1h)` is the rate-limit input: counts SENT + DELIVERED records (PENDING and FAILED are excluded — a failed delivery shouldn't penalize the user toward rate limit because the user never actually got it; the regression test pins this directly). The rate-limit window is rolling 60 minutes (60min ago boundary inclusive — pinned via test). **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Three notification kinds with priority ladder; CRITICAL bypasses ALL gates.** RISK_HALT at 3am during quiet hours sends; RISK_HALT with 1000 recent sends still sends. The pin is structurally important because the kill-switch's notification path can't be silenced — if the bot has tripped a halt, the operator must hear about it regardless of quiet hours or accumulated noise. The priority mapping is module-level so a contributor's "let me lower risk_halt priority" PR has to update the dict and the matching test. (2) **Quiet hours boundaries: start inclusive, end exclusive.** 22:00 user-local is in quiet hours (HOLD); 07:00 user-local is out of quiet hours (SEND). Pinned both directions because asymmetric boundaries are a common bug — a contributor that shifted to "start exclusive, end inclusive" would invert quiet hours by 2 minutes (sending at 22:00, holding at 07:00). The wraparound logic handles 22:00-07:00 spanning midnight via "current >= start OR current < end" rather than a same-day window. (3) **Rate limit at 30 non-critical sends/hour rolling window.** Boundary pinned: 29 recent sends → SEND; 30 recent sends → HOLD; CRITICAL bypasses regardless. The "60min ago boundary inclusive" pin in `count_recent_sends` (`>= cutoff` not `> cutoff`) keeps the count honest at the rolling-window edge. (4) **Delivery state machine: PENDING → SENT → DELIVERED → FAILED, forward only.** Cannot skip PENDING → DELIVERED (the dispatch confirmation MUST come from the platform's confirmation step, not be assumed); FAILED can come from any pre-FAILED state but is terminal so re-failing raises; FAILED requires non-empty failure_reason so the audit row carries a debuggable cause. (5) **Render output never includes device tokens / APNs keys / FCM keys.** The dataclasses don't leak the tokens in render (the regression test asserts `device_token` / `fcm` / `apns` / `key` substrings never appear in the rendered output); critical for compliance because device tokens routed to a wrong destination or logged to a non-secure log file constitute a privacy breach. Halal alignment: mobile push notifications keep the operator in the loop on bot decisions in real time — the `RISK_HALT` priority guarantees the operator hears about a halal-screen breach immediately, the per-user timezone conversion means a Saudi operator at 23:00 Riyadh time gets the right quiet-hours behavior (rather than the bot's host-local 23:00). The 30/hour rate limit is operator-protective: a noisy strategy that emits 200 trade fills wouldn't drown the halal-compliance halt notification in noise. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async / APNs/FCM SDK. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 71 tests cover: all 5 enum string-value pins; priority ladder pinned per-kind; NotificationPolicy validation including the quiet-start-equals-end rejection; DeviceRegistration validation including iOS token must be hex (with realistic non-hex `not_hex_!!@@` + valid `abc123DEADBEEF` examples); NotificationRequest validation including APNs title 101-char + body 1001-char rejections; evaluate_gate across all four GateOutcome paths (no device, revoked device, business hours sends, quiet hours holds non-critical, CRITICAL bypasses quiet hours, CRITICAL bypasses rate limit even with 1000 recent sends, 30-recent-sends rate-limits, 29 sends just-below-limit sends, per-user-tz conversion for NY operator across UTC times); quiet hours wraparound boundaries (22:00 inclusive, 07:00 exclusive, 06:00 quiet); GateDecision carries actionable message; delivery state machine forward only (PENDING → SENT → DELIVERED happy path; cannot skip PENDING → DELIVERED; mark_failed from PENDING + from SENT both work; already-failed re-fail rejected; mark_failed requires non-empty reason; DeliveryRecord validates FAILED-without-reason and non-FAILED-with-ghost-reason both rejected; immutable; immutability of state operations); count_recent_sends pins (basic 5-of-5 in last hour; 60min boundary inclusive; old records excluded; PENDING and FAILED excluded — only SENT + DELIVERED count; filter by user_notification_ids; naive now rejected); render kind emoji 💸/🚨/📊 + priority emoji 🔴/🟡/🔵 + status emoji ⏳/📤/✅/❌; no-secret regression; e2e flows (RISK_HALT at 3am operator-local delivers all the way through DELIVERED state; DAILY_SUMMARY at 3am held by quiet hours; noisy strategy at 30 sends rate-limits trade_fill but RISK_HALT still sends; replay consistency). The actual `web/api/mobile.py` FastAPI route series (POST `/api/mobile/devices` for registration, GET `/api/mobile/summary` for the daily-summary contract the roadmap names, the WebSocket `/ws/notifications` for real-time pushes), the APNs SDK wrapper (`apns2` Python lib) + FCM wrapper, the per-user `recent_send_count` tracker (Redis or Postgres-backed), the React Native / Flutter app implementations, and the dashboard "notification preferences" UI all deferred to follow-ups — policy + state engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 5.E — Voice command intent classifier** — `web/voice_intent.py` is the pure-Python intent classifier that consumes Whisper-transcribed text and maps it to a closed set of voice intents. The roadmap's voice surface is "operator says 'stop the crypto bot' / 'what's my drawdown today' / 'halt and close all positions' — local Whisper + gpt-oss handles it"; this module ships the deterministic grammar that the speech-to-text adapter outputs into. The Whisper STT integration + gpt-oss disambiguation are operator-side library work (deferred until Whisper.cpp + gpt-oss SDK adapters land). Picked a focused intent classifier over a "send the audio to an LLM and parse JSON" approach because (a) voice commands during incident response need to be deterministic and fast — a 200ms intent classification beats a 5s LLM round-trip when the operator is yelling "halt the bot" because something is wrong; the deterministic grammar guarantees the same input always produces the same intent, where an LLM would drift across versions, (b) the destructive-action confirmation gate is a regression-pinned safety contract — accidentally firing HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL because the operator said "halt? and close all" in a question is the worst-case failure mode this layer is preventing; (c) operator confidence in the voice surface depends on consistent recognition across phrasings ("stop the crypto bot" vs "stop crypto bot" vs "kill the crypto bot") — closed-set synonym matching gives the right answer every time. Six composed surfaces. (1) `VoiceIntent` enum (HALT / RESUME / STATUS / DRAWDOWN_QUERY / HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL / UNKNOWN) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability — adding an intent is a code review change; the grammar can't drift via a contributor adding "free-form" string handlers. (2) `_DESTRUCTIVE_INTENTS` frozenset names the two destructive intents (HALT and HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL); RESUME / STATUS / DRAWDOWN_QUERY are explicitly non-destructive (RESUME is recovery, not destructive — the operator's intent is to *re-enable* trading after a halt, which doesn't need confirmation; the regression test pins this). (3) Module-level `_INTENT_PATTERNS` is the priority-ordered grammar — a tuple of (intent, alternatives) pairs where alternatives are frozensets of required tokens. The order is the load-bearing pin: HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL is checked BEFORE HALT so that "halt and close all positions" classifies as the more destructive intent, not the simpler HALT. The synonym sets are token-set matches (using `frozenset.issubset(tokens)`) so "stop the bot", "stop bot", and "the bot, stop!" all match because the required tokens {"stop", "bot"} appear regardless of word order or filler words. (4) `_normalize(text)` lowercases + strips punctuation + tokenizes. Punctuation-strip means "halt!" and "halt." both match HALT; the regex `[^\w\s]` is broad enough to catch question marks too — but the question-mark semantic ("are you sure you want to halt?") is handled at the confirmation-gate layer rather than at the grammar, since destructive intents always require an explicit "yes confirm" follow-up regardless of question-mark presence. (5) `classify_intent(text)` is the entry point: returns UNKNOWN for empty/whitespace input (rather than guessing), iterates patterns in declared order, returns the first matching intent. The "halt" alone returning UNKNOWN pin is important — "halt" without "bot" or "trading" target is a fragment that could come from a partial Whisper transcription; classifying it as HALT would let a misheard word trigger the destructive flow. (6) `IntentRecognition` carries recognition_id + intent + raw_text + recognized_at + expires_at + optional confirmed_at. `recognize(*, recognition_id, raw_text, now, confirmation_window)` builds a recognition with default 10-second confirmation window. `confirm_recognition(recognition, *, now)` enforces: intent must be destructive (raises NotDestructiveError if RESUME / STATUS / DRAWDOWN_QUERY); not already confirmed (raises ValueError); within window (raises ConfirmationExpiredError if past expires_at). The boundary at exactly expires_at is *inclusive* — confirming at `now == expires_at` succeeds; only `now > expires_at` raises. `is_executable(recognition, *, now)` is the dispatcher's gate: UNKNOWN never executable; non-destructive immediately executable; destructive requires confirmed_at AND now <= expires_at (so even a confirmed destructive intent past the window doesn't execute — the operator confirmed but then waited too long, which is treated the same as not confirming). **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set VoiceIntent enum.** Adding an intent is a code review change. The closed grammar means a future "let me add ROLLBACK as a voice command" PR has to update the enum + pattern dict + destructive-set + tests in one place. (2) **HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL takes priority over HALT.** The patterns list is ordered; HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL is checked first. The pin matters because "halt and close all positions" must classify as the more-destructive intent — classifying it as HALT would let the operator's intent to *also liquidate* be silently dropped, leading to "I told the bot to halt and close, but it only halted" complaints. The regression test asserts both `result is HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL` AND `result is not HALT`. (3) **Destructive intents require confirmation within 10 seconds.** The 10s default window is operator-tunable via the `confirmation_window` arg. The boundary at `expires_at` is inclusive (last-millisecond confirmation succeeds); past `expires_at` raises ConfirmationExpiredError. The confirmation flow guards against misheard "stop everything" leading to instant liquidation — the operator must explicitly say "yes confirm" or click a UI button within 10s. (4) **UNKNOWN is a real outcome, not a fallback.** Empty/whitespace text returns UNKNOWN; random text returns UNKNOWN; "halt" without a target returns UNKNOWN. The operator UI treats UNKNOWN as "I didn't catch that, try again" rather than guessing, which prevents the worst voice-UX failure ("I said 'halt' once and it triggered different actions on different runs"). (5) **Render output never includes audio file paths / device IDs / Whisper model paths.** The IntentRecognition dataclass simply doesn't carry those fields; the render regression test asserts `.wav` / `.mp3` / `device_id` / `audio_path` substrings never appear. The structural no-secret pin matters because the rendered recognition rows go into the operator audit log; a voice command tied to an audio file path would leak the operator's microphone / device topology. Halal alignment: the confirmation gate for HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL is what prevents a Whisper transcription error from accidentally liquidating a halal trader's positions — a Saudi operator yelling "halal!" (in case of a halal-doubt) and Whisper mishearing as "halt" + auto-trigger would be a worst-case scenario; the confirmation gate makes it impossible. The intent for "what's my drawdown today" returns DRAWDOWN_QUERY which is a read-only inspection — the bot can answer the operator's question without any trading action. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `re` + `datetime`); no Whisper / gpt-oss / audio libs. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 73 tests cover: VoiceIntent enum string-value pins; classify HALT across 6 phrasings (halt the bot / stop the bot / kill the bot / pause the bot / halt trading / stop trading now — both bot and trading targets pinned); halt with punctuation matches (`halt the bot!` / `Stop the bot.`); classify HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL across 4 phrasings (halt + close + all; stop + close + all; emergency exit; liquidate everything); **HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL takes priority over HALT pin** (the load-bearing test asserting both directions: `is HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL` AND `is not HALT`); classify RESUME across 5 synonyms; classify STATUS across 4 phrasings; classify DRAWDOWN_QUERY across 5 phrasings; classify UNKNOWN for empty / whitespace / random text / partial-fragment "halt" alone (the load-bearing pin against accidental triggering); case-insensitive matching pinned both directions (HALT THE BOT and lowercase); is_destructive accuracy across all 6 intents (HALT + HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL True; RESUME / STATUS / DRAWDOWN_QUERY / UNKNOWN False — the RESUME-not-destructive pin is important because recovery actions shouldn't need confirmation); IntentRecognition validation (empty recognition_id / raw_text rejected; naive recognized_at / expires_at rejected; expires-before-recognized rejected; immutable); recognize default 10s window + custom 30s window; recognize empty / naive-now / zero-window rejections; confirm_recognition within window flow + custom-window flow + **boundary inclusive at expires_at pin** + **past-window raises ConfirmationExpiredError carrying recognition_id pin** + **non-destructive raises NotDestructiveError carrying intent pin** + already-confirmed rejected + naive-now rejected; is_executable across UNKNOWN false / non-destructive true / destructive-unconfirmed false / destructive-confirmed-within-window true / destructive-confirmed-past-window false; render output with intent emoji 🛑/▶️/📊/📉/🚨/❓ per intent; DESTRUCTIVE marker for unconfirmed; confirmed marker after; non-destructive intents don't show DESTRUCTIVE marker; no-secret regression (.wav / .mp3 / device_id / audio_path absent); e2e flows (status query runs immediately without confirmation; HALT requires confirmation then executes after 3s; emergency exit classified as HALT_AND_CLOSE_ALL with confirmation required; misheard "what time is it" returns UNKNOWN with no action; replay consistency — same operations produce equal recognitions). The Whisper STT adapter (operator-side `whisper.cpp` Python bindings or the OpenAI `whisper` package), the FastAPI `/api/voice/recognize` POST endpoint that consumes audio + returns `IntentRecognition`, the `/api/voice/confirm/{recognition_id}` POST endpoint that calls `confirm_recognition`, the dashboard UI's voice-button interaction, the `gpt-oss` disambiguation step that handles ambiguous transcripts (a deferred follow-up that can resolve "stop the bot" vs "stop everything" intent collisions), and the `--voice` CLI flag that enables/disables the voice surface (default off per the roadmap "operator-only feature, off by default") all deferred to follow-ups — intent classifier verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 10.C — Community moderation policy + escalation engine** — `web/moderation.py` is the pure-Python content classifier + review state engine the deferred Discord / Slack bot integrations consume to triage messages before a human moderator sees them. The roadmap calls for "active community space for halal traders... moderated by the core team" — this module ships the deterministic classifier + state machine that turns raw chat messages into actionable moderation decisions, regression-pinned so the bot integration sees a stable contract and operators have an inspectable audit trail. Picked a focused classifier + state engine over plugging directly into Discord auto-mod / Slack DLP because (a) "financial advice" detection is the load-bearing safety attribute for this specific community — the bot is paper-trading software, not investment advice; a member casually saying "you should buy AAPL" creates regulatory risk for the project unless flagged + replaced with a disclaimer, and Discord/Slack's built-in moderation has no concept of financial-advice-as-a-content-class; (b) PII detection (member accidentally pastes their broker API key thinking it's a public string) needs to run client-side before the message reaches the channel — Discord's auto-mod can be bypassed by a moderator's "approve" while ours short-circuits at the API boundary; (c) the moderation state machine gives moderators an audit trail for "why did this message get removed?" without correlating across Discord audit logs + Slack admin panels, important for the legal / compliance review when a member contests a removal. Six composed surfaces. (1) `ContentClassification` enum (CLEAN / SPAM / HARASSMENT / FINANCIAL_ADVICE / PII_LEAK) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability — adding a class is a code review change; the moderator dashboard groupings can't drift. (2) `ReviewStatus` state machine (PENDING / AUTO_APPROVED / FLAGGED / ESCALATED / REMOVED) — PENDING is the initial state before auto_decide; AUTO_APPROVED is the clean-message terminal; FLAGGED is visible-but-tagged (financial advice); ESCALATED is hidden-pending-human-review (harassment); REMOVED is hidden-and-deleted terminal (PII / spam / human-decided removal). (3) `ModerationPolicy` ships defaults: 3-message/60s spam threshold + `detect_pii=True`. The spam threshold is operator-tunable (constructor rejects below 2 since "1+ identical = spam" is too aggressive); `detect_pii` can be disabled for already-clean cohorts (e.g. a private channel that's allow-listed). (4) Module-level `_PII_PATTERNS` list tuples of (regex, label) for the five patterns: email, SSN, IP, phone, **40+-char alphanumeric "API key shape"** — the broker API key + LLM API key + Stripe webhook secret all match this pattern, so a member pasting any of them hits PII_LEAK. (5) `_FINANCIAL_ADVICE_PHRASES` ships 12 phrasings ("you should buy", "guaranteed profit", "risk free", "definitely buy", "i recommend buying", etc.) covering the most common patterns of crossing the regulatory line from "discussion of strategies" to "investment advice". `_HARASSMENT_PATTERNS` lists 6 personal-attack phrases conservatively (focused on "you are an idiot" / "kill yourself" rather than profanity, since profanity is community-context-sensitive and Discord's built-in word filter handles it well). (6) `classify(text, *, recent_identical_count, policy)` is the entry-point classifier with **strict priority order: PII_LEAK > HARASSMENT > FINANCIAL_ADVICE > SPAM > CLEAN**. PII is the load-bearing short-circuit — once detected, no further classification needed (the leak is the maximally destructive outcome regardless of other content); the priority pin is regression-tested with the explicit "you are an idiot, my email is trader@example.com" cohort that classifies as PII_LEAK rather than HARASSMENT. The `recent_identical_count` arg is the dispatcher's input for spam detection — the caller (the Discord/Slack bot) builds the count of identical recent messages from the same user. The state machine: `initial_review(*, message_id, classification, now)` builds PENDING; `auto_decide(review, *, now)` routes by classification — CLEAN → AUTO_APPROVED; PII_LEAK → REMOVED with `moderator="auto"` (the load-bearing safety pin); HARASSMENT → ESCALATED with `moderator="auto"`; FINANCIAL_ADVICE → FLAGGED (no moderator since it's transparent); SPAM → REMOVED with `moderator="auto"`. `moderator_remove(review, *, moderator, now)` and `moderator_approve(review, *, moderator, now)` are the human-review escape valves; both accept FLAGGED or ESCALATED only (rejecting PENDING — moderators wait for auto_decide to run first); both require non-empty moderator name. `is_visible_to_channel(review)` returns True for AUTO_APPROVED + FLAGGED only — PENDING is hidden until auto_decide; ESCALATED + REMOVED are hidden. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set ContentClassification enum.** Adding a class is a code review change. The moderator dashboard groupings (count by class, severity histograms) can't drift if a contributor sneaks in a free-form "spam_v2" string. (2) **PII detection blocks the message immediately, no human review.** PII_LEAK → REMOVED via auto_decide with `moderator="auto"`; the channel never sees the leak; pinned via the explicit "API key paste" e2e test using a 58-char "BinanceA" + "Bc"*30 decoy. The auto-block matters because moderators don't always read every message in real time — a leak that sits in the channel for an hour while a moderator wakes up is already exposed to every member viewing scrollback. (3) **Financial advice classification flags but doesn't auto-remove.** FINANCIAL_ADVICE → FLAGGED (visible) rather than REMOVED. Transparent moderation builds trust: members see their message stayed up but tagged, and the bot's reply-with-disclaimer (deferred follow-up) educates the community without playing whack-a-mole on individual posts. (4) **Spam threshold is inclusive at 3.** 2 recent identical messages → CLEAN; 3 → SPAM. Boundary pinned both directions. The financial-advice-priority-over-spam pin matters too: a spammed financial-advice message stays classified as advice (the more important moderator concern) rather than auto-removed as spam, so the moderator sees the regulatory risk pattern. (5) **Render output never includes raw message text.** The ClassificationResult carries `flagged_phrases` (e.g. `("email", "ssn")` labels for PII_LEAK or `("you should buy",)` for FINANCIAL_ADVICE) but the render functions never receive the original message text. This is the structural no-secret pin: a moderator reviewing the audit log of a PII_LEAK doesn't need to see the actual leaked email/SSN to know what happened — they see "PII pattern type: email" which is enough context to decide action. The render-no-leak test asserts no `@` substring (no email-shaped data) and no `123-45` substring (no SSN-shaped data) appear in render output even though the test's input message contains both. Halal alignment: the financial-advice classifier protects the project from regulatory risk that would harm halal traders the most — if the community gets shut down by a regulator for facilitating unlicensed investment advice, the halal traders lose their main discussion forum. The PII detector protects members from accidentally leaking broker API keys that would cost them real money (the 40+-char alphanumeric pattern matches Binance / Alpaca / Coinbase API key shapes). The harassment escalation guards the welcoming environment that's essential for users new to halal trading who may have basic questions; a hostile community that escalates harassment to human review keeps the door open for newcomers. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `re` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no Discord SDK / Slack SDK / DLP service. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 69 tests cover: ContentClassification + ReviewStatus enum string-value pins; ModerationPolicy validation including spam_threshold-below-2 + zero-spam_window rejection + immutable; ClassificationResult validation (severity_score [0,1] range pinned both directions; immutable); classify CLEAN for empty + normal strategy discussion + RSI Sharpe quotes; classify PII for each of 5 patterns (email / SSN / IP / phone / API-key with realistic 58-char "BinanceA"+"Bc"*25 decoy); **PII priority over harassment** ("you are an idiot, my email is trader@example.com" → PII_LEAK pin); **PII priority over financial advice** ("you should buy AAPL — DM me at me@example.com" → PII_LEAK); detect_pii=False allows fallthrough; classify HARASSMENT across 3 phrasings + case-insensitive; harassment-priority-over-financial-advice; classify FINANCIAL_ADVICE across 6 phrasings (you should buy/sell, guaranteed, risk free, definitely, i recommend); spam threshold inclusive at 3 boundary both directions; **financial-advice-priority-over-spam pin** (spammed advice stays classified as advice); custom strict 2-threshold; MessageReview validation including the escalated-requires-moderator + removed-requires-moderator pins (auto-approved doesn't require moderator); immutable; initial_review starts PENDING; auto_decide for each of 5 classifications (CLEAN→AUTO_APPROVED; **PII_LEAK→REMOVED+auto-moderator load-bearing pin**; HARASSMENT→ESCALATED+auto; FINANCIAL_ADVICE→FLAGGED+no-moderator transparent-moderation pin; SPAM→REMOVED+auto); already-decided rejected; naive-now rejected; moderator_remove from FLAGGED and ESCALATED + rejects PENDING + requires non-empty moderator name; moderator_approve as false-positive escape valve from FLAGGED and ESCALATED + rejects PENDING; is_visible_to_channel pinned per status (AUTO_APPROVED visible; FLAGGED visible — the transparent-moderation pin; PENDING hidden; ESCALATED hidden; REMOVED hidden); render classification emoji 🔓/⚠️/💼/📧/✅; render shows flagged_phrases as labels not raw content; render no-secret regression (no `@` from masked email; no `123-45` from masked SSN); render review with status emoji + classification emoji + auto/moderator name; e2e flows (API-key paste blocked immediately and channel never sees the leak; financial-advice stays visible with FLAGGED; human moderator reviews flagged then removes; replay consistency). The Discord bot integration (`discord.py` adapter consuming `classify` per message + dispatching `auto_decide` decisions back to Discord's API), the Slack equivalent (`slack_bolt` adapter), the FastAPI `/api/community/moderate` endpoint that the bots POST messages to + receive ClassificationResult JSON back, the moderator dashboard tile (rendering the audit log of recent reviews with the no-secret-leak rendering), the bot's "reply with disclaimer" automation for FINANCIAL_ADVICE classifications (that surfaces "the bot is paper-trading software, not investment advice; consult a registered advisor"), and the per-user reputation tracking (repeat-offenders escalate sooner) all deferred to follow-ups — classifier + state engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 10.D — Quarterly newsletter digest builder** — `web/newsletter.py` is the pure-Python digest builder + opt-in subscriber state machine that the deferred mailing-list send service (Mailgun/Postmark/SES) consumes. The roadmap pins four content kinds ("what worked, what didn't, regulatory changes, scholar updates") for the quarterly newsletter; this module ships the deterministic schema + validation + render so the operator can iterate quarters without re-deriving the format and a contributor can't accidentally paste raw user data into the digest. Picked a focused builder over hand-writing each newsletter because (a) the four section kinds are stable across quarters and structuring them as a closed enum means a future "let's add a community-spotlight section" PR has to update the schema + tests rather than just paste markdown into a draft, (b) the no-individual-trader-names contract is the load-bearing privacy attribute — the newsletter aggregates platform data but must never name an individual user (anonymous handles only, mirroring Wave 10.A gallery + 10.B dataset anonymisation); the validation runs at digest-build time so a contributor that pasted "alice.smith@halal-trader.dev" or "@alice_trader" into a section body gets caught at CI rather than after the email is sent to 1000 subscribers, (c) the opt-in subscriber list management is a discrete state machine (SUBSCRIBED → UNSUBSCRIBED one-way) that needs deterministic auditing for legal compliance — GDPR / CCPA right-to-be-forgotten requires the unsubscribe timestamp be permanently recorded so a regulator asking "when did this user unsubscribe?" can be answered from the audit row. Six composed surfaces. (1) `SectionKind` enum (TOP_PERFORMERS / REGULATORY / SCHOLAR_UPDATES / WHAT_DIDNT_WORK) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. The four kinds map directly to the roadmap's named content domains; adding a fifth (e.g. "community spotlight") would be a code review change requiring schema + emoji + canonical-order updates. (2) `SubscriptionStatus` enum (SUBSCRIBED / UNSUBSCRIBED). (3) Module-level `_PII_PATTERNS` (5 regexes mirroring Wave 10.B + 10.C: email / SSN / IP / phone / 40+-char alphanumeric API-key-shape) + `_HANDLE_PATTERN` (regex matching `(?:^|\s)@\w+` for Twitter / Discord handle preceded by whitespace or string-start, so "user@example.com" doesn't accidentally match the handle pattern — the handle pattern is targeting standalone `@username` not embedded `@` in emails which is already caught by the email pattern). The shared denylist across waves means a contributor that knows the Wave 10.B / 10.C contract automatically understands the 10.D contract — one mental model across all the platform's content surfaces. (4) `Section` carries section_id + kind + title + body. Validation enforces non-empty fields + 120-char title cap (matches typical email-header conventions) + 4000-char body cap (enough for a substantial paragraph but bounded so a malformed section can't blow up the email). `validate_section(section)` runs both PII denylist and handle denylist on title AND body; raises `DigestViolationError` carrying section_id + reason. (5) `Digest` ties digest_id + quarter_label ("2026-Q1") + published_at + sections tuple. Rejects duplicate section IDs + naive published_at + empty sections. `validate_digest(digest)` runs `validate_section` on every section — the load-bearing pre-send check; a digest that fails validation raises before any rendering can happen, so a contributor's "let me just look at the rendered output" can't accidentally bypass the gate. (6) `Subscription` carries subscription_id + subscriber_anonymous_handle + status + subscribed_at + optional unsubscribed_at. The dataclass deliberately doesn't carry the actual email address — that's operator-side state held by the mailing-list service, so render output is structurally email-leak-free. Validation enforces: UNSUBSCRIBED status requires unsubscribed_at; SUBSCRIBED must not have unsubscribed_at; unsubscribed_at >= subscribed_at. `subscribe(*, subscription_id, handle, now)` creates SUBSCRIBED; `unsubscribe(subscription, *, now)` returns a new UNSUBSCRIBED record with the timestamp recorded; double-unsubscribe raises `AlreadyUnsubscribedError`. `active_subscribers(subscriptions)` filters to SUBSCRIBED only — the send-list. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set SectionKind enum.** Adding a kind is a code review change. The canonical ordering in render (TOP → REG → SCH → NOPE) means a future contributor adding a new kind has to decide where it slots in the rendered digest. (2) **No PII in section bodies — pre-send pin.** The 5-pattern denylist runs at validate_digest time; the e2e regression test uses an explicit "alice.smith@halal-trader.dev" decoy and asserts validate_digest raises BEFORE any rendering happens. The pin matters because the worst-case failure mode is "we sent the digest to 1000 subscribers and now there's a leaked email circulating in the wild" — making it impossible to construct a valid Digest with PII in any section guarantees this can't happen in production. (3) **No individual trader names — handle denylist.** The handle regex catches `@username` patterns common on Twitter / Discord; a section body that praises "@alice_trader" for "the strategy" would identify a specific user contrary to the anonymisation contract. The handle pattern is whitespace-bounded so `email@example.com` doesn't false-positive as a handle (the email pattern catches it instead). (4) **Subscription state SUBSCRIBED → UNSUBSCRIBED one-way; re-subscription requires fresh record.** The audit trail preserves the unsubscribe timestamp; legally, the unsubscribed_at field is what regulators consult to verify "this user unsubscribed on date X and didn't receive newsletters after that date". The `AlreadyUnsubscribedError` on double-unsubscribe means the operator's idempotency guard at the unsubscribe handler won't accidentally clear the original timestamp.
