The pin matters because GDPR / CCPA right-to-be-forgotten requires the unsubscribe action be permanent and provable. (5) **Render output never includes operator-side credentials, send-service API keys, or subscriber email addresses.** The Subscription dataclass simply doesn't carry the email; the render functions don't have access to send-service credentials. The render-no-leak regression test asserts no email shape (`\w+@\w+\.\w+`) and no `@` substring appear in the rendered digest output — a structural pin since validation has already rejected any section containing those patterns. Halal alignment: the no-individual-names pin is doubly important for a halal community where members may be sensitive about their financial decisions being publicly identified ("alice's halal portfolio underperformed" would violate both privacy norms and the spirit of avoiding public shaming); the GDPR-compliant unsubscribe state machine respects the user's right to disconnect; the regulatory-updates section provides a low-friction channel to inform the community of changes (SEC RIA registration progress, scholar reaffirmations of AAOIFI standards) that affect their compliance posture. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `re` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no Mailgun/Postmark/SES SDK. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 57 tests cover: SectionKind + SubscriptionStatus enum string-value pins; Section field validation (empty section_id / title / body rejected; 120-char title cap; 4000-char body cap; frozen); validate_section across each of 5 PII patterns (email both in title and body / SSN / phone / IP / 58-char "BinanceA"+"Bc"*25 API-key decoy); handle pattern in title and body; clean strategy-discussion + Sharpe quotes passes; DigestViolationError carries section_id + reason; Digest field validation (empty digest_id / quarter_label / sections rejected; naive published_at rejected; duplicate section IDs rejected; frozen); validate_digest catches PII in any single section even when others are clean; sections_by_kind filters (multi-kind cohort returns only matching; missing kind returns empty); **Subscription validation pins: UNSUBSCRIBED requires unsubscribed_at + SUBSCRIBED must not have it (both directions pinned)**; render no-secret-leak structural pin (no email-shape regex match + no `@` + no `subscriber_email` / `send_api_key` substrings); e2e flows (full quarterly digest with all 4 section kinds + AAOIFI Standard 21 reaffirmation + SEC RIA progress + 1.8 Sharpe top performer + HFT-underperformed-DCA didn't-work case; subscription lifecycle Q1 subscribe → Q3 unsubscribe → already-unsubscribed raises; **PII caught BEFORE send load-bearing pin** — "alice.smith@halal-trader.dev" embedded in section body raises DigestViolationError during validate_digest; replay consistency). The Mailgun / Postmark / SES adapter (operator-side, picks a send service per environment), the FastAPI `/api/newsletter/subscribe` POST endpoint that creates a Subscription + the `/api/newsletter/unsubscribe/{token}` endpoint with single-use tokens, the quarterly cron that builds the Digest from platform-aggregate sources (Wave 3.H leaderboard provides TOP_PERFORMERS aggregates; Wave 11.A advisor registration provides REGULATORY updates; Wave 2.F scholar review provides SCHOLAR_UPDATES; Wave 5.A live-cycle replay provides WHAT_DIDNT_WORK insights), the unsubscribe-link generator (signs a one-time token per subscription), and the dashboard "newsletter preview" tile (renders the in-progress digest before send) all deferred to follow-ups — digest builder verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 10.E — Annual halal fintech conference planning engine** — `web/conference.py` is the pure-Python planning state machine the conference operations team consults to track speaker invitations, schedule sessions without conflict, and manage sponsor tiers. The roadmap pins the conference as "halal fintech founders, operators, scholars, academics" with the platform as host; this module ships the deterministic planning primitives (the actual venue + travel + catering are operator-side). Picked a focused planning state machine over a generic event-management SaaS approach because (a) speaker invitation lifecycle (invited → accepted/declined → confirmed) needs an audit trail for "did Mufti X confirm before we printed the schedule?" — a missed-confirmation that lands in the printed program and the speaker doesn't show up is the worst-case failure that damages the brand position the conference is meant to cement; the structural constraint (only CONFIRMED is print-safe) makes that mistake impossible at planning time, (b) session scheduling needs hard time-conflict detection — booking two sessions for Mufti X in overlapping slots is an error class that must fail at planning time rather than at the conference itself when 500 attendees are in two rooms expecting the same speaker, (c) sponsor tiers (PLATINUM / GOLD / SILVER / BRONZE) drive logo placement + booth size + speaking slots; encoding the tier ladder once means the printed program + signage + website all consult the same source and a future "let's bump Foo Capital from Gold to Platinum" change ripples consistently. Six composed surfaces. (1) `SpeakerStatus` enum (INVITED / ACCEPTED / DECLINED / CONFIRMED / WITHDRAWN) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability; CONFIRMED is the load-bearing print-safe state. (2) `SpeakerKind` enum (SCHOLAR / FOUNDER / OPERATOR / ACADEMIC / REGULATOR) — exactly the five kinds the roadmap names; the operator-side rotation balance check ("did we book enough scholars vs founders for a balanced agenda?") consults this enum. (3) `SponsorTier` enum + module-level `_TIER_ORDER` dict pinning the ladder (PLATINUM=3 > GOLD=2 > SILVER=1 > BRONZE=0). (4) `Speaker` dataclass carries speaker_id + display_handle + kind + status + invited_at + optional decided_at. The dataclass deliberately excludes contact email / phone — those are operator-side state held in a CRM the conference org uses, kept structurally out of the render path so a render of the speaker roster can't accidentally leak personal contact info. The validation enforces: INVITED must NOT have decided_at (a contributor that flipped status to INVITED but kept the decided_at would be confusing); ACCEPTED / DECLINED / CONFIRMED / WITHDRAWN all REQUIRE decided_at (the audit timestamp) — both directions pinned, so the "decided" status fields can't drift apart from the timestamp. (5) Lifecycle transition functions: `invite_speaker(*, speaker_id, display_handle, kind, now)` builds INVITED with no decided_at; `accept_invitation(speaker, *, now)` only from INVITED → ACCEPTED; `decline_invitation(speaker, *, now)` only from INVITED → DECLINED (terminal); `confirm_speaker(speaker, *, now)` ONLY from ACCEPTED → CONFIRMED — the load-bearing print-safety pin: cannot skip from INVITED → CONFIRMED, the speaker must explicitly accept first; `withdraw_speaker(speaker, *, now)` ONLY from CONFIRMED → WITHDRAWN — used when a confirmed speaker pulls out late; `is_print_safe(speaker)` returns True only for CONFIRMED, so the program-printing CLI keys on this single function. (6) `Session` carries session_id + title + room + tz-aware time bounds (`starts_at`, `ends_at` with `ends_at > starts_at` invariant) + frozenset of speaker_ids (panels can have multiple speakers). `_windows_overlap` uses half-open `[start, end)` intervals so back-to-back sessions (a.end == b.start) don't trigger a conflict — this matters because conference schedules are often built as `[09:00, 10:00) → [10:00, 11:00) → [11:00, 12:00)` in the same room, and a strict-overlap check would falsely fail. `assert_no_conflict(new_session, existing_sessions)` raises `SessionConflictError` for: (a) duplicate `session_id` (already exists); (b) speaker double-booking (any speaker_id in both sessions during overlapping window — handles panels where any of 3 speakers being double-booked elsewhere is a conflict); (c) room double-booking (same room in overlapping window even with different speakers). `Sponsor` carries sponsor_id + display_name + tier + onboarded_at; deliberately excludes invoice amount / contact email. `tier_outranks(a, b)` is strictly greater (same tier returns False). `sponsors_at_or_above(sponsors, *, minimum)` returns qualified sponsors sorted highest-tier-first for the printed program's "sponsors by tier" section. `speaker_kind_balance(speakers)` counts per-kind for CONFIRMED speakers only — INVITED / ACCEPTED don't count because the operator's "what's our actual roster look like?" question is about who's actually speaking. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Speaker invitation lifecycle: forward-only with strict prereqs.** INVITED → ACCEPTED / DECLINED → CONFIRMED → WITHDRAWN. The pin matters because an "I accepted but never confirmed travel" speaker shouldn't print, and a "confirmed but pulled out 2 weeks before" speaker needs a distinct status (WITHDRAWN) so the audit row tells the difference between "never said yes" and "said yes then pulled out" — different operator follow-up actions per case. The skip-from-INVITED-to-CONFIRMED rejection is pinned via test (`test_confirm_from_invited_rejected`). (2) **Only CONFIRMED is print-safe.** `is_print_safe(speaker)` returns True only for the CONFIRMED state; INVITED / ACCEPTED / DECLINED / WITHDRAWN all return False. The pin protects against the worst-case failure mode: speaker pulls out, operator forgets to update status, printed program lists them, attendees show up to a no-show. The structural pin makes this impossible when the printing pipeline keys on `is_print_safe`. (3) **Session conflict detection across speakers AND rooms.** Two distinct conflict classes — speakers (a speaker can't present two sessions at once) AND rooms (one room, one session at a time) — both checked in the same call. Adjacent windows (a.end == b.start) explicitly don't conflict so back-to-back scheduling works. The panel-speaker collision pin handles the case where a multi-speaker panel has any of its speakers double-booked elsewhere (the "sp1, sp2, sp3" panel + "sp2 elsewhere overlapping" raises with `sp2` named in the error message). (4) **SponsorTier ladder pinned via _TIER_ORDER dict.** PLATINUM > GOLD > SILVER > BRONZE; tier_outranks is strictly greater so "is PLATINUM > PLATINUM?" returns False (the operator-side benefits-comparison logic doesn't get confused by ties). The `sponsors_at_or_above` helper sorts highest-tier-first for the printed program. (5) **Render output never includes speaker contact emails or sponsor invoice amounts.** The Speaker dataclass simply doesn't carry email/phone; the Sponsor dataclass doesn't carry invoice amount. The render regression tests assert no `@` substring (no email-shape) and no `$` substring (no dollar amount) appear in render output. Halal alignment: the conference brings together scholars + founders + operators + academics + regulators; the SpeakerKind enum being closed enforces that balance is intentional rather than drifting (a future "let me add INFLUENCER as a speaker kind" PR would have to update the enum + the rotation rationale). The print-safe gate keying on CONFIRMED protects scholars (Mufti X who travels internationally) from being publicly committed before logistics are settled — a no-show on a printed program reflects badly on the speaker, which the structural pin prevents. The no-secret-leak render keeps speakers' contact info private (a published speaker bio shouldn't reveal personal email even if the operator's CRM has it). Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no event-management SDK / Eventbrite API / etc. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 61 tests cover: 3 enum string-value pins (SpeakerStatus / SponsorTier / SpeakerKind); Speaker field validation (empty speaker_id / display_handle rejected; naive invited_at rejected; **INVITED-must-not-have-decided-at + non-INVITED-requires-decided-at pin both directions**; decided-before-invited rejected; immutable); invite_speaker basic + empty-id + naive-now rejections; accept_invitation from INVITED + non-INVITED rejected + naive-now rejected; decline_invitation from INVITED + accepted-then-decline rejected; **confirm_speaker from ACCEPTED only + skip-from-INVITED rejected pin** (the load-bearing print-safety pin); confirm-from-DECLINED rejected; withdraw_speaker from CONFIRMED only + accepted-then-withdraw rejected; **is_print_safe across all 5 statuses pinned per status** (only CONFIRMED true); Session field validation (empty fields rejected; ends-before-starts rejected; equal-times rejected; empty speaker_ids rejected; immutable); assert_no_conflict (no-conflict with empty existing; non-overlapping time same room OK; **back-to-back sessions a.end == b.start same room don't conflict pin**); speaker double-booked across different rooms in overlapping windows raises; room double-booked across different speakers in overlapping windows raises; **panel session with 3 speakers catches ANY shared-speaker collision pin** (sp1+sp2+sp3 panel + elsewhere-sp2 raises with sp2 named); duplicate session_id rejected; Sponsor validation + immutability; tier_outranks strict (same returns False); sponsors_at_or_above filters + returns sorted highest-tier-first; speaker_kind_balance pins (CONFIRMED only counted; INVITED/ACCEPTED/DECLINED don't count; all kinds present in result dict even with zero count); render speaker with status + kind emoji per kind; render no-secret regression (no `@` no `+1` phone-shape no "phone"); render session with title + room + speakers; render sponsor with tier emoji + display_name + no-secret regression (no `$` no `USD` no "invoice" no `@`); e2e flows (Mufti Faraz Adam full lifecycle invite → accept → confirm with print-safe transitions; speaker pulls out after confirmation must be removed from program; 4-session schedule build with back-to-back validation succeeds; speaker double-booking caught at planning time pin; replay consistency). The conference operations CRM (operator-side, holds the actual speaker contact info this module deliberately excludes), the FastAPI `/api/conference/speakers` + `/sessions` + `/sponsors` route series, the printed-program PDF generator (consumes is_print_safe + sponsors_at_or_above + render functions), the conference website (renders the public schedule from confirmed sessions + sponsors), and the registration ticketing system (separate concern; could compose with Wave 7.E marketplace patterns) all deferred to follow-ups — planning state machine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 9.E — Architecture deep-dive video catalogue + production state machine** — `web/video_catalogue.py` is the pure-Python topic registry + production state machine the operator consults to track which architecture explainer videos exist, which are recorded vs published, and which prerequisites each viewer needs. The roadmap names four target topics (cycle pipeline, halal screener, LLM ensemble, replay store) for 5-10 minute videos posted publicly; this module ships the deterministic planning + lifecycle primitives — the actual recording / editing / hosting is operator-side. Picked a focused topic catalogue + state machine over an ad-hoc spreadsheet because (a) the prerequisites graph (the LLM ensemble video assumes the viewer watched the cycle pipeline video first) needs deterministic ordering — a regression-pinned DAG that operators can render as a "watch path" guide rather than a prose suggestion in the video description; the cycle-detection guarantee means a contributor that adds "watch X before Y" while X already requires Y fails CI rather than ships a confusing prereq chain, (b) the production lifecycle (drafted → recorded → edited → published) mirrors the Wave 6.I distillation deployment + 8.C DR drill state machines so operators have one mental model for "promoting a piece of content to public-release"; encoding it once means the operator dashboard's "what's the publish status of every topic?" tile reads from the same shape across modules, (c) duration estimates per topic are factual catalogue data — encoding them once means the CDN / hosting cost projection (deferred) consults one source rather than re-deriving from per-file metadata. Six composed surfaces. (1) `TopicArea` enum with 8 closed-set values: the four roadmap-named (CYCLE_PIPELINE / HALAL_SCREENER / LLM_ENSEMBLE / REPLAY_STORE) plus four foundational/advanced areas (PURIFICATION_LEDGER / KILL_SWITCH / BROKER_PLUGIN / OBSERVABILITY) that naturally expand the catalogue. Pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. Adding an area is a code review change so the viewer's mental map of "what's covered?" stays stable as new videos land. (2) `ProductionStatus` enum (DRAFTED / RECORDED / EDITED / PUBLISHED) with module-level `_PRODUCTION_ORDER` tuple for forward-only progression. PUBLISHED is intentionally terminal — content revisions require a NEW topic record, not editing the published one, so the audit trail "what was published when" stays clean for the public-channel timeline. (3) `_MIN_DURATION = 5min` and `_MAX_DURATION = 10min` — the load-bearing roadmap pin. The roadmap explicitly names "5-10 minute videos" as the format; the constructor rejects 4min59s and 11min so a contributor that drafted a 12-minute deep-dive realizes at planning time the format needs to be split, not at edit time. (4) `VideoTopic` dataclass with topic_id + title + area + estimated_duration + prerequisites frozenset + status + drafted_at + last_status_at. Validation enforces empty-field rejection + duration band + tz-aware datetimes + last_status_at >= drafted_at + the trivial-cycle pin (a topic in its own prerequisites set raises `PrerequisiteCycleError` at construction, since "watch X before X" is a useless circular instruction). (5) `draft_topic` builds the initial DRAFTED record; `advance_topic(topic, to_status, *, now)` enforces forward-only one-step-at-a-time via `_check_forward` — DRAFTED → RECORDED → EDITED → PUBLISHED; skipping (DRAFTED → EDITED) raises; backtracking (RECORDED → DRAFTED) raises; **post-PUBLISHED transitions all raise** (PUBLISHED is terminal). `is_publishable(topic)` returns True only for PUBLISHED. (6) `assert_no_prereq_cycle(topics)` walks the prereq graph detecting cycles via DFS with in-progress-stack tracking; handles 2-topic A→B→A and 3-topic A→B→C→A cycles; external prereqs (referenced but not in the batch) are skipped rather than raised — operators iteratively add topics, and a half-built batch shouldn't fail validation just because an external "cycle" prereq is documented elsewhere. `watch_path(target_id, *, topics)` returns a topological-order tuple of topic IDs ending at target — useful for the "before you watch X, watch Y first" UI hint; handles diamond DAG (A → B, A → C, B + C → D yields A exactly once before B/C/D); detects cycles during traversal; raises KeyError for unknown target. `total_runtime` sums durations; `published_topics` filters + sorts by topic_id. Render with area emoji (🔄 cycle / ✅ halal / 🧠 llm / 💾 replay / 🤲 purification / 🛑 halt / 🔌 broker / 📊 observability) + status emoji (📝 drafted / 🎥 recorded / ✂️ edited / 🚀 published). **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set TopicArea enum.** Adding an area is a code review change. The 8-area set is intentional — the four roadmap-named topics plus four natural extensions; a future "let me add ML_PIPELINE" PR has to update the enum + emoji map + tests, ensuring the new area gets a proper place in the rendered grouping. (2) **5-10 minute duration band pinned per roadmap.** The constructor rejects below 5min and above 10min. Pinned both directions: 5:00 inclusive lower (passes), 4:59 below (rejects); 10:00 inclusive upper (passes), 11:00 above (rejects). The pin matters because the roadmap chose 5-10 min for retention reasons; a contributor's "let me make a 30-minute deep-dive" undermines the format and the catalogue layer prevents that drift at planning time. (3) **Production lifecycle is forward-only with PUBLISHED terminal.** The structural guarantee that a published topic can't be re-edited (only superseded by a new topic record with a fresh ID) means the public-channel audit trail of "topic X was first published on date Y" stays accurate; a content correction needs a new topic_id (e.g. `cycle_pipeline_v2`) which the catalogue indexes alongside the original. The skip-rejection (DRAFTED → EDITED rejected) ensures no topic reaches public release without recording — a contributor can't accidentally publish an unrecorded outline. (4) **Prerequisites form a strict DAG with cycle detection.** The trivial self-cycle is caught at VideoTopic construction; the multi-topic cycle (A → B → A) is caught at `assert_no_prereq_cycle` time when validating the full batch. The DFS-based detection handles complex cases including diamond DAGs (which are valid — A → B, A → C, B+C → D is a tree, not a cycle) and 3-topic cycles (A → B → C → A) where the cycle isn't visible from any single topic's prerequisites alone. The `watch_path` traversal also detects cycles, so a misconfigured runtime batch fails fast. (5) **Render output never includes operator credentials, hosting service tokens (YouTube / Vimeo / Mux), or raw transcripts.** The dataclass simply doesn't carry those fields; the render regression test asserts no `api_key` / `youtube` / `vimeo` / `transcript` / `bearer` substrings appear. Halal alignment: the architecture deep-dive videos serve the halal-trader community by making the bot's compliance logic inspectable — a viewer who watches the halal screener video can verify the bot's screening matches their scholar's framework, and the prereq graph (cycle pipeline → halal screener) ensures viewers understand the cycle-level invariants before diving into the screening step. The 5-10 minute format respects the operator's time during the workday; a 30-minute deep-dive would be a barrier to broader community engagement. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no video SDK / hosting service. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 49 tests cover: 8 TopicArea + 4 ProductionStatus enum string-value pins; VideoTopic field validation including 5-min and 10-min duration boundaries inclusive both directions (the load-bearing roadmap pin) + 4:59 and 11:00 rejections + naive datetimes rejected + last_status_at-before-drafted rejected + immutable; **trivial self-prereq cycle caught at VideoTopic construction with PrerequisiteCycleError**; draft_topic basic + with-prereqs + naive-now rejection; advance_topic forward-step + full-lifecycle to PUBLISHED + skip-DRAFTED-to-EDITED rejected + skip-to-PUBLISHED rejected + backwards-to-DRAFTED rejected + **PUBLISHED-is-terminal rejection pin** + naive-now rejected + returns new state immutable; is_publishable per-status (only PUBLISHED true; DRAFTED/RECORDED/EDITED false); assert_no_prereq_cycle (linear chain OK; diamond DAG OK; 2-topic A→B→A cycle caught; 3-topic cycle caught; external prereq skipped not raised); watch_path no-prereqs single-element; linear chain (A,B,C); diamond DAG (A appears once, before B/C/D in topological order); unknown-target raises KeyError; external-prereq skipped; cycle detected during traversal; total_runtime basic + empty; published_topics filters + sorts by topic_id; render with topic_id + title + area emoji per kind + status emoji per status + 7.5-min duration display + prereqs visible + empty-prereqs renders as `—` + no-secret regression; e2e flows (cycle pipeline video full lifecycle drafted → recorded → edited → published; **realistic 4-topic catalogue with roadmap-named topics — cycle (no prereq) + halal (req cycle) + llm (req cycle) + replay (req cycle); assert_no_prereq_cycle passes; halal watch_path returns ("cycle", "halal"); total_runtime is exactly 30 minutes (7+8+9+6)** — the e2e pin that the catalogue actually composes correctly with the roadmap-named topics; replay consistency). The actual video recording + editing pipeline (operator-side using OBS / ScreenFlow / Camtasia + Final Cut / DaVinci Resolve), the hosting integration (`youtube_dl` for YouTube + Vimeo SDK for the public posts), the public landing page generator (consumes `published_topics` + `watch_path` to render a "Start Here" guide), the dashboard "video catalogue" tile (renders the production status of every topic for the operator to track which to record next), the auto-generated transcript pipeline (`whisper.cpp` STT against the recorded MP4s + accessibility check via Wave 5.J accessibility-audit module on the rendered captions), and the analytics integration (consumes the published_topics list + correlates with viewer drop-off data) all deferred to follow-ups — catalogue + state engine verified in isolation first so the production pipeline sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 8.E aux — Incident response state machine** — `ops/incident_response.py` is the pure-Python incident lifecycle engine that complements Wave 8.E's alert router + seed runbooks. Wave 8.E ships the alert *dispatch* layer (which channels get notified, what runbook URL to surface, how to dedup); this auxiliary primitive ships the post-dispatch *lifecycle* — once the on-call ack's the page, what's the canonical state machine + SLA-enforcement + post-mortem-requirement gate that turns the alert into a recorded incident. Picked a focused state engine over a generic ticketing tool because (a) severity-driven ack SLAs need deterministic enforcement — the dashboard tile "are any sev1 incidents unacked past SLA?" should answer in O(N) of incidents using `is_ack_overdue`, not require a Jira / PagerDuty query that depends on external service availability (which is itself fragile during an incident, the worst possible time for the answer to depend on a third-party API), (b) the lifecycle has a strict forward order (OPEN → ACKNOWLEDGED → MITIGATED → RESOLVED → POSTMORTEM_PUBLISHED) and skipping is the most common operator error during an outage — a contributor that "marked it resolved" without acking first is a confused-state bug; the structural skip-rejection makes that impossible, (c) post-mortem is required for sev1/sev2 incidents — a closed sev1 without a post-mortem published within 7 days is a process failure that must be visible on the dashboard, and `is_postmortem_overdue` makes that visibility deterministic without needing a Confluence / Notion sync. Six composed surfaces. (1) `Severity` enum (SEV1 / SEV2 / SEV3 / SEV4) with pinned string values + module-level `_SEVERITY_ORDER` dict for the strict ladder. SEV1 = production down or data loss; SEV2 = major degradation; SEV3 = minor degradation; SEV4 = informational / cleanup. The four-tier ladder is the industry standard (PagerDuty, ServiceNow, etc.) and pinning it as a closed enum means a contributor's "let me add SEV0 for catastrophic" PR has to update the ladder + ack SLA dict + tests in one place. (2) Module-level `_DEFAULT_ACK_SLAS` dict pins the per-severity ack timeline: SEV1=5min, SEV2=30min, SEV3=4h, SEV4=24h. The 5min SEV1 SLA is the load-bearing operator-protective number — production is down, the on-call must engage within 5 minutes or the dashboard tile turns red. The 24h SEV4 SLA is forgiving by design — informational alerts shouldn't page the on-call at 3am. (3) `_POSTMORTEM_REQUIRED` frozenset names the two severities that need post-mortems (SEV1, SEV2) — module-level so a contributor can't bypass it via attribute mutation. (4) `IncidentStatus` enum (OPEN / ACKNOWLEDGED / MITIGATED / RESOLVED / POSTMORTEM_PUBLISHED) with module-level `_STATUS_ORDER` tuple for forward-only progression. POSTMORTEM_PUBLISHED is terminal. (5) `IncidentPolicy` validates the ack_slas dict at construction: every severity must have an entry; SLAs must be positive timedeltas; the postmortem deadline (default 7 days) must be positive. The validation enforces the structural invariant that no severity slips through unhandled. (6) `Incident` frozen dataclass carries incident_id + severity + summary + opened_at + status + last_status_at + per-status attribution fields (acker / resolver / postmortem_author). The validation enforces the load-bearing **per-status attribution pin** in both directions: OPEN must NOT have any attribution set (a contributor that pre-filled acker on construction would create a confused state); ACKNOWLEDGED requires non-empty acker AND must NOT have resolver/postmortem_author (those come later); MITIGATED requires acker (carried forward); RESOLVED requires acker + resolver; POSTMORTEM_PUBLISHED requires all three (acker + resolver + postmortem_author). The structural pin guarantees the audit row is always consistent with the status. The lifecycle transition functions enforce forward-only one-step progression: `acknowledge(incident, *, acker, now)` only OPEN → ACKNOWLEDGED with non-empty acker; `mitigate(incident, *, now)` only ACKNOWLEDGED → MITIGATED (carries acker forward); `resolve(incident, *, resolver, now)` only MITIGATED → RESOLVED with non-empty resolver; `publish_postmortem(incident, *, author, now)` only RESOLVED → POSTMORTEM_PUBLISHED with non-empty author AND **only for SEV1+SEV2** (raises `PostmortemNotRequiredError` carrying severity for SEV3+SEV4). `is_ack_overdue(incident, *, now, policy)` returns True only when the incident is OPEN AND now - opened_at > policy.ack_slas[severity]; ACKNOWLEDGED+ are never ack-overdue (they've been ack'd already, so the "is it overdue?" question is moot). The boundary is exclusive (>, not >=) — exactly 5min for SEV1 is NOT overdue, the 5min+1sec mark is. `is_postmortem_overdue(incident, *, now, policy)` returns True only for SEV1+SEV2 RESOLVED past 7 days; SEV3+SEV4 never overdue (don't need postmortems); already-published never overdue; non-RESOLVED states (OPEN/ACK/MITIGATED) never overdue (postmortem isn't ready yet). `filter_overdue(incidents, *, now, policy)` combines both flavors and sorts SEV1-first for the on-call dashboard. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Severity ladder pinned: SEV1=5min, SEV2=30min, SEV3=4h, SEV4=24h.** The roadmap-pinned numbers are the operator-protective thresholds; the per-severity boundaries pinned in tests both directions per severity ensure a contributor that "let me lower SEV3 to 1h" has to update the test rather than ship silently. (2) **Forward-only lifecycle with skip rejected.** Cannot skip OPEN → MITIGATED (must ack first); cannot skip MITIGATED → POSTMORTEM_PUBLISHED (must resolve first); cannot revert (RESOLVED → MITIGATED rejected). The structural pin protects against the contributor-confusion failure mode where someone marks an incident "resolved" while it's still actively burning. (3) **Post-mortem required for SEV1+SEV2 only; SEV3+SEV4 raise PostmortemNotRequiredError.** The pin matters because a SEV3 "minor degradation" doesn't warrant the operator-time of a full post-mortem; allowing operators to skip it for low-severity reduces the postmortem queue to incidents that actually warrant deep analysis. The error carries the severity so the operator's exception handler knows which incident class triggered (the operator's "oh I forgot this was SEV3" recovery is straightforward). (4) **Per-status attribution required and structurally enforced.** The validation that OPEN must not have acker, ACKNOWLEDGED requires acker, RESOLVED requires acker+resolver, POSTMORTEM_PUBLISHED requires all three — this is what makes the audit row honest. A future "anonymous incident" attempt would have to bypass the dataclass validator, which is not a feature. (5) **Render output never includes raw alert payload / stack traces / log lines / API keys.** The dataclass simply doesn't carry those fields; the render shows summary + severity emoji + status emoji + attribution. The raw error details belong in the runbook drill (the operator's deep-dive workspace) not the incident card (the operator's at-a-glance dashboard tile). The render-no-leak regression test asserts no `stack` / `traceback` / `api_key` / `bearer` substrings appear. Halal alignment: the load-bearing kill-switch is itself a SEV1-class event (the operator manually halting the bot); pairing the kill-switch wave with this incident lifecycle ensures every halt is recorded, acked within 5 minutes, and post-mortemed within 7 days — providing a paper trail that protects both operator and any halal-trader user during a potential dispute. The 30-minute SEV2 SLA matches the typical Saudi/Pakistani operator's response window during prayer times; the 24-hour SEV4 SLA respects operator off-hours for low-severity items. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async / PagerDuty SDK. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 65 tests cover: 4 Severity + 5 IncidentStatus enum string-value pins; **roadmap-pinned ack SLA defaults** (5min/30min/4h/24h asserted directly on DEFAULT_POLICY); 7-day postmortem deadline pin; IncidentPolicy validation (zero SLAs rejected; missing-severity rejected with explicit "missing" message; zero postmortem deadline rejected); severity_outranks strict (SEV1 > SEV4 True; SEV1 > SEV2 True; SEV3 > SEV2 False; SEV1 > SEV1 False — strict pin); Incident field validation (empty incident_id / summary rejected; naive opened_at / last_status_at rejected; last-status-before-opened rejected); **per-status attribution pin both directions** (OPEN with acker rejected; ACKNOWLEDGED without acker rejected; RESOLVED with only acker rejected; POSTMORTEM_PUBLISHED without all three rejected; immutable); open_incident basic + empty_id / empty_summary / naive_now rejections; acknowledge OPEN→ACK with acker; acknowledge requires non-empty acker; acknowledge already-acked rejected; mitigate from ACK + skip-from-OPEN rejected; resolve from MITIGATED + requires resolver + skip-from-ACK rejected; **publish_postmortem SEV1+SEV2 supported, SEV3+SEV4 raise PostmortemNotRequiredError carrying severity**; publish requires non-empty author; publish skip-from-OPEN rejected; **is_ack_overdue boundary inclusive at exactly-SLA-time per severity** (5min/30min/4h/24h); ACKNOWLEDGED never ack-overdue (the structural pin); naive-now rejected; is_postmortem_overdue past-7-days for SEV1+SEV2; **7-day boundary inclusive (exact 7d not overdue)**; SEV3+SEV4 never overdue regardless of elapsed; already-published never overdue; non-RESOLVED never overdue; filter_overdue combines ack-overdue + postmortem-overdue; **sorts SEV1-first**; rejects naive now; render with severity emoji 🔴/🟠/🟡/🔵 + status emoji ⚠️/👀/🛡️/✅/📋 + attribution shown when set + omitted when OPEN; render no-secret regression (no stack/traceback/api_key/bearer); e2e flows (full SEV1 lifecycle 2min ack → 30min mitigate → 1hr resolve → 3-day postmortem all within SLA; SEV1 postmortem-overdue at 14 days; SEV1 unacked at 6 min triggers ack-overdue; SEV3 no postmortem required pin; replay consistency). The Postgres `incidents` audit table + repository, the FastAPI `/api/ops/incidents` route series (POST `/open`, POST `/{id}/ack`, POST `/{id}/mitigate`, POST `/{id}/resolve`, POST `/{id}/postmortem`), the dashboard "incidents" tile (rendering `filter_overdue` output sorted SEV1-first), the AlertRouter integration (cycle's `AlertSink.notify` → automatic `open_incident` for severity-mapped incidents), and the per-incident postmortem template generator (consumes the runbook from Wave 8.E + the timeline from `last_status_at` chain) all deferred to follow-ups — incident lifecycle engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 10.F aux — Feature flag rollout engine** — `web/feature_flags.py` is the runtime-rollout complement to Wave 10.F edition gating. Wave 10.F's `feature_gate.py` answers "is feature X available in this build's edition + tier?" (build-time / commercial); this module answers "is feature X enabled for THIS user RIGHT NOW during the gradual rollout?" (runtime / staged). The two layers compose — a feature must be both edition-available AND flag-enabled for the user to see it. Picked a focused rollout engine over scattered `if random() < 0.1:` checks because (a) gradual rollout needs deterministic per-user evaluation — a user assigned to the 10% test bucket should stay in that bucket across reloads; SHA-256 hashing of (flag_id, user_id) gives that deterministic bucket assignment without needing to persist per-user state, (b) the flag registry needs to be inspectable at runtime so operators can answer "what's currently rolling out?" without grepping logs, (c) cohort allowlists are explicit (operator-curated user IDs) rather than hash-based — beta-tester cohorts shouldn't drift if a user_id hashes into a different bucket after a salt rotation. Five composed surfaces. (1) `RolloutKind` enum (OFF / ON / PERCENTAGE / COHORT_ALLOWLIST) with pinned string values. OFF and ON are the trivial cases; PERCENTAGE is hash-based gradual rollout; COHORT_ALLOWLIST is explicit beta-tester membership. (2) `FeatureFlag` dataclass carries flag_id + description + kind + percentage + cohort_user_ids. The validation enforces consistency: percentage must be in [0, 100]; **PERCENTAGE kind with 0% is rejected** (operators should use OFF instead — a 0% rollout is a confused state); **PERCENTAGE with 100% is rejected** (use ON); COHORT_ALLOWLIST requires non-empty cohort_user_ids; non-cohort kinds must NOT have cohort_user_ids set (a contributor that put cohort users on a PERCENTAGE flag would create a confused state). (3) `_bucket_for(flag_id, user_id)` computes deterministic 0-99 bucket via SHA-256 of `f"{flag_id}:{user_id}"` taking the first 4 bytes mod 100. The flag_id salt is the load-bearing correlation-free pin: two flags rolling out at 50% would otherwise enable the *same* user-half (since they'd hash the user_id identically), creating correlated rollout buckets that are useless for A/B testing; salting by flag_id breaks the correlation so two 50% rollouts enable independent halves with ~25% overlap. (4) `is_enabled(flag, *, user_id)` evaluates: OFF returns False; ON returns True; PERCENTAGE returns `bucket_for < percentage`; COHORT_ALLOWLIST returns `user_id in cohort_user_ids`. The deterministic pin (same flag + same user always returns same answer) is the load-bearing UX guarantee — feature flicker (on/off/on/off across reloads) is the worst possible A/B testing outcome. (5) `FlagRegistry` is the frozen registry; rejects duplicate flag_ids. `lookup` raises KeyError for missing flags; `is_enabled_in(registry, flag_id, *, user_id)` is the convenience combiner; `all_flags(registry)` returns sorted-by-id; `enabled_count(flag, *, sample_user_ids)` lets operators verify "did the 10% rollout actually enable ~10% of active users?" without leaking individual user IDs to the dashboard. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set RolloutKind enum.** Adding a kind is a code review change. (2) **Per-user evaluation is deterministic — no flicker.** Same (flag_id, user_id) → same answer across reloads. The pin is tested with three repeated `is_enabled` calls asserting equal results. (3) **Percentage rollout uses SHA-256 of (flag_id, user_id), not random sampling.** The hash-based bucket assignment means user_id mid-rollout doesn't shift if the operator restarts the bot — a user enabled at 10% stays enabled when they upgrade to 11%. (4) **Correlation-free across flags.** Two 50% flags don't enable the same user-half because the flag_id salt differentiates them; pinned via empirical test that overlap is in [180, 320] of 1000 users (≈25% expected for independent halves). (5) **Render output never includes individual user_ids — only counts.** The cohort render shows `3 users` not `alice, bob, charlie`; the registry summary shows `cohort: 1` per kind. The privacy pin protects beta-tester membership from being leaked through dashboard or log surfaces. Halal alignment: the gradual rollout engine respects the conservative-defaults bias of the rest of the platform — new features start OFF, move to a small COHORT (trusted halal-trader operators who can verify the feature doesn't violate halal screening), then graduate to PERCENTAGE rollout, then ON. The flag_id salt prevents two flags rolling out simultaneously from accidentally testing the same user-half twice (which would skew the experiment results). The render shows cohort sizes not individual user_ids, respecting beta-tester privacy. Pure-Python (stdlib `hashlib` + `dataclasses` + `enum` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 44 tests cover: RolloutKind enum string-value pins; FeatureFlag validation across 4 kinds; **PERCENTAGE-with-0%-rejected** + **PERCENTAGE-with-100%-rejected** + COHORT-requires-cohort_user_ids + non-cohort-must-not-have-cohort all pinned; immutable; OFF always-false / ON always-true; **deterministic-per-user pin** (3 repeated calls return same answer — no flicker); 50% rollout enables ~half of 1000 users (empirical 400-600); 10% rollout enables ~100 (empirical 70-130); **correlation-free pin** (two 50% flags overlap ~25% not 50% — empirical 180-320); COHORT_ALLOWLIST explicit hits + misses; **cohort-explicit-not-hash-based pin** (a user in cohort A but not cohort B gets the right answer per flag); FlagRegistry duplicate-flag-id rejection; immutable; lookup hit + miss-raises-KeyError; is_enabled_in convenience; all_flags sorted; enabled_count basic + OFF returns 0 + ON returns all; render flag emoji per kind ⚫/✅/📊/👥; render percentage shows value; **render cohort shows SIZE not user_ids load-bearing privacy pin** (3-user cohort renders "3 users" with no `@`/`alice`/`bob` substrings); render registry summary counts per kind; e2e flows (**monotonic gradual rollout 0→10→50→100% pin** — each user enabled at stage N must stay enabled at stage N+1; no flicker possible); cohort-then-percentage transition (beta cohort first, then percentage); replay consistency.

* **Round-4 Wave 2.D aux — Charity disbursement reconciler** — `halal/disbursement_reconciler.py` is the paid-side complement to Wave 2.D's purification-schedule owed-side. Wave 2.D's `purification_schedule.py` answers "what does the operator owe to charity this quarter?"; this module answers "did the operator actually pay it?" by matching disbursement receipts (the operator's bank wire confirmations) against the owed-period totals. The composition gives halal-compliance auditors a single deterministic answer to "is the bot's purification ledger reconciled?" without cross-referencing multiple spreadsheets. Picked a focused reconciler over a generic accounting tool because (a) the halal-compliance audit trail must be inspectable: a scholar reviewing the bot's purification record asks "did the operator actually pay $487.32 to charity in 2026-Q1?" and the answer must be a single deterministic match against the operator's bank-wire confirmation rather than requiring cross-correlation across QuickBooks + the bot's audit log + the charity's receipt email; (b) the shortfall threshold (default $0.01 — full payment required modulo cents rounding) is the load-bearing audit attribute — anything more permissive would let the operator silently under-pay and still appear reconciled, defeating the audit purpose; (c) overdue detection (default 90 days past period end) flags periods where the operator hasn't yet disbursed, which is the most common operational failure (operator gets the receipt → forgets to wire → period drifts months out → the dashboard "purification overdue" tile is the only timely surface). Six composed surfaces. (1) `ReconciliationStatus` enum (UNRECONCILED / UNDERPAID / RECONCILED / OVERPAID) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. (2) `ReconcilerPolicy` ships defaults: `cents_tolerance_usd=0.01` + `overdue_threshold=timedelta(days=90)`. The policy's `cents_tolerance_usd > 1.0` check is the load-bearing pin against operator self-deception — a contributor that "let me bump the tolerance to $5 because it's just a few bucks" gets caught by the constructor: tolerance > $1 means we'd allow underpayment of more than a dollar, which is too lax for a halal-compliance audit. (3) `OwedPeriod` mirrors Wave 2.D's `DisbursementReceipt` shape with the minimum fields needed for reconciliation (period_label + owed_usd + starts_at + ends_at). Operators bridge by extracting these fields from the scheduler's output. Validation rejects empty period_label + negative owed_usd + naive datetimes + ends-before-starts; **zero owed accepted** (a quarter with no purification entries is valid). (4) `DisbursementReceipt` carries receipt_id + period_label + amount_usd + wired_at + optional `wire_reference` — the wire_reference is operator audit metadata kept structurally out of the render path (operators store the actual wire reference in their accounting system; the dataclass just keeps the link). Validation requires positive amount_usd (a $0 wire isn't a meaningful disbursement); naive wired_at rejected. (5) `_classify` is the status decision rule: `paid <= 0` → UNRECONCILED; `|shortfall| <= tolerance` → RECONCILED; `shortfall > tolerance` → UNDERPAID; `shortfall < -tolerance` → OVERPAID. The boundaries are inclusive at the tolerance value, so a 0.5-cent rounding overpayment is treated as RECONCILED (not OVERPAID), which matches operator intent. (6) `reconcile_period(period, receipts, *, now, policy)` filters receipts by period_label, sums the paid amount, classifies status, computes overdue (status in UNRECONCILED/UNDERPAID + now ≥ ends_at + threshold). The pin: `now >= ends_at + threshold` rather than `>` — the 90-day boundary is inclusive, so exactly 90 days past period end IS overdue; pinned via test. `reconcile_all(periods, receipts, *, now, policy)` returns results sorted by `period.starts_at` ascending so the operator's audit log is chronological. `total_outstanding(reconciliations)` sums **positive shortfalls only** — the load-bearing audit pin: overpayments do NOT net against underpayments (a $50 overpayment in Q1 doesn't reduce a $200 underpayment in Q2 without an explicit operator-side accounting decision). The pin matters because halal-compliance auditing treats each period as independent (the obligation to pay $200 in Q2 isn't satisfied by having paid $250 in Q1); pinned via test asserting total_outstanding=$200 rather than $150 in the over+under cohort. `overdue_periods(reconciliations)` returns the audit-tile candidates filtered to `is_overdue=True`. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **RECONCILED requires zero shortfall within $0.01 tolerance.** Any shortfall above $0.01 → UNDERPAID. The 1-cent tolerance handles floating-point quirks (operator wires the rounded sum of multiple dollar amounts that happens to differ by a fraction of a cent from the computed owed total) without permitting silent underpayment. (2) **Overpayment is allowed and tracked separately.** OVERPAID status carries forward as a credit (operator-side decision); the reconciler doesn't auto-net it against future underpayments. (3) **Overdue threshold default 90 days, boundary inclusive.** A period whose `ends_at + 90d <= now` and is still UNDERPAID/UNRECONCILED flags overdue. The 90-day window is the typical zakat-paying cadence (the obligation to pay this period's purification is due within the same broader fiscal cycle). (4) **One disbursement record per bank wire; multiple wires per period sum together.** Operators who pay in installments (e.g. $200 in February + $287.32 in March against a $487.32 Q1 owed) get RECONCILED status with `receipt_count=2`. (5) **Render output never includes the operator's bank account number, charity recipient bank details, or wire-transfer reference IDs.** The wire_reference field is structurally kept out of render. The render-no-leak regression test asserts `WIRE-` / `CONFIDENTIAL` / `@` (no email) / `routing` / `iban` substrings never appear. Mirrors no-secret patterns of upstream waves. Halal alignment: this is the audit-completing primitive for the bot's halal-compliance posture. Wave 2.D scheduling tells the operator what they owe; this module verifies they actually paid it. Together they produce an inspectable per-period audit trail that a scholar or external auditor (say, AAOIFI) can review without trusting the operator's self-report. The structural pin against silent underpayment (cents tolerance ≤ $1; overpayments NOT netted) means the audit log is honest by construction — there's no place for the operator to hide a missed disbursement behind cumulative-balance accounting. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 49 tests cover: ReconciliationStatus enum string-value pin; ReconcilerPolicy validation (negative tolerance rejected; **tolerance above $1 rejected — load-bearing audit pin**; zero overdue threshold rejected; immutable); OwedPeriod field validation including zero-owed accepted; DisbursementReceipt validation including zero-amount rejected; **status classification per ReconciliationStatus** (no receipts → UNRECONCILED; exact match → RECONCILED; within 0.5-cent tolerance → RECONCILED; $1.50 short → UNDERPAID; over → OVERPAID); multiple receipts sum; receipts filter by period_label; reconcile_period rejects naive now; **overdue boundary at 90 days inclusive** (91 days overdue; exactly 90 days overdue per `>=` semantics; 89 days NOT overdue both directions pinned); RECONCILED never overdue regardless of elapsed; OVERPAID never overdue; UNDERPAID + 100 days overdue; custom 30-day strict overdue flips a 31-day-old period; reconcile_all sorted by start ascending; empty input; naive now rejected; **total_outstanding excludes overpayments load-bearing pin** (over $50 + under $200 → total $200, NOT $150); overdue_periods filter; render with period label + status emoji ❓/⚠️/✅/💚 + OVERDUE marker on overdue + no marker on paid; render amounts visible ($487.32 + 2 receipts); render no-secret regression (no `WIRE-`/`CONFIDENTIAL`/`@`/`routing`/`iban`); render_summary with per-status counts + total outstanding; e2e full year audit (4 quarters: Q1 reconciled with $487.32 wire; Q2 underpaid $400 of $523.18 → overdue; Q3 overpaid $700 of $601.55 → not overdue; Q4 unpaid $478.91 → overdue; total_outstanding sums Q2 shortfall + Q4 shortfall correctly); replay consistency. The Postgres `disbursement_receipts` table + repository, the FastAPI `/api/halal/reconciliation` route surface that returns the per-period reconciliation matrix, the dashboard "purification status" tile (rendering total outstanding + overdue count for the operator's at-a-glance check), the operator email summary integration (Wave 5.I) that highlights overdue periods, and the AAOIFI-export PDF generator (Wave 11.B governance integration) that includes the full reconciliation audit log all deferred to follow-ups — reconciler verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 4.F aux — Strategy backtest comparator** — `ml/backtest_comparator.py` is the A-vs-B complement to Wave 4.F's single-strategy walk-forward + out-of-sample validation gate. Wave 4.F gates one strategy against its historical baseline; this module compares TWO strategies head-to-head with significance testing so operators running A/B experiments get a deterministic clear-winner / clear-loser / inconclusive verdict rather than reading two spreadsheets and eyeballing differences. Picked a focused comparator over scipy's `ttest_ind` because (a) the bot must run without scipy at the comparator layer (scipy is already deferred to optional dependencies), so a pure-Python Welch's t-test approximation using `math.erf` for the p-value keeps the comparator usable in any environment including the lightweight live-cycle path, (b) the verdict (clear winner / clear loser / inconclusive) is the load-bearing operator decision rather than the raw p-value — encoding alpha + minimum sample size + minimum effect-size as a closed policy means a contributor that "flipped strategy" based on a 0.04 p-value with 30 samples gets a clear "inconclusive — sample too small" answer rather than shipping a noisy strategy switch that loses real money in production, (c) the comparator must respect ALL four metrics (Sharpe, win rate, total return, max drawdown) as the four standard backtest summaries — a strategy with higher Sharpe but worse drawdown shouldn't auto-win; the comparator surfaces per-metric verdicts so the operator sees the trade-off explicitly. Five composed surfaces. (1) `ComparisonVerdict` enum (A_WINS / B_WINS / TIE / INCONCLUSIVE) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. INCONCLUSIVE is a real outcome — the structural pin against shipping noisy comparisons. (2) Module-level `_LOWER_IS_BETTER` frozenset names the metrics where lower is better (currently just `max_drawdown_pct` — drawdown is a positive magnitude where 5% is better than 15%). The set drives the verdict-direction inversion in `_classify_verdict`. (3) `ComparisonPolicy` defaults: `alpha=0.05` + `min_samples_per_arm=50` + `min_effect_size=0.1` (Cohen's d). Validation rejects alpha at 0 or 1; min_samples below 2 (t-test undefined); negative effect_size. The defaults match common A/B testing practice — alpha=0.05 is the conventional significance threshold; min_samples=50 is the rough lower bound where the normal approximation to t becomes accurate (within 5%); min_effect_size=0.1 is "small" per Cohen's conventions, screening out statistically-significant-but-meaningless differences. (4) `BacktestResult` carries strategy_id + summary stats per metric (mean + std + sample size), deliberately NOT raw return series — operators populate from their backtest engine output, and the comparator only needs the summaries. The validation pin: **`max_drawdown_pct` must be non-negative** (positive magnitude convention). The trade_count is the sample size for significance testing. (5) `_welch_t_test` is the pure-Python Welch's t-test approximation: variance of the difference in means as `var_a/n_a + var_b/n_b`, t-statistic via standard error, p-value via the normal approximation `2 * (1 - Phi(|t|))` where `Phi(t) = 0.5 * (1 + erf(t / sqrt(2)))`. The normal approximation is accurate within 5% for n>=30 per arm; the min_samples_per_arm threshold (default 50) protects against the small-sample inaccuracy. The zero-variance edge case (both arms identical) returns t=0, p=1.0, leading to INCONCLUSIVE verdict (zero effect size). `_cohens_d` uses pooled std `sqrt((var_a + var_b) / 2)`; positive when A > B. `_classify_verdict` runs the priority gate: insufficient samples → INCONCLUSIVE (regardless of p-value); insufficient effect size → INCONCLUSIVE (a tiny "statistically significant" difference isn't worth shipping a strategy change); p > alpha → TIE (no significant difference); p ≤ alpha → A_WINS or B_WINS by direction (with drawdown inverted: lower wins). `compare_metric(*, metric_name, a_mean, a_std, a_n, b_mean, b_std, b_n, policy)` is the per-metric API. `compare_backtests(a, b, *, policy)` runs all 4 metrics and returns `StrategyComparison`. The `overall_verdict` property aggregates per-metric verdicts: **any INCONCLUSIVE metric → overall INCONCLUSIVE** (the load-bearing pin against premature decisions); A_WINS if A wins majority AND no metric where A clearly loses; B_WINS symmetric; TIE otherwise. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Welch's t-test approximation pure-Python.** Pinned via known-result test: mean diff=2, std=1, n=100 each → t ≈ 14.14 (matches scipy to 1%). The pin protects against accidental algorithm drift (a contributor "fixing" the formula could silently change p-values). (2) **Verdict thresholds operator-tunable but constructor-validated.** Strict policy (alpha=0.01 + min_samples=200 + min_effect_size=0.5) flips a 100-sample comparison from A_WINS to INCONCLUSIVE — pinned via test. The validation prevents the operator-bug "I set min_samples=1 because I want answers fast" failure mode. (3) **Drawdown is inverted in the verdict direction.** Pinned via the `_LOWER_IS_BETTER` frozenset both directions (5% beats 15% → A_WINS; 15% loses to 5% → B_WINS). The structural pin matters because a contributor adding a new metric where lower is better (e.g. cost_pct, slippage_pct) just needs to add it to the frozenset rather than re-implement comparison logic. (4) **Inconclusive verdict is a real outcome.** Insufficient samples or insufficient effect size returns INCONCLUSIVE rather than guessing. The overall_verdict aggregator's "any inconclusive → overall inconclusive" pin is the load-bearing operator-protective rule: 3 metrics showing A_WINS but 1 showing INCONCLUSIVE means the operator should wait for more data before flipping strategies. (5) **Render output never includes raw return series, operator-side fields, or PII.** The dataclass shape doesn't carry those fields; the render shows summary statistics + verdict. Halal alignment: the comparator protects halal-trader operators from the "I switched strategies based on a noisy backtest and lost real money" failure mode that would damage user trust in the platform. The conservative-default thresholds (50 samples + Cohen's d 0.1 + alpha 0.05) reflect the operator-protective bias of the rest of the platform — small or noisy A/B experiments get clear "wait" answers rather than premature commits. The drawdown-inverted comparison protects against operators who would optimize Sharpe at the cost of larger drawdowns (which is bad for halal-trader users sensitive to capital preservation). Pure-Python (stdlib `math` + `dataclasses` + `enum`); no scipy / numpy. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 44 tests cover: ComparisonVerdict + policy validation (alpha bounds; min_samples ≥ 2; non-negative effect_size); BacktestResult validation including **negative drawdown rejected** (positive magnitude pin); compare_metric per verdict (low samples / low effect / clear A wins / clear B wins / TIE / drawdown inverted A wins / drawdown inverted B wins / zero variance equal means / custom strict policy); **Welch t-test pinned against known value** (mean diff=2 std=1 n=100 → t≈14.14); extreme t → tiny p; identical means → p=1.0; Cohen's d sign + magnitude pinned (d=1.0 for mean diff=1.0 std=1.0); compare_backtests A clearly wins all 4 metrics; B clearly wins all 4; **inconclusive when any metric inconclusive (overall_verdict pin)**; mixed 2-2 split → TIE; same strategy_id rejected; **drawdown inverted in overall pin** (A wins lower drawdown → counts as A_WINS in aggregate); StrategyComparison overall_verdict tests (any inconclusive → INCONCLUSIVE; A majority + no losses → A_WINS; 2-2 split → TIE; all tie → TIE); render with verdict emoji 🅰️/🅱️/🟰/❓; render no-secret regression (no `raw_returns` / `trades_list` / `broker_id`); e2e flows (momentum_v2 clearly beats momentum on all 4 metrics → B_WINS; 30-trade pilot → INCONCLUSIVE — wait for more data; replay consistency). The Wave 4.F walk-forward gate integration (gate keys on `compare_backtests` for promotion decisions), the FastAPI `/api/strategies/compare` endpoint that takes two strategy IDs + returns the comparison JSON, the dashboard "A/B comparison" tile, and the integration with Wave 4.B genetic strategy generator (auto-compare each new candidate against the current production strategy and only promote on clear-winner verdict) all deferred to follow-ups — comparator verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 Wave 4.G aux — Portfolio risk aggregator + pre-trade gate** — `ml/risk_aggregator.py` is the account-level complement to Wave 4.G's per-symbol HRP weights and the crypto monitor's per-position SL/TP enforcement. The cycle's `crypto/cycle.py` runs a portfolio risk engine (correlation/heat/drawdown) inline; this module factors out the canonical "what's our total at-risk capital?" view and adds a **forward-looking pre-trade gate** that simulates the post-trade state to answer "can we afford this new buy?". Picked a focused aggregator over scattering the risk math because (a) the pre-trade gate is the load-bearing safety check before placing a buy — a single function `evaluate_pre_trade_gate(...)` that the executor calls before `place_order` means a single inspectable check rather than scattered conditionals across the cycle / executor / monitor layers; (b) the account-level caps (max total at-risk %, max single-position %, max position count) are the structural guards against the concentration failure modes — encoding them as a frozen policy with constructor validation means a misconfigured "let me put 50% in one symbol" gets caught at the gate rather than after the order ships; (c) the aggregation is pure: deterministic for given (positions, account_value), so the dashboard's "account risk" tile is inspectable + replay-able for the audit trail. Five composed surfaces. (1) `RiskGateOutcome` enum (APPROVED / REJECTED_TOTAL_RISK / REJECTED_SINGLE_POSITION / REJECTED_POSITION_COUNT) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. The three rejection outcomes are distinct so the operator's exception handler can render per-outcome guidance ("you're at the position-count cap; close one before adding new" vs "this single position would risk 5% which exceeds the 2% cap; reduce notional"). (2) `RiskPolicy` ships defaults: 6% total at-risk + 2% per-position + 20 positions max. The defaults match the conventional retail risk cap ("no more than 6% of capital at risk across all open positions") used by Sharpe-optimizing literature. The validation enforces a structural invariant: **single-position cap can't exceed the total cap** — pinned because a misconfiguration like "20% single, 5% total" is contradictory (a single position can't risk more than the total cap allows). (3) `Position` carries symbol + notional_usd + entry_price + stop_loss_price. The validation enforces **long-only at this layer** (SL strictly below entry) — short positions are a deferred follow-up that would invert the SL relationship; pinning long-only structurally prevents a contributor from accidentally configuring a "short with SL above entry" position that the per-position risk math would compute incorrectly. (4) `at_risk_usd(position)` computes `notional × (entry - SL) / entry` — the canonical "if SL hits, how much capital lost?" math. The formula is pinned via known-result test ($1000 × (100-95)/100 = $50). The proportional-to-notional pin (a $1000 position at 5% stop loses 10× a $100 position at the same stop) is also pinned. (5) `aggregate_risk(positions, *, account_value_usd)` returns `RiskSnapshot` with: position_count + total_notional_usd + total_at_risk_usd + total_at_risk_pct + max_single_position_risk_pct + largest_position_symbol + largest_position_risk_usd. Pure function: same input → same output; the dashboard tile renders deterministic numbers from the snapshot. `evaluate_pre_trade_gate(*, open_positions, new_position, account_value_usd, policy)` is the forward-looking gate — simulates the post-trade state by computing `projected_count = current + 1`, `projected_total_risk = current_risk + new_risk`, and checking all three caps. Returns `RiskGateDecision` with outcome + actionable message + projected_total_at_risk_pct. The check order matters and is pinned: position count first, then single-position, then total — the "position-count-first" priority pin ensures that an obviously-too-many-positions request gets the position-count rejection (not a single-position-size rejection that would leave the operator confused about whether reducing notional would help). **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Per-position risk = notional × (entry − SL) / entry.** The known-result pin ($1000 × 5/100 = $50) protects against accidental algorithm drift. The formula assumes long positions (SL below entry); the position-validation invariant guarantees this. (2) **Account-level caps: 6% total / 2% single / 20 positions.** Operator-tunable, but the defaults are pinned and match the conventional retail-risk literature. The structural pin "single ≤ total" prevents misconfiguration. (3) **Pre-trade gate is forward-looking.** Simulates post-trade state rather than checking current state. The pin matters because checking current state would always pass (the bot wouldn't be in a state of breach); the operator-protective question is "would adding this trade put us in breach?" — which only the forward-looking simulation answers correctly. (4) **All cap boundaries inclusive — APPROVED at exactly cap.** A new position whose addition brings total to exactly 6% is APPROVED (=, not >); pinned both directions per cap. The pin matters because asymmetric boundary handling is a common bug, and a strict-greater check would cause flicker at the cap. (5) **Render output never includes broker account numbers, position IDs, or operator-side fields.** The dataclass shape doesn't carry those fields; the render shows symbols + USD amounts + percentages. The render-no-leak regression test asserts no `account_id` / `broker_id` / `position_id` / `@` (no email) substrings appear. Halal alignment: the conservative-default 6%/2%/20 caps reflect the operator-protective bias of the rest of the platform — halal-trader users sensitive to capital preservation get structural protection against over-concentration. The pre-trade gate prevents the "I clicked place-order on a too-large position" failure mode that would lose halal-trader capital with no recourse. The single-position cap matches the practical concern that even a halal-screened position can lose unexpectedly (operator news, sudden NPI breach, market regime change), so concentration is risk-additive regardless of compliance. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 46 tests cover: RiskGateOutcome enum string-value pin; **6%/2%/20 default policy pin**; policy validation (zero / above-1 total cap rejected; **single > total cap rejection pin**; zero position count rejected; immutable); Position validation including **long-only SL-strictly-below-entry pin both directions** (SL=entry rejected; SL>entry rejected); immutable; at_risk_usd known-result ($50/$10/$200) + proportional-to-notional; aggregate_risk empty / single / multi / largest-identified pin; deterministic; rejects zero or negative account; RiskSnapshot validation including non-negative pin; immutable; pre-trade gate APPROVED on clean book; **REJECTED_SINGLE_POSITION when 5% > 2% cap**; **2% boundary inclusive APPROVED pin** (exact boundary accepted); **REJECTED_TOTAL_RISK when projected 7% > 6% cap**; **6% total boundary inclusive APPROVED pin**; **REJECTED_POSITION_COUNT 21 > 20 pin**; **20 boundary inclusive APPROVED pin**; **position-count-first priority pin** (count breach + single breach → POSITION_COUNT outcome); custom strict 1%/0.5%/10 policy flows through; decision message non-empty; rejects zero account; render snapshot with $-amounts + percentages + no-largest-shows-dash; render no-secret regression (no `account_id` / `broker_id` / `position_id` / `@`); render decision approved with ✅; per-outcome emoji distinct; e2e flows (realistic $100k account 5×1% existing + 0.5% new = 5.5% → APPROVED with projected total 5.5%; over-concentrated single 4% rejected; replay consistency). The executor pre-submit hook (`crypto/executor.py:execute_plan` calls `evaluate_pre_trade_gate` before `_place_order`), the dashboard "account risk" tile (renders `RiskSnapshot` with at-glance risk percentage), the AlertSink integration (fires WARN when total_at_risk_pct > 4%, PAGE when > 5%), and the operator email summary integration (Wave 5.I includes daily account-risk summary) all deferred to follow-ups — aggregator + gate verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 aux — Settings drift detector** — `ops/settings_drift.py` is the operator's audit primitive answering "which knobs have I tuned away from defaults?". The bot's Settings model has 80+ knobs (LLM provider, broker keys, tier caps, risk thresholds); operators typically tune 5-10 for their deployment, but a misconfigured override can silently weaken the whole stack. Picked a focused detector over operators eyeballing their `.env` because (a) the .env shows what the operator set but not what *differs* from the codebase default — a value of "0.05" might be the default OR an aggressive override, and the drift report makes that distinction explicit; (b) magnitude classification (TINY / MODERATE / SIGNIFICANT / EXTREME) lets the dashboard prioritize which drifts matter — a 0.001 lr override is irrelevant; a 50% position cap is dangerous, and the report routes attention accordingly; (c) numeric bounds catch operator typos at audit time — a bot configured with max_position_pct=5.0 (operator typed 500% expecting 5%) is an obvious mistake the bounds detection surfaces as EXTREME+OUT_OF_BOUNDS rather than letting the config ship live. Five composed surfaces. (1) `DriftMagnitude` enum (NONE / TINY / MODERATE / SIGNIFICANT / EXTREME) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. The five-tier ladder gives operators a coarse-but-useful priority signal — "show me everything ≥ MODERATE" filters out cosmetic tweaks while surfacing aggressive overrides. (2) `NumericBounds` carries `[min_value, max_value]` with `contains(value)` returning bounds-inclusive; constructor rejects `max <= min`. The bounds-inclusive boundary (≤ both ends) is intentional — values exactly at the boundary are valid, not edge-case "almost out of bounds". (3) `SettingSpec` carries name + default_value + description + optional bounds + is_secret. Validation enforces structural invariants: empty name / description rejected; **bounds only valid on numeric defaults** (string + bounds combination is meaningless); **default itself must be within declared bounds** (a contributor that set `default=2.0, bounds=[0, 1]` would have shipped a guaranteed-out-of-bounds default). (4) `detect_drift_for_setting(spec, current_value)` dispatches by type (bool / numeric / string), each with its own classification logic. **Type mismatch raises TypeError** rather than silently coercing — a contributor that passed `1` for a bool setting would create a confused state. The numeric classifier handles the `default == 0` edge case (would divide by zero) by falling back to absolute-magnitude bands. The boolean classifier returns MODERATE on any flip (any boolean change is potentially material). The string classifier returns MODERATE on changes between two non-empty values, but **SIGNIFICANT on empty→set or set→empty** transitions (the typical case is a credential being set or unset, which is operationally important). (5) `build_drift_report(catalogue, current_values)` is the entry-point that runs detect_drift_for_setting across the catalogue. **Every catalogued setting must be in current_values** (raises KeyError on missing — operators must explicitly provide every value, no silent fallback to defaults that would mask drift); **operator-defined env vars not in the catalogue are silently ignored** (the closed-catalogue pin keeps the report focused on managed settings). The returned entries are sorted by setting name for deterministic display. Filter helpers: `filter_drifted(report, *, minimum=DriftMagnitude.TINY)` returns entries at or above the threshold magnitude — operators iterate at MODERATE+ to skip cosmetic drift. Render helpers: `render_entry` emits per-entry line with magnitude emoji + name + values + out-of-bounds marker; `render_report` emits the full audit. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **DriftMagnitude is closed-set with five tiers.** TINY (within 10% numeric) / MODERATE (10-50% / boolean flip / non-empty string change) / SIGNIFICANT (50-100% / empty↔set string) / EXTREME (>100% / out-of-bounds). Each tier's threshold is pinned in tests. (2) **Numeric bounds enforce hard invariants.** A setting declared with bounds `[0.001, 0.5]` flags any value outside as EXTREME + out_of_bounds=True. Pinned via the realistic "max_position_pct=5.0" operator-typo test. (3) **Settings catalogue is closed.** Only catalogued settings appear in the drift report — operator-defined custom env vars (e.g. `MY_DEBUG_VAR`) are silently ignored. The pin matters because operators add ad-hoc env vars for debugging; the drift report shouldn't surface them as "drifted" since they have no canonical default. (4) **Type mismatch raises TypeError.** A bool setting with `1` as current value, a numeric setting with `"fast"` — both raise TypeError rather than silently coerce. The structural pin protects against operator-config bugs. (5) **Render output never includes API keys, broker secrets, or vault references.** Sensitive settings tagged `is_secret=True` render as `<secret>` placeholder; the comparator still runs against the actual value to detect drift, but the rendered output never contains the secret. The render-no-leak regression test asserts a specific decoy `sk_live_VERYSENSITIVE12345` value never appears in the rendered output even though it would be the "current" value. Halal alignment: the bounds detection protects halal-trader operators from misconfiguring risk caps in ways that would let the bot trade at unsafe sizes. The secret masking protects broker API keys + LLM API keys + vault references from leaking into operator-shared audit logs. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `typing` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 55 tests cover: DriftMagnitude enum string-value pins; NumericBounds inclusive-boundary + max-at-min + max-below-min rejections + immutable; SettingSpec validation including **bounds-on-string rejected** + **default-out-of-its-own-bounds rejected** + immutable; detect_drift_for_setting boolean (no-drift / flip=MODERATE / non-bool TypeError); string (no-drift / change=MODERATE / **empty↔set=SIGNIFICANT credential pin**); numeric across all 5 magnitude bands (default=1.0: 1.05=TINY, 1.3=MODERATE, 1.75=SIGNIFICANT, 3.0=EXTREME); negative-direction symmetric (0.3 from default 1.0 → 70% drift = SIGNIFICANT); **default=0 special-cased to absolute bands**; int default works (64→128 = exactly 100% rel_drift = SIGNIFICANT, the ">1.0 = EXTREME" boundary is exclusive); bool not treated as numeric int 0/1 (TypeError); **out-of-bounds high + low both EXTREME pin**; within-bounds uses normal magnitude; bounds boundary inclusive; DriftEntry validation; DriftReport invariants (drifted ≤ total; out_of_bounds ≤ drifted); build_report no drift + some drift + **missing setting raises KeyError** + **extra keys silently ignored** + entries sorted by name + out_of_bounds_count tracked + deterministic; filter_drifted default includes TINY+ + minimum=SIGNIFICANT excludes lower; render entry with magnitude emoji + secret placeholder + out-of-bounds marker + long-string truncation to 37 chars + "..."; render report no-drift "no drift detected" + with-drift; **render no-secret-leak pin** (sk_live key never in output, only `<secret>`); e2e flows (realistic 5-setting audit with secret masked correctly + `max_position_pct=5.0` typo caught as EXTREME+out-of-bounds + 4 of 5 settings drifted in the cohort; replay consistency). The integration with `Settings` model + the `halal-trader settings drift` CLI command + the dashboard "settings drift" tile all deferred to follow-ups — detector verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 aux — Deprecation policy + sunset timeline engine** — `ops/deprecation.py` is the sunset-lifecycle complement to Wave 9.F's API reference. Wave 9.F surfaces what's currently public in the API docs; this module is the **pure-Python lifecycle engine** that tracks how a public symbol moves from "announced as deprecated" through "actively deprecated" through "removed" with deterministic timeline enforcement so operators can't accidentally remove an API before users have had time to migrate. Picked a focused engine over scattered `@deprecated` decorators because (a) the sunset timeline (announced → 60 days → deprecated → 90 days → removed) needs deterministic enforcement: the removal-readiness gate answers "is symbol X past its scheduled removal date?" without operator interpretation, so the dashboard tile can surface "X has been REMOVED for 14 days but still in the codebase — safe to hard-delete" rather than requiring the operator to compute timeline math; (b) the structured per-symbol record gives the API reference layer something to surface ("this method was announced as deprecated on 2026-Q1, will be removed by 2026-Q3") so users planning their migration see clear timing; (c) the warning-emission classification (no warning during ANNOUNCED window; DeprecationWarning during DEPRECATED; RuntimeError during REMOVED) is a single inspectable rule rather than a scattered conditional in each deprecated function — operators understand the contract once, and contributors can't accidentally fire DeprecationWarning during the announce grace period (which would surprise users). Six composed surfaces. (1) `DeprecationStage` enum (ANNOUNCED / DEPRECATED / REMOVED) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability + module-level `_STAGE_ORDER` tuple for forward-only progression. (2) `DeprecationPolicy` ships defaults: 60-day announce + 90-day deprecated = 150-day total sunset. The validation enforces minimum **30-day announce + 60-day deprecated** — pinned because users need migration time; an operator that "let me deprecate over a week" would break library consumers without enough warning. The 60-day announce default matches the typical industry standard (Python's PEP 387 backwards compatibility policy uses similar windows). (3) `DeprecatedSymbol` carries symbol + announced_at + stage + optional replacement + migration_url + reason. The optional fields are intentionally optional — sometimes operators deprecate without a replacement (the feature is just gone), but when there is a replacement, it surfaces in render and in the warning message. (4) `announce_deprecation(*, symbol, now, ...)` creates the initial ANNOUNCED record. `advance_stage(record, *, now)` enforces strict forward-only one-step progression; **REMOVED is terminal** (cannot advance from REMOVED). The metadata (replacement / migration_url / reason) carries forward through stage transitions — pinned via test that an ANNOUNCED record's replacement still surfaces in DEPRECATED + REMOVED records. (5) `scheduled_deprecated_at(record)` and `scheduled_removal_at(record)` compute the timeline dates from `announced_at + announce_window` and `+ deprecated_window`. `is_overdue_for_advancement(record, *, now, policy)` flags records past their scheduled date — boundary inclusive (`now >= scheduled`) so exactly at the 60-day mark IS overdue. The pin matters because asymmetric boundary handling could let a record sit in ANNOUNCED "almost" forever; the inclusive boundary surfaces it the moment it should advance. REMOVED records are never overdue (terminal). (6) `emit_warning_if_needed(record)` emits DeprecationWarning ONLY in the DEPRECATED stage. ANNOUNCED stage is the silent grace period (operators document the deprecation but don't yet warn users); REMOVED stage doesn't warn — callers should `assert_not_removed(record)` first to raise `SymbolRemovedError`.
