The split between warning and error is the load-bearing safety pattern: a DEPRECATED symbol still works (with warning); a REMOVED symbol fails fast (with error). `SymbolRemovedError` inherits `RuntimeError` so callers' generic exception handlers catch it; the `symbol`, `replacement`, and `migration_url` attributes let the dashboard surface "caller X still uses removed symbol Y; migrate to Z". `filter_overdue(records, *, now, policy)` returns overdue records sorted by `announced_at` ascending — pinned so operators tackle the longest-overdue first. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set DeprecationStage enum, forward-only with REMOVED terminal.** Cannot skip ANNOUNCED → REMOVED (must DEPRECATE first); cannot revert; cannot advance from REMOVED. (2) **Default sunset policy: 60d + 90d = 150d total.** Validation enforces minimum 30d announce + 60d deprecated. The minimums protect against operator misconfiguration that would shorten user migration time. (3) **Warning emission per stage is the contract.** ANNOUNCED → silent (grace period); DEPRECATED → DeprecationWarning fires with migration_url; REMOVED → no warning, raise SymbolRemovedError instead. The split is structural — `emit_warning_if_needed` and `assert_not_removed` are separate functions so callers can compose them as `assert_not_removed(record); emit_warning_if_needed(record)` to get fail-fast on REMOVED + warn on DEPRECATED. (4) **Removal-readiness boundary inclusive at scheduled date.** A record at exactly its scheduled removal date IS overdue; the dashboard surfaces it for advancement. The boundary is `>= scheduled`, pinned both directions (60d → True; 59d → False). (5) **Render output never includes operator email / Slack handles.** The dataclass deliberately doesn't carry support contacts; only the public migration_url surfaces. The render-no-leak regression test asserts no `@` / `slack` / `email` substrings appear. Halal alignment: when the bot's halal screener changes its public API (e.g. renaming `screen_with_zoya` → `screen_with_consensus`), the deprecation engine ensures users running on older docs get migration time + clear pointers to the new API rather than hitting silent breakage that could affect their halal-compliance verification. The 60-day announce window matches the typical scholar review cadence — gives reviewers time to update their compliance documents to reference the new API. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `warnings` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 48 tests cover: DeprecationStage enum string-value pins; **60d announce + 90d deprecated default pin** (matches industry-standard sunset windows); **minimum 30d announce / 60d deprecated rejected pin** both directions; immutable; DeprecatedSymbol validation; announce + with-replacement; advance_stage forward-only (ANNOUNCED→DEPRECATED, full lifecycle; **REMOVED-is-terminal pin**; metadata carries forward); scheduled_deprecated_at + scheduled_removal_at math; custom policy flows; **is_overdue boundary inclusive at 60d / 150d both directions pinned** (60d overdue, 59d not); REMOVED never overdue; **no warning in ANNOUNCED stage** (silent grace period pin); **DeprecationWarning fires in DEPRECATED stage** with replacement + migration_url visible in message; **no warning in REMOVED** (callers should use assert_not_removed instead); assert_not_removed passes on ANNOUNCED + DEPRECATED + raises SymbolRemovedError on REMOVED carrying symbol + replacement + migration_url; **SymbolRemovedError inherits RuntimeError** so generic except clauses catch it; works without replacement (just-gone features); filter_overdue returns only overdue + sorted by announced_at ascending (oldest first — operators tackle longest-overdue first); render with stage emoji 📣/⚠️/🗑️ + scheduled date for ANNOUNCED (next-step DEPRECATED) and DEPRECATED (next-step REMOVED) but NOT for REMOVED (no future steps); replacement / migration_url / reason rendered when set + omitted when empty; **render no-secret leak pin** (no `@` / `slack` / `email`); e2e flows (full sunset Q1 announce → 60d advance to DEPRECATED → 150d advance to REMOVED with SymbolRemovedError on use; warning emission during DEPRECATED with migration link visible in captured warning message; replay consistency). The integration with the `@deprecated` decorator (wraps target function with `assert_not_removed` + `emit_warning_if_needed`), the build-time check that fails CI when a REMOVED symbol is still imported anywhere in the codebase, the dashboard "deprecation queue" tile (renders `filter_overdue` output sorted by oldest), and the auto-generated CHANGELOG entries (each stage transition logs to a structured changelog) all deferred to follow-ups — engine verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 aux — Scholar consultation calendar** — `halal/scholar_calendar.py` is the cadence-meeting scheduler that complements Wave 2.F scholar review (ad-hoc verdict workflow) and Wave 11.B SSB governance (structured board meetings). The bot needs both *event-driven* reviews (exception queue triggers a verdict request) AND *cadence-driven* reviews (annual compliance audit, quarterly portfolio review); this module ships the cadence side with deterministic scheduling, a 30d/7d/1d reminder ladder, and a special 60-day confirmation deadline for annual audits. Picked a focused calendar over generic ical / Google Calendar because (a) the consultation kinds have very different cadence + lead-time requirements: an annual audit needs months of advance scheduling, a quarterly review needs ~2 weeks, an ad-hoc may need same-week turnaround — encoding the cadence as policy means the dashboard surfaces "your next quarterly review is overdue" without operator interpretation; (b) the reminder ladder is the load-bearing "will the scholar actually show up?" attribute — encoding it explicitly means a missed reminder gets caught at the audit-trail layer rather than after the consultation date passes; (c) the deterministic state transitions mirror the lifecycle pattern used in 8.E incident-response and 6.I distillation deployment, giving operators one mental model. Five composed surfaces. (1) `ConsultationKind` enum (ANNUAL_AUDIT / QUARTERLY_REVIEW / AD_HOC) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability — three kinds matches the documented cadence; adding a kind is a code review change. (2) `ConsultationStatus` enum (SCHEDULED → CONFIRMED → COMPLETED + terminal CANCELLED) with module-level `_HAPPY_PATH_ORDER` tuple. SCHEDULED means the slot is booked but the scholar hasn't confirmed; CONFIRMED means the scholar locked it in; COMPLETED means the meeting happened and minutes are recorded. (3) `CalendarPolicy` ships defaults: `reminder_lead_times=(30d, 7d, 1d)` + `annual_confirm_lead_time=60d`. The validation enforces descending order on lead times (a contributor that put 7d before 30d would create a confused reminder ladder); rejects empty lead-times, non-positive leads, zero annual confirm. The 30d/7d/1d ladder matches standard cadence-meeting best-practice (early, standard, last-minute). (4) `Consultation` carries consultation_id + kind + scholar_handle (the scholar's public identifier, NOT contact email — operator-side state) + scheduled_at + status + topic + optional minutes_url. Validation enforces tz-aware datetimes, non-empty fields, and the load-bearing **COMPLETED-requires-minutes-url + non-COMPLETED-must-not-have-it** invariant in both directions: a COMPLETED row without a minutes URL is missing its audit trail (a contributor that "marked it done" without recording what was discussed is making the audit useless); a SCHEDULED row with a pre-set minutes URL is a confused state (no minutes exist yet). (5) `is_due_for_reminder(consultation, *, now, last_reminder_at, policy)` walks the threshold ladder: for each lead-time, computes `threshold = scheduled_at - lead`; if `now >= threshold` AND `last_reminder_at < threshold` (or None), returns True. Only SCHEDULED + CONFIRMED states fire reminders (COMPLETED + CANCELLED are skipped). The "last_reminder_at < threshold" check ensures we don't re-fire for a threshold we already reminded for. `annual_audit_overdue_for_confirmation` is the special-case gate: an ANNUAL_AUDIT still in SCHEDULED at the 60d-before-scheduled mark flags overdue (scholar calendars fill up; if they haven't confirmed by 60 days out, the operator should escalate). The boundary is inclusive (`now >= deadline`). **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **State machine SCHEDULED → CONFIRMED → COMPLETED forward-only.** Cannot revert; CANCELLED is terminal from any pre-COMPLETED state but cannot transition from COMPLETED. (2) **Reminder ladder 30d / 7d / 1d in descending order.** The constructor enforces ordering; the runtime `is_due_for_reminder` walks the ladder threshold-by-threshold. The "last_reminder at the active threshold means we already fired" semantics is pinned via test (last_reminder=T0 + scheduled=T0+7d → not due because the 7d threshold = T0 was already crossed and reminded for). (3) **Annual audit must be CONFIRMED at least 60 days before scheduled.** A SCHEDULED ANNUAL_AUDIT at 60d out flags overdue; pinned both directions (60d → True; 61d → False). The pin matters because scholar calendars fill up months in advance, and finding out at 30d that the scholar can't make it is operationally too late. (4) **COMPLETED requires minutes_url; non-COMPLETED must NOT have it.** Structural invariant in both directions. The audit trail is the load-bearing record of what was discussed; a COMPLETED row without minutes is missing its purpose. (5) **Render output never includes scholar contact emails or meeting URLs.** The dataclass deliberately doesn't carry those fields (operator-side state held in their CRM); render shows only `scholar_handle` + `topic` + `scheduled_at` + the `minutes_url` for COMPLETED records (the public audit link). Render-no-leak regression asserts no `@` / `zoom.us` / `meet.google` substrings appear. Halal alignment: the module respects the conservative-default bias of the rest of the platform — the 60-day annual-audit confirmation window prevents the operator from finding out at the last minute that their compliance audit can't happen, which would create a gap in the halal-compliance audit trail visible to scholars and regulators. The minutes_url requirement guarantees the audit trail is honest (the operator can't claim a consultation happened without producing the minutes); pinned structurally rather than by convention. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / calendar SDK. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 60 tests cover: ConsultationKind + ConsultationStatus enum string-value pins; **30d/7d/1d reminder ladder + 60d annual confirm default pins**; **descending-order lead-times pin** (7d before 30d rejected with explicit "descending" message); zero-lead rejected; Consultation validation including **COMPLETED-requires-minutes-url + non-COMPLETED-must-not-have-it both directions pinned**; immutable; schedule_consultation rejects past + now-equal dates; rejects naive datetimes for scheduled_at and now; lifecycle SCHEDULED → CONFIRMED → COMPLETED happy path with metadata carried; cancel from any pre-COMPLETED; **revert from COMPLETED rejected pin**; cancel-already-cancelled rejected; reminder ladder pins (due at 30d threshold; not due at 31d; due at 7d threshold if 30d already fired; **not-due if last_reminder AT or past active threshold pin**; due at 1d boundary); COMPLETED + CANCELLED never fire reminders; **annual-audit overdue at 60d boundary inclusive pin** both directions (60d → True; 61d → False); only ANNUAL_AUDIT triggers the check (QUARTERLY_REVIEW at 10d-out doesn't); CONFIRMED audits never overdue; filter_due_for_reminder returns sorted by scheduled_at ascending (sooner first); **last_reminders dict suppresses already-fired reminders pin**; upcoming within 90d horizon excludes COMPLETED + CANCELLED + sorted ascending; custom horizon excludes 30d-out for 14d horizon; zero horizon rejected; render with kind + status emojis + minutes when COMPLETED + omitted otherwise + **no-secret-leak pin** (no `@` / `zoom.us` / `meet.google`); e2e flows (annual audit full lifecycle Q1 schedule 90d-out → 30d-later confirm → day-of complete with minutes URL recorded; **overdue annual-audit at 50d-out caught pin**; reminder ladder fires at 30d threshold then re-fires at 7d threshold after 23 more days; replay consistency). The Wave 2.F exception queue integration (auto-schedules AD_HOC consultations when the queue exceeds threshold), the Wave 11.B SSB governance integration (per-meeting consultation records), the dashboard "scholar calendar" tile (renders `upcoming` + `filter_due_for_reminder` outputs), the operator email summary (Wave 5.I) integration that surfaces overdue annual audits, and the `halal-trader scholar consult --schedule` CLI command all deferred to follow-ups — calendar verified in isolation first so the integration sees a stable contract.

* **Round-4 aux — Pre-flight check engine** — `ops/preflight.py` complements the bot's startup sequence. Before the first cycle runs, the bot needs to verify every critical dependency is wired correctly: secrets vault returns valid keys, DB is reachable + at the right schema revision, broker plugin can authenticate, halal screener is responsive, alert router has at least one reachable channel. Each check runs independently and reports PASS / WARN / CRITICAL; the engine aggregates into a unified pre-flight report. Picked a focused engine over scattered startup logging because (a) the "are all systems go?" question is the load-bearing operator decision before letting the bot trade real money — a single inspectable report ("✅ all critical checks passed") is far more reliable than reading 30 lines of startup log scrolling past, and a critical failure ("❌ DB at wrong schema revision — run migrations first") needs to surface immediately rather than get buried in info-level startup chatter; (b) the severity ladder (INFO / WARN / CRITICAL) lets operators distinguish "everything's fine" from "operator-tunable optimization opportunity" from "DO NOT START THE BOT"; (c) the report is structured so the dashboard's "system status" tile + the operator email summary + the kill-switch's safety gate all consult the same source rather than re-implementing the check. Six composed surfaces. (1) `CheckSeverity` enum (INFO < WARN < CRITICAL) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. INFO checks are documentation-only (always pass even on negative result); WARN checks log but don't fail the report; CRITICAL checks fail the report. The three-tier ladder matches the standard observability convention but is pinned to a closed set so a contributor can't slip in a "FATAL" or "DEBUG" tier without a code review. (2) `CheckOutcome` enum (PASSED / WARNED / FAILED) — the per-check outcome after applying severity logic to the boolean result. PASSED includes both genuinely-passing checks AND failed-but-informational checks (a failed INFO check is still "passing" by design — INFO is documentation-only). (3) `CheckSpec` frozen dataclass carries name + description + severity, with empty-string rejection on both name and description. The name is operator-facing identifier (`db_reachable`, `secrets_vault_valid`); description is what the check verifies. (4) `CheckResult` frozen dataclass carries spec + passed bool + non-empty message. The `outcome` property maps (passed, severity) → CheckOutcome via four cases: passed=True → PASSED regardless of severity; passed=False + INFO → PASSED (info-failure is documented but doesn't block); passed=False + WARN → WARNED; passed=False + CRITICAL → FAILED. The non-empty message invariant ensures the report always has actionable text — a passing check might say "DB reachable at localhost:5433", a warning "broker rate limit at 80%", a failure "secrets vault returned no key for DATABASE_URL". (5) `PreflightReport` frozen dataclass aggregates results tuple + counts. The `passed_count + warned_count + failed_count == len(results)` invariant is checked in `__post_init__` (a contributor that builds a report manually can't ship inconsistent counts). The load-bearing **`is_safe_to_start` property returns `failed_count == 0`** — the gate the cycle's startup sequence and the kill-switch's safety check both consult. WARN-level issues don't block startup; only CRITICAL does. (6) `run_checks(checks, *, fail_fast=False)` runs each (spec, runner) tuple. Runner returns `(passed, message)`; if runner raises, the engine catches and treats as `passed=False, message="check runner raised: <exc!r>"` so a buggy check doesn't crash the entire pre-flight engine. Results are sorted by spec name for deterministic ordering — the same set of checks always produces the same report shape regardless of execution order, which matters for diff-stable reporting. `fail_fast=True` stops on first CRITICAL failure (useful for fast-feedback CI runs); default is False (run every check for full report). **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set CheckSeverity ladder.** A contributor that wants a "FATAL" or "DEBUG" tier needs a code review; the closed enum prevents silent severity inflation/deflation. (2) **Per-severity outcome mapping pinned in all four directions.** passed=True regardless of severity → PASSED; failed/INFO → PASSED (info checks never fail the report); failed/WARN → WARNED; failed/CRITICAL → FAILED. The mapping is tested in both directions to catch inversion bugs. (3) **fail_fast stops on CRITICAL but not WARN.** A WARN failure with fail_fast=True does NOT stop iteration — that's the difference between "report has issues" and "stop the bot from starting." (4) **Deterministic ordering by spec.name.** The same set of checks always produces the same report regardless of operator-supplied order; this matters for diff-stable display in the dashboard tile and the operator email summary. (5) **Render output never includes raw error messages from check runners.** Each CheckResult carries a high-level operator-facing message ("DB reachable at localhost:5433"); raw stack traces / API responses go to the operator's debug log. The render-no-leak pin is regression-tested against API tokens / connection strings appearing in the rendered output. The load-bearing `is_safe_to_start` gate keys on zero CRITICAL failures: WARN-level issues are surfaced in the dashboard tile but don't block startup. The runner-exception-captured-as-failed behavior means a buggy check (e.g., a thrown `ConnectionError`) doesn't crash the pre-flight engine itself — the operator sees "check X failed to run: ConnectionError(...)" in the report rather than a stack trace from the bot's startup code. Render with outcome emoji (✅/⚠️/❌) + per-section ordering (failures first → warnings → passed) so operators see blockers at-a-glance. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async — runners are operator-supplied closures (because they touch DB / network); the engine just composes. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 38 tests cover: enum string-value pins; CheckSpec validation (empty name + empty description rejected); **outcome mapping all four (passed, severity) combinations**; frozen dataclass invariants on CheckSpec / CheckResult / PreflightReport; **count-consistency invariant pin** (passed+warned+failed must equal len(results), mismatch raises ValueError); **is_safe_to_start gates only on CRITICAL pin** (warning-only report still safe; report with one CRITICAL not safe; report with WARN+CRITICAL not safe); run_checks empty / all-passing / one-failure / warning / info-failure (info-failure becomes PASSED); **runner exception captured as failure pin** (runner raising ValueError doesn't crash the engine; result has `passed=False, message="check runner raised: ValueError(...)"`); sorted-by-name determinism (operators supply checks in arbitrary order; report sorted alphabetically); **fail_fast stops on CRITICAL pin** (3-check sequence with CRITICAL second halts); **fail_fast does NOT stop on WARN pin** (3-check sequence with WARN second runs all 3); default fail_fast=False runs every check; critical_failures filter (returns only FAILED); warnings_only filter (returns only WARNED); render top-line ALL GO (zero warned + zero failed) / GO with N warnings (zero failed) / NO-GO with N critical failures (failed > 0); render lists failures first → warnings → passed in that order; **no-secret-leak pin** (raw API token / connection string in runner exception captured as `passed=False` doesn't render — only the high-level summary message; regression test asserts no `sk_live_` / `password=` substrings in render); e2e realistic 6-check startup sequence (secrets_vault PASS + db_reachable PASS + db_schema PASS + broker_auth PASS + halal_screener WARN + alert_router CRITICAL → NO-GO with 1 critical failure surfaced); replay consistency (same operations → equal report). The `halal-trader preflight` CLI command (renders the report and exits with code 1 on NO-GO), the `BaseTradingBot.initialize()` integration (calls `run_checks` before the first cycle and refuses to start on NO-GO), the dashboard "system status" tile (consumes the report shape), the operator email summary (Wave 5.I) integration that surfaces NO-GO + warnings, and the per-environment check catalogue (test/staging/prod with different severity ladders) all deferred to follow-ups — engine verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-4 aux — Adapter circuit breaker** — `core/circuit_breaker.py` ships the classic three-state circuit breaker pattern as a pure-Python snapshot-based engine that broker / screener / LLM-provider adapters consult before making network calls. When an upstream is failing (rate-limited, down, slow), the bot needs to stop hammering it after N consecutive failures and let it recover before retrying — the standard CLOSED (normal) → OPEN (rejecting all calls) → HALF_OPEN (probing one or two calls to test recovery) state machine. Picked a pure-Python snapshot-based engine over a stateful object with internal timers because (a) the bot is single-threaded async on the cycle path; passing `now` explicitly makes time-based transitions trivially testable without freezegun / sleep / clocks; (b) the snapshot can be persisted to DB across restarts (a 5-minute cooldown that started 30s before a crash should still have ~4.5 minutes left after recovery — pure functions over snapshots make this work for free); (c) operators can read the current state + counters without grabbing a lock or interrupting the adapter. Nine composed surfaces. (1) `BreakerState` enum (CLOSED / OPEN / HALF_OPEN) with pinned string values for JSON / DB persistence. (2) `CallOutcome` enum (SUCCESS / FAILURE) — the per-call outcome the adapter reports. (3) `BreakerPolicy` defaults: `failure_threshold=5` + `cooldown_seconds=60` + `half_open_probe_count=2`. The defaults are tuned for "transient network blip" (a 60s cooldown is enough for a rate-limit window to clear) and "real outage" (5 consecutive failures is past the noise floor). Validation rejects zero/negative thresholds + non-positive cooldowns + zero probe counts. (4) `BreakerSnapshot` is the persistable state: state + consecutive_failures + opened_at + half_open_successes. The **OPEN-requires-opened_at** structural invariant is checked in `__post_init__` (a contributor that builds an OPEN snapshot without setting opened_at would create a snapshot that crashes `tick`); naive datetimes rejected. (5) `is_call_allowed(snapshot)` is the load-bearing gate (True for CLOSED + HALF_OPEN, False for OPEN) the adapter consults BEFORE making the actual call. (6) `record_outcome(snapshot, outcome, *, now, policy)` updates per the state machine: CLOSED + SUCCESS resets failures to 0; CLOSED + FAILURE increments and trips to OPEN at threshold; OPEN is identity (defensive — a stray outcome that arrived after the breaker tripped doesn't punish it further); HALF_OPEN + SUCCESS increments and closes at probe count (resetting all counters); HALF_OPEN + FAILURE re-opens with **fresh cooldown** (timed from the new opened_at, not the original). (7) `tick(snapshot, *, now, policy)` drives the OPEN → HALF_OPEN transition once cooldown elapses. Boundary inclusive at `now - opened_at >= cooldown` (60s exactly triggers); CLOSED + HALF_OPEN are no-ops (their transitions are outcome-driven). (8) `time_until_retry(snapshot, *, now, policy)` returns the remaining timedelta until the breaker can probe again — the dashboard tile shows "retrying in 23s". Returns `timedelta(0)` outside OPEN or after expiry. (9) `render_snapshot(snapshot, *, name, now, policy)` formats with state emoji 🟢/🔴/🟡 + retry ETA when OPEN + probe progress when HALF_OPEN. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Forward state machine: CLOSED → OPEN → HALF_OPEN → {CLOSED | OPEN}.** The only way back to CLOSED is via successful HALF_OPEN probes. CLOSED never goes directly to HALF_OPEN — that would skip the cooldown protection. (2) **OPEN → HALF_OPEN is time-driven, boundary inclusive.** The cooldown timer starts when the breaker opens; `tick(now)` transitions to HALF_OPEN when `now - opened_at >= cooldown`. The `>=` is intentional — at exactly the cooldown second the upstream is fair-game for a probe. (3) **HALF_OPEN → CLOSED requires consecutive successes.** A single failure in HALF_OPEN re-opens the breaker (with a fresh cooldown timed from the new failure, NOT the original open). The fresh-cooldown semantic matters: if the upstream is still failing 60s later, we want the next probe at 120s out, not "any moment now" — exponential-feel without compounding state. (4) **`is_call_allowed` only looks at state, never wall-clock.** The gate is purely state-driven; if the operator wants the OPEN → HALF_OPEN transition to happen, they call `tick(now)` first. This separation means an adapter that's already paid the cost of a snapshot read doesn't need to know about cooldown math. (5) **Render output never includes adapter call args / responses.** The snapshot deliberately doesn't carry these fields; render shows only state + counters + retry ETA. Adapter-side loggers handle raw API call details. The render-no-leak pin asserts no `sk_live` / `password` / `Bearer` / `Authorization` / `token` substrings can appear. The load-bearing `is_call_allowed` is the gate adapters consult BEFORE making the call: in CLOSED state calls pass through (counters track); in OPEN state calls are rejected with a clear "circuit breaker open, retry in Xs" error; in HALF_OPEN state limited probe calls test recovery. The defensive OPEN-state identity in `record_outcome` means a buggy adapter that ignored `is_call_allowed` and made a call anyway doesn't extend the cooldown — only `tick(now)` and HALF_OPEN failures move the state. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `datetime` + `enum`); no DB / network / async — `now` is passed explicitly so all time-based transitions are pure-function-testable. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 49 tests cover: BreakerState + CallOutcome enum string-value pins; BreakerPolicy default pins (5 / 60s / 2) + validation (zero/negative all rejected); policy immutability; BreakerSnapshot defaults; immutability; **negative counts rejected pin**; **OPEN-requires-opened_at structural pin**; **naive opened_at rejected pin**; is_call_allowed across all three states; **CLOSED + SUCCESS resets pin** (3 → 0); **CLOSED + FAILURE increments pin**; **CLOSED at-threshold trips OPEN pin** (5th failure with default policy → OPEN with opened_at=now); **CLOSED below-threshold stays CLOSED pin** (4th failure stays CLOSED); custom threshold (2-failure policy trips on 2nd); **OPEN identity pin both directions** (stray FAILURE no-op + stray SUCCESS no-op); HALF_OPEN + SUCCESS increments; **HALF_OPEN at-probe-count closes pin** (2nd success → CLOSED with all counters reset); **HALF_OPEN + FAILURE reopens with fresh cooldown pin** (opened_at set to current now, not the original open); custom probe count above + below threshold; **naive now rejected pin** in record_outcome and tick; tick CLOSED + HALF_OPEN no-ops; tick OPEN before cooldown stays OPEN; **tick OPEN at cooldown boundary inclusive pin** (60s exact triggers HALF_OPEN); tick after cooldown transitions; custom cooldown; time_until_retry returns 0 in CLOSED + HALF_OPEN + OPEN-after-expiry; returns remaining when OPEN before expiry; render closed clean (no failure count if zero); render closed with recent failures (count shown); render open shows retry ETA; render open at cooldown says "ready to probe"; render half_open shows probe progress (1/2); **render no-secret-leak pin** (no `sk_live` / `password` / `token` / `Authorization` / `Bearer` substrings); e2e flows (full recovery cycle 5-fail → OPEN → 70s cooldown → HALF_OPEN → 2-success → CLOSED with consecutive_failures=0; **failed-recovery pin** HALF_OPEN failure re-opens with fresh cooldown timed from the second open such that 30s into the second cooldown the breaker is still OPEN even though it would have expired from the first open; **intermittent-failures-don't-trip pin** 3 failures + 1 success + 3 failures stays CLOSED at 3 — success resets the count; replay consistency same operations → equal final state). The `BinanceAdapter`/`AlpacaAdapter` integration (each adapter holds a `BreakerSnapshot` per upstream and consults `is_call_allowed` before each call), the `core/halt.py` integration (per-adapter circuit breaker tripping should escalate to operator alert via `notifications/telegram.py`), the dashboard "adapter health" tile (renders one breaker snapshot per upstream), and DB persistence of the snapshot across bot restarts (so a cooldown that started before a crash isn't reset on restart) all deferred to follow-ups — breaker engine verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-4 aux — Idempotency key store** — `core/idempotency.py` ships the local-ledger half of retry-safe broker submission. When the bot submits an order to a broker and the network call times out, the bot needs to retry — but retrying naively could double-submit the order if the original request actually reached the broker. The standard pattern: attach an idempotency key to each request; the broker (or a local ledger) deduplicates on the key. This module ships deterministic key generation from (operation, payload) + a forward state machine PENDING → {SUCCEEDED | FAILED} + a pending-timeout reclaim path for genuinely stuck requests. Picked a pure-functional snapshot ledger over a stateful service because (a) the cycle path is single-threaded async; the ledger is read + advisory-lock + write in one shot, with no concurrent mutators; (b) snapshots are persistable to DB for cross-restart deduplication (a 30-second pending request that crashed the bot is still pending after restart — pure functions over the dict make this work for free); (c) operators can read the ledger state without grabbing a lock or interrupting the executor. Different from `web/quotas.py` (per-user rolling-window spend) and `core/circuit_breaker.py` (per-adapter outage gate); idempotency is the per-request deduplication layer above both. Eight composed surfaces. (1) `IdempotencyState` enum (PENDING / SUCCEEDED / FAILED) with pinned string values for JSON / DB persistence. Forward-only; once terminal, an entry stays terminal until evicted. (2) `IdempotencyAction` enum (PROCEED_NEW / PROCEED_RETRY / REPLAY / IN_FLIGHT_REJECT) — what the caller should do given the ledger state. PROCEED_NEW = no entry exists, claim. PROCEED_RETRY = stale PENDING or FAILED, retry. REPLAY = SUCCEEDED, return cached. IN_FLIGHT_REJECT = fresh PENDING, back off. (3) `IdempotencyPolicy` defaults: `pending_timeout_seconds=300` (long enough that a real network call can finish; short enough that a crashed caller's stuck entry doesn't block retries forever) + `entry_ttl_seconds=86400` (24h — long enough to deduplicate same-day retries; short enough to keep the ledger small). The structural invariant **`entry_ttl_seconds >= pending_timeout_seconds`** is checked in `__post_init__` (otherwise pending entries get evicted before they can be reclaimed — silent correctness bug). (4) `IdempotencyEntry` carries key + state + result (None for PENDING/FAILED, required for SUCCEEDED) + attempts (>=1) + first_seen_at + last_attempt_at + terminal_at (None for PENDING, required for terminal). Five structural invariants pinned: PENDING-must-not-have-result (no cached result before terminal); PENDING-must-not-have-terminal_at; terminal-requires-terminal_at; SUCCEEDED-requires-result (the result IS the cache); FAILED-must-not-have-result (failures don't carry partial state). The `last_attempt_at >= first_seen_at` invariant is also pinned. (5) `make_idempotency_key(operation, payload)` produces canonical SHA-256 hex (64 chars). The payload is JSON-serialized with `sort_keys=True` so dict insertion order doesn't change the key (regression-pinned: `{"a":1,"b":2}` and `{"b":2,"a":1}` produce the same key). The PayloadValue type is `str | int | float | bool | None` — nested structures not supported in v1; operator flattens before passing. (6) `decide(entries, key, *, now, policy)` is pure read returning the action: no entry → PROCEED_NEW; SUCCEEDED → REPLAY; FAILED → PROCEED_RETRY; PENDING within timeout → IN_FLIGHT_REJECT; PENDING past timeout → PROCEED_RETRY (stuck-caller reclaim, boundary inclusive at `now - last_attempt_at >= pending_timeout`). (7) `claim` marks key PENDING (creates new entry with attempts=1, or increments existing entry's attempts and resets state to PENDING preserving first_seen_at — this is critical because the entry's identity is the key + first_seen_at; subsequent attempts shouldn't change first_seen_at). `record_success(entries, key, result, *, now)` and `record_failure` mark terminal — both reject calls on already-terminal entries (forward-only state machine pin); both raise KeyError on unknown key. `replay_result` returns the cached SUCCEEDED result; raises on PENDING/FAILED. (8) `evict_expired(entries, *, now, policy)` drops entries past TTL. **TTL is computed from first_seen_at not terminal_at** (so long-lived stuck PENDING gets cleaned up) and the boundary is inclusive (entry exactly at TTL is evicted). **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Forward state machine PENDING → {SUCCEEDED | FAILED}.** No PENDING revival once terminal; no SUCCEEDED → FAILED rewrite. The forward-only constraint matters because a SUCCEEDED entry's cached result is the source of truth for "this work was done"; rewriting it to FAILED would make the original caller's view inconsistent with the ledger. (2) **Stable key generation regardless of dict insertion order.** `make_idempotency_key` uses `json.dumps(sort_keys=True)` so `{"symbol": "BTC", "qty": 0.1}` and `{"qty": 0.1, "symbol": "BTC"}` produce the same key. This matters because Python dicts preserve insertion order; without canonical sorting, two callers building the same payload could get different keys. (3) **Pending-timeout reclaim with boundary-inclusive trigger.** If a PENDING entry's `last_attempt_at` is `>= pending_timeout_seconds` ago, `decide` returns PROCEED_RETRY. The original caller likely crashed; let the retry through. The 300s default balances "real network call can finish" against "stuck entry blocking retries forever." (4) **Replay only on SUCCEEDED.** A FAILED entry returns PROCEED_RETRY (failures should retry); only SUCCEEDED entries replay the cached result. The distinction matters because a FAILED entry represents work that wasn't done — replaying its (None) result would be wrong. (5) **Render output never includes the result payload.** The payload is operator data (could contain order_id / fill_price / API tokens / secret material); render shows only key prefix + state + attempts + timestamps. The DB-side query is the audit trail — render is for ops dashboards. The render-no-leak pin asserts no `sk_live` / `order_id` / `fill_price` / `$45000` substrings can appear in the rendered output even when the result contains all of them. The TTL-from-first_seen_at semantic is load-bearing: if TTL were computed from terminal_at, a stuck PENDING entry would never expire (it has no terminal_at) — forever blocking retries from the same key. By using first_seen_at, the ledger self-cleans even in the failure mode where a PENDING never reaches terminal. The decide-then-claim two-step (rather than a fused get-or-create) means the caller can decide based on the action: PROCEED_* paths call claim, REPLAY paths call replay_result, IN_FLIGHT_REJECT paths back off. The claim function does not enforce decide's gate — it's operator-level discipline (a caller that ignores decide and claims an in-flight entry would just bump attempts; the original PENDING is logically still in flight). Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `hashlib` + `json` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 69 tests cover: state + action enum string-value pins; policy default pins (300s / 86400s) + validation (zero rejected + **TTL >= pending_timeout pin**) + immutability; key determinism + **dict-order-independent pin** + 64-char-hex pin + supports all PayloadValue types (str/int/float/bool/None) + different operations differ + different payload differs; empty + whitespace operation rejected; entry validation pinned in all 5 directions (PENDING-no-result, PENDING-no-terminal_at, terminal-requires-terminal_at, SUCCEEDED-requires-result, FAILED-no-result); **last_attempt_at >= first_seen_at pin**; **terminal_at >= last_attempt_at pin**; naive datetime rejected on every datetime field; entry immutability; decide returns PROCEED_NEW for missing key; REPLAY for SUCCEEDED; PROCEED_RETRY for FAILED; **IN_FLIGHT_REJECT for fresh PENDING within timeout pin**; **PROCEED_RETRY at pending-timeout boundary inclusive pin** (300s exact reclaims); just-below-timeout (299s) still rejects; far-past-timeout (1h) proceeds; custom timeout both directions (29s rejects, 30s reclaims with custom policy); decide naive now rejected; claim creates new entry with attempts=1 + first_seen_at=now + last_attempt_at=now; **claim increments attempts on existing entry pin** (FAILED entry re-claimed becomes PENDING with attempts=2 + first_seen_at preserved); **claim returns new dict not mutate input pin**; **claim clears terminal state pin** (re-claiming FAILED resets state=PENDING + result=None + terminal_at=None); claim naive now rejected; record_success marks terminal with result + terminal_at; **forward-only pin both functions** (cannot record_success on SUCCEEDED + cannot record_failure on terminal — both raise ValueError "forward-only"); empty result rejected on record_success; KeyError on unknown key both functions; replay returns cached; **replay only on SUCCEEDED pin** (PENDING + FAILED both rejected with "only SUCCEEDED" message); replay KeyError on unknown; evict drops old entries + keeps fresh; **TTL boundary inclusive pin** (at 86400s exact, evicted; at 86399s, kept); **TTL uses first_seen_at not terminal_at pin** (a PENDING that's been pending for >24h with last_attempt_at 1h ago still gets evicted because first_seen_at is the anchor); custom TTL; evict naive now rejected; render pending/succeeded/failed each show their emoji + state + attempt count; **render no-secret-leak pin** (entry with result containing `order_id=xyz123 fill_price=$45000 secret_token=sk_live_abc` produces render output with NONE of those substrings, only the key prefix + state + attempts + timestamps); e2e flows (first-call-succeeds happy path: PROCEED_NEW → claim → record_success → REPLAY returns cached `broker_order_id_42`; failure-retries-to-success path: claim → fail → PROCEED_RETRY → claim2 → success returns `order_99` with attempts=2; **stuck-pending-reclaimed pin** original caller crashed at T0, 6 minutes later second caller decides PROCEED_RETRY and claim returns attempts=2 + first_seen_at=T0 preserved; **concurrent-callers-blocked pin** fresh PENDING within 30 seconds blocks second caller with IN_FLIGHT_REJECT; replay consistency same operations → equal final ledger). The `BinanceAdapter.place_order` / `AlpacaAdapter.place_order` integration (each adapter calls `make_idempotency_key("place_order", {"symbol": ..., "qty": ..., "side": ..., "cycle_id": ...})` and consults `decide` before issuing the API call), the broker-side X-Idempotency-Key / clientOrderId header propagation (each adapter passes the local key as the broker's idempotency header), the DB persistence layer (snapshots reload on bot restart so a 30s pending request that crashed remains pending after restart with the original timeout still ticking), and the eviction sweeper (a per-cycle hook that calls `evict_expired` to keep the ledger small) all deferred to follow-ups — ledger verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-4 aux — Token bucket rate limiter** — `core/rate_limiter.py` ships the public reusable token bucket as the proactive complement to `core/circuit_breaker.py`. Broker / screener / LLM-provider adapters need to stay BELOW the upstream's published rate limit to avoid getting throttled in the first place; the breaker reacts AFTER a call fails (cascading-failure protection), the limiter prevents the call BEFORE it would fail (proactive throttling). The two compose: the limiter gates the call; if the limiter denies, the breaker isn't even consulted. Picked a pure-functional snapshot-based engine over a stateful object with internal timers because (a) the cycle path is single-threaded async; passing `now` explicitly makes time-based refills trivially testable without freezegun / sleep / clocks; (b) snapshots are persistable to DB across restarts (a partially-filled bucket from before a crash should still reflect the in-flight refill state — pure functions over snapshots make this work for free); (c) operators can read the current token count without grabbing a lock or interrupting the adapter. Distinct from the private `_Bucket` in `web/research_api_keys.py` (stateful, tied to the research API tier registry); this module ships the public reusable primitive. Eight composed surfaces. (1) `ConsumeOutcome` enum (ALLOWED / DENIED_INSUFFICIENT / DENIED_OVERSIZED) with pinned string values. The three-tier outcome distinguishes "wait and retry" from "this request is fundamentally too big" — operators handle them differently (the first is a transient backoff signal; the second is a programming error). (2) `BucketPolicy` carries `capacity` (max tokens, also burst size) + `refill_rate_per_sec` (steady-state replenishment). Together they encode the upstream's published rate limit (e.g., Binance 1200 weight per minute → capacity=1200, refill_rate_per_sec=20). Validation rejects zero/negative on both fields plus non-finite (inf/NaN) — a refill rate of inf or 0 would silently break the math. (3) `BucketSnapshot` carries `tokens` (>=0, finite) + `last_refill_at` (tz-aware). The naive-datetime + non-finite-token rejections are pinned via test. (4) `full_bucket(*, now, policy)` is the operator entry point — typically called when the limiter is first armed or after an explicit operator reset. (5) `refill(snapshot, *, now, policy)` advances the bucket: tokens grow proportional to elapsed time, capped at capacity. **Backwards-clock rejected** (now < last_refill_at raises ValueError "clock went backwards") — silent backwards-clock would otherwise let tokens go negative or fail to advance state monotonically. (6) `try_consume(snapshot, n, *, now, policy)` is **atomic refill+spend**: refills first, then spends if sufficient; returns (new_snapshot, ConsumeOutcome). On ALLOWED, tokens are spent. On DENIED_INSUFFICIENT, the snapshot reflects the refill (so the caller's `time_until_available` is meaningful) but no tokens are spent. On DENIED_OVERSIZED, the snapshot reflects the refill but the request is fundamentally impossible — n > capacity is a programming error from the caller (or a misconfigured policy); we never let it through regardless of refill. Zero/negative/non-finite n rejected. Float costs supported for cost-weighted calls (Binance weight-based limits where a kline call costs 1 weight but a /api/v3/klines costs 10). (7) `time_until_available(snapshot, n, *, now, policy)` returns timedelta until n tokens will be available. Returns `timedelta(0)` if already available. Returns the sentinel `timedelta.max` if `n > capacity` (never available — caller should treat as a programming error). The deficit math: `seconds = (n - tokens) / refill_rate_per_sec` after refill. (8) `fill_ratio` returns the bucket fill in [0.0, 1.0] for the dashboard tile "alpaca limiter at 83%". `render_snapshot` formats with ratio-based emoji (🟢 ≥50% / 🟡 ≥20% / 🔴 <20%) + tokens/capacity + refill rate. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Refill is monotonic.** Calling `refill` with a `now` earlier than `last_refill_at` is a programming error — rejected at the function boundary. Otherwise the bucket fills proportional to elapsed time, capped at capacity. The cap matters because without it, a long pause would let `tokens` grow unbounded — which would defeat the whole point of "max burst is capacity." (2) **Consume is atomic refill+spend.** `try_consume` refills first (advancing last_refill_at to now), then spends. If insufficient tokens, the snapshot is returned unchanged except for the refill; the caller sees `allowed=False` and a hint via `time_until_available`. The atomicity matters because a non-atomic refill-then-check-then-spend would have a race window (in async code) where a second caller could see different post-refill state. (3) **`n > capacity` always denied.** A request larger than the bucket can ever hold is a programming error from the caller (or a misconfigured policy); we return `DENIED_OVERSIZED` with `time_until_available=timedelta.max` rather than ever allowing it. The pin matters because a caller that sees DENIED_INSUFFICIENT might naively wait + retry forever; DENIED_OVERSIZED tells them "don't bother, fix the request." (4) **Tokens are float-valued.** Fractional refills are real (a 0.5 tokens/sec rate ticking for 1.5 seconds adds 0.75 tokens). Consume costs are also float-valued for cost-weighted calls. The float pin is regression-tested via the fractional-rate + fractional-cost cases. (5) **Render output never includes adapter call args / responses.** The snapshot deliberately doesn't carry these fields; render shows only bucket state + refill rate. Adapter-side loggers handle raw API call details. The render-no-leak pin asserts no `sk_live` / `password` / `Authorization` / `Bearer` / `secret` substrings can appear. The atomic-refill-then-spend semantic is load-bearing for the caller pattern: a typical adapter calls `try_consume(1.0, now=time())` before each API call; if denied, it consults `time_until_available` for the wait, sleeps that long, then retries. Without atomicity, the retry would have to redo the refill-check work; with atomicity, the second `try_consume` after the wait is guaranteed to succeed (the earlier refill already advanced last_refill_at). The DENIED_INSUFFICIENT-still-advances-last_refill_at semantic matters because it means `time_until_available` after a denial returns the correct wait (3 seconds for a 5-token request against 2 tokens at 1/s — not 5 seconds for the post-refill-but-pre-deficit math). The cap-at-capacity refill semantic prevents a pathological case where a long-paused adapter (say, 24 hours idle) would accumulate 86400 tokens against a 100 capacity bucket — the cap means the worst-case burst is exactly capacity, regardless of pause length. The clock-backwards rejection prevents NTP-correction silent corruption: if the operator's NTP daemon adjusts the clock backward by 30 seconds, a refill call would otherwise silently NOT advance state (negative elapsed multiplied by rate gives a smaller value, but the min() with capacity hides it); the explicit error means operators see and fix the clock issue rather than getting subtle rate-limit drift. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `datetime` + `enum` + `math`); no DB / network / async — `now` is passed explicitly so all time-based refills are pure-function-testable. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 52 tests cover: ConsumeOutcome enum string-value pin; BucketPolicy validation (zero/negative/inf/NaN rejected on both fields); policy immutability; BucketSnapshot validation (negative + non-finite tokens + naive datetime rejected); snapshot immutability; full_bucket starts at capacity + naive now rejected; **refill proportional pin** (3 sec * 1/s = 3 tokens added); **caps at capacity pin** (100s pause + 1/s rate against 10 capacity caps at 10); zero-elapsed no-op on tokens but advances last_refill_at; **fractional rate pin** (0.5/s * 3 sec = 1.5 tokens — sub-second refill cadence works); naive now rejected; **backwards-clock rejected pin** ("clock went backwards" message); advances last_refill_at; try_consume ALLOWED when sufficient; **DENIED_INSUFFICIENT no-spend pin** (snapshot reflects refill but tokens unchanged on the spend side); **atomic refill+spend pin** (zero-token bucket + 5 sec * 1/s = 5 tokens then spend 3 → final 2); **DENIED_OVERSIZED pin** (n=11 against capacity=10 at full bucket → DENIED + tokens unchanged at 10); **n == capacity allowed at full pin** (10/10 → 0/10); zero / negative / inf n rejected; fractional cost (0.5) supported; advances last_refill_at on ALLOWED + on DENIED_INSUFFICIENT (the latter is the load-bearing behavior for time_until_available correctness); time_until_available 0 when sufficient; proportional to deficit (need 5, have 2 at 1/s → 3 sec); with partial refill (0 + 2 sec refill → 2 tokens; need 5 → 3 sec wait); **oversized returns timedelta.max pin**; zero n rejected; fractional rate (need 1 at 0.5/s → 2 sec); fill_ratio full=1.0 + empty=0.0 + after-refill (0 + 5 sec * 1/s on capacity 10 → 0.5); render emoji per band (🟢 ≥50%, 🟡 ≥20%, 🔴 <20%); render includes refill rate; render no-secret-leak pin; e2e flows (steady drain and recover: full bucket of 5; burst 5 calls at T0 each ALLOWED; 6th immediate call DENIED_INSUFFICIENT; 1 second later 1 token refilled and next call ALLOWED; 100-second pause refills bucket to capacity 5); **oversized-permanently-impossible pin** (very fast 1000/s refill against capacity 5; n=10 still DENIED_OVERSIZED at T+100s because 10 > capacity regardless of refill state; time_until_available returns max); **caller-uses-time-until-to-back-off pin** (denied 5-token request against 2-token bucket at 1/s → time_until = 3 sec; caller waits 3 sec; retry succeeds with final tokens=0); replay consistency (same operations → equal final snapshot). The Binance adapter integration (per-endpoint weight policy: `BucketPolicy(capacity=1200, refill_rate_per_sec=20)` for the spot endpoint, `BucketPolicy(capacity=600, refill_rate_per_sec=10)` for the futures endpoint), the per-API-key Alpaca adapter integration (`BucketPolicy(capacity=200, refill_rate_per_sec=200/60)` for the 200-req/min plan), the LLM provider adapter integration (per-provider token-budget bucket parallel to the existing `LLM_DAILY_USD_CAP`), the dashboard "adapter health" tile (renders `fill_ratio` per upstream alongside the breaker state), and the DB persistence layer (snapshot reload on bot restart so a partially-filled bucket from before a crash isn't reset to full) all deferred to follow-ups — limiter verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-5 Wave 1.G — Maysir (gambling) screen** — `halal/maysir_screen.py` ships the structural overlay on the standard halal screener that catches the case where a name is technically halal-compliant on paper but trades like gambling rather than investment. Standard halal screening checks debt ratios + revenue purity + sector; it does NOT catch penny stocks with no business model, meme stocks driven by Reddit pumps, names with zero analyst coverage and 200% short interest — these embody maysir (gambling), independently prohibited in Shariah regardless of the company's debt ratios. Picked a closed-set signal ladder + tunable policy thresholds because (a) maysir patterns evolve (today's meme dynamics weren't on anyone's radar five years ago), so the catalogue of signals is documentation that operators read + scholars reference; (b) the thresholds (penny <$5, retail-flow >70%, etc.) are operator-tunable because some operators want stricter screens; (c) the scoring is rule-based + interpretable — no black-box "trust this score" — which matches the auditability standard of Wave 11.B SSB governance. The maysir screen is a structural overlay: a name passes the standard halal screen AND the maysir screen → tradable; passes standard but fails maysir → flagged to operator with the specific maysir signals. Eight composed surfaces. (1) `MaysirRisk` enum (NONE / LOW / MODERATE / HIGH / EXTREME) with pinned string values for JSON / DB stability. HIGH + EXTREME are non-tradable by default; the operator can override via policy if they want to take a calculated bet on a marginal name. (2) `MaysirSignal` enum with seven detectors: PENNY_PRICE / EXTREME_SHORT_INTEREST / RETAIL_FLOW_DOMINANT / NO_ANALYST_COVERAGE / EXTREME_VOLATILITY / MEME_PUMP_PATTERN / ZERO_REVENUE. The closed catalogue means adding a new signal is a code review change — keeps operators + scholars in sync on what the screener checks. (3) Module-level `_SIGNAL_WEIGHT` dict assigns signal severities: ZERO_REVENUE=3 (most severe — no business model is the strongest gambling tell), PENNY_PRICE / MEME_PUMP_PATTERN / EXTREME_SHORT_INTEREST=2 (mechanical signs of speculation), the rest=1. The weights are documented design decisions, not magic constants. (4) `MaysirPolicy` ships defaults calibrated against the documented "meme stock" pattern (GME / AMC era): penny <$5, short interest >50%, retail-flow >70%, zero analyst coverage, vol >100% annualized, vertical 30d move >100%. Validation enforces **score-threshold ordering** (`moderate_score_threshold < high_score_threshold < extreme_score_threshold` = 2 < 4 < 6 default) — out-of-order thresholds would create a confusing risk ladder. (5) `MaysirInputs` carries the per-ticker feature inputs (stock_price + short_interest_pct + retail_flow_pct + analyst_coverage_count + realized_vol + 30d_change + revenue_ttm). Validation: `short_interest_pct` accepts >100% (synthetic shorts can exceed float — pinned via test) but caps at 1000 for sanity; `retail_flow_pct` ∈ [0, 100]; `revenue_ttm_usd >= 0`. (6) `MaysirAssessment` carries ticker + frozenset of fired signals + risk + score with the **NONE ↔ empty-signals structural invariant** pinned in both directions: NONE risk requires empty signals (otherwise the assessment is internally inconsistent — there's something flagged but the risk says nothing); non-NONE risk requires at least one fired signal (no risk without evidence). (7) `screen_for_maysir(inputs, *, policy)` runs each signal detector independently against the inputs, sums the weights of fired signals, and maps via score cutoffs to risk level via `_score_to_risk`. `screen_batch` returns a sorted-by-ticker tuple for deterministic display. (8) `is_tradable(assessment)` is the load-bearing gate (True for NONE/LOW/MODERATE; False for HIGH/EXTREME) the screener consults. `filter_blocked` returns only the failed assessments for the dashboard "rejected" tile. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set MaysirRisk ladder.** The five tiers are documented in the enum docstring; adding a tier is a code review change. (2) **Closed-set MaysirSignal catalogue.** Same reasoning — the signal set is documentation + audit surface. (3) **Signals are independent boolean detectors.** Each has its own clear tunable threshold; the overall risk is a function of how many fire, weighted by severity. The independence pin matters because operators can adjust one threshold without rebalancing others (e.g., loosen penny to $3 without touching short-interest). (4) **Render output never includes alt-data feed details.** The render shows only ticker + risk + signal labels; raw Reddit posts / Robinhood holding lists go to operator-side debug log. The render-no-leak pin asserts no `reddit.com` / `robinhood` / `Authorization` / `Bearer` / `sk_live` / `/api/` substrings appear. (5) **`is_tradable` is the load-bearing gate.** True only for risk in {NONE, LOW, MODERATE}; HIGH + EXTREME block the trade. The two-tier-block (HIGH + EXTREME both block; LOW + MODERATE both pass) gives operators a useful middle ground — a MODERATE-risk name can still be traded with appropriate operator awareness, but a HIGH-risk name is blocked outright. The boundary-strict-less-than semantic on numeric thresholds matters operationally: penny threshold at $5.0 means a stock at exactly $5.00 doesn't fire (most "penny stock" definitions are "below $5"); short-interest at 50% means 50.0% doesn't fire (the 51% "extreme" threshold needs to be clearly above the 50% checkpoint). The meme-pump one-sided semantic (only positive 30d moves > threshold count) matters because a -50% move is the OPPOSITE of meme-pump behavior — it's an oversold tell, not gambling. The synthetic-short >100% allowance matters because GME's documented short interest hit ~140% of float; rejecting >100% would make the screen unable to flag the canonical maysir example. Halal alignment: the module respects the conservative-default bias of the rest of the platform — defaults are calibrated against the documented meme-stock era; operators wanting stricter screens just tighten the cutoffs. The seven signals are derived from documented Shariah scholarly opinions on maysir (excessive speculation, lack of underlying value, dominance of speculation over investment intent). Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async — alt-data adapter is operator-supplied; the screen just composes. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 57 tests cover: MaysirRisk + MaysirSignal enum string-value pins; policy default pins (5.0 / 50% / 70% / 0 / 1.0 / 100% / 2/4/6) + validation (zero/negative rejected on all numeric fields, range-bounded on percentages); **score-threshold ordering pin both directions** (moderate=5 high=4 rejected; moderate=2 high=6 extreme=4 rejected); zero moderate threshold rejected; immutability; MaysirInputs validation (empty ticker / zero price / negative price / short-interest >1000 / retail-flow >100 / negative revenue all rejected); **synthetic-short >100% allowed pin** (200% accepted); inputs immutability; healthy ticker fires zero signals; signal detection tested in isolation for each of the 7 detectors; **boundary-strict-less-than pins** (penny at $5.0 doesn't fire, $4.99 does; short-interest at 50% doesn't fire, 51% does); zero-coverage at 0 fires, 1 doesn't; **meme-pump one-sided pin** (negative 30d move doesn't fire); zero-revenue at 0 fires, 1 doesn't; score-to-risk mapping at each band: score=1 → LOW (NO_ANALYST_COVERAGE alone, weight 1); score=2 → MODERATE (PENNY_PRICE alone, weight 2); score=4 → HIGH (PENNY_PRICE + MEME_PUMP_PATTERN, 2+2); score=7 → EXTREME (PENNY_PRICE + MEME_PUMP_PATTERN + ZERO_REVENUE, 2+2+3); **extreme inclusive at threshold pin** (score=7 with PENNY_PRICE + EXTREME_SHORT_INTEREST + ZERO_REVENUE = 2+2+3 = 7 ≥ 6 → EXTREME); MaysirAssessment validation **both-direction structural pins** (NONE-with-signals rejected; non-NONE-without-signals rejected); negative score rejected; empty ticker rejected; assessment immutability; is_tradable across all 5 risk levels (NONE/LOW/MODERATE → True; HIGH/EXTREME → False); filter_blocked returns only HIGH/EXTREME from a mixed list; screen_batch returns sorted-by-ticker (ZZZ, AAA, MMM input → AAA, MMM, ZZZ output); empty batch returns empty tuple; render healthy shows ✅ + "none"; render extreme shows 🔴 + "extreme"; includes signal labels; **render signals sorted alphabetically pin** (meme-pump comes before penny price); render no-secret-leak pin (no reddit.com / robinhood / Authorization / Bearer / sk_live / /api/ substrings); e2e flows (**meme-stock 6-signal EXTREME pin** GME-style profile penny=$2.50 + short=200% + retail=85% + coverage=0 + vol=2.0 + 30d=500% + revenue=$1M fires every signal except ZERO_REVENUE → score 10 → EXTREME → not tradable; **blue-chip MSFT-style passes clean** $420 + 0.5% short + 15% retail + 45 coverage + 22% vol + 3% 30d + $240B revenue → NONE risk + empty signals → tradable; **pre-revenue biotech HIGH pin** $15 + 20% short + 40% retail + 2 coverage + 150% vol + 20% 30d + $0 revenue → ZERO_REVENUE (3) + EXTREME_VOLATILITY (1) = score 4 → HIGH → not tradable; replay consistency same inputs → equal assessment; custom-policy loosens to LOW with score-thresholds 4/8/12 making PENNY_PRICE-alone fall into LOW instead of MODERATE). The screener integration (`halal/zoya.py` + `crypto/screener.py` consult `is_tradable` after the standard halal verdict before allowing entry), the alt-data adapter integration (Reddit sentiment via Wave 11.A; Robinhood holdings via Wave 11.D + Wave 11.A), the dashboard "rejected by maysir" tile (consumes `filter_blocked` output), the operator email summary (Wave 5.I) integration that surfaces newly-flagged HIGH/EXTREME holdings overnight, and the per-jurisdiction scholarly review of the signal weights (Wave 11.B SSB governance) all deferred to follow-ups — screen verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-5 Wave 1.D — Multi-school Shariah consensus engine** — `halal/multi_school_consensus.py` ships the multi-school aggregator that runs the halal verdict across the four Sunni majority schools (Hanafi/Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali) plus optional Ja'fari (Shia) for inclusivity, surfacing consensus level (unanimous/majority/split) so operators can apply their preferred strictness based on jurisdiction. The standard halal screener returns a single PERMISSIBLE/IMPERMISSIBLE verdict using one school's methodology (typically Hanafi defaults); many trades are halal in one school but disputed in another — a Saudi user (often Hanbali/Maliki) and a Pakistani user (often Hanafi) might reach different verdicts on the same name. Picked an explicit consensus aggregator over hard-coding one school's verdict because (a) the platform's user base is multi-school by definition (a global halal trading platform must serve users following different fiqh schools); (b) operators in some jurisdictions (Saudi/UAE) prefer unanimous Sunni consensus as the strictness gate; in others (Pakistan/India) majority is acceptable; encoding the strictness as an operator-tunable mode keeps the engine policy-free; (c) the consensus output feeds the dashboard "school disagreement" tile which surfaces edge cases for the scholar review queue (Wave 2.F). Nine composed surfaces. (1) `School` enum (HANAFI/SHAFII/MALIKI/HANBALI/JAFARI) with pinned string values for JSON / DB persistence — five total schools, four Sunni majority + Ja'fari Shia. The closed catalogue means adding a school is a code review change. (2) Module-level `SUNNI_SCHOOLS: frozenset[School]` containing exactly the four Sunni schools — used by the `is_sunni_consensus` predicate. The Sunni-only set is regression-pinned (excludes Ja'fari) because some operator workflows need a "Sunni-quadripartite consensus" gate distinct from the broader 5-school check. (3) `SchoolVerdict` enum (PERMISSIBLE / IMPERMISSIBLE / ABSTAIN) — ABSTAIN means the school hasn't formally opined (common for novel fintech instruments the school hasn't reviewed yet). The three-way enum (vs binary) matters because abstaining is operationally distinct from impermissible: an ABSTAIN doesn't break unanimity (the school just hasn't weighed in), but it also doesn't count as engagement for the Sunni-consensus check. (4) `ConsensusMode` enum (UNANIMOUS / MAJORITY / ANY) — the operator-tunable strictness gate. UNANIMOUS = strict (any disagreement blocks); MAJORITY = strict permissible-count > impermissible-count; ANY = at least one PERMISSIBLE position is enough. The three modes map to documented operator postures: Saudi/UAE compliance-strict operators pick UNANIMOUS; Pakistan/India majority-acceptable operators pick MAJORITY; ANY is the most permissive (rare; only used when one trusted scholar's PERMISSIBLE verdict is decisive for the operator). (5) `SchoolPosition` carries school + verdict + reasoning + optional `scholar_handle` (e.g., "mufti_taqi_usmani"). The reasoning field is brief operator-facing explanation ("permitted under Salam construct per Standard 7"); the full scholar transcript lives in `halal/scholar_review.py`. Validation: empty reasoning rejected; scholar_handle if provided must be non-empty (None allowed but empty string rejected — the latter is silent corruption). (6) `ConsensusReport` enforces two structural invariants: **count-consistency** (`permissible_count + impermissible_count + abstain_count == len(positions)` checked in `__post_init__`) and **no-duplicate-schools** (a school cannot appear twice in one report). The duplicate check matters because two scholars from the same school producing different verdicts is its own data-quality issue that should be resolved before aggregation, not silently averaged. (7) Six derived properties on the report: `total_engaged` (excludes ABSTAIN — only schools that took a position); `is_unanimous_permissible` (every engaged school says PERMISSIBLE AND at-least-one-engaged); `is_unanimous_impermissible` (mirror); `is_majority_permissible` (STRICT permissible > impermissible — ties don't count); `is_split` (at least one PERMISSIBLE AND at least one IMPERMISSIBLE); `is_sunni_consensus` (all four Sunni schools have engaged AND all four say PERMISSIBLE — Ja'fari excluded entirely from this property's logic). (8) `build_report(positions)` sorts by School enum order (HANAFI → SHAFII → MALIKI → HANBALI → JAFARI) for deterministic output — the dashboard tile and operator email summary expect diff-stable rendering. (9) `tradable_under_consensus(report, *, mode)` applies the strictness gate per the mode; `disagreement_summary(report)` returns the minority side (tied → IMPERMISSIBLE side by conservative convention) for the scholar-review-queue surface. Render with verdict emoji ✅/❌/❔ + canonical school labels ("Shafi'i" with apostrophe, "Ja'fari" with apostrophe — Arabic-transliteration convention) + top-line ✅/❌ TRADABLE marker + per-section split warning. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set School + SchoolVerdict + ConsensusMode catalogues.** Adding any value is a code review change — the catalogue is documentation that scholars + operators read. (2) **No duplicate schools.** A `ConsensusReport` cannot have two positions from the same school; pinned in `__post_init__`. The constraint matters because the report's properties (counts, majority math) assume one position per school; allowing duplicates would make `is_majority_permissible` ambiguous (does one school's two scholars vote twice?). (3) **ABSTAIN doesn't break unanimity.** The unanimous-permissible / unanimous-impermissible properties consult `total_engaged` (= permissible + impermissible) — abstaining schools are excluded. The semantic matters because a brand-new fintech instrument might have only 2 of 4 Sunni schools opined; if both opined PERMISSIBLE, that IS unanimous-of-the-engaged (operator can confidently proceed) — pinning otherwise would force the operator to wait for all schools regardless. The **unanimous-requires-engagement** corollary: an empty report or all-abstain report is NOT unanimous either way (no one has opined → no consensus to claim). (4) **Majority is strict greater-than.** A 1-1 tie is NOT a majority; a 2-1 split IS. Pinned via test. The strict semantic matters because a tied vote is operationally a "no consensus" state, not "majority for either side"; conflating them would let operators silently default to permissive. (5) **Render output never includes scholar contact emails or transcripts.** The render shows only school label + verdict + brief reasoning + optional scholar handle; the full scholar correspondence lives in `halal/scholar_review.py`. The render-no-leak pin asserts no `@` / `zoom.us` / `meet.google` / `private_email` / `+1-` substrings appear. Halal alignment: the module respects the multi-school reality of the global Muslim user base; defaults are policy-free (the engine doesn't pick a school for the operator); the disagreement_summary's tied → IMPERMISSIBLE convention is the conservative reading (when in doubt, lean against trading). The Sunni-consensus property + the Ja'fari-included-in-broader-mode design lets a Shia operator opt into the Ja'fari verdict explicitly without forcing Sunni operators to consider it. The disagreement_summary output is operator-actionable: "schools voting against the majority are X, Y" tells the operator which scholars to consult further before proceeding. The render canonical school labels (Shafi'i/Ja'fari with apostrophes) match the standard Arabic-transliteration convention used in academic Islamic-finance texts; consistency matters for operator-scholar communication. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async — scholar verdict capture is operator-supplied via `halal/scholar_review.py`; this module just composes. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 59 tests cover: School + SchoolVerdict + ConsensusMode enum string-value pins; **SUNNI_SCHOOLS exact-set pin** (contains exactly Hanafi/Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali; excludes Ja'fari); SchoolPosition validation (empty reasoning rejected, whitespace reasoning rejected, optional scholar_handle accepted as None or non-empty string, empty scholar_handle rejected); position immutability; report **count-consistency invariant pin** (counts != positions length raises ValueError); negative counts rejected; **no-duplicate-schools pin** (same school twice raises "duplicate position for school"); report immutability; total_engaged excludes ABSTAIN (3 schools, 1 abstaining → engaged=2); **unanimous-permissible-when-all-say-yes pin** (4 PERMISSIBLE → True); **abstain-doesn't-break-unanimity pin** (1 PERMISSIBLE + 1 ABSTAIN → unanimous_permissible True); unanimous-permissible False with one impermissible; unanimous-impermissible mirror; **unanimous-requires-engagement pin** (empty report → both unanimous properties False; all-abstain report → both False); **majority strict-greater-than pin** (2P-1I → True; 1P-1I → False); split with both sides present; not-split when one-sided; **Sunni-consensus all-4-Sunni-PERMISSIBLE pin** (4 Sunni PERMISSIBLE → True); **Sunni-consensus excludes-Ja'fari pin** (Ja'fari engagement irrelevant); **Sunni-consensus needs-all-4 pin** (3-of-4 fails); Sunni-consensus False with one impermissible; **Sunni-consensus needs-engagement-not-abstain pin** (1 Sunni ABSTAIN → False even if other 3 say PERMISSIBLE); build_report empty + counts correctly + sorts by School-enum order (JAFARI/HANAFI/HANBALI input → HANAFI/HANBALI/JAFARI output); **UNANIMOUS-mode-blocks-split pin**; UNANIMOUS-mode-allows-unanimous-permissible; **UNANIMOUS-mode-blocks-empty pin**; UNANIMOUS-mode-blocks-all-abstain; MAJORITY-mode-allows-2P-1I; **MAJORITY-mode-blocks-tied pin** (1-1 → False); **ANY-mode-allows-with-one-permissible pin**; ANY-mode-blocks-no-permissible; **default-mode-is-MAJORITY pin** (call without mode kwarg uses MAJORITY); disagreement returns minority side both directions (majority-P → impermissibles; majority-I → permissibles); **tied-returns-impermissible-side conservative convention pin**; disagreement empty for unanimous-permissible + unanimous-impermissible; render includes verdict emoji + school label + reasoning; scholar_handle included with "via" prefix when set; omits when None; ABSTAIN gets ❔ emoji; render report tradable shows ✅ TRADABLE + "unanimous"; not-tradable-split shows ❌ NOT TRADABLE + "schools disagree"; per-school lines included; **render no-secret-leak pin** (no `@` / `zoom.us` / `meet.google` / `private_email` / `+1-` substrings); e2e flows (AAPL unanimous PERMISSIBLE — passes all three modes; **disputed-name 3-vs-1 split** — UNANIMOUS blocks, MAJORITY allows — matches Saudi-strict vs Pakistani-permissive operator preferences, disagreement_summary surfaces the dissenting school; tobacco unanimous IMPERMISSIBLE — every mode blocks; **novel-fintech partial-abstain pin** — 2 PERMISSIBLE + 2 ABSTAIN → unanimous-permissible True (engaged agree) but is_sunni_consensus False (not all 4 Sunni opined) — UNANIMOUS mode allows; replay consistency same positions → equal report). The screener integration (each ticker's halal verdict run through `multi_school_consensus.build_report` once per quarterly review cycle), the dashboard "school disagreement" tile (consumes `disagreement_summary` for operator review queue), the operator profile setting (each user picks their preferred ConsensusMode + their default school for the personal feed), the Wave 2.F scholar review queue integration (auto-flag splits for human scholar review), and the Wave 11.B SSB governance integration (quarterly compliance attestation cites the per-position scholar handles) all deferred to follow-ups — engine verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-5 Wave 1.J — Multi-currency Zakat calculator** — `halal/zakat.py` ships the pure-functional Zakat math distinct from the existing `halal/purification.py` (purification covers riba income from holdings; zakat is the broader wealth-tax obligation on net assets above nisab at the end of one lunar year). Zakat is the annual wealth tax owed by Muslims whose net assets exceed nisab (the threshold) at hawl-end (one lunar year of continuous holding); the standard rate is 2.5% (1/40th) on net wealth above nisab. Picked a pure-functional calculator with operator-supplied FX rates over an internal FX feed because (a) the calculator must be testable without network calls; (b) the FX rates used for zakat calculation are a documented decision the user makes once per year (typically the spot rate at hawl-end), so making them operator-supplied is the right user experience; (c) the lunar-year arithmetic is operator-tunable (some users use the actual moon-sighting date, others use the algorithmic Hijri calendar); encoding hawl_start_date as input keeps the engine policy-free; (d) the multi-currency reality of global Muslim users (a UAE-based user holds AED + USD + GBP + investments + gold) requires a primitive that handles the conversion math correctly at the source. Six composed surfaces. (1) Module-level documented constants: `DEFAULT_GOLD_NISAB_GRAMS=87.48` (20 mithqal × 4.374g — classical fiqh reference), `DEFAULT_SILVER_NISAB_GRAMS=612.36` (200 dirham × 3.0618g), `DEFAULT_ZAKAT_RATE=0.025` (Sunni majority 1/40), `LUNAR_YEAR_DAYS=354` (Hijri year approximation). The constants are exported so test fixtures + integration code can reference them without re-importing the policy. (2) `NisabBasis` enum (GOLD / SILVER) with pinned string values for JSON / DB persistence. The default is SILVER — at modern gold/silver prices, silver-nisab (~$582 at $0.95/g) is below gold-nisab (~$6561 at $75/g), so silver-basis captures more zakat-eligible holders, which most contemporary scholars recommend (because the historic intent of nisab — the threshold separating "small enough to need help" from "wealthy enough to give") is best preserved by the lower modern threshold). (3) `ZakatPolicy` with operator-tunable rate ∈ (0, 1] (default 2.5% Sunni; allows 20% for Khums and 100% as upper bound) + nisab grams + lunar_year_days. Validation rejects zero/negative on each numeric field. (4) `FxRates` carries base_currency + per-currency multipliers + gold/silver per-gram prices in base. The structural invariant that base_currency itself has implicit rate 1.0 (handled in `to_base`) means the operator doesn't need to add a self-referential entry. Validation rejects empty base + zero metal prices + zero/negative rates + empty currency codes (the empty-code rejection prevents silent corruption from a bug-introduced empty key). The `to_base(amount, currency)` method returns the amount unchanged for the base currency; raises KeyError on unknown currency (loud failure rather than silent zero — operator sees they're missing a rate). (5) `ZakatInputs` carries six per-currency mappings + gold_grams + silver_grams + reporting_currency + optional hawl_start_date. Mappings default to empty via `field(default_factory=dict)` so operators only need to populate the ones they have. All amounts must be non-negative; empty currency codes rejected per mapping. The structural choice to split `debts_owed_to_user` (added to net) from `debts_owed_by_user` (subtracted) matters because they have opposite zakat treatment — money you've lent counts as your asset (you'll get it back), while money you owe is a liability subtracted from your zakatable wealth. The two-mapping design prevents the operator from accidentally summing them with the wrong sign. (6) `ZakatCalculation` carries net_assets (can be negative when debts > assets — semantically informative even though zakat is clamped at 0) + nisab_value + meets_nisab + zakat_owed + basis_used + reporting_currency + hawl_due_date. **Two cross-check structural invariants** pinned in `__post_init__`: meets_nisab=True with zakat_owed=0 (and net>0) is rejected (inconsistent — meeting nisab with positive net should always owe SOME zakat); meets_nisab=False with zakat_owed>0 is rejected (you can't owe zakat without meeting nisab). The cross-check matters because external code constructing the calculation directly (rather than via `calculate_zakat`) could otherwise produce internally-inconsistent state. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set NisabBasis enum.** GOLD or SILVER. The two-tier choice is documentation: scholars recommending each have published reasoning; the operator picks based on their school + scholar's preference. (2) **2.5% standard rate, operator-tunable up to 100%.** The 2.5% rate is the Sunni majority position (1/40); some Shia methodologies use Khums (20% on certain categories). The (0, 1] validation lets Khums users override without allowing nonsense rates >100%. (3) **Net assets = cash + investments + monetized gold/silver + loans-owed-to-user - debts-owed-by-user**, all converted to the reporting currency via supplied FX rates. The formula matches the Sunni majority position; Shia operators with different Khums methodology can use a custom policy + apply the Khums-specific filter on inputs before passing to the calculator. (4) **Hawl is 354 lunar days (Hijri year approximation).** The due_date computation uses 354 days from hawl_start_date — operators wanting moon-sighting precision feed the actual hawl_start_date themselves. The `lunar_year_days` policy field lets operators override (e.g., 365 for solar year if their scholar follows a Gregorian-anchored methodology). (5) **Render output never includes per-account balances.** The render shows only nisab status + total + zakat owed; the detailed per-currency / per-asset breakdown is operator-private (that information lives in the user's account dashboard, not the zakat receipt). The render-no-leak pin asserts no `SAR` / `EUR` / large per-currency balances / `Authorization` / `account_id` substrings appear.
