The default-SILVER-basis is a deliberate operator-favorable conservative default: a user who doesn't know which basis to use gets the stricter calculation (more zakat owed) by default, which is the safer answer (under-paying zakat is a religious obligation problem; over-paying is just generosity). The operator can flip to GOLD if their scholar prefers it. The negative-net handling (zakat clamped at 0 but net_assets reflects the true negative) preserves operator information without violating the zakat semantics — a heavily-indebted user sees their net is -$4000 but doesn't owe zakat. The strict reporting-currency-must-match-FX-base check prevents silent currency-conversion bugs (an operator supplying USD-base FxRates but EUR reporting currency would otherwise quietly compute zakat in the wrong currency). The unknown-currency-raises-KeyError semantic (rather than silent zero) means operators see immediately if they're missing an FX rate. The default factory empty-mapping fields let operators populate only the categories they have without constructing the full mapping shape. The two-cross-check invariant on the calculation prevents externally-constructed inconsistent state. The custom-lunar_year_days policy field is a flexibility lever for solar-year users (who exist in some scholars' methodology). Halal alignment: the module respects the multi-school reality (default-SILVER conservative bias matches majority contemporary scholar recommendation; Khums-rate flexibility serves Shia users; gold-basis flexibility serves classical-historic methodology); the multi-currency support serves the global Muslim user base (Saudi/UAE/Pakistan/Malaysia/UK/US/Indonesia/Turkey users with multiple-currency holdings); the operator-supplied-FX design respects the once-per-year decision the user makes about which exchange rate is canonical for their hawl-end. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async — FX rates are operator-supplied; the calculator just composes. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 64 tests cover: module-constant pins (87.48 / 612.36 / 0.025 / 354); NisabBasis enum string-value pin; ZakatPolicy validation (zero rate rejected, rate-above-1 rejected, **rate=1.0 allowed pin** as upper bound, zero gold/silver nisabs rejected, zero lunar_year_days rejected, immutability); FxRates validation (empty base rejected, zero gold/silver prices rejected, zero/negative rates rejected, empty currency code rejected; to_base returns amount for base unchanged + converts non-base correctly + raises KeyError on unknown); ZakatInputs validation (default empty mappings + gold=0 + silver=0; empty reporting rejected, negative gold/silver/cash/investment/debts rejected, empty currency code per mapping rejected; immutability); ZakatCalculation validation (negative zakat rejected, zero nisab rejected, **meets_nisab=True+zakat=0 inconsistent rejected pin**, **meets_nisab=False+zakat>0 inconsistent rejected pin**, immutability); zero-assets-below-nisab; **simple cash above silver-nisab** ($10000 → $250 zakat with silver basis); above gold-nisab; **below silver-nisab** ($500 < $582 → no zakat); **default basis is SILVER pin**; **silver-more-conservative-than-gold pin** ($5000 meets silver but not gold); multi-currency summing (USD 1000 + SAR 5000@0.27 + EUR 500@1.10 = $2900); investments added; gold holdings priced (100g × $75 = $7500); silver holdings priced; loans-to-user added; debts-owed subtracted; **debts-can-drop-below-nisab pin** ($800 - $500 debt = $300 < silver-nisab); **debts-can-make-net-negative pin** ($1000 - $5000 debt = -$4000 net + zakat=0); **reporting-currency must match fx-base pin** (EUR reporting + USD FxRates raises ValueError); unknown currency KeyError; **hawl due date 354 days after start pin** (2026-01-01 → 2026-12-21); none without start; custom lunar_year_days=365; **custom Khums rate 0.20 pin** ($10000 → $2000); days_until_hawl returns None without due / positive before due (203 days) / negative past due (-11); render meets-nisab shows 💰 + OWED + amount + currency; below-nisab shows ✅ + BELOW NISAB; due_date in render when set; **render no-secret-leak pin** (multi-currency input USD+SAR+EUR + investments → render contains NONE of `SAR`/`EUR`/`5000`/`50000`/`Authorization`/`account_id`); e2e flows (**Saudi-diaspora user pin** USD+SAR cash + USD investments + 50g gold + credit-card debt → correct net = $5000+$5400+$50000+$3750-$2000 = $62150 + meets nisab + 2.5% rate + due date 354d later 2027-03-04; replay consistency same inputs → equal calculation; **gold-basis-lets-smaller-holder-skip pin** $5000 with silver basis owes $125, with gold basis owes $0). The dashboard "your zakat" tile (consumes `calculate_zakat` per user once daily; surfaces days_until_hawl as a countdown), the operator email summary (Wave 5.I) integration that surfaces hawl-due-soon users, the per-jurisdiction tax/Zakat report generator (Wave 18.D for Saudi/UAE Zakat-only reports; Wave 18.J for the year-end checklist), the FX-rate provider integration (CoinGecko/exchangerate-api auto-populates FxRates for the user's hawl-end date), the precious-metal price oracle (Kitco/LBMA spot for the hawl-end date), the DocuSign-ready Zakat receipt generator (Wave 18.I), and the Zakat-Sadaqah charity payment rail (Wave 25.F integration with verified charities) all deferred to follow-ups — calculator verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-5 Wave 1.E — Gharar (excessive uncertainty) detector** — `halal/gharar_detector.py` ships the structural-uncertainty overlay that catches the third independently-prohibited Shariah issue (after standard halal screening for debt/sector + Wave 1.G maysir for gambling-pattern equities): gharar — excessive uncertainty in the contract or instrument itself. Examples: a structured note where you can't see the underlying basket; an asset-backed security where the asset quality is opaque; a forward-sale where the delivery date keeps slipping; dual-class shares where one class has voting rights the other doesn't. Where maysir catches "this stock trades like gambling" (a behavioral / market-structure signal), gharar catches "this contract has hidden uncertainty" (a structural / disclosure signal). The two compose: a name passes the standard halal screen AND the maysir screen AND the gharar detector → tradable. Picked a closed-set signal catalogue + structural boolean inputs because (a) gharar signals are mostly disclosure-quality flags, not continuous metrics — a counterparty is either disclosed or not, an underlying basket is either transparent or opaque; (b) the catalogue is documentation that scholars + operators read + AAOIFI Standard 21 references; (c) operators across schools agree more on gharar than on subtler issues (Hanafi/Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali all classify undisclosed-underlying as severe gharar) — the engine is policy-light because the underlying fiqh is well-settled. Six composed surfaces. (1) `GhararLevel` enum (NONE / MINOR / MODERATE / SEVERE) with pinned string values for JSON / DB persistence. The 4-tier ladder (vs maysir's 5-tier) reflects the more binary nature of gharar — either disclosure is adequate or it isn't; the gradient between MINOR and MODERATE captures cumulative-concern cases. (2) `GhararSignal` enum with eight detectors split across three weight tiers. UNDISCLOSED_UNDERLYING and COUNTERPARTY_UNDISCLOSED are weight 3 because either alone is enough to make a contract void per AAOIFI Standard 21 — both are documented "I don't know what I'm buying" / "I don't know who I'm trading with" failures. ASSET_BACKING_OPAQUE, CONTINGENT_PAYOFF, FUTURE_DELIVERY_INDETERMINATE, NESTED_DERIVATIVE_LAYERS are weight 2 — significant gharar that's potentially mitigable with additional disclosure. DUAL_CLASS_UNEQUAL_RIGHTS and OPAQUE_FEE_STRUCTURE are weight 1 — minor cumulative concerns. (3) Module-level `_SIGNAL_WEIGHT` dict documents the per-signal severity. The weights are derived from AAOIFI Standard 21 + classical fiqh references; the dict is internal but the weight tiers are documented in the module docstring + roadmap. (4) `GhararPolicy` defaults: nested_layers_threshold=2 (the documented scholar position that 2+ wrappers around a single underlying obscures economic substance) + score cutoffs 1/3/5. Validation rejects nested_layers_threshold below 2 (a single wrapper isn't gharar — it's just structuring); enforces score-threshold ordering (minor < moderate < severe); requires minor_score_threshold ≥ 1. (5) `GhararInputs` carries instrument_id + 8 disclosure flags, all defaulting to the "clean" / "transparent" position so operators only need to set the ones that flag concerns. The "boolean inverts per signal" pattern (e.g., `underlying_disclosed=False` fires UNDISCLOSED_UNDERLYING) keeps the inputs reading as positive-sense flags ("is this disclosed?"). Validation rejects empty/whitespace instrument_id + negative derivative_layers. (6) `GhararAssessment` carries id + frozenset of fired signals + level + score with **NONE ↔ empty-signals structural invariant** pinned in both directions: NONE level requires empty signals (otherwise the assessment is internally inconsistent); non-NONE level requires at least one fired signal. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set GhararLevel ladder.** NONE < MINOR < MODERATE < SEVERE. The 4-tier choice (vs maysir's 5-tier) reflects that gharar's binary disclosure nature doesn't need a "LOW" sub-tier; SEVERE is the only blocked level, all others pass. (2) **Closed-set GhararSignal catalogue.** 8 documented detectors covering the AAOIFI Standard 21 + classical fiqh gharar concerns. Adding a signal is a code review change — the catalogue is documentation. (3) **Each signal has documented severity weight.** Most-severe weight-3 signals (undisclosed underlying, undisclosed counterparty) are the AAOIFI "void contract" triggers; weight-2 signals are significant-but-mitigable; weight-1 signals are minor cumulative concerns. The weight-3 design ensures a single weight-3 signal cleanly puts the assessment at MODERATE (3=threshold), and any weight-3 signal combined with another concern (3+2=5 or 3+3=6) cleanly puts it at SEVERE. (4) **`is_tradable(assessment)` is the load-bearing gate.** Returns True for NONE/MINOR/MODERATE; False for SEVERE. The MODERATE-still-tradable design (distinct from maysir's HIGH-blocked design) reflects that gharar's MODERATE often means a single weight-3 signal that an operator might still trade with full awareness — the operator-flagged surface is in the dashboard tile, not a hard block. The hard block is reserved for SEVERE = multiple gharar concerns or weight-3 + significant additional concerns. (5) **Render output never includes the underlying instrument's prospectus / disclosure-document text.** The render shows only instrument id + level + signal labels; the full prospectus / disclosure document lives in the operator-side compliance archive. The render-no-leak pin asserts no `prospectus` / `Annex A` / `Schedule II` / `Authorization` / `Bearer` / `/api/` / `private_key` substrings appear. The "default-clean inputs" design is operator-friendly: an operator constructing a `GhararInputs` for a plain common stock just passes `instrument_id` and gets all clean defaults; only structured products / derivatives need explicit flag setting. The composition with maysir + multi-school-consensus + standard halal screen means the platform's tradability gate is a four-tier check: (a) standard halal screen passes (debt + sector + revenue ratios); (b) multi-school consensus reaches operator-configured strictness (UNANIMOUS/MAJORITY/ANY); (c) maysir screen returns is_tradable=True (no HIGH/EXTREME gambling pattern); (d) gharar detector returns is_tradable=True (no SEVERE structural uncertainty). All four must pass; any one blocks. The four checks are independent (a name can pass standard but fail maysir; pass standard + maysir but fail gharar; etc.) — operators see which check failed and can take targeted action. Halal alignment: the module respects the AAOIFI Standard 21 framework; weight-3 signals match documented "void contract" triggers; the score-threshold ordering enforces the standard's MODERATE+ gating; the nested_layers_threshold of 2 matches documented scholar position on layered derivative structures. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async — instrument metadata is operator-supplied; the detector just composes. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 47 tests cover: GhararLevel + GhararSignal enum string-value pins; policy default pins (2 / 1 / 3 / 5) + validation (**nested_layers below 2 rejected pin**, **score-threshold ordering pin** both directions, zero minor-threshold rejected, immutability); GhararInputs validation (empty + whitespace instrument_id rejected, negative derivative_layers rejected, immutability); clean instrument fires zero signals; signal detection tested in isolation for all 8 detectors (each fired by inverting the corresponding flag in default-clean inputs); **nested-layers-threshold inclusive pin** (derivative_layers=2 fires; =1 doesn't); score-to-level mapping at each band: weight-1 alone (OPAQUE_FEE_STRUCTURE) = score 1 = MINOR; weight-2 alone (ASSET_BACKING_OPAQUE) = score 2 = MINOR (still below 3); **weight-3 alone (UNDISCLOSED_UNDERLYING) = score 3 = MODERATE pin** (single AAOIFI "void contract" trigger pushes to MODERATE at threshold); weight-3 + weight-2 = 5 = SEVERE; two weight-3 (UNDISCLOSED_UNDERLYING + COUNTERPARTY_UNDISCLOSED) = 6 = SEVERE; assessment **both-direction structural pins** (NONE-with-signals rejected; non-NONE-without-signals rejected); negative score rejected; empty id rejected; immutability; **is_tradable only blocks SEVERE pin** (NONE / MINOR / MODERATE all True; SEVERE False — distinct from maysir's HIGH+EXTREME blocked design); filter_blocked returns only SEVERE; assess_batch sorted by id; empty batch returns empty tuple; render clean shows ✅ + "none"; render severe shows 🔴 + "severe"; signal labels included; **render signals sorted alphabetically pin** (counterparty before undisclosed alphabetically); **render no-secret-leak pin** (no `prospectus` / `Annex A` / `Schedule II` / `Authorization` / `Bearer` / `/api/` / `private_key` substrings); e2e flows (**opaque-structured-note 4-signal SEVERE pin** — STRUCTNOTE_42 with undisclosed underlying + opaque counterparty + 3 nested layers + opaque fees → score 9 → SEVERE → not tradable; plain-equity MSFT-style passes clean as NONE → tradable; **dual-class governance MINOR-only pin** — Google-style with unequal rights alone fires only DUAL_CLASS_UNEQUAL_RIGHTS = score 1 = MINOR = tradable; **Salam-indeterminate-delivery + undisclosed-counterparty SEVERE pin** — SALAM_42 with delivery_date_specified=False + counterparty_disclosed=False = weight 2 + 3 = score 5 = SEVERE = not tradable, matching the AAOIFI Standard 7 voidable-contract semantic; replay consistency same inputs → equal assessment; **custom-strict policy SEVERE-at-3 pin** — operator with stricter cutoffs (minor=1, moderate=2, severe=3) gets SEVERE on a single weight-3 signal alone, blocking even moderate-default cases). The screener integration (`halal/zoya.py` + `crypto/screener.py` consult `is_tradable` after Wave 1.G maysir + after Wave 1.D multi-school consensus + after standard halal verdict — four-tier composed gate), the prospectus-parser integration (NLP pipeline that extracts disclosure flags from SEC filings + 8-K reports + offering memoranda to populate `GhararInputs`), the dashboard "rejected by gharar" tile (consumes `filter_blocked` output alongside the maysir tile), the operator email summary (Wave 5.I) integration that surfaces newly-flagged SEVERE holdings overnight, the structured-product specific pre-trade approval workflow (any SEVERE assessment routes to scholar review queue from Wave 2.F), and the Wave 11.B SSB governance integration (per-signal scholar verdict tracking) all deferred to follow-ups — detector verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-5 Wave 1.F — Riba detector across derivatives** — `halal/riba_detector.py` ships the instrument-class-keyed riba (interest / usury) classifier, completing the four-tier halal compliance gate (standard halal screen + Wave 1.D multi-school consensus + Wave 1.G maysir + Wave 1.E gharar + this 1.F riba). Riba is the oldest and most fundamental Shariah prohibition; classical fiqh distinguishes riba al-nasiyah (interest on delayed payment / loans — every conventional bond pays this) from riba al-fadl (excess in same-genus exchange — swapping 1kg gold-now for 1.1kg gold-later). Modern instruments embed riba in subtler forms: embedded financing rate in conventional futures (cost-of-carry includes the risk-free rate), leverage interest in CFDs / margin trading / leveraged ETFs, debt sale (bay' al-dayn) when bonds trade at non-face value. Picked an instrument-class-keyed classifier with additive signal flags because (a) most riba determinations are deterministic from the instrument type — every conventional bond pays riba al-nasiyah, period — so a lookup table is the natural representation; (b) overlay flags (uses_margin, has_embedded_financing, etc.) catch the operator-supplied edge cases on top of the base class; (c) the mapping is well-settled fiqh and matches AAOIFI Standard 21 Section 3 + Standard 30 (commodity Murabaha) — operators don't need to interpret, they look up. Eight composed surfaces. (1) `RibaType` enum (NASIYAH / FADL / EMBEDDED_FINANCING / DEBT_SALE / LEVERAGE_INTEREST) with pinned string values for JSON / DB persistence. The five types span classical (NASIYAH/FADL) + structural (EMBEDDED_FINANCING/DEBT_SALE/LEVERAGE_INTEREST) categories so operators see the specific violation type rather than just "riba present." (2) `InstrumentClass` enum with 14 documented classes covering the canonical halal-tradable set (SPOT_EQUITY / PHYSICAL_COMMODITY / SUKUK / WAAD_FORWARD / SALAM_FORWARD / ARBOUN_OPTION) AND the canonical non-halal set (CONVENTIONAL_BOND / CONVENTIONAL_FUTURE / CONVENTIONAL_OPTION / INTEREST_RATE_SWAP / CURRENCY_SWAP / CFD / LEVERAGED_ETF / INVERSE_ETF). The closed catalogue means adding a class is a code review change — the catalogue is documentation that scholars + operators read. (3) Module-level `_BASE_VERDICT` dict maps each InstrumentClass to the frozenset of riba types it always carries (regardless of operator flags). The mapping is the load-bearing fiqh determination: SPOT_EQUITY/PHYSICAL_COMMODITY/SUKUK/WAAD_FORWARD/SALAM_FORWARD/ARBOUN_OPTION → empty (clean); CONVENTIONAL_BOND/INTEREST_RATE_SWAP → {NASIYAH}; CONVENTIONAL_FUTURE/CONVENTIONAL_OPTION/CURRENCY_SWAP/INVERSE_ETF → {EMBEDDED_FINANCING}; LEVERAGED_ETF → {LEVERAGE_INTEREST}; CFD → {EMBEDDED_FINANCING, LEVERAGE_INTEREST}. (4) Module-level `HALAL_BY_DEFAULT_CLASSES` frozenset auto-derived from the base verdict (the classes whose verdict is empty). Used by the operator dashboard to filter the tradable-universe view; regression-pinned to exactly the 6 documented clean classes. (5) `RibaPolicy` defaults: `flag_margin_as_riba=True` + `flag_borrow_as_riba=True` (conservative). The two flags exist because some operators follow rare scholar positions permitting margin under specific Murabaha-like structures; the policy exposes the override. **Critically, there is no policy knob to remove a base verdict for non-halal instrument classes** — that's a fiqh determination, not configuration. An operator who wants to permit conventional bonds needs a code review change to `_BASE_VERDICT`, not a policy override. (6) `RibaInputs` carries id + class + 5 boolean flags (uses_margin / uses_borrowed_securities / has_embedded_financing_rate / pays_or_receives_fixed_interest / is_debt_traded_off_face). All flags default to False so operators only set the ones that apply. Validation rejects empty/whitespace instrument_id. (7) `RibaAssessment` carries id + class + frozenset of detected riba types; `is_clean` property True only when riba_types is empty. The class is preserved in the assessment so the render output can show "AAPL (spot equity)" rather than just "AAPL." (8) `assess_riba(inputs, *, policy)` combines the base verdict for the class with the flag-driven extras via union: `base | extra`. The union semantics matters because the same riba type can be flagged by both the base and a flag (e.g., a CONVENTIONAL_FUTURE base flags EMBEDDED_FINANCING; if `has_embedded_financing_rate=True` is also set, the type appears once in the resulting frozenset). `assess_batch` sorts by id for deterministic output. `filter_blocked` returns only assessments with at least one riba type. **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set RibaType + InstrumentClass catalogues.** Each enum's value set is documentation that scholars + operators read; adding a value is a code review change. (2) **Base verdict is fiqh, not policy.** A CONVENTIONAL_BOND always carries NASIYAH regardless of operator policy; a SPOT_EQUITY is clean unless flags fire. The asymmetry matters: the platform's authority comes from saying "yes" to halal instruments even when operators want flexibility, AND saying "no" to non-halal instruments even when operators want flexibility. The policy can only ADD flags (e.g., decide whether margin counts) — it cannot REMOVE a class's structural riba. (3) **Operator flags add to base verdict; never subtract.** The union-based combination means an operator who buys a SUKUK with `has_embedded_financing_rate=True` (e.g., a poorly-structured sukuk that effectively embeds a financing rate) still gets the EMBEDDED_FINANCING flag — even though SUKUK's base verdict is clean. The flag-driven additions are how operators surface specific concerns about an otherwise-clean class. (4) **`is_clean` is the load-bearing gate.** Returns True only when riba_types is empty. The four-tier halal gate consults: `halal_screen.passed AND multi_school_consensus.tradable_under_consensus(report, mode=op_mode) AND maysir_screen.is_tradable(maysir_assessment) AND gharar_detector.is_tradable(gharar_assessment) AND riba_assessment.is_clean`. All four must pass; any one blocks. (5) **Render output never includes broker-internal funding rate details or counterparty-specific terms.** The render shows only instrument id + class + sorted riba type labels; per-trade financing schedules / counterparty BPS quotes / wire references go to the operator-side DB. The render-no-leak pin asserts no `financing_schedule` / `counterparty_id` / `/api/` / `Authorization` / `Bearer` / `bps` substrings appear. The "policy cannot clear base verdict" asymmetric design is the load-bearing fiqh-vs-config separation: by encoding the base verdict in module-level data not policy, the platform's halal compliance becomes a contract that operators cannot accidentally weaken. The flag-driven extras path remains operator-tunable because it captures genuinely operator-specific information (whether THIS TRADE uses margin, not whether margin in general is permissible). The two-policy-knob design (flag_margin / flag_borrow) reflects the rare scholar positions permitting these under specific Murabaha-like structures — operators who follow such scholars can opt out, but the default conservative posture treats both as riba. The HALAL_BY_DEFAULT_CLASSES module-level set is the operator's universe-filter — when scrolling the broker's instrument list, only these 6 classes show up by default; toggling to "show all" surfaces the conventional classes with red ❌ markers. The 14-class catalogue is also the foundation for the Wave 4 halal options + structured products waves (4.A Wa'd structuring, 4.B Arboun, 4.C Salam) which all build on instrument classes already pre-classified here as halal-by-default. The interest-rate-swap-NASIYAH classification matches AAOIFI Standard 38 + Standard 21; the CFD-both-EMBEDDED-and-LEVERAGE classification reflects the documented two-violation nature of CFDs (daily financing charge + leverage); the leveraged-ETF-LEVERAGE classification + inverse-ETF-EMBEDDED classification distinguish the two structural ways modern ETFs embed riba. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `collections.abc`); no DB / network / async. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 46 tests cover: RibaType + InstrumentClass enum string-value pins; **HALAL_BY_DEFAULT_CLASSES exact-set pin** (6 documented clean classes); **conventional-classes-excluded-from-halal-by-default pin** (8 classes never in the set); RibaPolicy default pins + immutability; RibaInputs validation (empty id rejected, immutability); **all 6 halal-by-default classes return is_clean pin** (spot equity / physical commodity / sukuk / wa'd forward / salam forward / arboun option); **conventional bond ALWAYS NASIYAH pin**; conventional future EMBEDDED_FINANCING; conventional option EMBEDDED_FINANCING; interest rate swap NASIYAH; currency swap EMBEDDED_FINANCING; **CFD both EMBEDDED + LEVERAGE pin** (the documented two-violation CFD nature); leveraged ETF LEVERAGE_INTEREST; inverse ETF EMBEDDED_FINANCING; **margin-flag adds LEVERAGE_INTEREST to clean class pin** (SPOT_EQUITY + uses_margin = LEVERAGE_INTEREST); **borrow-flag adds NASIYAH pin** (SPOT_EQUITY + uses_borrowed_securities = NASIYAH because the lending fee is interest); embedded-financing-flag adds EMBEDDED_FINANCING; fixed-interest-flag adds NASIYAH; debt-sale-flag adds DEBT_SALE; **permissive policy can disable margin/borrow flag pin** (flag_margin_as_riba=False with margin trade returns clean); **permissive policy CANNOT clear base verdict pin** (conventional bond stays NASIYAH even with both policy flags off — the asymmetric fiqh-vs-config separation); **base + extra combine pin** (conventional future + margin = EMBEDDED_FINANCING + LEVERAGE); RibaAssessment validation (immutability, empty id rejected); is_clean property both directions; assess_batch sorted by id + empty-batch returns empty; filter_blocked returns only dirty; render clean shows ✅ + "no riba detected"; render dirty shows ❌ + class label + sorted riba labels; **render riba labels sorted alphabetically pin** (CFD shows "embedded financing" before "leverage interest"); class label included in render (e.g., "wa'd forward"); **render no-secret-leak pin** (no `financing_schedule` / `counterparty_id` / `/api/` / `Authorization` / `Bearer` / `bps` substrings); e2e flows (**classic halal portfolio all clean pin** — 5-instrument portfolio of spot equities + sukuk + physical gold + wa'd forward returns all is_clean and zero blocked; **classic non-halal bundle all blocked pin** — 5-instrument bundle of margin stocks + bonds + CFDs + futures + leveraged ETFs returns all not-clean and 5 blocked; replay consistency same inputs → equal assessment; **AAOIFI Standard 21 + 30 reference pin** — USD_LIBOR_SWAP_5Y interest-rate swap correctly classified as NASIYAH and rendered with "interest rate swap" + "riba al-nasiyah" labels for the operator-facing audit trail). The screener integration (`halal/zoya.py` + `crypto/screener.py` consult `is_clean` after Wave 1.G maysir + Wave 1.E gharar + Wave 1.D multi-school consensus + standard halal verdict — five-tier composed gate when combined with all the prior compliance primitives), the broker adapter integration (each adapter provides its instrument's `InstrumentClass` per quote so the gate can be applied at order-submission time), the dashboard "non-halal instrument blocked" tile (consumes `filter_blocked` output alongside the maysir + gharar tiles for a unified compliance-rejection view), the Wave 4 halal options + structured products (4.A/4.B/4.C all build on the WAAD_FORWARD / ARBOUN_OPTION / SALAM_FORWARD instrument classes already pre-classified here as halal-by-default), the Wave 3 sukuk universe (3.A SUKUK ingestion uses the SUKUK class as the canonical halal fixed-income marker), and the operator email summary integration (Wave 5.I) that surfaces newly-flagged non-halal instruments overnight all deferred to follow-ups — detector verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

* **Round-5 Wave 1.I — Time-weighted purification for partial holdings** — `halal/time_weighted_purification.py` ships the prorating complement to the existing `halal/purification.py` (basic per-dividend ledger) + `halal/purification_schedule.py` (period grouping + disbursement) + `halal/round_trip_purification.py` (capital-gains flavor). The platform's existing purification covers the standard case: receive a dividend, compute impure_pct × dividend → purification owed. That assumes the holder has held the shares for the full revenue-generation period (typically a quarter for US equities). For actively-traded portfolios this assumption breaks: a user who buys XYZ on day 88 of a 91-day quarter, holds through ex-date on day 90, sells on day 92 — under the standard rule, owes the full impure portion of the dividend. Some scholars argue the purification should be prorated by the holding fraction (3/91 in this example) on the reasoning that the impure earnings accrued over the full period; the user's economic share of those earnings is proportional to their holding window. Picked a pure-functional calculator over an in-place mutator because (a) the calculation is keyed on a holding + a dividend event — both inputs are stable point-in-time data; (b) operators run the calculation per-trade after dividend confirm, so one-shot pure functions match the call pattern; (c) the two methodologies share enough math that fusing them into a single function with a method parameter keeps the surface area small + tests covering both don't double in size. Five composed surfaces. (1) `PurificationMethod` enum (FULL_AMOUNT / HOLDING_PRORATED) with pinned string values for JSON / DB persistence stability. The default is FULL_AMOUNT — the more conservative methodology. The flexibility to opt into HOLDING_PRORATED serves operators following scholars who explicitly endorse prorating for actively-traded positions; the conservative default protects operators who haven't made that explicit choice. (2) `HoldingPeriod` carries holding_id + start_date + end_date (None when still held) + share_count. Validation rejects empty/whitespace id, zero/negative shares, and end_date-before-start_date. The end_date=None semantic for "still held" matters because actively-traded portfolios constantly have new positions opened that haven't closed yet; the calculator handles them via a `today` parameter. (3) `DividendEvent` carries period_start + period_end + ex_date + amount_per_share + impure_revenue_pct ∈ [0.0, 1.0]. The structural invariant **ex_date must be within [period_start, period_end]** is checked in `__post_init__` (otherwise the dividend would be inconsistent — the ex-date determines who receives the dividend, and a dividend with ex-date outside its own revenue period is data corruption). The `days_in_period` property is inclusive of both endpoints (period 2026-01-01 to 2026-03-31 = 90 days, not 89); the inclusive convention matters because the ex-date itself is one of the days in the period. (4) `PurificationAssessment` carries holding_id + eligible (binary on ex-date) + gross_dividend + impure_amount_full + purification_owed + method_used + days_held_in_period + days_in_period + holding_fraction. **Five structural invariants** pinned in `__post_init__`: purification_owed cannot exceed impure_amount_full (the prorating method only ever reduces the obligation, never inflates it); holding_fraction ∈ [0.0, 1.0]; days_held >= 0; days_in_period >= 1; ineligible holdings cannot have gross_dividend > 0 or purification_owed > 0 (an ineligible holding by definition received nothing). The five-invariant cross-check matters because external code constructing the assessment directly (rather than via `calculate_purification`) could otherwise produce internally-inconsistent state that would propagate to the operator-side ledger as silent corruption. (5) `calculate_purification(holding, dividend, *, today, method)` runs the full computation: eligibility = `holding.start_date <= dividend.ex_date <= effective_end_date` (where effective_end_date is `holding.end_date` or `today` for still-held positions); ineligible holdings short-circuit to all zeros; eligible holdings compute gross = `amount_per_share × share_count`, impure_full = `gross × impure_revenue_pct`, then apply the method: FULL_AMOUNT uses impure_full directly; HOLDING_PRORATED applies × holding_fraction. The `_holding_overlap_days` private helper computes the inclusive overlap of holding with [period_start, period_end], clamped to [0, days_in_period] (a holding longer than the period doesn't earn extra purification — a long-term holder spanning multiple quarters owes one quarter's worth, not two). **Five pinned semantics** are the load-bearing surface. (1) **Closed-set PurificationMethod ladder.** Adding a method (e.g., a more sophisticated time-weighted formula like exponential decay) is a code review change — keeps the operator-facing methodology choice documented + scholar-reviewable. (2) **Default is FULL_AMOUNT.** The more conservative methodology by default; operators wanting prorating opt in explicitly. The asymmetric default-to-conservative posture matches the platform's broader design pattern (default-strict halal, default-conservative Zakat, default-strict gharar) — over-paying purification is just generosity; under-paying is a religious obligation gap that violates trust. (3) **Eligibility is binary on ex-date.** A holding is eligible for the dividend iff `start_date <= ex_date <= end_date` (or end_date is None for still-held). The broker pays the dividend based on this binary determination; our calculator mirrors that determination. The semantics matters because both pre-ex-date sells and post-ex-date buys are legitimately ineligible — the broker won't pay; we shouldn't compute purification on a phantom dividend. (4) **Holding fraction is `min(days_held, days_in_period) / days_in_period`.** Capped at 1.0 because a holding longer than the period doesn't earn extra purification. The cap matters because without it, a long-term holder spanning two quarters would compute holding_fraction = 2.0 and owe DOUBLE the purification on a single dividend — that's mathematically wrong (the dividend covers ONE period's earnings; you can't purify based on two periods of accrual). The min() cap prevents the silent-corruption variant. (5) **Render output never includes per-trade buy/sell prices or P&L.** The render shows only holding id + eligibility + summary numbers (purification owed, days held, method); per-trade economics (cost basis, sell price, realized P&L) live in the operator-side ledger. The render-no-leak pin asserts no `buy_price` / `sell_price` / `P&L` / `cost_basis` / `Authorization` substrings appear. The composition with the existing purification modules is operator-friendly: `halal/purification.py` covers the standard per-dividend obligation; this module covers the prorating math when the operator has chosen HOLDING_PRORATED methodology; `halal/purification_schedule.py` groups assessments into monthly/quarterly disbursement bundles; `halal/round_trip_purification.py` covers capital-gains-side purification on round-trip trades. Operators pick which of the four flows applies to each trade based on the type of revenue (dividend vs capital gain) + their scholar's methodology preference (full-amount vs holding-prorated). The active-trader use case is the load-bearing one for this Wave 1.I module: a quant strategy that opens + closes positions in days rather than quarters needs the prorating math to avoid over-purifying its short-window dividend captures. Without prorating, an active strategy that captures 50 dividends a year on 5-day holdings owes 50× the purification of a buy-and-hold portfolio capturing the same 50 dividends — even though the active strategy "earned" the impure portion for only 50 × 5 = 250 days vs the buy-and-hold's 365 × 50 = 18,250 days of accrual. The prorating reflects the actual economic share of impure earnings. Pure-Python (stdlib `dataclasses` + `enum` + `datetime`); no DB / network / async. Frozen dataclasses on every output. 47 tests cover: PurificationMethod enum string-value pin; HoldingPeriod validation (empty id rejected, zero/negative shares rejected, end-before-start rejected, immutability, **still-held end_date=None allowed pin**); DividendEvent validation (period_end-before-start rejected, **ex_date-outside-period pin both directions** rejected with explicit message, negative amount_per_share rejected, **impure_pct outside [0.0, 1.0] both bounds rejected pin**, **impure_pct=0.0 allowed pin** for fully-clean dividends, **impure_pct=1.0 allowed pin** for fully-haram dividends, days_in_period inclusive single-day pin = 1 day for one-day period); eligibility (covers-ex-date eligible; bought-after-ex ineligible; sold-before-ex ineligible; still-held-through-today eligible; **start-on-ex-date inclusive pin**; **end-on-ex-date inclusive pin**; ineligible returns zero dividend + zero purification); FULL_AMOUNT method (full quarter → 100 shares × $1 × 5% = $5; **brief 3-day holding still pays full $5 pin** — load-bearing because this is exactly the active-trader scenario the prorating method addresses; **default method is FULL_AMOUNT pin**); HOLDING_PRORATED method (full period prorates to 1.0 → equal to FULL_AMOUNT; partial 30/90 days → $5 × 30/90 = $1.67; 3-day window → $5 × 3/90 = $0.17; **caps-at-period pin** holding longer than period gives fraction=1.0 not 1.5+; partial overlap Feb 15 → Mar 31 = 45 days = 5 × 45/90 = $2.50); PurificationAssessment validation (immutability; **purification_owed cannot exceed impure_amount_full pin** — invariant holds for both methods; **holding_fraction outside [0,1] rejected pin**; **ineligible-with-dividend rejected pin** preventing silent corruption; negative days_held rejected; zero days_in_period rejected); total_owed sums two assessments correctly ($5 + $10 = $15); empty returns 0; render eligible shows 💧 + amount with 4-decimal precision + method label; render ineligible shows ⏸ + "not eligible (didn't hold ex-date)"; method label included for both methods; **render no-secret-leak pin** (no `buy_price` / `sell_price` / `P&L` / `cost_basis` / `Authorization` substrings); e2e flows (**active-trader 5-day-window pin** — FULL_AMOUNT owes $5, HOLDING_PRORATED owes $5 × 5/90 = $0.28, demonstrating the active-trader scenario where the methodology choice has a 18× impact on the obligation; long-term-holder methods agree (both give $5 for full-period coverage); replay consistency same inputs → equal assessment; **zero-impure dividend zero purification regardless of method pin** — when the company's revenue is fully halal, no purification is owed regardless of methodology choice). The active-trader integration (each strategy's per-cycle dividend confirmer calls `calculate_purification` with the operator-configured method as soon as the dividend posts), the operator settings UI (each user picks their preferred method as a one-time setting that applies to all subsequent dividends), the Wave 1.K signed-receipt generator (consumes `total_owed` for the receipt PDF), the dashboard "purification owed (time-weighted)" tile (renders sorted-by-amount assessments alongside the standard purification tile), the Wave 5.I operator email summary that surfaces total purification owed across the period, and the Wave 18.I DocuSign-ready Zakat-Sadaqah-purification combined receipt all deferred to follow-ups — calculator verified in isolation first so the integrations see a stable contract.

## Round-5 progress (auto-mode batch 4 — 2026-05-07)

Fourth batch — 12 new modules / 386 new unit tests. Closes the remaining
pure-Python core gaps in Waves 3 (sukuk), 4 (halal options), 7 (Mudarabah-
flavoured constructs), 8 (committee), 13 (FX hedge), and 18 (multi-jurisdiction
tax). Highlights:

* **Wave 3.C — `markets/sukuk_allocation.py`** — Mean-variance sukuk allocator with halal sector / jurisdiction / type caps and a TARGET_DURATION objective; pure-Python projected-gradient solver, water-filling cap enforcement (32 tests).
* **Wave 3.F — `markets/sukuk_default.py`** — Sukuk default + recovery model with per-(sukuk_type × region) calibration (Asia / GCC / Europe / Africa) and Vasicek-style hazard with type multipliers; deterministic Monte-Carlo loss simulator + portfolio VaR / CVaR report (49 tests).
* **Wave 3.G — `markets/hybrid_optimizer.py`** — Unified equity-sukuk optimiser with class-band feasibility checks, AAOIFI Standard 21 default sector caps (financials 33%, utilities 25%, real-estate 20%, …), sukuk-only duration target, and a class-band feasibility contract that respects single-name × class-size limits (32 tests).
* **Wave 4.C — `halal/salam_forward.py`** — Salam-forward hedge planner + counterparty matching engine; FungibleClass closed set excludes equities (forced through Wa'd-puts instead); FIFO matching, AAOIFI Standard 10 cl. 4.4 ≤ 365-day tenor pin, full-prepayment pin (33 tests).
* **Wave 4.E — `ml/vol_target.py`** — Vol-targeted allocator with three modes (SCALE_DOWN_ONLY / SCALE_BOTH / SALAM_OVERLAY); annualised log-return σ pinned to √252 (stocks) / √365 (crypto); Salam-overlay path engages when realised vol < target instead of using interest margin (35 tests).
* **Wave 4.F — `halal/halal_put.py`** — Tail-risk Wa'd-put planner with closed-set ConditionType ladder (PRICE_BELOW / DRAWDOWN_OVER / VOL_ABOVE / TIME_ELAPSED), AND/OR exercise semantics, OTM-only strike pin, Arboun-as-collateral default, and a `propose_hedge` helper that builds a sane default contract from operator intent (44 tests).
* **Wave 7.D — `halal/pls_strategy.py`** — Profit-loss-sharing performance-fee accounting with three structures (HURDLE_ONLY / HURDLE_HWM / HURDLE_HWM_LOSS_SHARE); high-water-mark monotone pin, AAOIFI Standard 13 capital-proportional loss-share semantics, optional Wakalah-flat-fee leg (26 tests).
* **Wave 7.E — `ml/halal_optimizer.py`** — Halal-native Markowitz with hard Mudarabah-pool floor + AAOIFI sector caps + sukuk min/max band; raises `InfeasibleBasketError` when pool weight is set but no MUDARABAH_POOL asset exists in the universe (27 tests).
* **Wave 7.F — `ml/halal_alpha_beta.py`** — Pure-Python OLS α/β decomposer + Wa'd-replication planner that substitutes the implicit-leverage β leg with an explicit Wa'd notional + cash sleeve; β clipped to [-2, 3] reliability band; attribution report decomposes realised P&L into β + α + cash-drag legs (23 tests).
* **Wave 8.F — `core/contradiction_detector.py`** — Cross-agent contradiction surfacer with five detector types (STANCE / CONFIDENCE_OUTLIER / HALAL_DISSENT / QUANT_FUNDAMENTAL_GAP / CONFIDENCE_MISALIGNMENT) + NOTE / WARN / BLOCK severity ladder; halal-judge SKIP against active majority is the only BLOCK; vote rationales are *not* echoed in the renderer (prompt-injection safe) (27 tests).
* **Wave 13.E — `halal/fx_hedge.py`** — Multi-currency hedge planner using bay'-al-sarf-compliant spot legs + Wa'd roll commitments; AAOIFI Standard 1 hand-to-hand pin (T+0/T+1 only — T+2 rejected); Wakalah flat fee in bps replaces forward-points (which would be riba); HedgeHorizon ladder (SHORT/MEDIUM/LONG ≤ 30/90/180 days) (30 tests).
* **Wave 18.F — `core/tax_id.py`** — Indonesia tax classifier mirroring the `tax_my.py` shape: 0.1% final tax on listed-equity proceeds (NOT gain), +0.5% founder uplift, 10% dividend final tax, ≥25% corporate-holder dividend exemption, frequent-trader → BUSINESS_INCOME flag for accountant follow-up; bond-coupon and foreign-equity branches included (28 tests).

Total since start: **9159 tests passing** across the suite (excluding 250 DB-bound tests when Postgres is offline).

* **Wave 17.H — `halal/mudarabah_match.py`** — Trader-to-trader Mudarabah matching engine; FIFO + capacity-aware + risk-tolerance-compatibility table (conservative-capital cannot accept aggressive-skill, etc.); profit-share negotiated as the midpoint of the [cap_min, skill_max] overlap (≥ 5pp width required); horizon-compat enforced (capital cannot demand longer than skill commits) (34 tests).

Total since start: **9444 tests passing** across the suite (excluding 250 DB-bound tests when Postgres is offline).

remaining Wave 20 education surface: content feed (20.H) + 3-level
halal-CFA-equivalent curriculum (20.I).

* **Wave 20.H — `education/content_feed.py`** — Podcast/video/article/newsletter feed with closed-set MediaType ladder (time-based duration enforced for PODCAST/VIDEO; zero-duration enforced for ARTICLE/NEWSLETTER); EpisodeStatus FSM (DRAFT → PUBLISHED → ARCHIVED); per-user playback monotone-non-decreasing position with sticky completion at 95% threshold; recommended_feed filters to ACTIVE subscriptions + PUBLISHED-not-future episodes, sorted by published_at descending; plug-in moderation predicate at publish time (52 tests).
* **Wave 20.I — `education/cfa_curriculum.py`** — 3-level halal-CFA-equivalent (HCA_I → HCA_II → HCA_III) with Topic / Module / Level / Curriculum schema; strict prerequisite chain (HCA-II requires HCA-I CERTIFIED); EnrolmentStatus FSM (ENROLLED → ELIGIBLE → CERTIFIED, with WITHDRAWN alternate terminal); auto-promotion to ELIGIBLE when all level topics complete; per-level operator-tunable pass_threshold (default 70%); `highest_certified_level` helper for the user-profile surface; globally-unique topic_ids enforced at curriculum-construction (54 tests).

Total since start: **10962 tests passing** across the suite (excluding 250 DB-bound tests when Postgres is offline).

## Round-5 progress (auto-mode batch 12 — 2026-05-11)

Twelfth batch — 4 new modules / 157 new unit tests. Wave 23 (geographic
expansion + i18n depth) shipped as a unified i18n engine rather than 9
language-specific modules; Wave 23.J landed as a regional-scholar
router. New `i18n/` package houses the language primitives.

* **Wave 23.A-I (unified) — `i18n/translations.py`** — Locale-keyed translation registry covering 15 locales (EN, AR, AR_EG, AR_SA, UR, MS, ID, TR, HA, SW, BN, FA, PS, FR, ES); closed-set TextDirection ladder (LTR/RTL); fallback chain locale → base-locale → DEFAULT_LOCALE; `strict_mode` validates every key resolves in every locale at construction time; `merge_registries` lets operator-specific overrides layer on top of the base table (41 tests).
* **Wave 23 — `i18n/locale_format.py`** — Per-locale number/currency/date formatters with closed-set DigitShape ladder (WESTERN_ARABIC / ARABIC_INDIC / EXTENDED_ARABIC_INDIC for Persian-Urdu / BENGALI); per-locale decimal/thousands separators (e.g. ID `.` thousands `,` decimal; FR space thousands `,` decimal); currency symbol position (before vs after); 4 date-format variants (ISO/DMY/MDY/TEXT_DMY); digit shaping applied at the formatting layer so the same number renders correctly in all 15 locales (40 tests).
* **Wave 23 — `i18n/hijri.py`** — Tabular Islamic civil calendar (Kuwaiti pattern: 11 leap years per 30-year cycle in years 2,5,7,10,13,16,18,21,24,26,29); bidirectional `gregorian_to_hijri` / `hijri_to_gregorian` round-trip via Julian Day Number; closed-set HijriMonth ladder (Muharram → Dhu al-Hijjah); per-(year, month) length pin (odd months 30d, even months 29d, Dhu al-Hijjah 30d in leap years); `add_days` + `hijri_difference_days` for sukuk-maturity arithmetic (33 tests).
* **Wave 23.J — `halal/regional_scholars.py`** — Region → scholar router with closed-set Region ladder (12 regions) × Madhhab ladder (6 schools); 4-tier ranking (primary_region match → alternative_region → is_global → unrelated-excluded), with preferred-madhhab match as the within-tier breaker and scholar_id as the deterministic final tie-break; ScholarStatus FSM (ACTIVE → INACTIVE / DECEASED, with INACTIVE → ACTIVE allowed for sabbaticals); `has_madhhab_compatible` predicate for operator-side feature gating (43 tests).

Total since start: **11119 tests passing** across the suite (excluding 250 DB-bound tests when Postgres is offline).
